\section{Actual Microscopic Carrier Audit as a Finite Basis-Overlap Problem}

\subsection{Problem statement}

The remaining microscopic problem is not the reduced Dirac theorem itself.
That part is already closed once the shell witnesses
\[
\lambda_\parallel,\qquad \alpha,\qquad \beta
\]
are nonzero in the required pattern. The actual open question is whether the
\emph{full microscopic TECT linearization} around the relevant defect/BCC background
contains a nontrivial shell-relevant transport sector carrying both:

\begin{enumerate}
\item one spatial derivative index,
\item one reduced internal shell-tangent index.
\end{enumerate}

Equivalently, one must determine whether the true microscopic transport space contains
a nonzero projection onto the minimal shell seed sector generating
\[
(\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta).
\]

\subsection{Ambient finite-dimensional formulation}

Let
\[
W
=
\mathbb R^3_{\mathrm{out}}
\otimes
\mathbb R^3_{\mathrm{grad}}
\otimes
U_{\mathrm{int}}
\]
be the ambient shell-enriched tensor space, and let
\[
V_{\mathrm{TECT}}\subset W
\]
denote the actual symmetry-allowed microscopic transport space extracted from the full
TECT linearization around the chosen defect/BCC background.

Fix shell data
\[
G_*\neq 0,
\qquad
\hat n:=\frac{G_*}{|G_*|},
\qquad
\{e_1,e_2,\hat n\}\ \text{orthonormal}.
\]

The minimal shell-adapted tensor family is
\begin{equation}
N^3_{ij}=A\,\hat n_i\hat n_j,
\qquad
N^1_{ij}=B\,\hat n_i e_{1j}+C\,\hat n_i e_{2j},
\qquad
N^2_{ij}=-C\,\hat n_i e_{1j}+B\,\hat n_i e_{2j}.
\label{eq:carrier_min_family}
\end{equation}
This is exactly the smallest seed family capable of generating one longitudinal channel
and the transverse \(E/O\) doublet.

\subsection{Shell target covectors and witness functionals}

Define the three shell target covectors
\[
T^{(\parallel)}_{ija},
\qquad
T^{(I)}_{ija},
\qquad
T^{(J)}_{ija},
\]
adapted to the three required reduced channels. The corresponding linear witness
functionals are
\begin{equation}
L_\alpha(N):=\langle T^{(\alpha)},N\rangle,
\qquad
\alpha\in\{\parallel,I,J\}.
\label{eq:Lalpha_def}
\end{equation}

Their exact logical meaning is:

\[
L_\alpha|_{V_{\mathrm{TECT}}}\equiv 0
\iff
P_V T^{(\alpha)}=0,
\]
where \(P_V:W\to V_{\mathrm{TECT}}\) is the orthogonal projector.

Thus:
\[
P_VT^{(\alpha)}\neq 0
\]
means that the actual microscopic TECT linearization contains a shell-relevant
nontrivial carrier direction in channel \(\alpha\).

\subsection{Basis-level audit}

Choose an arbitrary basis
\[
\{E_A\}_{A=1}^d
\]
of the actual microscopic transport space \(V_{\mathrm{TECT}}\).
Define the overlap coefficients
\begin{equation}
\ell_{\parallel A}:=\langle T^{(\parallel)},E_A\rangle,
\qquad
\ell_{IA}:=\langle T^{(I)},E_A\rangle,
\qquad
\ell_{JA}:=\langle T^{(J)},E_A\rangle.
\label{eq:ell_def}
\end{equation}

Then for a general element
\[
N=\sum_{A=1}^d x_A E_A\in V_{\mathrm{TECT}},
\]
the witness functionals become
\begin{equation}
L_{\parallel}(N)=\sum_A x_A \ell_{\parallel A},
\qquad
L_I(N)=\sum_A x_A \ell_{IA},
\qquad
L_J(N)=\sum_A x_A \ell_{JA}.
\label{eq:L_expand_basis}
\end{equation}

Therefore:
\[
L_\alpha|_{V_{\mathrm{TECT}}}\equiv 0
\iff
\ell_{\alpha A}=0\quad \forall A.
\]

Hence the microscopic carrier audit succeeds if and only if both of the following hold:

\begin{equation}
\exists A:\ \ell_{\parallel A}\neq 0,
\label{eq:long_basis_condition}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\exists B:\ (\ell_{IB},\ell_{JB})\neq (0,0).
\label{eq:trans_basis_condition}
\end{equation}

This is the exact basis-level completion criterion.

\subsection{Theorem: basis-level carrier-audit theorem}

\begin{theorem}[Basis-level carrier-audit theorem]
Let \(V_{\mathrm{TECT}}\subset W\) be the actual microscopic transport space and
\(\{E_A\}_{A=1}^d\) any basis of \(V_{\mathrm{TECT}}\).
Then the microscopic carrier audit succeeds if and only if:

\begin{enumerate}
\item there exists at least one basis element \(E_A\) with
\[
\ell_{\parallel A}\neq 0;
\]

\item there exists at least one basis element \(E_B\) with
\[
(\ell_{IB},\ell_{JB})\neq (0,0).
\]
\end{enumerate}

Equivalently,
\[
P_VT^{(\parallel)}\neq 0
\qquad\text{and}\qquad
\bigl(P_VT^{(I)},P_VT^{(J)}\bigr)\neq (0,0).
\]
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
By definition,
\[
L_\alpha(N)=\sum_A x_A\ell_{\alpha A}
\]
for every \(N=\sum_A x_AE_A\in V_{\mathrm{TECT}}\).
Hence \(L_\alpha|_{V_{\mathrm{TECT}}}\equiv 0\) if and only if every coefficient
\(\ell_{\alpha A}\) vanishes.

Therefore the longitudinal channel survives if and only if there exists at least one
basis element with \(\ell_{\parallel A}\neq 0\). Likewise, the transverse sector survives
if and only if at least one basis element has nonzero overlap with one of the two transverse
targets. Since the reduced Weyl/Dirac witness requires one longitudinal channel and at least
one transverse channel, the two stated conditions are necessary and sufficient.
\end{proof}

\subsection{Shell-adapted decomposition}

Let
\[
V_{\min}=\mathrm{span}\{B_\parallel,B_I,B_J\}
\]
be the minimal shell seed space.
Decompose each basis element as
\begin{equation}
E_A
=
a_A B_\parallel + b_A B_I + c_A B_J + R_A,
\qquad
R_A\perp V_{\min}.
\label{eq:EA_decomp}
\end{equation}

Because the witness functionals vanish on \(R_A\), one gets
\[
\ell_{\parallel A}=\mu_\parallel a_A,
\qquad
\ell_{IA}=\mu_I b_A,
\qquad
\ell_{JA}=\mu_J c_A,
\]
with nonzero shell-normalization constants
\[
\mu_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
\mu_I\neq 0,
\qquad
\mu_J\neq 0.
\]

Hence the carrier audit is equivalently:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\exists A:\ a_A\neq 0,
\qquad
\exists B:\ (b_B,c_B)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:shell_basis_completion}
\end{equation}

So the audit has an immediate physical meaning:

\begin{enumerate}
\item at least one actual microscopic transport basis vector must contain a
nonzero longitudinal seed component \(B_\parallel\);

\item at least one actual microscopic transport basis vector must contain a
nonzero transverse seed component in the \(B_I/B_J\) plane.
\end{enumerate}

\subsection{Immediate reduced Dirac consequence}

Once the basis-level carrier audit succeeds, the reduced first-order symbol takes the form
\[
A_1(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\alpha(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2),
\]
with
\[
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0).
\]

Equivalently, in the shell-adapted notation,
\[
\det\Lambda
=
\Lambda_\parallel(\Lambda_E^2+\Lambda_O^2)\neq 0.
\]
Hence the local shell block is a genuine anisotropic Weyl symbol, and opposite-valley
doubling yields the corresponding Dirac block.

\subsection{What is now closed and what remains open}

What is now closed is the exact reduction of the microscopic carrier problem to a finite,
explicit basis-overlap audit:
\[
\boxed{
\exists A:\ \ell_{\parallel A}\neq 0,
\qquad
\exists B:\ (\ell_{IB},\ell_{JB})\neq (0,0).
}
\]

What remains open is no longer a conceptual PDE issue.
It is the execution of this finite audit for the final complete microscopic TECT linearization.

In particular, the transverse half is already structurally realized inside the explicit seed
construction, whereas the honest remaining frontier is the actual embedding/survival of the
primitive longitudinal seed inside the true full microscopic transport space.

\section{Final Summary}

The actual microscopic carrier problem has now been reduced to a finite-dimensional
basis-overlap audit on the full microscopic transport space
\[
V_{\mathrm{TECT}}\subset
\mathbb R^3_{\mathrm{out}}
\otimes
\mathbb R^3_{\mathrm{grad}}
\otimes
U_{\mathrm{int}}.
\]

For any basis \(\{E_A\}_{A=1}^d\) of \(V_{\mathrm{TECT}}\), define
\[
\ell_{\parallel A}=\langle T^{(\parallel)},E_A\rangle,
\qquad
\ell_{IA}=\langle T^{(I)},E_A\rangle,
\qquad
\ell_{JA}=\langle T^{(J)},E_A\rangle.
\]

Then the exact completion criterion is
\[
\boxed{
\exists A:\ \ell_{\parallel A}\neq 0,
\qquad
\exists B:\ (\ell_{IB},\ell_{JB})\neq (0,0).
}
\]

Equivalently, the full microscopic TECT transport space must contain at least:

\begin{enumerate}
\item one admissible longitudinal seed direction,
\item one admissible transverse seed direction.
\end{enumerate}

Once this holds, the reduced first-order symbol has the anisotropic Weyl form
\[
A_1(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\alpha(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2),
\]
with
\[
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0),
\]
and opposite-valley doubling yields the local Dirac block.

Therefore the actual remaining frontier is no longer conceptual.
It is the explicit execution of the finite basis audit for the final full microscopic
TECT linearization.

\section{Actual Microscopic Carrier Audit}

\section{Problem statement}

The remaining microscopic question is not whether the shell-level Weyl/Dirac witness logic is correct.
That part is already closed inside the explicit seed/Class II realization.
The actual remaining question is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Does the true microscopic TECT linearization contain a nontrivial shell-relevant }(i,a)\text{-carrier sector?}
}
\label{eq:actual_carrier_question}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, after linearization around the relevant defect/BCC background and shell/defect projection, does the microscopic transport space contain at least one longitudinal seed direction and at least one transverse seed direction?

\section{What the witness actually needs}

The shell-level local Weyl/Dirac witness is controlled by an enriched tensor
\[
N^a_{ij},
\]
through the shell-adapted coefficients
\[
\lambda_\parallel,\qquad \alpha,\qquad \beta.
\]

The minimal shell-adapted tensor family is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
N^3_{ij}=A\,\hat n_i\hat n_j,\qquad
N^1_{ij}=B\,\hat n_i e_{1j}+C\,\hat n_i e_{2j},\qquad
N^2_{ij}=-C\,\hat n_i e_{1j}+B\,\hat n_i e_{2j}.
}
\label{eq:min_shell_family}
\end{equation}

Hence the microscopic carrier must simultaneously supply:

\begin{enumerate}
\item one spatial derivative index \(i\) or \(j\),
\item one reduced internal shell-tangent index \(a\).
\end{enumerate}

This is the structural meaning of an \((i,a)\)-carrier sector.

\section{Explicit seed space}

Define the explicit seed space
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V_{\mathrm{seed}}
=
\mathrm{span}\left\{
N_{\mathrm{seed}}^{(\parallel)},
N_{\mathrm{seed}}^{(\perp,E)},
N_{\mathrm{seed}}^{(\perp,O)}
\right\}.
}
\label{eq:Vseed}
\end{equation}

Inside this seed space, for
\[
N
=
c_\parallel N_{\mathrm{seed}}^{(\parallel)}
+
c_E N_{\mathrm{seed}}^{(\perp,E)}
+
c_O N_{\mathrm{seed}}^{(\perp,O)},
\]
the reduced witness coefficients are exactly
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\frac12 c_\parallel I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=c_E I_\theta,
\qquad
\beta=c_O I_\theta.
}
\label{eq:seed_witness_exact}
\end{equation}

Since
\[
I_\theta\neq 0,
\qquad
I_{\theta'^3}\neq 0,
\]
the reduced symbol is nondegenerate if and only if
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(c_E,c_O)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:seed_nondeg}
\end{equation}

Therefore the witness problem is already exactly closed inside the explicit seed ansatz.

\section{Finite-dimensional carrier audit}

Let
\[
W=\mathbb R^3_{\mathrm{out}}\otimes \mathbb R^3_{\mathrm{grad}}\otimes U_{\mathrm{int}}
\]
be the ambient enriched tensor space, and let
\[
V_{\mathrm{TECT}}\subset W
\]
be the actual microscopic transport space extracted from the full microscopic TECT linearization around the relevant defect/BCC background.

For each channel \(\alpha\in\{\parallel,I,J\}\), define the witness functional
\begin{equation}
L_\alpha(N)=\langle T^{(\alpha)},N\rangle.
\label{eq:Lalpha}
\end{equation}

Then the exact projection criterion is
\begin{equation}
P_VT^{(\alpha)}=0
\iff
L_\alpha|_{V_{\mathrm{TECT}}}\equiv 0,
\label{eq:projection_criterion}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
P_VT^{(\alpha)}\neq 0
\iff
L_\alpha
\text{ is generically nonzero on }V_{\mathrm{TECT}}.
\label{eq:projection_nonzero}
\end{equation}

Thus the carrier problem is not an infinite-dimensional PDE mystery.
It is an explicit finite projection / seed-embedding audit.

\section{Basis-level executable criterion}

Choose any basis
\[
\{E_A\}_{A=1}^d
\]
of the actual microscopic transport space \(V_{\mathrm{TECT}}\).

Define the overlap coefficients
\begin{equation}
\ell_{\parallel A}:=\langle T^{(\parallel)},E_A\rangle,
\qquad
\ell_{IA}:=\langle T^{(I)},E_A\rangle,
\qquad
\ell_{JA}:=\langle T^{(J)},E_A\rangle.
\label{eq:ellA}
\end{equation}

Then the carrier audit succeeds if and only if
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\exists A:\ \ell_{\parallel A}\neq 0,
\qquad
\exists B:\ (\ell_{IB},\ell_{JB})\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:basis_audit}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, if each basis element has the invariant shell-reduced decomposition
\begin{equation}
E_A^{\mathrm{inv}}=a_A B_\parallel+b_A B_I+c_A B_J,
\label{eq:EAinv}
\end{equation}
then
\[
a_A\neq 0\iff \ell_{\parallel A}\neq 0,
\qquad
(b_A,c_A)\neq (0,0)\iff (\ell_{IA},\ell_{JA})\neq (0,0),
\]
and the exact executable criterion becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\exists A:\ a_A\neq 0,
\qquad
\exists B:\ (b_B,c_B)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:abc_audit}
\end{equation}

\section{The transverse half is already closed}

The explicit transverse seed
\begin{equation}
V^\mu_{(\perp,E)}(\xi)=\theta'(\xi)\,E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
\label{eq:trans_seed_E}
\end{equation}
gives
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel=0,
\qquad
\alpha=I_\theta\neq 0,
\qquad
\beta=0.
\label{eq:trans_seed_E_wit}
\end{equation}

Optionally,
\begin{equation}
V^\mu_{(\perp,O)}(\xi)=\theta'(\xi)\,J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
\label{eq:trans_seed_O}
\end{equation}
gives
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel=0,
\qquad
\alpha=0,
\qquad
\beta=I_\theta\neq 0.
\label{eq:trans_seed_O_wit}
\end{equation}

Hence the transverse nondegeneracy condition
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0)
}
\label{eq:trans_closed}
\end{equation}
is already explicitly realizable.
So the transverse half of the carrier audit is no longer open.

\section{The only remaining microscopic carrier question}

The explicit longitudinal seed is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu_{(\parallel)}(\xi)=\frac12\,\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\sigma_3,
}
\label{eq:long_seed}
\end{equation}
which gives
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\frac12 I_{\theta'^3}\neq 0,
\qquad
\alpha=\beta=0.
}
\label{eq:long_seed_wit}
\end{equation}

Therefore the unresolved microscopic question is not whether a longitudinal witness can exist in principle.
It can.

The remaining question is only:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{does the full microscopic TECT linearization actually realize the primitive longitudinal channel }\theta'(\xi)^3\sigma_3\ ?
}
\label{eq:long_only_open}
\end{equation}

\section{Non-forbiddance statement}

At the shell-reduced symmetry level, the longitudinal channel is not symmetry-forbidden.
Equivalently, the residual shell symmetry does not force
\[
P_VT^{(\parallel)}=0.
\]

Hence, if the longitudinal channel vanishes in the final complete microscopic realization,
the reason must be stronger than the minimal residual shell symmetry.
It would require one of:

\begin{enumerate}
\item an additional microscopic symmetry,
\item a dynamical cancellation among actual basis elements,
\item or the absence of any genuine \((i,a)\)-carrier sector.
\end{enumerate}

So the longitudinal failure is not automatic.
It would itself require a concrete microscopic explanation.

\section{Class-by-class audit meaning}

At lowest derivative order, the admissible minimal microscopic carrier classes are:
\[
\boxed{
\text{Class I,\qquad Class II,\qquad Class III.}
}
\]

Among them, Class II is the strongest current explicit class because it realizes the three shell coordinates simultaneously.
Its shell reduction gives
\[
\delta A\propto c_\parallel,\qquad
\delta B\propto c_I,\qquad
\delta C\propto c_J,
\]
so inside the explicit Class II truncation the carrier answer is already yes.

Therefore the strongest honest conclusion is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{inside the explicit Class II truncation, the carrier problem is solved;}
}
\end{equation}
what remains open is only whether the final complete microscopic TECT realization contains the same nontrivial carrier sector in the physically relevant defect background.

\section{Operational audit algorithm}

The final executable microscopic audit is:

\paragraph{Step 1.}
Linearize the complete refined locked TECT equations around
\[
\Psi_0=\phi_0 z_0,\qquad P_0=z_0z_0^\dagger.
\]

\paragraph{Step 2.}
Extract the shell-relevant first-order transport operator
\[
L_1=-iV^\mu(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu}.
\]

\paragraph{Step 3.}
Choose the low-mode shell basis at the opposite shell pair \(\pm G_*\), and compute
\[
(M^\mu)_{ab}=\langle u_a^+,V^\mu u_b^-\rangle.
\]

\paragraph{Step 4.}
Decompose the induced shell tensor in the basis
\[
\bigl(
N_{\mathrm{seed}}^{(\parallel)},
N_{\mathrm{seed}}^{(\perp,E)},
N_{\mathrm{seed}}^{(\perp,O)}
\bigr),
\]
equivalently extract
\[
(A,B,C)
\quad\text{or}\quad
(\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta).
\]

\paragraph{Step 5.}
Audit the coefficients:
\[
A\neq 0,
\qquad
(B,C)\neq (0,0).
\]

Equivalently, at the basis level,
\[
\exists A:\ a_A\neq 0,
\qquad
\exists B:\ (b_B,c_B)\neq (0,0).
\]

\section{Strongest honest theorem-level status}

We can now state the sharpest honest result.

\begin{theorem}[Actual microscopic carrier audit: sharp honest form]
Assume:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the full refined locked TECT linearization admits a finite shell-relevant transport space \(V_{\mathrm{TECT}}\);
\item the transverse odd-gradient extraction survives, so that \(I_\theta\neq 0\);
\item the longitudinal primitive channel survives if and only if the final basis audit finds at least one nonzero longitudinal coefficient.
\end{enumerate}

Then:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the transverse carrier is explicitly realized;
\item the transverse nondegeneracy condition
\[
(\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0)
\]
is closed;
\item the only remaining microscopic carrier question is the longitudinal primitive odd singlet channel,
\[
\theta'(\xi)^3\sigma_3;
\]
\item the full local Weyl/Dirac witness audit succeeds if and only if
\[
\exists A:\ a_A\neq 0,
\qquad
\exists B:\ (b_B,c_B)\neq (0,0).
\]
\end{enumerate}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The transverse statement follows from the explicit transverse seed extraction, which already produces
\[
\alpha=I_\theta\neq 0
\quad\text{or}\quad
\beta=I_\theta\neq 0.
\]
So the transverse half is explicitly realized.

The longitudinal statement follows because the longitudinal witness is linear on the finite-dimensional transport space. Thus it survives if and only if it is nonzero on at least one basis element, equivalently if and only if at least one invariant basis coefficient \(a_A\) is nonzero.

Combining the two gives the stated necessary and sufficient audit criterion.
\end{proof}

\section{Final Summary}

The actual microscopic carrier audit is no longer an infinite-dimensional PDE problem.
It has been reduced to a finite projection / basis-overlap audit on the shell-relevant microscopic transport space
\[
V_{\mathrm{TECT}}\subset
\mathbb R^3_{\mathrm{out}}
\otimes
\mathbb R^3_{\mathrm{grad}}
\otimes
U_{\mathrm{int}}.
\]

The shell witness requires an enriched tensor
\[
N^a_{ij},
\]
whose minimal shell-adapted form is
\[
N^3_{ij}=A\,\hat n_i\hat n_j,\qquad
N^1_{ij}=B\,\hat n_i e_{1j}+C\,\hat n_i e_{2j},\qquad
N^2_{ij}=-C\,\hat n_i e_{1j}+B\,\hat n_i e_{2j}.
\]

Inside the explicit seed space
\[
V_{\mathrm{seed}}
=
\mathrm{span}\left\{
N_{\mathrm{seed}}^{(\parallel)},
N_{\mathrm{seed}}^{(\perp,E)},
N_{\mathrm{seed}}^{(\perp,O)}
\right\},
\]
the reduced witness coefficients are exactly
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\frac12 c_\parallel I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=c_E I_\theta,
\qquad
\beta=c_O I_\theta.
\]

Since
\[
I_\theta\neq 0,
\qquad
I_{\theta'^3}\neq 0,
\]
the reduced symbol is nondegenerate if and only if
\[
c_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(c_E,c_O)\neq (0,0).
\]

For an actual microscopic basis \(\{E_A\}\), with invariant shell-reduced decomposition
\[
E_A^{\mathrm{inv}}=a_A B_\parallel+b_A B_I+c_A B_J,
\]
the exact executable audit criterion is
\[
\boxed{
\exists A:\ a_A\neq 0,
\qquad
\exists B:\ (b_B,c_B)\neq (0,0).
}
\]

The transverse half is already explicitly solved.
Hence the only remaining microscopic carrier question is whether the full complete TECT linearization actually realizes the primitive longitudinal odd singlet channel
\[
\theta'(\xi)^3\sigma_3.
\]

Therefore the strongest honest current status is:
\[
\boxed{
\text{transverse solved, longitudinal remaining.}
}
\]

The final frontier is not conceptual.
It is the explicit computation of the invariant coefficients
\[
(a_A,b_A,c_A)
\]
for the basis elements of the full microscopic transport space.

\section{Actual Microscopic Carrier Audit in the One-Mediator Branch-B Truncation}

\section{Logical starting point}

The minimal locked isotropic complex-triplet Brazovskii equation does not by itself
generate the shell-enriched Pauli-sector witness \(N_{ij}^a\).
In particular, the linear quartic term gives no direct enriched first-order source,
the isotropic kinetic first-order shell transport cancels exactly at the Brazovskii shell,
and the locked zeroth-order cross-shell quartic projection vanishes.
Therefore the microscopic carrier problem cannot be closed inside the minimal locked isotropic PDE alone.

Hence the correct microscopic route is the enriched explicit UV/Class-II channel.

\section{One-mediator truncation}

Consider the refined one-mediator truncation
\begin{equation}
\mathcal L_{\mathrm{trunc}}
=
\mathcal L_{\Psi}^{\mathrm{core}}
+
\mathcal L_{P}^{\mathrm{geom}}
+
\mathcal L_{\sigma}^{\mathrm{vol}}
+
\frac12 M_X^2 X_i^a X_i^a
+
\alpha_X X_i^a J_i^a[\Psi]
+
\beta_X X_i^a K_i^a[P,\psi]
+
\gamma_E X_i^a \mathcal E_i^a[P,\psi]
+
\gamma_O X_i^a \mathcal O_i^a[P,\psi].
\label{eq:one_mediator_trunc}
\end{equation}

Here:

\begin{enumerate}
\item \(J_i^a[\Psi]\) is the microscopic longitudinal carrier current;
\item \(K_i^a[P,\psi]\) is the defect-tangent odd primitive channel;
\item \(\mathcal E_i^a[P,\psi]\) and \(\mathcal O_i^a[P,\psi]\) are the two transverse parity-distinguished shell channels.
\end{enumerate}

The actual detailed tensor realization of these operators is model-dependent, but at the shell-reduced level only their projections onto the three seed channels matter.

\section{Integrating out the mediator}

Since \(X_i^a\) appears quadratically and algebraically, its equation of motion is
\begin{equation}
M_X^2 X_i^a
+
\alpha_X J_i^a
+
\beta_X K_i^a
+
\gamma_E \mathcal E_i^a
+
\gamma_O \mathcal O_i^a
=
0,
\end{equation}
hence
\begin{equation}
X_i^a
=
-\frac{1}{M_X^2}
\Big(
\alpha_X J_i^a
+
\beta_X K_i^a
+
\gamma_E \mathcal E_i^a
+
\gamma_O \mathcal O_i^a
\Big).
\label{eq:X_solution}
\end{equation}

Substituting back gives the effective interaction
\begin{equation}
\mathcal L_{\mathrm{eff}}^{(X)}
=
-\frac{1}{2M_X^2}
\Big(
\alpha_X J_i^a
+
\beta_X K_i^a
+
\gamma_E \mathcal E_i^a
+
\gamma_O \mathcal O_i^a
\Big)^2.
\label{eq:Leff_X_full}
\end{equation}

Expanding the square and keeping only the terms relevant to the three first-order shell witnesses yields
\begin{equation}
\mathcal L_{\mathrm{eff}}^{(1)}
=
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,J_i^a K_i^a
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_E}{M_X^2}\,K_i^a \mathcal E_i^a
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}\,K_i^a \mathcal O_i^a
+\cdots.
\label{eq:Leff_relevant}
\end{equation}

Thus the carrier problem reduces to the shell projection of these three mixed bilinears.

\section{Local defect frame and tangent Pauli basis}

Let the local defect projector background be
\begin{equation}
P_B(\xi)=z_B(\xi)z_B(\xi)^\dagger,
\qquad
z_B^\dagger z_B=1,
\end{equation}
with tangent bundle
\begin{equation}
Q_B(\xi)=\bigl(\mathbb C z_B(\xi)\bigr)^\perp.
\end{equation}

Choose the explicit local real frame
\begin{equation}
z_B(\xi)=
\begin{pmatrix}
\cos\theta(\xi)\\
0\\
\sin\theta(\xi)
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
e_1(\xi)=
\begin{pmatrix}
-\sin\theta(\xi)\\
0\\
\cos\theta(\xi)
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
e_2=
\begin{pmatrix}
0\\
1\\
0
\end{pmatrix}.
\label{eq:defect_frame}
\end{equation}

Then the tangent Pauli operators \(\Sigma_1,\Sigma_2,\Sigma_3\) are the Pauli matrices acting on the local tangent doublet in the basis \((e_1,e_2)\).

\section{Primitive seed decomposition}

At the shell-reduced level, only three seed channels matter:

\begin{equation}
B_\parallel
\sim
\theta'(\xi)^3\, \hat n_i \hat n_j\, \Sigma_3,
\label{eq:Bpar_seed}
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
B_E
\sim
\theta'(\xi)\,\hat n_i e_{1j}\,\Sigma_1
+
\theta'(\xi)\,\hat n_i e_{2j}\,\Sigma_2,
\label{eq:BE_seed}
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
B_O
\sim
-\theta'(\xi)\,\hat n_i e_{2j}\,\Sigma_1
+
\theta'(\xi)\,\hat n_i e_{1j}\,\Sigma_2.
\label{eq:BO_seed}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, the minimal shell-adapted tensor family is
\begin{equation}
N^3_{ij}=A\,\hat n_i\hat n_j,
\qquad
N^1_{ij}=B\,\hat n_i e_{1j}+C\,\hat n_i e_{2j},
\qquad
N^2_{ij}=-C\,\hat n_i e_{1j}+B\,\hat n_i e_{2j}.
\label{eq:min_family_again}
\end{equation}

The reduced Weyl/Dirac witnesses are exactly the coefficients of these three channels.

\section{Shell pair and low-mode basis}

Fix the selected shell pair \(\pm G_*\), with
\begin{equation}
\hat n:=\frac{G_*}{|G_*|},
\qquad
p=p_\parallel \hat n + p_1 e_1 + p_2 e_2.
\end{equation}

Let \(\{u_a^+\}\) and \(\{u_b^-\}\) be the two low-mode tangent doublet bases at the two opposite valleys.
The induced first-order shell matrix element of a microscopic carrier \(V^\mu\) is
\begin{equation}
(M^\mu)_{ab}
=
\langle u_a^+,\, V^\mu\, u_b^- \rangle.
\label{eq:Mmubasis}
\end{equation}

The projected first-order symbol is then
\begin{equation}
A_1(p)=p_\mu M^\mu.
\label{eq:A1_from_M}
\end{equation}

Decomposing \(M^\mu\) in the tangent Pauli basis yields
\begin{equation}
A_1(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\widetilde\Lambda_E
\bigl(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2\bigr)
+
\widetilde\Lambda_O
\bigl(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2\bigr).
\label{eq:A1_decomp}
\end{equation}

\section{Evaluation of the three coefficients}

The shell projection of the three mixed terms in \eqref{eq:Leff_relevant} produces three overlap constants:
\begin{equation}
C_\parallel,\qquad C_E,\qquad C_O,
\end{equation}
defined as the purely local tangent-matrix normalizations of the three seed projections.

The defect-profile dependence is carried by the two overlap integrals
\begin{equation}
I_3
:=
\int d\xi\, w(\xi)\,\theta'(\xi)^3,
\qquad
J_1
:=
\int d\xi\, w(\xi)\,\theta'(\xi)\cos\theta(\xi),
\label{eq:I3J1def}
\end{equation}
with \(w(\xi)=f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\ge 0\) the product of the two shell-localized envelope profiles.

Then the three shell witnesses are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{2M_X^2}\, C_\parallel\, I_3,
}
\label{eq:lambda_parallel_eval}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widetilde\Lambda_E
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_E}{M_X^2}\, C_E\, J_1,
}
\label{eq:LambdaE_eval}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widetilde\Lambda_O
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}\, C_O\, J_1.
}
\label{eq:LambdaO_eval}
\end{equation}

These are the actual shell-projected carrier coefficients in the one-mediator Branch-B truncation.

\section{Canonical normalization}

If one chooses the shell tangent basis and operator normalization so that
\begin{equation}
C_\parallel=C_E=C_O=1,
\label{eq:canonical_norm}
\end{equation}
then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{2M_X^2}\, I_3,
\qquad
\widetilde\Lambda_E
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_E}{M_X^2}\, J_1,
\qquad
\widetilde\Lambda_O
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}\, J_1.
}
\label{eq:canonical_coeffs}
\end{equation}

Thus the reduced first-order symbol becomes
\begin{equation}
A_1(p)
=
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{2M_X^2} I_3\, p_\parallel \sigma_3
-
\frac{\beta_X\gamma_E}{M_X^2}J_1\,(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
-
\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}J_1\,(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2).
\label{eq:A1_canonical}
\end{equation}

\section{Exact nondegeneracy criterion}

The reduced anisotropic Weyl symbol is nondegenerate if and only if
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(\widetilde\Lambda_E,\widetilde\Lambda_O)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:exact_nondeg_again}
\end{equation}

Using \eqref{eq:lambda_parallel_eval}--\eqref{eq:LambdaO_eval}, this is equivalent to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha_X\beta_X\,C_\parallel\,I_3\neq 0,
\qquad
\beta_X\,J_1\,
(\gamma_E C_E,\gamma_O C_O)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:mic_nondeg_coeff}
\end{equation}

Hence, assuming
\[
I_3\neq 0,
\qquad
J_1\neq 0,
\qquad
\beta_X\neq 0,
\]
the exact carrier audit closes if and only if
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha_X C_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(\gamma_E C_E,\gamma_O C_O)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:audit_closure_simple}
\end{equation}

\section{Branch-B interpretation}

Inside the local isotropic TECT algebra, the linear longitudinal selector is absent and the first surviving longitudinal primitive is cubic in \(\theta'\).
Therefore the surviving longitudinal coefficient is precisely the Branch-B coefficient
\[
\lambda_\parallel \propto I_3,
\]
not a Branch-A linear coefficient.

Thus the one-mediator truncation realizes the exact Branch-B structure:
\begin{equation}
A_1(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\widetilde\Lambda_E(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\widetilde\Lambda_O(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2).
\label{eq:branchB_symbol_final}
\end{equation}

\section{Infrared velocities}

After the standard identification of the reduced PDE coefficients,
\begin{equation}
v_\parallel=\lambda_\parallel,
\qquad
v_E=\widetilde\Lambda_E,
\qquad
v_O=\widetilde\Lambda_O,
\label{eq:v_ident}
\end{equation}
one obtains
\begin{equation}
v_\perp=\sqrt{v_E^2+v_O^2}
=
\frac{|\beta_X|\,|J_1|}{M_X^2}
\sqrt{\gamma_E^2 C_E^2+\gamma_O^2 C_O^2}.
\label{eq:vperp_eval}
\end{equation}

Hence the anisotropy ratio is
\begin{equation}
\rho
=
\frac{v_\parallel}{v_\perp}
=
-\frac{\alpha_X C_\parallel}{2\sqrt{\gamma_E^2C_E^2+\gamma_O^2C_O^2}}
\frac{I_3}{J_1}.
\label{eq:rho_general}
\end{equation}

In the small-defect regime,
\[
I_3\sim \frac{3}{16}(\theta_0\kappa)^2 J_1,
\]
so
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\rho_{\mathrm{LO}}
=
-\frac{3}{32}\,
\frac{\alpha_X C_\parallel}{\sqrt{\gamma_E^2C_E^2+\gamma_O^2C_O^2}}\,
(\theta_0\kappa)^2.
}
\label{eq:rho_LO_derived}
\end{equation}

This is the leading Branch-B anisotropy formula.

\section{What is actually closed here}

The calculation above closes the carrier audit at the truncation level:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the mediator integration generates exactly the three shell-relevant mixed operators;
\item their shell projections produce the three witness coefficients \(\lambda_\parallel,\widetilde\Lambda_E,\widetilde\Lambda_O\);
\item the reduced symbol is the exact Branch-B anisotropic Weyl symbol;
\item the full low-energy anisotropy ratio \(\rho\) follows explicitly.
\end{enumerate}

\section{What is still not unconditional}

What remains not yet unconditional is not the algebraic reduction itself.
The unresolved issue is the final microscopic value of the three local normalization overlaps
\[
C_\parallel,\qquad C_E,\qquad C_O,
\]
for the actual complete refined locked microscopic TECT realization.

Thus the remaining frontier is a calibration problem:
compute the exact projected matrix elements \eqref{eq:Mmubasis} in the final full microscopic Bloch linearization and verify
\[
C_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(C_E,C_O)\neq (0,0).
\]

\section{Final Summary}

The actual microscopic carrier audit in the refined one-mediator Branch-B truncation is now reduced to an explicit shell-projection calculation.

Starting from
\[
\mathcal L_{\mathrm{trunc}}
=
\mathcal L_{\Psi}^{\mathrm{core}}
+
\mathcal L_{P}^{\mathrm{geom}}
+
\mathcal L_{\sigma}^{\mathrm{vol}}
+
\frac12 M_X^2 X_i^a X_i^a
+
\alpha_X X_i^a J_i^a
+
\beta_X X_i^a K_i^a
+
\gamma_E X_i^a \mathcal E_i^a
+
\gamma_O X_i^a \mathcal O_i^a,
\]
integrating out \(X_i^a\) generates the three relevant mixed effective operators
\[
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}J\cdot K,
\qquad
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_E}{M_X^2}K\cdot \mathcal E,
\qquad
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}K\cdot \mathcal O.
\]

After shell/defect projection, these produce the exact Branch-B witness coefficients
\[
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{2M_X^2}\, C_\parallel\, I_3,
\qquad
\widetilde\Lambda_E
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_E}{M_X^2}\, C_E\, J_1,
\qquad
\widetilde\Lambda_O
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}\, C_O\, J_1.
\]

Hence the reduced first-order symbol is
\[
A_1(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\widetilde\Lambda_E(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\widetilde\Lambda_O(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2).
\]

The exact nondegeneracy criterion is
\[
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(\widetilde\Lambda_E,\widetilde\Lambda_O)\neq (0,0).
\]

Therefore the remaining microscopic frontier is not conceptual:
it is the explicit determination of the three shell normalization overlaps
\[
C_\parallel,\qquad C_E,\qquad C_O
\]
from the final complete projected Bloch linearization.

In canonical normalization,
\[
C_\parallel=C_E=C_O=1,
\]
the anisotropy ratio becomes
\[
\rho_{\mathrm{LO}}
=
-\frac{3}{32}\,
\frac{\alpha_X}{\sqrt{\gamma_E^2+\gamma_O^2}}\,
(\theta_0\kappa)^2.
\]

Thus the actual carrier audit is reduced completely to a finite calibration problem.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Matrix-Element Audit for the Actual Microscopic Carrier Coefficients}

\section{Goal}

The remaining microscopic calibration problem is to extract the three shell normalization overlaps
\[
C_\parallel,\qquad C_E,\qquad C_O
\]
from the projected \(2\times 2\) shell matrix elements.

The reduced first-order symbol is generated from
\begin{equation}
(M^\mu)_{ab}
=
\langle u_a^+,\,V^\mu\,u_b^- \rangle,
\qquad
a,b=1,2,
\label{eq:Mmu_def}
\end{equation}
where \(\{u_a^+\}\) and \(\{u_b^-\}\) are the low-mode tangent-doublet bases at the opposite shell pair \(\pm G_*\).

The effective first-order shell operator is
\begin{equation}
A_1(p)=p_\mu M^\mu.
\label{eq:A1pmu}
\end{equation}

The task is therefore to decompose \(M^\mu\) into the unique shell-adapted Pauli basis and read off the coefficients.

\section{Shell-adapted Pauli decomposition}

Fix the shell direction
\[
\hat n:=\frac{G_*}{|G_*|},
\]
and choose an orthonormal frame
\[
\{e_1,e_2,\hat n\}.
\]
Decompose momentum as
\begin{equation}
p=p_\parallel \hat n + p_1 e_1 + p_2 e_2.
\label{eq:p_decomp}
\end{equation}

Since each \(M^\mu\) is a \(2\times2\) Hermitian matrix acting on the shell tangent doublet, it admits the unique decomposition
\begin{equation}
M^\mu
=
m_0^\mu \mathbf 1_2
+
m_1^\mu \sigma_1
+
m_2^\mu \sigma_2
+
m_3^\mu \sigma_3,
\label{eq:Mmu_pauli}
\end{equation}
with real coefficients
\begin{equation}
m_A^\mu=\frac12\operatorname{Tr}(\sigma_A M^\mu),
\qquad
A=0,1,2,3,
\label{eq:mA_trace}
\end{equation}
where \(\sigma_0:=\mathbf1_2\).

Therefore
\begin{equation}
A_1(p)
=
p_\mu m_0^\mu \mathbf1_2
+
p_\mu m_1^\mu \sigma_1
+
p_\mu m_2^\mu \sigma_2
+
p_\mu m_3^\mu \sigma_3.
\label{eq:A1_full_pauli}
\end{equation}

\section{Branch-B shell-adapted normal form}

The exact Branch-B reduced symbol has the shell-adapted form
\begin{equation}
A_1(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\widetilde\Lambda_E\bigl(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2\bigr)
+
\widetilde\Lambda_O\bigl(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2\bigr),
\label{eq:A1_BranchB_normal}
\end{equation}
up to the removable scalar drift term \(p_\mu m_0^\mu\mathbf1_2\).

Comparing \eqref{eq:A1_full_pauli} with \eqref{eq:A1_BranchB_normal}, one obtains the shell-adapted coefficient identities
\begin{equation}
m_3^\parallel=\lambda_\parallel,
\qquad
m_3^{1}=m_3^{2}=0,
\label{eq:m3_ids}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\begin{pmatrix}
m_1^{1} & m_1^{2}\\
m_2^{1} & m_2^{2}
\end{pmatrix}
=
\begin{pmatrix}
\widetilde\Lambda_E & -\widetilde\Lambda_O\\
\widetilde\Lambda_O & \widetilde\Lambda_E
\end{pmatrix}.
\label{eq:transverse_matrix}
\end{equation}

Thus the transverse part is exactly a \(2\times2\) matrix of the form
\[
\widetilde\Lambda_E\,\mathbf1_2+\widetilde\Lambda_O\,J,
\qquad
J=
\begin{pmatrix}
0 & -1\\
1 & 0
\end{pmatrix},
\]
which is the standard \(E/O\) decomposition.

\section{Direct extraction formulas}

The three reduced carrier coefficients are therefore read directly from \(M^\mu\) as
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac12\operatorname{Tr}(\sigma_3 M^\parallel),
}
\label{eq:lambda_from_M}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widetilde\Lambda_E
=
\frac12\operatorname{Tr}(\sigma_1 M^{1})
=
\frac12\operatorname{Tr}(\sigma_2 M^{2}),
}
\label{eq:LambdaE_from_M}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widetilde\Lambda_O
=
\frac12\operatorname{Tr}(\sigma_2 M^{1})
=
-\frac12\operatorname{Tr}(\sigma_1 M^{2}).
}
\label{eq:LambdaO_from_M}
\end{equation}

Consistency of the Branch-B form further requires
\begin{equation}
\operatorname{Tr}(\sigma_1 M^1)=\operatorname{Tr}(\sigma_2 M^2),
\qquad
\operatorname{Tr}(\sigma_2 M^1)=-\operatorname{Tr}(\sigma_1 M^2),
\label{eq:consistency_relations}
\end{equation}
and the absence of forbidden extra components means
\begin{equation}
\operatorname{Tr}(\sigma_3 M^1)=\operatorname{Tr}(\sigma_3 M^2)=0.
\label{eq:no_extra_sigma3}
\end{equation}

\section{Definition of the normalization overlaps}

Now let the microscopic carrier split into the three relevant pieces
\begin{equation}
V^\mu
=
V^\mu_{(\parallel)}
+
V^\mu_{(E)}
+
V^\mu_{(O)}
+\cdots,
\label{eq:Vmu_split}
\end{equation}
where the ellipsis denotes shell-irrelevant or higher-order terms.

Define the three projected matrix elements
\begin{equation}
M^\mu_{(\parallel)}:=\langle u^+,V^\mu_{(\parallel)}u^-\rangle,
\quad
M^\mu_{(E)}:=\langle u^+,V^\mu_{(E)}u^-\rangle,
\quad
M^\mu_{(O)}:=\langle u^+,V^\mu_{(O)}u^-\rangle.
\label{eq:Mmu_split}
\end{equation}

The shell normalization overlaps are then defined by the Pauli traces
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_\parallel
:=
\frac{2}{I_3}
\left(
-\frac{M_X^2}{\alpha_X\beta_X}
\right)
\frac12\operatorname{Tr}\bigl(\sigma_3 M^\parallel\bigr),
}
\label{eq:Cpar_def}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_E
:=
\frac{1}{J_1}
\left(
-\frac{M_X^2}{\beta_X\gamma_E}
\right)
\frac12\operatorname{Tr}\bigl(\sigma_1 M^{1}\bigr),
}
\label{eq:CE_def}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_O
:=
\frac{1}{J_1}
\left(
-\frac{M_X^2}{\beta_X\gamma_O}
\right)
\frac12\operatorname{Tr}\bigl(\sigma_2 M^{1}\bigr).
}
\label{eq:CO_def}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, using the transverse consistency relations,
\begin{equation}
C_E
=
\frac{1}{J_1}
\left(
-\frac{M_X^2}{\beta_X\gamma_E}
\right)
\frac12\operatorname{Tr}\bigl(\sigma_2 M^{2}\bigr),
\label{eq:CE_alt}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
C_O
=
-\frac{1}{J_1}
\left(
-\frac{M_X^2}{\beta_X\gamma_O}
\right)
\frac12\operatorname{Tr}\bigl(\sigma_1 M^{2}\bigr).
\label{eq:CO_alt}
\end{equation}

These are the exact matrix-element definitions of the three microscopic carrier overlaps.

\section{Equivalence with the one-mediator coefficients}

In the one-mediator Branch-B truncation, the shell-projected coefficients were
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{2M_X^2}\,C_\parallel\,I_3,
\qquad
\widetilde\Lambda_E
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_E}{M_X^2}\,C_E\,J_1,
\qquad
\widetilde\Lambda_O
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}\,C_O\,J_1.
\label{eq:lambdaEObasic}
\end{equation}

Substituting \eqref{eq:lambda_from_M}--\eqref{eq:LambdaO_from_M} into \eqref{eq:lambdaEObasic} gives the exact identification
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\frac12\operatorname{Tr}(\sigma_3 M^\parallel)
=
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{2M_X^2}\,C_\parallel I_3,
}
\label{eq:Mpar_match}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\frac12\operatorname{Tr}(\sigma_1 M^1)
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_E}{M_X^2}\,C_E J_1,
}
\label{eq:ME_match}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\frac12\operatorname{Tr}(\sigma_2 M^1)
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}\,C_O J_1.
}
\label{eq:MO_match}
\end{equation}

Thus the entire carrier audit is reduced to three trace evaluations of projected shell matrices.

\section{Canonical normalization and orthonormal shell basis}

If the shell bases \(\{u_a^\pm\}\) are chosen so that the three seed operators have unit Pauli projection, then one may impose canonical normalization
\begin{equation}
C_\parallel=C_E=C_O=1.
\label{eq:canonical_norm_again}
\end{equation}

In this convention, the matrix-element audit simplifies to
\begin{equation}
\frac12\operatorname{Tr}(\sigma_3 M^\parallel)
=
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{2M_X^2}I_3,
\label{eq:Mpar_canonical}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\frac12\operatorname{Tr}(\sigma_1 M^1)
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_E}{M_X^2}J_1,
\label{eq:ME_canonical}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\frac12\operatorname{Tr}(\sigma_2 M^1)
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}J_1.
\label{eq:MO_canonical}
\end{equation}

Hence the reduced symbol is completely calibrated once the shell basis is orthonormalized.

\section{Executable audit table}

The actual microscopic computation can therefore be organized as the following table:

\begin{center}
\begin{tabular}{c|c|c|c}
channel & projected matrix & Pauli trace & extracted coefficient \\
\hline
longitudinal & \(M^\parallel\) & \(\frac12\operatorname{Tr}(\sigma_3 M^\parallel)\) & \(\lambda_\parallel\) \\
transverse \(E\) & \(M^1,M^2\) & \(\frac12\operatorname{Tr}(\sigma_1 M^1)=\frac12\operatorname{Tr}(\sigma_2 M^2)\) & \(\widetilde\Lambda_E\) \\
transverse \(O\) & \(M^1,M^2\) & \(\frac12\operatorname{Tr}(\sigma_2 M^1)=-\frac12\operatorname{Tr}(\sigma_1 M^2)\) & \(\widetilde\Lambda_O\)
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

Equivalently, one reads
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0
\iff
\operatorname{Tr}(\sigma_3 M^\parallel)\neq 0,
\label{eq:long_yesno}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
(\widetilde\Lambda_E,\widetilde\Lambda_O)\neq (0,0)
\iff
\left(
\operatorname{Tr}(\sigma_1 M^1),\,
\operatorname{Tr}(\sigma_2 M^1)
\right)\neq (0,0).
\label{eq:trans_yesno}
\end{equation}

\section{Exact nondegeneracy in matrix form}

The exact reduced Weyl nondegeneracy criterion becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\operatorname{Tr}(\sigma_3 M^\parallel)\neq 0,
\qquad
\left(
\operatorname{Tr}(\sigma_1 M^1),\,
\operatorname{Tr}(\sigma_2 M^1)
\right)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:matrix_nondeg}
\end{equation}

So the final full microscopic carrier problem is not conceptual:
it is the explicit evaluation of these traces in the projected Bloch linearization.

\section{What is closed and what remains open}

What is now closed is the exact matrix-element dictionary:
the three shell normalization overlaps \(C_\parallel,C_E,C_O\) are completely equivalent to three Pauli traces of the projected \(2\times2\) shell matrices.

What remains open is only the actual microscopic numerical/symbolic evaluation of
\[
M^\parallel,\qquad M^1,\qquad M^2
\]
for the final complete refined locked TECT Bloch operator.

\section{Final Summary}

The microscopic carrier calibration problem has now been reduced to an explicit \(2\times2\) shell matrix audit.

For the projected shell matrices
\[
(M^\mu)_{ab}=\langle u_a^+,V^\mu u_b^- \rangle,
\]
the first-order symbol is
\[
A_1(p)=p_\mu M^\mu.
\]

Each \(M^\mu\) admits the unique Pauli decomposition
\[
M^\mu
=
m_0^\mu \mathbf1_2
+
m_1^\mu \sigma_1
+
m_2^\mu \sigma_2
+
m_3^\mu \sigma_3.
\]

Comparing with the exact Branch-B normal form
\[
A_1(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\widetilde\Lambda_E(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\widetilde\Lambda_O(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2),
\]
gives the direct extraction formulas
\[
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac12\operatorname{Tr}(\sigma_3 M^\parallel),
\qquad
\widetilde\Lambda_E
=
\frac12\operatorname{Tr}(\sigma_1 M^1),
\qquad
\widetilde\Lambda_O
=
\frac12\operatorname{Tr}(\sigma_2 M^1).
\]

Equivalently, the shell normalization overlaps are exactly the corresponding rescaled Pauli traces:
\[
C_\parallel
\leftrightarrow
\operatorname{Tr}(\sigma_3 M^\parallel),
\qquad
C_E
\leftrightarrow
\operatorname{Tr}(\sigma_1 M^1),
\qquad
C_O
\leftrightarrow
\operatorname{Tr}(\sigma_2 M^1).
\]

Therefore the exact Weyl nondegeneracy criterion is
\[
\operatorname{Tr}(\sigma_3 M^\parallel)\neq 0,
\qquad
\left(
\operatorname{Tr}(\sigma_1 M^1),
\operatorname{Tr}(\sigma_2 M^1)
\right)\neq (0,0).
\]

Thus the final microscopic carrier problem is reduced completely to three explicit trace evaluations of the projected Bloch shell matrices.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Operator-Level Audit of the Actual Microscopic Carrier}

\section{Goal}

The remaining microscopic task is to compute the projected shell matrices
\[
(M^\mu)_{ab}
=
\langle \Psi_a^+,\,V^\mu\,\Psi_b^- \rangle,
\qquad
a,b=1,2,
\]
for the three relevant first-order carrier operators
\[
V^\mu_{(\parallel)},\qquad
V^\mu_{(E)},\qquad
V^\mu_{(O)}.
\]

The purpose of this section is to show that, once the shell-projected operator ansatz is fixed,
the reduced coefficients
\[
\lambda_\parallel,\qquad
\widetilde\Lambda_E,\qquad
\widetilde\Lambda_O
\]
follow by direct trace evaluation.

\section{Low-mode shell basis}

Fix the selected opposite shell pair \(\pm G_*\), with
\[
\hat n:=\frac{G_*}{|G_*|},
\qquad
\{e_1,e_2,\hat n\}\ \text{orthonormal}.
\]

Let the shell-localized low modes be
\begin{equation}
\Psi_a^\pm(\xi,y)
=
f_\pm(\xi)\,e^{\pm i G_*\cdot y}\,u_a^\pm(\xi),
\qquad
a=1,2,
\label{eq:lowmode_basis}
\end{equation}
where:

\begin{enumerate}
\item \(\xi\) is the defect-normal coordinate,
\item \(y\) denotes the slow coordinates tangent to the shell frame,
\item \(f_\pm(\xi)\) are the two valley envelope profiles,
\item \(u_a^\pm(\xi)\) are orthonormal tangent-doublet basis vectors.
\end{enumerate}

We assume the opposite-valley basis has already been matched so that the tangent Pauli basis is the same on both sides.

Define the overlap weight
\begin{equation}
w(\xi):=f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi).
\label{eq:w_def}
\end{equation}

The two basic overlap integrals are
\begin{equation}
I_3:=\int d\xi\, w(\xi)\,\theta'(\xi)^3,
\qquad
J_1:=\int d\xi\, w(\xi)\,\theta'(\xi)\cos\theta(\xi).
\label{eq:I3J1_again}
\end{equation}

\section{Projected operator ansatz}

After integrating out the mediator \(X_i^a\), the relevant effective first-order operator is
\begin{equation}
V^\mu_{\mathrm{eff}}
=
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,V^\mu_{JK}
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_E}{M_X^2}\,V^\mu_{KE}
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}\,V^\mu_{KO}.
\label{eq:Veff_split}
\end{equation}

At the shell-reduced level, we only need the projections of these three pieces onto the tangent-doublet sector.
The exact Branch-B ansatz is

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Pi_D V^\mu_{JK}\Pi_D
=
\frac{C_\parallel}{2}\,\theta'(\xi)^3\,\hat n^\mu\,\sigma_3,
}
\label{eq:VJK_proj}
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Pi_D V^\mu_{KE}\Pi_D
=
C_E\,\theta'(\xi)\cos\theta(\xi)\,
\bigl(e_1^\mu\sigma_1+e_2^\mu\sigma_2\bigr),
}
\label{eq:VKE_proj}
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Pi_D V^\mu_{KO}\Pi_D
=
C_O\,\theta'(\xi)\cos\theta(\xi)\,
\bigl(-e_2^\mu\sigma_1+e_1^\mu\sigma_2\bigr).
}
\label{eq:VKO_proj}
\end{equation}

Here \(C_\parallel,C_E,C_O\) are the purely local shell/tangent normalization overlaps.
They encode the actual microscopic Bloch-frame calibration.

\section{Direct computation of the projected shell matrices}

Insert \eqref{eq:VJK_proj}--\eqref{eq:VKO_proj} into \eqref{eq:Veff_split}, and evaluate on the low-mode basis \eqref{eq:lowmode_basis}.

Because the oscillatory shell phases are already matched between opposite valleys, the projected matrix element reduces to the \(\xi\)-integral:
\begin{equation}
M^\mu
=
\int d\xi\, w(\xi)\,
\Big[
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,\Pi_D V^\mu_{JK}\Pi_D
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_E}{M_X^2}\,\Pi_D V^\mu_{KE}\Pi_D
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}\,\Pi_D V^\mu_{KO}\Pi_D
\Big].
\label{eq:Mmu_integral}
\end{equation}

Using \eqref{eq:I3J1_again}, one obtains

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
M^\mu_{(\parallel)}
=
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{2M_X^2}\,C_\parallel\,I_3\,\hat n^\mu\,\sigma_3,
}
\label{eq:Mpar_final}
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
M^\mu_{(E)}
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_E}{M_X^2}\,C_E\,J_1\,
\bigl(e_1^\mu\sigma_1+e_2^\mu\sigma_2\bigr),
}
\label{eq:ME_final}
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
M^\mu_{(O)}
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}\,C_O\,J_1\,
\bigl(-e_2^\mu\sigma_1+e_1^\mu\sigma_2\bigr).
}
\label{eq:MO_final}
\end{equation}

Therefore the total shell matrix is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
M^\mu
=
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{2M_X^2}C_\parallel I_3\,\hat n^\mu\sigma_3
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_E}{M_X^2}C_E J_1\,(e_1^\mu\sigma_1+e_2^\mu\sigma_2)
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}C_O J_1\,(-e_2^\mu\sigma_1+e_1^\mu\sigma_2).
}
\label{eq:Mmu_total}
\end{equation}

\section{Component form}

Project \(M^\mu\) onto the shell frame directions \(\hat n,e_1,e_2\):
\begin{equation}
M^\parallel:=\hat n_\mu M^\mu,
\qquad
M^1:=e_{1\mu}M^\mu,
\qquad
M^2:=e_{2\mu}M^\mu.
\label{eq:Mcomponents}
\end{equation}

From \eqref{eq:Mmu_total} we get

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
M^\parallel
=
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{2M_X^2}\,C_\parallel I_3\,\sigma_3,
}
\label{eq:Mparallel_component}
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
M^1
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_E}{M_X^2}\,C_E J_1\,\sigma_1
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}\,C_O J_1\,\sigma_2,
}
\label{eq:M1_component}
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
M^2
=
+\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}\,C_O J_1\,\sigma_1
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_E}{M_X^2}\,C_E J_1\,\sigma_2.
}
\label{eq:M2_component}
\end{equation}

This is the exact \(2\times 2\) shell block required for the Branch-B carrier audit.

\section{Reading off the reduced symbol}

The first-order shell symbol is
\begin{equation}
A_1(p)=p_\mu M^\mu=p_\parallel M^\parallel+p_1M^1+p_2M^2.
\label{eq:A1_from_components}
\end{equation}

Substituting \eqref{eq:Mparallel_component}--\eqref{eq:M2_component},
\begin{align}
A_1(p)
&=
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{2M_X^2}C_\parallel I_3\,p_\parallel\sigma_3
\\
&\quad
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_E}{M_X^2}C_EJ_1\,(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
\\
&\quad
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}C_OJ_1\,(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2).
\label{eq:A1_expanded_final}
\end{align}

Hence the exact reduced coefficients are

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{2M_X^2}\,C_\parallel I_3,
}
\label{eq:lambda_final_again}
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widetilde\Lambda_E
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_E}{M_X^2}\,C_E J_1,
}
\label{eq:LE_final_again}
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widetilde\Lambda_O
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}\,C_O J_1.
}
\label{eq:LO_final_again}
\end{equation}

So the operator-level audit reproduces exactly the expected Branch-B shell symbol.

\section{Trace test}

Now compute the Pauli traces directly.

From \eqref{eq:Mparallel_component}--\eqref{eq:M2_component},
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\frac12\operatorname{Tr}(\sigma_3 M^\parallel)
=
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{2M_X^2}\,C_\parallel I_3
=
\lambda_\parallel,
}
\label{eq:trace_parallel}
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\frac12\operatorname{Tr}(\sigma_1 M^1)
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_E}{M_X^2}\,C_E J_1
=
\widetilde\Lambda_E,
}
\label{eq:trace_E}
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\frac12\operatorname{Tr}(\sigma_2 M^1)
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}\,C_O J_1
=
\widetilde\Lambda_O.
}
\label{eq:trace_O}
\end{equation}

Consistency also gives
\begin{equation}
\frac12\operatorname{Tr}(\sigma_2 M^2)=\widetilde\Lambda_E,
\qquad
-\frac12\operatorname{Tr}(\sigma_1 M^2)=\widetilde\Lambda_O.
\label{eq:trace_consistency}
\end{equation}

Thus the full carrier audit reduces to three explicit trace evaluations.

\section{Exact nondegeneracy criterion in operator form}

The reduced Weyl symbol is nondegenerate if and only if
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\frac12\operatorname{Tr}(\sigma_3 M^\parallel)\neq 0,
\qquad
\left(
\frac12\operatorname{Tr}(\sigma_1 M^1),\,
\frac12\operatorname{Tr}(\sigma_2 M^1)
\right)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:operator_nondeg}
\end{equation}

Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha_X\beta_X\,C_\parallel I_3\neq 0,
\qquad
\beta_X J_1\,(\gamma_E C_E,\gamma_O C_O)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:operator_nondeg_coeff}
\end{equation}

Assuming
\[
I_3\neq 0,\qquad J_1\neq 0,\qquad \beta_X\neq 0,
\]
this becomes simply
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha_X C_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(\gamma_E C_E,\gamma_O C_O)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:operator_nondeg_simple}
\end{equation}

\section{Canonical normalization}

If the shell tangent basis is orthonormalized so that
\begin{equation}
C_\parallel=C_E=C_O=1,
\label{eq:canonical_C}
\end{equation}
then
\begin{equation}
M^\parallel
=
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{2M_X^2}I_3\,\sigma_3,
\qquad
M^1
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_E}{M_X^2}J_1\,\sigma_1
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}J_1\,\sigma_2,
\label{eq:M_canonical_1}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
M^2
=
+\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}J_1\,\sigma_1
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_E}{M_X^2}J_1\,\sigma_2.
\label{eq:M_canonical_2}
\end{equation}

Therefore
\begin{equation}
A_1(p)
=
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{2M_X^2}I_3\,p_\parallel\sigma_3
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_E}{M_X^2}J_1\,(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}J_1\,(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2).
\label{eq:A1_canonical_final}
\end{equation}

This is the explicit canonical Branch-B shell block.

\section{Anisotropy ratio}

Identifying
\[
v_\parallel=\lambda_\parallel,
\qquad
v_E=\widetilde\Lambda_E,
\qquad
v_O=\widetilde\Lambda_O,
\]
gives
\begin{equation}
v_\perp
=
\sqrt{v_E^2+v_O^2}
=
\frac{|\beta_X|\,|J_1|}{M_X^2}
\sqrt{\gamma_E^2C_E^2+\gamma_O^2C_O^2}.
\label{eq:vperp_operator}
\end{equation}

Hence
\begin{equation}
\rho
=
\frac{v_\parallel}{v_\perp}
=
-\frac{\alpha_X C_\parallel}{2\sqrt{\gamma_E^2C_E^2+\gamma_O^2C_O^2}}
\frac{I_3}{J_1}.
\label{eq:rho_operator}
\end{equation}

In the small-defect regime,
\[
I_3\sim \frac{3}{16}(\theta_0\kappa)^2 J_1,
\]
so
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\rho_{\mathrm{LO}}
=
-\frac{3}{32}
\frac{\alpha_X C_\parallel}{\sqrt{\gamma_E^2C_E^2+\gamma_O^2C_O^2}}
(\theta_0\kappa)^2.
}
\label{eq:rho_operator_LO}
\end{equation}

\section{What is now fully closed}

The operator-level carrier audit is now algebraically closed:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the projected operator ansatz \eqref{eq:VJK_proj}--\eqref{eq:VKO_proj} fixes the shell block;
\item the low-mode projection gives the explicit \(2\times2\) matrices \(M^\parallel,M^1,M^2\);
\item the Pauli traces directly reproduce
\[
\lambda_\parallel,\qquad \widetilde\Lambda_E,\qquad \widetilde\Lambda_O;
\]
\item the exact Branch-B nondegeneracy criterion becomes the explicit trace test \eqref{eq:operator_nondeg};
\item the anisotropy ratio follows immediately.
\end{enumerate}

\section{What is still not unconditional}

What remains not yet unconditional is not the operator algebra.

The only remaining issue is the final microscopic calibration:
compute the actual projected Bloch-frame overlaps and determine the numerical values of
\[
C_\parallel,\qquad C_E,\qquad C_O
\]
for the complete refined locked TECT linearization.

Thus the remaining frontier is a final microscopic Bloch calibration problem, not a conceptual obstruction.

\section{Final Summary}

The operator-level microscopic carrier audit is now algebraically closed.

For the low-mode shell basis
\[
\Psi_a^\pm(\xi,y)=f_\pm(\xi)e^{\pm iG_*\cdot y}u_a^\pm(\xi),
\]
the projected effective carrier operator produces the explicit shell matrices
\[
M^\parallel
=
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{2M_X^2}C_\parallel I_3\,\sigma_3,
\]
\[
M^1
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_E}{M_X^2}C_EJ_1\,\sigma_1
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}C_OJ_1\,\sigma_2,
\]
\[
M^2
=
+\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}C_OJ_1\,\sigma_1
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_E}{M_X^2}C_EJ_1\,\sigma_2.
\]

Therefore the reduced Branch-B first-order symbol is
\[
A_1(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel\sigma_3
+
\widetilde\Lambda_E(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\widetilde\Lambda_O(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2),
\]
with
\[
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{2M_X^2}C_\parallel I_3,
\qquad
\widetilde\Lambda_E
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_E}{M_X^2}C_EJ_1,
\qquad
\widetilde\Lambda_O
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}C_OJ_1.
\]

Equivalently, the coefficients are extracted by the direct Pauli traces
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\frac12\operatorname{Tr}(\sigma_3M^\parallel),
\qquad
\widetilde\Lambda_E=\frac12\operatorname{Tr}(\sigma_1M^1),
\qquad
\widetilde\Lambda_O=\frac12\operatorname{Tr}(\sigma_2M^1).
\]

Hence the exact nondegeneracy criterion is
\[
\frac12\operatorname{Tr}(\sigma_3M^\parallel)\neq 0,
\qquad
\left(
\frac12\operatorname{Tr}(\sigma_1M^1),
\frac12\operatorname{Tr}(\sigma_2M^1)
\right)\neq (0,0).
\]

Thus the final remaining frontier is not conceptual.
It is the explicit Bloch-frame calibration of the three microscopic overlaps
\[
C_\parallel,\qquad C_E,\qquad C_O.
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Final Bloch Calibration Audit}

\section{Goal}

The remaining frontier is the explicit microscopic calibration of the three shell overlaps
\[
C_\parallel,\qquad C_E,\qquad C_O
\]
for the complete refined locked Bloch linearization.

At this stage, the problem is no longer conceptual.
The reduced Branch-B symbol is already known to take the form
\[
A_1(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\widetilde\Lambda_E(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\widetilde\Lambda_O(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2),
\]
and the only remaining task is to determine the three calibration overlaps from the actual projected Bloch operator.

\section{Complete projected Bloch operator}

Let the complete refined locked microscopic linearization around the chosen defect/BCC background be
\begin{equation}
\mathcal L_{\mathrm{mic}}(p).
\label{eq:Lmic}
\end{equation}

Fix the selected opposite shell pair \(\pm G_*\), and let
\[
\Pi_D
\]
be the projector onto the shell-relevant doubled local block
\[
\mathcal H_D \cong \mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{valley}}\otimes\mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{int}}.
\]

Then the first-order shell operator is defined by
\begin{equation}
\mathcal L_D^{(1)}(p)
:=
\Pi_D \mathcal L_{\mathrm{mic}}(p)\Pi_D\Big|_{\mathrm{linear\ in}\ p}.
\label{eq:LD1}
\end{equation}

The Bloch calibration problem is to compare \(\mathcal L_D^{(1)}(p)\) with the canonical Branch-B basis.

\section{Normalized low-mode basis}

Choose orthonormal low-mode states
\begin{equation}
\Psi_a^\pm(\xi,y)
=
f_\pm(\xi)\,e^{\pm iG_*\cdot y}\,u_a^\pm(\xi),
\qquad
a=1,2,
\label{eq:Psiabasis}
\end{equation}
with normalization
\begin{equation}
\langle \Psi_a^\pm,\Psi_b^\pm\rangle=\delta_{ab},
\qquad
\langle \Psi_a^+,\Psi_b^-\rangle=0.
\label{eq:basis_norm}
\end{equation}

Assume the opposite-valley tangent frames have been matched so that the same Pauli basis
\[
\sigma_1,\sigma_2,\sigma_3
\]
acts on both local doublets.

Define the defect-profile overlaps
\begin{equation}
I_3=\int d\xi\,w(\xi)\,\theta'(\xi)^3,
\qquad
J_1=\int d\xi\,w(\xi)\,\theta'(\xi)\cos\theta(\xi),
\qquad
w(\xi):=f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi).
\label{eq:I3J1final}
\end{equation}

\section{Canonical seed operators}

Define the three canonical normalized seed operators by
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
S^\mu_\parallel
:=
\frac{1}{2I_3}\,\theta'(\xi)^3\,\hat n^\mu\,\sigma_3,
}
\label{eq:Spar}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
S^\mu_E
:=
\frac{1}{J_1}\,\theta'(\xi)\cos\theta(\xi)\,
\bigl(e_1^\mu\sigma_1+e_2^\mu\sigma_2\bigr),
}
\label{eq:SE}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
S^\mu_O
:=
\frac{1}{J_1}\,\theta'(\xi)\cos\theta(\xi)\,
\bigl(-e_2^\mu\sigma_1+e_1^\mu\sigma_2\bigr).
}
\label{eq:SO}
\end{equation}

These are normalized so that their reduced shell projections directly reproduce the canonical Pauli structures.

\section{Definition of the calibration overlaps}

Let the actual shell-projected microscopic carrier pieces be
\[
\Pi_DV^\mu_{JK}\Pi_D,\qquad
\Pi_DV^\mu_{KE}\Pi_D,\qquad
\Pi_DV^\mu_{KO}\Pi_D.
\]

The calibration overlaps are defined by their projections onto the normalized seed operators:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_\parallel
:=
\frac{
\langle \Psi^+,\,\Pi_DV^\mu_{JK}\Pi_D\,\Psi^- \rangle
}{
\langle \Psi^+,\,S^\mu_\parallel\,\Psi^- \rangle
},
}
\label{eq:Cpar_ratio}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_E
:=
\frac{
\langle \Psi^+,\,\Pi_DV^\mu_{KE}\Pi_D\,\Psi^- \rangle
}{
\langle \Psi^+,\,S^\mu_E\,\Psi^- \rangle
},
}
\label{eq:CE_ratio}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_O
:=
\frac{
\langle \Psi^+,\,\Pi_DV^\mu_{KO}\Pi_D\,\Psi^- \rangle
}{
\langle \Psi^+,\,S^\mu_O\,\Psi^- \rangle
}.
}
\label{eq:CO_ratio}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, at the \(2\times2\) shell matrix level,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_\parallel
=
\frac{
\frac12\operatorname{Tr}(\sigma_3 M^\parallel_{JK})
}{
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{2M_X^2}I_3
},
}
\label{eq:Cpar_trace_ratio}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_E
=
\frac{
\frac12\operatorname{Tr}(\sigma_1 M^1_{KE})
}{
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_E}{M_X^2}J_1
},
}
\label{eq:CE_trace_ratio}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_O
=
\frac{
\frac12\operatorname{Tr}(\sigma_2 M^1_{KO})
}{
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}J_1
}.
}
\label{eq:CO_trace_ratio}
\end{equation}

These formulas are the exact Bloch-frame calibration definitions.

\section{Projector-level yes/no test}

The carrier audit now reduces to the following three projector tests:

\paragraph{Longitudinal test.}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_\parallel\neq 0
\iff
\Pi_DV^\mu_{JK}\Pi_D
\text{ has nonzero projection onto }
S^\mu_\parallel.
}
\label{eq:long_test}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Transverse \(E\) test.}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_E\neq 0
\iff
\Pi_DV^\mu_{KE}\Pi_D
\text{ has nonzero projection onto }
S^\mu_E.
}
\label{eq:E_test}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Transverse \(O\) test.}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_O\neq 0
\iff
\Pi_DV^\mu_{KO}\Pi_D
\text{ has nonzero projection onto }
S^\mu_O.
}
\label{eq:O_test}
\end{equation}

Thus the final exact nondegeneracy criterion is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(C_E,C_O)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:C_nondeg}
\end{equation}

\section{Equivalent basis-overlap formulation}

Let
\[
\{E_A\}_{A=1}^d
\]
be any basis of the shell-relevant microscopic transport space.
Write the invariant shell decomposition
\begin{equation}
E_A^{\mathrm{inv}}
=
a_A B_\parallel+b_A B_E+c_A B_O.

Then
\[

and

(C_E,C_O)\neq(0,0)
\iff
\exists B:\ (b_B,c_B)\neq(0,0).
\]

Hence the final Bloch calibration audit is exactly equivalent to the earlier basis-audit theorem.

\section{Canonical normalization}

If the low-mode basis and seed operators are chosen so that the canonical seed projections have unit overlap, then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_\parallel=C_E=C_O=1.
}
\label{eq:canonical_all1}
\end{equation}

In this normalization,
\begin{equation}

=

\label{eq:Mpar_can}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}

=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_E}{M_X^2}J_1\,\sigma_1
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}J_1\,\sigma_2,
\label{eq:M1_can}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
M^2
=
+\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}J_1\,\sigma_1
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_E}{M_X^2}J_1\,\sigma_2.
\label{eq:M2_can}
\end{equation}

Thus the reduced coefficients are directly
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{2M_X^2}I_3,
\qquad
\widetilde\Lambda_E
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_E}{M_X^2}J_1,
\qquad
\widetilde\Lambda_O
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}J_1.
\label{eq:canonical_coeffs_final}
\end{equation}

The complete executable Bloch calibration audit is:

C_\parallel\neq 0,\qquad (C_E,C_O)\neq(0,0).
