\section{Folded-Bragg Bloch-Fiber Construction in the Locked 12-Mode BCC Branch}

\section{Working convention}

From this point onward, we use the folded Bragg convention
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
k_*=\frac{G_*}{2},
\qquad
k=k_*+p,
\qquad
|p|\ll |G_*|.
}
\label{eq:folded_bragg_conv}
\end{equation}
This is the correct finite-dimensional Bloch-fiber convention for the shell-pair calculation.

We work in the strongest currently explicit microscopic branch
\begin{equation}
L_{\mathrm{mic}}
=
L_{\Psi}^{\mathrm{ref}}[\Psi,P]
+
\frac{M_X^2}{2}X_i^aX_i^a
+
\alpha_X X_i^aJ_i^a[\Psi]
+
\beta_X X_i^aK_i^a[P,\psi].
\label{eq:working_branch_folded}
\end{equation}

\section{Locked 12-mode BCC background}

Let the first BCC reciprocal shell be
\begin{equation}
\mathcal S_{12}
=
\frac{q_*}{\sqrt2}
\left\{
(\pm1,\pm1,0),\,
(\pm1,0,\pm1),\,
(0,\pm1,\pm1)
\right\},
\qquad
|\mathcal S_{12}|=12.
\label{eq:S12_folded}
\end{equation}
The locked equal-amplitude background is
\begin{equation}
\phi_0(x)=A\sum_{Q\in\mathcal S_{12}}e^{iQ\cdot x}
=
2A\sum_{\alpha=1}^6 \cos(Q_\alpha\cdot x),
\label{eq:phi0_12mode_folded}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\Psi_0(x)=z_0\,\phi_0(x),
\qquad
P_0=z_0z_0^\dagger.
\label{eq:Psi0_locked_folded}
\end{equation}

Choose an internal basis
\begin{equation}
u_0=z_0,
\qquad
u_1,u_2\in Q_{z_0},
\qquad
u_r^\dagger u_s=\delta_{rs},
\label{eq:internal_basis_folded}
\end{equation}
so that
\[
\mathbb C^3=\mathbb C z_0\oplus Q_{z_0}.
\]

\section{Bloch fiber and shell-pair basis}

Because the linearized operator around \(\Psi_0\) is periodic, it admits Bloch decomposition.
At the folded Bragg point \(k_*=G_*/2\), the two shell-harmonic states
\[
e^{+iG_*\cdot x/2},
\qquad
e^{-iG_*\cdot x/2}
\]
are degenerate modulo reciprocal-lattice folding.

We therefore define the shell-pair basis
\begin{equation}
\Phi_{+,a}(x)=e^{+iG_*\cdot x/2}\,u_a,
\qquad
\Phi_{-,a}(x)=e^{-iG_*\cdot x/2}\,u_a,
\qquad
a=1,2,
\label{eq:shell_pair_basis}
\end{equation}
which spans the \(4\)-dimensional shell-relevant doubled block
\[
\mathcal H_*=
\mathrm{span}\{\Phi_{+,1},\Phi_{+,2},\Phi_{-,1},\Phi_{-,2}\}
\cong
\mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{valley}}\otimes \mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{int}}.
\]

Let \(P_*\) denote the orthogonal projector onto \(\mathcal H_*\).

\section{Bloch fiber matrix and primitive-cell Fourier coefficients}

Let \(L_{\mathrm{act}}(k)\) be the Bloch fiber of the microscopic linearized operator.
Because the coefficients are periodic, the matrix elements between shell-pair basis vectors are governed by primitive-cell Fourier coefficients.

For any periodic scalar coefficient \(U(x)\),
\begin{equation}
\langle \Phi_{+,a},\,U(x)\,\Phi_{-,b}\rangle
=
\widehat U(G_*)\,\delta_{ab},
\label{eq:scalar_bragg_block}
\end{equation}
because
\[
e^{-iG_*\cdot x/2}\,U(x)\,e^{-iG_*\cdot x/2}
\]
selects exactly the \(Q=G_*\) Fourier mode of \(U\).

Hence the constant intervalley Bragg block is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
M_0
=
\widehat U_{\mathrm{eff}}(G_*)\,\mathbf 1_2.
}
\label{eq:M0_folded}
\end{equation}

Likewise, for a traceless enriched coefficient \(\mathcal T^\alpha(x)\otimes s^\alpha\),
\begin{equation}
\langle \Phi_{+,a},\,\mathcal T^\alpha(x)\otimes s^\alpha\,\Phi_{-,b}\rangle
=
\widehat{\mathcal T^\alpha}(G_*)\,(s^\alpha)_{ab}.
\label{eq:Talpha_block}
\end{equation}
Thus the transverse Dirac block is controlled by
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
W^\alpha
=
\widehat T^\alpha_{\mathrm{eff}}(G_*)\,s^\alpha,
\qquad
\alpha=1,2.
}
\label{eq:Walpha_folded}
\end{equation}

Therefore the full shell-pair problem is reduced to Fourier extraction at the selected shell vector \(G_*\). 

\section{First-derivative extraction}

The local Weyl data are determined by the projected first derivatives of the Bloch fiber:
\begin{equation}
K_i:=\partial_{k_i}L_{\mathrm{act}}(k)\Big|_{k=k_*}.
\label{eq:Ki_folded}
\end{equation}
The actual shell-reduced test is therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
P_*K_iP_*
\to
(\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta).
}
\label{eq:PKP_dictionary}
\end{equation}

Choose the adapted shell frame
\[
\hat n=\frac{G_*}{|G_*|},
\qquad
\{e_1,e_2,\hat n\}\ \text{orthonormal},
\]
and write
\[
p=p_\parallel\hat n+p_1e_1+p_2e_2.
\]

Then define
\begin{equation}
K_\parallel:=\hat n_iK_i,
\qquad
K_1:=e_{1i}K_i,
\qquad
K_2:=e_{2i}K_i.
\label{eq:Kframe_folded}
\end{equation}

\section{Projected axial ansatz}

The minimal shell-enriched axial form is
\begin{equation}
K_i
=
A\,\hat n_i\,\tau^3\otimes\mathbf 1_2
+
B\,(e_{1i}\tau^1\otimes s_1+e_{2i}\tau^1\otimes s_2)
+
C\,(-e_{2i}\tau^1\otimes s_1+e_{1i}\tau^1\otimes s_2).
\label{eq:Ki_axial_folded}
\end{equation}

Therefore
\begin{equation}
K_\parallel=A\,\tau^3\otimes\mathbf 1_2,
\label{eq:Kpar_axial_folded}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
K_1=B\,\tau^1\otimes s_1+C\,\tau^1\otimes s_2,
\label{eq:K1_axial_folded}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
K_2=-C\,\tau^1\otimes s_1+B\,\tau^1\otimes s_2.
\label{eq:K2_axial_folded}
\end{equation}

Projecting to the selected positive-valley two-band block \(P_+\subset P_*\),
\[
P_+(\tau^3\otimes\mathbf 1_2)P_+\mapsto \sigma^3,
\qquad
P_+(\tau^1\otimes s_1)P_+\mapsto \sigma^1,
\qquad
P_+(\tau^1\otimes s_2)P_+\mapsto \sigma^2,
\]
we obtain
\begin{equation}
h_+(p)
=
A\,p_\parallel\sigma^3
+
B(p_1\sigma^1+p_2\sigma^2)
+
C(-p_2\sigma^1+p_1\sigma^2)
+
O(|p|^2).
\label{eq:hplus_folded}
\end{equation}

Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=A,
\qquad
\alpha=B,
\qquad
\beta=C.
}
\label{eq:ABC_to_lambda_folded}
\end{equation}
This is exactly the finite extraction dictionary. 

\section{Direct projector-trace formulas}

The three coefficients are extracted directly by projector traces:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac12
\operatorname{Tr}_{\mathcal H_*}
\!\bigl(
\sigma^3\,P_*K_\parallel P_*
\bigr),
}
\label{eq:lambda_trace_folded}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
=
\frac14
\sum_{a=1}^2
\operatorname{Tr}_{\mathcal H_*}
\!\bigl(
\sigma^a\,P_*(e_{ai}K_i)P_*
\bigr),
}
\label{eq:alpha_trace_folded}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta
=
\frac14
\left[
\operatorname{Tr}_{\mathcal H_*}\!\bigl(\sigma^2P_*(e_{1i}K_i)P_*\bigr)
-
\operatorname{Tr}_{\mathcal H_*}\!\bigl(\sigma^1P_*(e_{2i}K_i)P_*\bigr)
\right].
}
\label{eq:beta_trace_folded}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, the Weyl matrix is
\begin{equation}
M=
\begin{pmatrix}
\alpha & -\beta & 0\\
\beta & \alpha & 0\\
0 & 0 & \lambda_\parallel
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
\det M=\lambda_\parallel(\alpha^2+\beta^2).
\label{eq:Weyl_matrix_folded}
\end{equation}
Thus local Weyl nondegeneracy is exactly
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:Weyl_nondeg_folded}
\end{equation}


\section{12-mode BCC shell-sum input}

Inside the locked equal-amplitude 12-mode BCC branch, the selected-shell combinatorics satisfy
\[
N(G_*)=\#\{(Q_1,Q_2)\in S_{\mathrm{BCC}}^2:Q_1+Q_2=G_*\}=4,
\]
so the first-shell convolution is nontrivial. In particular, the 12-mode shell sum already shows that the witness does not disappear upon lifting the single-mode representative to the locked BCC shell sum. :contentReference[oaicite:7]{index=7}

This means the actual remaining bottleneck is no longer “does a shell witness exist at all?” but rather:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{compute the actual }P_*K_iP_*\text{ of the final refined locked Bloch operator.}
}
\label{eq:actual_bottleneck_folded}
\end{equation}

\section{Honest status}

What is now closed:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the correct Bragg convention is fixed:
\[
k_*=\frac{G_*}{2};
\]
\item the shell-relevant Bloch basis is fixed:
\[
\Phi_{\pm,a}(x)=e^{\pm iG_*\cdot x/2}u_a;
\]
\item constant and enriched Bragg blocks are read from the \(Q=G_*\) primitive-cell Fourier coefficients;
\item the local Weyl data are reduced to the finite derivative blocks
\[
P_*K_iP_*;
\]
\item the exact yes/no test is the triple
\[
(\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta)
\]
extracted by \eqref{eq:lambda_trace_folded}--\eqref{eq:beta_trace_folded}.
\end{enumerate}

What is still open:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the explicit symbolic/numerical evaluation of }K_i=\partial_{k_i}L_{\mathrm{act}}(k)|_{k=k_*}
\text{ for the final complete refined locked TECT/Class II operator.}
}
\label{eq:still_open_folded}
\end{equation}
This is now a finite operator-construction problem, not a conceptual one. 

\section{Final Summary}

Using the folded Bragg convention
\[
k_*=\frac{G_*}{2},
\qquad
k=k_*+p,
\]
the locked 12-mode BCC microscopic linearization reduces to a finite shell-pair Bloch problem on
\[
\mathcal H_*=\mathrm{span}\{\Phi_{+,a},\Phi_{-,a}\}_{a=1,2},
\qquad
\Phi_{\pm,a}(x)=e^{\pm iG_*\cdot x/2}u_a.
\]

The constant intervalley Bragg block and the enriched transverse blocks are controlled by the primitive-cell Fourier coefficients at \(Q=G_*\):
\[
M_0=\widehat U_{\mathrm{eff}}(G_*)\mathbf 1_2,
\qquad
W^\alpha=\widehat T^\alpha_{\mathrm{eff}}(G_*)s^\alpha.
\]

The local Weyl data are extracted from the projected first derivatives
\[
K_i=\partial_{k_i}L_{\mathrm{act}}(k)\big|_{k=k_*},
\qquad
P_*K_iP_*.
\]

In the minimal axial shell-adapted ansatz,
\[
K_i
=
A\,\hat n_i\,\tau^3\otimes\mathbf 1_2
+
B\,(e_{1i}\tau^1\otimes s_1+e_{2i}\tau^1\otimes s_2)
+
C\,(-e_{2i}\tau^1\otimes s_1+e_{1i}\tau^1\otimes s_2),
\]
so that
\[
\lambda_\parallel=A,\qquad
\alpha=B,\qquad
\beta=C.
\]

Equivalently,
\[
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac12\operatorname{Tr}_{\mathcal H_*}(\sigma^3P_*K_\parallel P_*),
\]
\[
\alpha
=
\frac14\sum_{a=1}^2
\operatorname{Tr}_{\mathcal H_*}(\sigma^aP_*(e_{ai}K_i)P_*),
\]
\[
\beta
=
\frac14\left[
\operatorname{Tr}_{\mathcal H_*}(\sigma^2P_*(e_{1i}K_i)P_*)
-
\operatorname{Tr}_{\mathcal H_*}(\sigma^1P_*(e_{2i}K_i)P_*)
\right].
\]

Thus the final microscopic Weyl test is
\[
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0).
\]

So the remaining frontier is completely localized:
compute the actual projected derivative blocks \(P_*K_iP_*\) for the final refined locked TECT/Class II Bloch operator.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Explicit Coefficient Bookkeeping for the Folded-Bragg 12-Mode Bloch Audit}

\section{Immediate goal}

The next concrete task is not to introduce a new mechanism, but to write the actual
periodic coefficient extraction formulas for
\[
\widehat U_{\mathrm{eff}}(G_*),\qquad
\widehat T_{\mathrm{eff}}^1(G_*),\qquad
\widehat T_{\mathrm{eff}}^2(G_*),\qquad
v_\parallel.
\]

These are the four microscopic quantities from which the shell data
\[
M_0,\qquad W^1,\qquad W^2,\qquad v_\parallel
\]
are obtained in the folded Bragg convention.

\section{Folded-Bragg shell dictionary}

Work at
\[
k_*= \frac{G_*}{2},\qquad k=k_*+p,\qquad |p|\ll |G_*|.
\]
Then the shell-relevant Bloch basis is
\[
\Phi_{+,a}(x)=e^{+iG_*\cdot x/2}u_a,\qquad
\Phi_{-,a}(x)=e^{-iG_*\cdot x/2}u_a,\qquad a=1,2.
\]

The exact shell quantities are:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
M_0=B^{\mathrm{eff}}(E_*,0),
}
\label{eq:M0_exact_shell}
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
W^i=\partial_{p_i}B^{\mathrm{eff}}(E_*,p)\big|_{p=0},\qquad i=1,2,
}
\label{eq:Wi_exact_shell}
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v_\parallel
=
\frac12
\partial_{p_\parallel}
\operatorname{tr}_{\mathrm{int}}
\frac{E_+^{\mathrm{eff}}(E_*,p)-E_-^{\mathrm{eff}}(E_*,p)}{2}
\Big|_{p=0}.
}
\label{eq:vpar_exact_shell}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, in the primitive-cell Fourier language,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
M_0=\widehat U_{\mathrm{eff}}(G_*)\,\mathbf 1_2,
\qquad
W^\alpha=\widehat T^\alpha_{\mathrm{eff}}(G_*)\,s^\alpha,\quad \alpha=1,2.
}
\label{eq:UThat_dictionary}
\end{equation}

\section{Three-way decomposition of the effective coefficients}

The exact bookkeeping decomposition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat U_{\mathrm{eff}}(G_*)
=
\widehat U_{\mathrm{bare}}(G_*)
+
\widehat U_{(II)}(G_*)
+
\widehat U_{(\mathrm{sp})}(G_*),
}
\label{eq:Ueff_split}
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat T^\alpha_{\mathrm{eff}}(G_*)
=
\widehat T^\alpha_{\mathrm{bare}}(G_*)
+
\widehat T^\alpha_{(II)}(G_*)
+
\widehat T^\alpha_{(\mathrm{sp})}(G_*),
\qquad \alpha=1,2,
}
\label{eq:Teff_split}
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v_\parallel
=
v_\parallel^{\mathrm{bare}}
+
\delta v_\parallel^{(II)}
+
\delta v_\parallel^{(\mathrm{sp})}.
}
\label{eq:vpar_split}
\end{equation}

So the actual full-PDE work is now reduced to computing exactly these four quantities.
This reduction is already fixed in the project notes. 

\section{Bare periodic-core contribution}

Let the \(\Psi\Psi\)-block of the Bloch operator be
\[
H_{\Psi\Psi}(k)=H_0(k)+U^{(\mathrm{per})}+U^{(\mathrm{lock})}.
\]
Its harmonic matrix elements are
\[
\bigl(H_{\Psi\Psi}(k)\bigr)_{(G,r),(G',s)}
=
\delta_{GG'}\delta_{rs}\,h_r(k+G)
+
U^{(\mathrm{per})}_{rs}(G-G')
+
U^{(\mathrm{lock})}_{rs}(G-G').
\]

Then the direct periodic-core Bragg coefficients are:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat U_{\mathrm{bare}}(G_*)
=
\bigl[U^{(\mathrm{per})}(G_*)+U^{(\mathrm{lock})}(G_*)\bigr]_{\mathrm{scalar\ on}\ Q_{z_0}},
}
\label{eq:Ubare_def}
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat T^\alpha_{\mathrm{bare}}(G_*)
=
\bigl[U^{(\mathrm{per})}(G_*)+U^{(\mathrm{lock})}(G_*)\bigr]_{\mathrm{traceless},\,\alpha},
\qquad
\alpha=1,2,
}
\label{eq:Tbare_def}
\end{equation}
where “scalar” means proportional to \(\mathbf 1_2\) on the tangent doublet, and “traceless,\(\alpha\)” means the coefficient of the Pauli matrix \(s^\alpha\).

For the longitudinal slope, the direct periodic-core contribution is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v_\parallel^{\mathrm{bare}}
=
\frac12
\partial_{p_\parallel}
\operatorname{tr}_{\mathrm{int}}
\frac{E_+^{\mathrm{bare}}(p)-E_-^{\mathrm{bare}}(p)}{2}\Big|_{p=0}.
}
\label{eq:vpar_bare_def}
\end{equation}

As already emphasized in the notes, the constant Bragg channel \(M_0\) and the longitudinal slope \(v_\parallel\) can have direct periodic-core contributions. :contentReference[oaicite:4]{index=4}

\section{Class II self-energy contribution}

Let
\[
\mathcal C(k)=\alpha_X\mathcal J(k)+\beta_X\mathcal K(k),
\qquad
H_{XX}(k)=M_X^2\mathbf 1+\Delta^{XX}(k),
\]
and
\[
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k)
=
H_{\Psi\Psi}(k)-\mathcal C(k)H_{XX}(k)^{-1}\mathcal C(k)^\dagger.
\]

At leading heavy-mass order,
\[
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k)
=
H_{\Psi\Psi}(k)-\frac1{M_X^2}\mathcal C(k)\mathcal C(k)^\dagger+O(M_X^{-4}).
\]

Therefore the Class II contributions to the Bragg Fourier coefficients are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat U_{(II)}(G_*)
=
-\frac1{M_X^2}
\widehat{\bigl(\mathcal C\mathcal C^\dagger\bigr)}_{\mathrm{scalar}}(G_*),
}
\label{eq:UII_def}
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat T^\alpha_{(II)}(G_*)
=
-\frac1{M_X^2}
\widehat{\bigl(\mathcal C\mathcal C^\dagger\bigr)}_{\mathrm{traceless},\,\alpha}(G_*),
\qquad
\alpha=1,2.
}
\label{eq:TII_def}
\end{equation}

Likewise the longitudinal derivative correction is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta v_\parallel^{(II)}
=
-\frac1{M_X^2}
\partial_{p_\parallel}
\operatorname{tr}_{\mathrm{int}}
\frac{
\bigl(\mathcal C\mathcal C^\dagger\bigr)_+(p)
-
\bigl(\mathcal C\mathcal C^\dagger\bigr)_-(p)
}{4}
\Big|_{p=0}.
}
\label{eq:vparII_def}
\end{equation}

At the shell-block derivative level this is exactly
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
K_i^{(II)}
=
-\frac1{M_X^2}\Pi_{S_*}
\Big[
(\partial_{k_i}\mathcal C)\mathcal C^\dagger
+
\mathcal C(\partial_{k_i}\mathcal C^\dagger)
\Big]_{k=k_*}
\Pi_{S_*}.
}
\label{eq:KiII_exact}
\end{equation}
This is the correct leading target because the isotropic on-shell first derivative of the bare Brazovskii kernel vanishes at \(q_*\). :contentReference[oaicite:5]{index=5}

\section{One-step spectator-shell correction}

If a single spectator shell is retained and integrated out, the exact renormalized core blocks are
\[
E_\pm^{\mathrm{eff}}(E,p)
=
E_\pm(p)-C_\pm(p)\bigl(H_{ss}(p)-E\bigr)^{-1}C_\pm(p)^\dagger,
\]
\[
B^{\mathrm{eff}}(E,p)
=
B(p)-C_+(p)\bigl(H_{ss}(p)-E\bigr)^{-1}C_-(p)^\dagger.
\]

Hence the spectator contributions are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat U_{(\mathrm{sp})}(G_*)
=
-\widehat{
C_+(0)\,(H_{ss}(0)-E_*)^{-1}\,C_-(0)^\dagger
}_{\mathrm{scalar}}(G_*),
}
\label{eq:Usp_def}
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat T^\alpha_{(\mathrm{sp})}(G_*)
=
-\widehat{
C_+(0)\,(H_{ss}(0)-E_*)^{-1}\,C_-(0)^\dagger
}_{\mathrm{traceless},\,\alpha}(G_*),
\qquad \alpha=1,2,
}
\label{eq:Tsp_def}
\end{equation}

and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta v_\parallel^{(\mathrm{sp})}
=
\frac12
\partial_{p_\parallel}
\operatorname{tr}_{\mathrm{int}}
\frac{
\delta E_+^{(\mathrm{sp})}(p)-\delta E_-^{(\mathrm{sp})}(p)
}{2}
\Big|_{p=0}.
}
\label{eq:vparsp_def}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, for the transverse matrices,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
W^i
=
\partial_{p_i}B
-
(\partial_{p_i}C_+)R_0C_-^\dagger
-
C_+R_0(\partial_{p_i}C_-^\dagger)
+
C_+R_0(\partial_{p_i}H_{ss})R_0C_-^\dagger
\Big|_{p=0},
\qquad
R_0=(H_{ss}(0)-E_*)^{-1}.
}
\label{eq:Wi_spectator_exact}
\end{equation}
This exact spectator-shell formula is already in the notes. :contentReference[oaicite:6]{index=6}

\section{Term-by-term harmonic extraction at \(Q=G_*\)}

Now fix any periodic operator kernel \(F(x)\) acting on the tangent doublet.
Its first-shell Bragg coefficient is
\begin{equation}
\widehat F(G_*)
=
\frac{1}{|\Omega|}
\int_{\Omega} d^3x\, e^{-iG_*\cdot x}F(x),
\label{eq:Fhat_def}
\end{equation}
where \(\Omega\) is the primitive cell.

Decompose \(F\) on the tangent doublet as
\[
F(x)=f_0(x)\mathbf1_2+f_1(x)s^1+f_2(x)s^2+f_3(x)s^3.
\]
Then
\begin{equation}
\widehat U(G_*)=\widehat f_0(G_*),
\qquad
\widehat T^1(G_*)=\widehat f_1(G_*),
\qquad
\widehat T^2(G_*)=\widehat f_2(G_*).
\label{eq:FT_dictionary}
\end{equation}

So the actual extraction rule is brutally simple:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{compute the }Q=G_*\text{ Fourier coefficient of each periodic kernel, then split it into }
\mathbf1_2,\ s^1,\ s^2 \text{ parts.}
}
\label{eq:actual_extraction_rule}
\end{equation}

\section{Immediate practical audit table}

The practical bookkeeping table is therefore:

\[
\begin{array}{c|c|c}
\text{microscopic source} & Q=G_* \text{ coefficient to compute} & \text{output}\\
\hline
H_{\Psi\Psi} & \widehat U_{\mathrm{bare}},\ \widehat T^1_{\mathrm{bare}},\ \widehat T^2_{\mathrm{bare}} & M_0^{\mathrm{bare}},W_{\mathrm{bare}}^1,W_{\mathrm{bare}}^2\\
-\frac1{M_X^2}\mathcal C\mathcal C^\dagger & \widehat U_{(II)},\ \widehat T^1_{(II)},\ \widehat T^2_{(II)} & M_0^{(II)},W_{(II)}^1,W_{(II)}^2\\
-C_+R_0C_-^\dagger & \widehat U_{(\mathrm{sp})},\ \widehat T^1_{(\mathrm{sp})},\ \widehat T^2_{(\mathrm{sp})} & M_0^{(\mathrm{sp})},W_{(\mathrm{sp})}^1,W_{(\mathrm{sp})}^2\\
E_+-E_- & \partial_{p_\parallel}\text{ at }p=0 & v_\parallel
\end{array}
\]

Then assemble
\[
M_0=
\bigl[\widehat U_{\mathrm{bare}}+\widehat U_{(II)}+\widehat U_{(\mathrm{sp})}\bigr]\mathbf1_2,
\]
\[
W^\alpha=
\bigl[\widehat T^\alpha_{\mathrm{bare}}+\widehat T^\alpha_{(II)}+\widehat T^\alpha_{(\mathrm{sp})}\bigr]s^\alpha,
\qquad \alpha=1,2,
\]
and
\[
v_\parallel=v_\parallel^{\mathrm{bare}}+\delta v_\parallel^{(II)}+\delta v_\parallel^{(\mathrm{sp})}.
\]

\section{Final local Weyl test}

Once the four coefficient sets above are computed, the final shell test is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
M_0=0,
\qquad
v_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
\widetilde W^1,\widetilde W^2
\ \text{linearly independent traceless Hermitian matrices.}
}
\label{eq:local_Weyl_final_test}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, in the reduced \(S2\) parametrization,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:S2_final_test_again}
\end{equation}

\section{What is honestly closed now}

At this point, the following is closed:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the full periodic coefficient-extraction problem has been reduced to a finite Fourier bookkeeping problem at }Q=G_*.
}
\]

What is not yet closed is numerical or symbolic execution for the final chosen
\(L_{\Psi}^{\mathrm{ref}}[\Psi,P]\).
That is a real calculation still to be done, but it is no longer conceptually open.

\section{Final Summary}

The full periodic folded-Bragg Bloch audit has now been reduced to the explicit extraction of four microscopic quantities:
\[
\widehat U_{\mathrm{eff}}(G_*),\qquad
\widehat T^1_{\mathrm{eff}}(G_*),\qquad
\widehat T^2_{\mathrm{eff}}(G_*),\qquad
v_\parallel.
\]

Each of them splits as
\[
\text{effective}=\text{bare}+\text{Class II}+\text{spectator}.
\]

The bare contribution comes from the periodic \(\Psi\Psi\)-block,
the Class II contribution from the self-energy
\[
-\frac1{M_X^2}\mathcal C\mathcal C^\dagger,
\]
and the spectator contribution from
\[
-C_+R_0C_-^\dagger.
\]

Therefore the actual remaining microscopic work is:

\begin{enumerate}
\item compute the \(Q=G_*\) Fourier coefficient of each periodic kernel;
\item split it into \(\mathbf1_2,s^1,s^2\) parts on the tangent doublet;
\item assemble \(M_0,W^1,W^2,v_\parallel\);
\item check
\[
M_0=0,\qquad
v_\parallel\neq 0,\qquad
\widetilde W^1,\widetilde W^2\ \text{independent}.
\]
\end{enumerate}

Equivalently, the final local Weyl test is
\[
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0,\qquad
(\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0).
\]

So the frontier is no longer conceptual.
It is the explicit symbolic or numerical execution of the Fourier bookkeeping for the final chosen refined locked microscopic operator.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Harmonic Selection Rule for the Class II Bloch Coupling Matrix}

\section{Goal}

The next explicit calculation is to derive the harmonic selection rule for the Class II coupling matrix
\[
\mathcal C_{(G,r),(G',i,a)}(k),
\]
defined by the linearized shell--mediator mixing between the Bloch harmonics of \(\delta\Psi\) and \(\delta X_i^a\).

The purpose of this section is not yet to fix a unique microscopic closed form of
\[
J_i^a[\Psi],\qquad K_i^a[P,\psi],
\]
but to derive the exact Bloch-harmonic bookkeeping rule that any such local periodic coupling must satisfy.

\section{Periodic background and Bloch expansions}

Work in the folded Bragg convention
\[
k_*=\frac{G_*}{2},\qquad k=k_*+p,\qquad |p|\ll |G_*|.
\]

The locked 12-mode BCC background is
\begin{equation}
\Psi_0(x)=z_0\,\phi_0(x),
\qquad
\phi_0(x)=\sum_{Q\in\mathcal S_{12}}A_Q e^{iQ\cdot x},
\qquad
P_0=z_0z_0^\dagger,
\label{eq:background_locked_12}
\end{equation}
with \(\mathcal S_{12}\) the first BCC reciprocal shell.

Choose the internal basis
\[
u_0=z_0,\qquad u_1,u_2\in Q_{z_0},\qquad u_r^\dagger u_s=\delta_{rs}.
\]

Expand the microscopic fluctuation in Bloch harmonics:
\begin{equation}
\delta\Psi(x)
=
\sum_{G\in\Lambda^*}\sum_{r=0}^2
\psi_{G,r}(k)\,
e^{i(k+G)\cdot x}\,u_r,
\label{eq:dPsi_Bloch}
\end{equation}
and the Class II mediator fluctuation as
\begin{equation}
\delta X_i^a(x)
=
\sum_{G'\in\Lambda^*}
X_{G',i}^a(k)\,
e^{i(k+G')\cdot x}.
\label{eq:dX_Bloch}
\end{equation}

Here \(\Lambda^*\) is the reciprocal lattice generated by the periodic BCC condensate.

\section{Linearized shell--mediator block}

The linearized Class II mixing comes from
\[
\alpha_X X_i^aJ_i^a[\Psi]+\beta_X X_i^aK_i^a[P,\psi].
\]
Around the background \((\Psi_0,P_0)\), the linearized off-diagonal block is schematically
\begin{equation}
L_{\Psi X}^{\mathrm{lin}}
=
\alpha_X\,\delta J_i^a[\Psi_0;\delta\Psi]
+
\beta_X\,\delta K_i^a[P_0;\delta\Psi].
\label{eq:L_PsiX_lin}
\end{equation}

Because the background is periodic, the coefficients of this linearized operator are periodic.
Therefore the corresponding Bloch matrix elements are translation-covariant and admit a harmonic expansion.

\section{Generic local harmonic form}

Any local first-order shell--mediator coupling generated by the periodic background can be written in the form
\begin{equation}
\delta J_i^a[\Psi_0;\delta\Psi](x)
=
\sum_{Q\in\Lambda^*}
e^{iQ\cdot x}\,
\mathsf J_{i,r}^{a}(Q;k+G)\,
\psi_{G,r}(k)\,
e^{i(k+G)\cdot x},
\label{eq:J_local_harmonic}
\end{equation}
and similarly
\begin{equation}
\delta K_i^a[P_0;\delta\Psi](x)
=
\sum_{Q\in\Lambda^*}
e^{iQ\cdot x}\,
\mathsf K_{i,r}^{a}(Q;k+G)\,
\psi_{G,r}(k)\,
e^{i(k+G)\cdot x}.
\label{eq:K_local_harmonic}
\end{equation}

Thus the total Class II coupling takes the harmonic form
\begin{equation}
\delta J_i^a+\delta K_i^a
=
\sum_{G,Q,r}
\mathsf C_{i,r}^{a}(Q;k+G)\,
\psi_{G,r}(k)\,
e^{i(k+G+Q)\cdot x},
\label{eq:C_local_harmonic}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\mathsf C_{i,r}^{a}(Q;k+G)
=
\alpha_X \mathsf J_{i,r}^{a}(Q;k+G)
+
\beta_X \mathsf K_{i,r}^{a}(Q;k+G).
\label{eq:C_from_JK}
\end{equation}

\section{Exact Bloch selection rule}

Projecting onto the mediator harmonic \(e^{i(k+G')\cdot x}\) gives the exact selection rule
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal C_{(G,r),(G',i,a)}(k)
=
\sum_{Q\in\Lambda^*}
\delta_{G',\,G+Q}\,
\mathsf C_{i,r}^{a}(Q;k+G).
}
\label{eq:Bloch_selection_rule}
\end{equation}

Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal C_{(G,r),(G',i,a)}(k)
=
\mathsf C_{i,r}^{a}(G'-G\,;\,k+G).
}
\label{eq:Bloch_selection_rule_compact}
\end{equation}

This is the fundamental harmonic bookkeeping formula:
the Class II coupling connects harmonic \(G\) to harmonic \(G'\) only through the Fourier mode
\[
Q=G'-G
\]
of the periodic background coefficient.

\section{Specialization to the locked 12-mode branch}

In the locked equal-amplitude 12-mode BCC background, the only nonzero fundamental background harmonics at leading shell order are
\[
Q\in \mathcal S_{12}.
\]
Therefore the leading shell-mixing block satisfies
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal C_{(G,r),(G',i,a)}(k)
=
\sum_{Q\in\mathcal S_{12}}
\delta_{G',\,G+Q}\,
\mathsf C_{i,r}^{a}(Q;k+G),
}
\label{eq:C_S12_rule}
\end{equation}
up to higher-harmonic corrections generated by nonlinear products of the background.

Hence, at leading locked-shell order, only differences \(G'-G\in\mathcal S_{12}\) can contribute.

\section{Folded shell-pair intervalley channel}

For the selected folded shell pair, the relevant two Bloch harmonics are
\[
G_+=+\frac{G_*}{2},\qquad
G_-=-\frac{G_*}{2},
\]
or equivalently the basis states
\[
\Phi_{+,a}(x)=e^{+iG_*\cdot x/2}u_a,
\qquad
\Phi_{-,a}(x)=e^{-iG_*\cdot x/2}u_a.
\]

The intervalley block connecting \(-\) to \(+\) therefore has
\[
G_+ - G_- = G_*.
\]
So the selection rule \eqref{eq:Bloch_selection_rule_compact} reduces immediately to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal C_{(-,r),(+,i,a)}(k_*)
=
\mathsf C_{i,r}^{a}(G_*;k_*-\tfrac{G_*}{2}).
}
\label{eq:intervalley_Gstar_rule}
\end{equation}

Thus the entire shell-pair carrier audit is controlled by the single first-shell Fourier coefficient
\[
Q=G_*.
\]

This is exactly why the reduced dictionary uses
\[
\widehat U_{\mathrm{eff}}(G_*),\qquad
\widehat T_{\mathrm{eff}}^1(G_*),\qquad
\widehat T_{\mathrm{eff}}^2(G_*).
\]

\section{Derivative content and parity structure}

At first derivative order, the local shell--mediator tensors \(\mathsf J,\mathsf K\) decompose into the three shell-adapted seed sectors:

\begin{equation}
\mathsf C_{i,r}^{a}(G_*;\cdot)
=
c_\parallel\,\hat n_i\,(\Sigma_3)_r{}^{a}
+
c_E\,(e_{1i}\Sigma_1+e_{2i}\Sigma_2)_r{}^{a}
+
c_O\,(-e_{2i}\Sigma_1+e_{1i}\Sigma_2)_r{}^{a}
+\cdots,
\label{eq:C_seed_decomp}
\end{equation}
where the omitted terms are shell-irrelevant, higher-derivative, or symmetry-forbidden components.

In particular:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the longitudinal primitive odd singlet contributes to \(B_\parallel\),
\item the transverse even doublet contributes to \(B_E\),
\item the transverse odd doublet contributes to \(B_O\).
\end{enumerate}

Therefore the reduced witness coefficients are nothing but the three seed coefficients extracted from the \(Q=G_*\) harmonic of the Class II mixing block.

\section{Index-level bookkeeping formula}

Using the shell-adapted basis \(u_r\), the explicit coefficient extraction is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_\parallel
\propto
\hat n^i
(\Sigma_3)^{r}{}_{a}\,
\mathsf C_{i,r}^{a}(G_*;k_*-\tfrac{G_*}{2}),
}
\label{eq:cpar_bookkeeping}
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_E
\propto
\frac12
\left[
e_1^i(\Sigma_1)^{r}{}_{a}
+
e_2^i(\Sigma_2)^{r}{}_{a}
\right]
\mathsf C_{i,r}^{a}(G_*;k_*-\tfrac{G_*}{2}),
}
\label{eq:cE_bookkeeping}
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_O
\propto
\frac12
\left[
-\,e_2^i(\Sigma_1)^{r}{}_{a}
+
e_1^i(\Sigma_2)^{r}{}_{a}
\right]
\mathsf C_{i,r}^{a}(G_*;k_*-\tfrac{G_*}{2}).
}
\label{eq:cO_bookkeeping}
\end{equation}

These coefficients then feed directly into
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\frac12 c_\parallel I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=c_E I_\theta,
\qquad
\beta=c_O I_\theta.
\]

\section{Final practical form for the Class II coupling matrix}

Combining everything, the actual working coupling matrix is

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal C_{(G,r),(G',i,a)}(k)
=
\delta_{G'-G\in\mathcal S_{12}}\,
\Big[
\alpha_X\,\mathsf J_{i,r}^{a}(G'-G;k+G)
+
\beta_X\,\mathsf K_{i,r}^{a}(G'-G;k+G)
\Big]
}
\label{eq:C_final_practical}
\end{equation}
at leading locked-shell order.

For the shell-pair intervalley block relevant to the Dirac audit, this collapses to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal C^{\mathrm{valley}}_{r,(i,a)}
=
\alpha_X\,\mathsf J_{i,r}^{a}(G_*;0)
+
\beta_X\,\mathsf K_{i,r}^{a}(G_*;0),
}
\label{eq:C_valley_final}
\end{equation}
where we used \(k_*-\frac{G_*}{2}=0\).

This is the concrete object whose three shell projections must be evaluated.

\section{What is closed and what remains open}

What is now closed:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the exact Bloch-harmonic selection rule;
\item the fact that the intervalley shell-pair channel is controlled only by the \(Q=G_*\) harmonic;
\item the index-level formula reducing the carrier audit to the three shell projections of
\[
\mathsf C_{i,r}^{a}(G_*;0).
\]
\end{enumerate}

What remains open is the explicit microscopic closed form of the coefficient functions
\[
\mathsf J_{i,r}^{a}(G_*;0),\qquad
\mathsf K_{i,r}^{a}(G_*;0)
\]
for the final chosen refined locked microscopic operator.
That is now a concrete tensor-contraction computation, not a conceptual problem.

\section{Final Summary}

For the refined locked + Class II microscopic branch, the Bloch-harmonic shell--mediator coupling matrix satisfies the exact selection rule
\[
\mathcal C_{(G,r),(G',i,a)}(k)
=
\mathsf C_{i,r}^{a}(G'-G;k+G),
\]
or equivalently
\[
\mathcal C_{(G,r),(G',i,a)}(k)
=
\sum_{Q}\delta_{G',\,G+Q}\,\mathsf C_{i,r}^{a}(Q;k+G).
\]

In the locked 12-mode BCC branch, the leading background harmonics satisfy \(Q\in\mathcal S_{12}\), so the intervalley shell-pair channel is controlled only by the single coefficient
\[
Q=G_*.
\]

Thus the actual microscopic carrier audit reduces to the evaluation of
\[
\mathsf C_{i,r}^{a}(G_*;0)
=
\alpha_X\,\mathsf J_{i,r}^{a}(G_*;0)
+
\beta_X\,\mathsf K_{i,r}^{a}(G_*;0).
\]

Its three shell-adapted projections define the seed coefficients
\[
c_\parallel,\qquad c_E,\qquad c_O,
\]
which feed into the reduced witnesses
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\frac12 c_\parallel I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=c_E I_\theta,
\qquad
\beta=c_O I_\theta.
\]

Therefore the remaining frontier is no longer conceptual.
It is the explicit tensor-contraction computation of the \(Q=G_*\) harmonic coefficients of the linearized Class II currents \(J_i^a\) and \(K_i^a\).

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Lowest-Derivative Local Ansatz for \(J_i^a[\Psi]\) and \(K_i^a[P,\psi]\)}

\section{Goal}

The next concrete task is to write the most general lowest-derivative local ansatz for the Class II currents
\[
J_i^a[\Psi],\qquad K_i^a[P,\psi],
\]
compatible with the refined locked background, and then extract the Bloch-harmonic coefficients
\[
\mathsf J_{i,r}^{a}(G_*;0),\qquad
\mathsf K_{i,r}^{a}(G_*;0)
\]
that control the shell-pair intervalley channel.

The purpose is not to fix a unique final complete TECT action, but to reduce the remaining microscopic work to explicit tensor contractions at the single harmonic
\[
Q=G_*.
\]

\section{Working microscopic branch}

We work in the strongest currently explicit branch,
\begin{equation}
\mathcal L_{\mathrm{UV}}^{(II)}
=
\frac{M_X^2}{2}X_i^aX_i^a
+
\alpha\,X_i^aJ_i^a[\Psi]
+
\beta\,X_i^aK_i^a[P,\psi].
\label{eq:UVII_working}
\end{equation}
The minimal explicit current choices already recorded in the notes are
\begin{equation}
J_i^a[\Psi]
=
(\partial_i\Psi^\dagger)T^a\Psi+\Psi^\dagger T^a(\partial_i\Psi),
\label{eq:J_minimal_explicit}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
K_i^a[P,\psi]
\sim
(T^a\partial_iP)\,\mathcal O[\psi].
\label{eq:K_minimal_explicit}
\end{equation}
A bookkeeping-equivalent lowest-order parametrization is
\begin{equation}
J_i^a[\phi_0,P_0]
=
m^a(P_0)\,\partial_i\phi_0,
\label{eq:J_bookkeeping}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
K_i^a[\psi]
=
\mathcal C_{ij}^{ab}\,(-i\partial_j)\,s_b\,\psi,
\label{eq:K_bookkeeping}
\end{equation}
with \(m^a(P_0)\) a constant internal vector fixed by the locked projector background and \(\mathcal C_{ij}^{ab}\) a fixed UV tensor kernel. :contentReference[oaicite:4]{index=4} 

\section{Locked background expansion}

Write the refined locked background as
\begin{equation}
\Psi_0(x)=z_0\,\phi_0(x),
\qquad
\phi_0(x)=\sum_{Q\in \mathcal S_{12}}A_Q e^{iQ\cdot x},
\qquad
P_0=z_0z_0^\dagger.
\label{eq:locked_background_again}
\end{equation}
Expand the full field as
\begin{equation}
\Psi=(\phi_0+\sigma)z_0+\psi,
\qquad
P=P_0+\delta P,
\qquad
\delta P\sim z_0\xi^\dagger+\xi z_0^\dagger.
\label{eq:refined_locked_expansion}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
\partial_i\Psi
=
(\partial_i\phi_0)z_0
+
\partial_i\psi
+
(\partial_i\sigma)z_0
+\cdots,
\label{eq:dPsi_expand}
\end{equation}
while
\begin{equation}
\partial_iP
=
\partial_i\delta P+\cdots
\sim
z_0(\partial_i\xi)^\dagger+(\partial_i\xi)z_0^\dagger+\cdots.
\label{eq:dP_expand}
\end{equation}
Therefore \(J_i^a\) is linear in the shell gradient \(\partial_i\phi_0\), and \(K_i^a\) is linear in the reduced defect/projector derivative sector. This is exactly the required \((i,a)\)-carrier structure. :contentReference[oaicite:6]{index=6}

\section{Most general lowest-derivative local ansatz}

At the lowest local derivative order compatible with the locked background and tangent-doublet structure, the most general linearized current ansatz may be written as follows.

\subsection{Background current}

The linearized background current has the form
\begin{equation}
\delta J_i^a[\Psi_0;\delta\Psi]
=
\mathcal A_r^a\,(\partial_i\phi_0)\,\psi_r
+
\mathcal B_{jr}^a\,(\partial_i\phi_0)\,(-i\partial_j)\psi_r
+
\mathcal D_{ir}^a\,\psi_r
+\cdots,
\label{eq:J_general_lowest}
\end{equation}
where \(r\) labels the shell-reduced internal/tangent basis.

For the first-order shell witness, only the piece with exactly one worldvolume derivative on the test mode is load-bearing. Therefore the relevant part is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta J_i^a[\Psi_0;\delta\Psi]_{\mathrm{lb}}
=
\mathcal B_{jr}^a\,(\partial_i\phi_0)\,(-i\partial_j)\psi_r.
}
\label{eq:J_load_bearing}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Projector/test current}

Likewise the linearized projector/test current has the general lowest-order form
\begin{equation}
\delta K_i^a[P_0;\delta\Psi]
=
\mathcal E_{ir}^{ab}\,(\partial_i\xi^a)\,s_b\psi_r
+
\mathcal F_{ijr}^{ab}\,(\partial_i\xi^a)\,(-i\partial_j)s_b\psi_r
+\cdots.
\label{eq:K_general_lowest}
\end{equation}
Again, for the shell witness we retain only the piece with exactly one worldvolume derivative:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta K_i^a[P_0;\delta\Psi]_{\mathrm{lb}}
=
\mathcal F_{ijr}^{ab}\,(\partial_i\xi^a)\,(-i\partial_j)s_b\psi_r.
}
\label{eq:K_load_bearing}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Minimal factorized form}

A practical minimal factorized specialization consistent with the notes is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta J_i^a[\Psi_0;\delta\Psi]_{\mathrm{lb}}
=
m^a(P_0)\,(\partial_i\phi_0)\,
\mathcal U_{jr}^{\ b}\,(-i\partial_j)s_b\psi_r,
}
\label{eq:J_factorized}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta K_i^a[P_0;\delta\Psi]_{\mathrm{lb}}
=
(\partial_i\xi^a)\,
\mathcal V_{jr}^{\ b}\,(-i\partial_j)s_b\psi_r.
}
\label{eq:K_factorized}
\end{equation}
This is the most useful form for explicit harmonic bookkeeping.

\section{Bloch-harmonic expansion}

Expand the reduced test mode in Bloch harmonics:
\begin{equation}
\psi_r(x)
=
\sum_{G\in\Lambda^*}\psi_{G,r}(k)\,e^{i(k+G)\cdot x}.
\label{eq:psi_bloch_again}
\end{equation}
Expand the locked shell background gradient:
\begin{equation}
\partial_i\phi_0(x)
=
\sum_{Q\in \mathcal S_{12}} iQ_i A_Q e^{iQ\cdot x}.
\label{eq:dphi_bloch}
\end{equation}

Then \eqref{eq:J_factorized} gives
\begin{align}
\delta J_i^a[\Psi_0;\delta\Psi]_{\mathrm{lb}}
&=
m^a(P_0)
\sum_{Q\in \mathcal S_{12}}iQ_i A_Q e^{iQ\cdot x}
\sum_{G,r}\mathcal U_{jr}^{\ b}(k+G)_j s_b\,\psi_{G,r}(k)e^{i(k+G)\cdot x}
\\
&=
\sum_{G,Q,r}
\underbrace{
m^a(P_0)\,iQ_i A_Q\,\mathcal U_{jr}^{\ b}(k+G)_j s_b
}_{\displaystyle \mathsf J_{i,r}^{a}(Q;k+G)}
\psi_{G,r}(k)e^{i(k+G+Q)\cdot x}.
\label{eq:J_harmonic_expand}
\end{align}
Thus
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathsf J_{i,r}^{a}(Q;k+G)
=
m^a(P_0)\,iQ_i A_Q\,\mathcal U_{jr}^{\ b}(k+G)_j s_b.
}
\label{eq:Jharm_final}
\end{equation}

Similarly, for \eqref{eq:K_factorized}, expand
\[
\partial_i\xi^a(x)
=
\sum_{Q\in \Lambda^*}\Xi_i^a(Q)\,e^{iQ\cdot x},
\]
to obtain
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathsf K_{i,r}^{a}(Q;k+G)
=
\Xi_i^a(Q)\,\mathcal V_{jr}^{\ b}(k+G)_j s_b.
}
\label{eq:Kharm_final}
\end{equation}

\section{Intervalley shell-pair reduction}

For the folded shell-pair audit, the only relevant harmonic is
\[
Q=G_*,
\qquad
k_*-\frac{G_*}{2}=0.
\]
Therefore the intervalley Class II mixing block is controlled by
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathsf J_{i,r}^{a}(G_*;0)
=
m^a(P_0)\,i(G_*)_i A_{G_*}\,\mathcal U_{jr}^{\ b}(0)_j s_b,
}
\label{eq:J_Gstar_zero}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathsf K_{i,r}^{a}(G_*;0)
=
\Xi_i^a(G_*)\,\mathcal V_{jr}^{\ b}(0)_j s_b.
}
\label{eq:K_Gstar_zero}
\end{equation}

Hence the actual Class II harmonic block is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathsf C_{i,r}^{a}(G_*;0)
=
\alpha_X\,\mathsf J_{i,r}^{a}(G_*;0)
+
\beta_X\,\mathsf K_{i,r}^{a}(G_*;0).
}
\label{eq:C_Gstar_zero}
\end{equation}

This is the concrete object whose shell projections define
\[
c_\parallel,\qquad c_E,\qquad c_O.
\]

\section{Shell-seed projection formulas}

Let \((\hat n,e_1,e_2)\) be the adapted shell frame and \((\Sigma_1,\Sigma_2,\Sigma_3)\) the tangent-doublet Pauli basis.
Then the three seed coefficients are extracted by

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_\parallel
=
\mathcal N_\parallel\,
\hat n^i(\Sigma_3)^{r}{}_{a}\,
\mathsf C_{i,r}^{a}(G_*;0),
}
\label{eq:cpar_proj_final}
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_E
=
\mathcal N_E\,
\frac12
\left[
e_1^i(\Sigma_1)^{r}{}_{a}
+
e_2^i(\Sigma_2)^{r}{}_{a}
\right]
\mathsf C_{i,r}^{a}(G_*;0),
}
\label{eq:cE_proj_final}
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_O
=
\mathcal N_O\,
\frac12
\left[
-\,e_2^i(\Sigma_1)^{r}{}_{a}
+
e_1^i(\Sigma_2)^{r}{}_{a}
\right]
\mathsf C_{i,r}^{a}(G_*;0),
}
\label{eq:cO_proj_final}
\end{equation}
with \(\mathcal N_\parallel,\mathcal N_E,\mathcal N_O\) fixed normalization constants.

Then
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel=\frac12 c_\parallel I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=c_E I_\theta,
\qquad
\beta=c_O I_\theta.
\label{eq:lambda_alpha_beta_fromC}
\end{equation}

\section{Immediate yes/no criterion}

Therefore the full remaining microscopic question is reduced to the finite tensor-contraction test:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\hat n^i(\Sigma_3)^{r}{}_{a}\,\mathsf C_{i,r}^{a}(G_*;0)\neq 0,
\qquad
\left(
[e_1^i\Sigma_1+e_2^i\Sigma_2]^{r}{}_{a}\mathsf C_{i,r}^{a}(G_*;0),\,
[-e_2^i\Sigma_1+e_1^i\Sigma_2]^{r}{}_{a}\mathsf C_{i,r}^{a}(G_*;0)
\right)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:final_tensor_test}
\end{equation}

This is exactly equivalent to
\[
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0).
\]

\section{What is closed and what remains open}

What is now closed:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the most general lowest-derivative local ansatz for \(J_i^a\) and \(K_i^a\);
\item the explicit Bloch-harmonic formulas for
\[
\mathsf J_{i,r}^{a}(Q;k+G),\qquad
\mathsf K_{i,r}^{a}(Q;k+G);
\]
\item the reduction of the intervalley shell-pair channel to the single harmonic
\[
Q=G_*;
\]
\item the final shell-seed projection formulas producing
\[
c_\parallel,\qquad c_E,\qquad c_O.
\]
\end{enumerate}

What remains open is only the explicit microscopic evaluation of the background tensors
\[
m^a(P_0),\qquad
\mathcal U_{jr}^{\ b}(0),\qquad
\Xi_i^a(G_*),\qquad
\mathcal V_{jr}^{\ b}(0)
\]
for the final chosen refined locked operator.
That is now a direct tensor-contraction computation.

\section{Final Summary}

The Class II microscopic carrier audit is now reduced to the explicit \(Q=G_*\) harmonic coefficients of the lowest-derivative local current ansatz.

The general lowest-order local forms are
\[
\delta J_i^a[\Psi_0;\delta\Psi]_{\mathrm{lb}}
=
m^a(P_0)\,(\partial_i\phi_0)\,
\mathcal U_{jr}^{\ b}\,(-i\partial_j)s_b\psi_r,
\]
\[
\delta K_i^a[P_0;\delta\Psi]_{\mathrm{lb}}
=
(\partial_i\xi^a)\,
\mathcal V_{jr}^{\ b}\,(-i\partial_j)s_b\psi_r.
\]

Their Bloch-harmonic coefficients are
\[
\mathsf J_{i,r}^{a}(Q;k+G)
=
m^a(P_0)\,iQ_i A_Q\,\mathcal U_{jr}^{\ b}(k+G)_j s_b,
\]
\[
\mathsf K_{i,r}^{a}(Q;k+G)
=
\Xi_i^a(Q)\,\mathcal V_{jr}^{\ b}(k+G)_j s_b.
\]

For the folded shell-pair intervalley channel, only
\[
Q=G_*,\qquad k_*-\frac{G_*}{2}=0
\]
survives, so the relevant coupling is
\[
\mathsf C_{i,r}^{a}(G_*;0)
=
\alpha_X\,\mathsf J_{i,r}^{a}(G_*;0)
+
\beta_X\,\mathsf K_{i,r}^{a}(G_*;0).
\]

Its three shell-adapted projections define
\[
c_\parallel,\qquad c_E,\qquad c_O,
\]
which determine
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\frac12 c_\parallel I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=c_E I_\theta,
\qquad
\beta=c_O I_\theta.
\]

Therefore the final remaining frontier is the explicit tensor-contraction evaluation of
\[
m^a(P_0),\qquad
\mathcal U_{jr}^{\ b}(0),\qquad
\Xi_i^a(G_*),\qquad
\mathcal V_{jr}^{\ b}(0)
\]
for the final chosen refined locked microscopic operator.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Canonical Normalization of the Class II Shell Coefficients}

\section{Goal}

The remaining task is to choose a canonical local gauge/basis in the locked background and reduce
the tensor contractions
\[
c_\parallel,\qquad c_E,\qquad c_O
\]
to explicit scalar coefficients multiplying the three shell seeds
\[
B_\parallel,\qquad B_E,\qquad B_O.
\]

At this stage, the problem is no longer to prove the existence of the carrier mechanism.
It is to normalize the internal and shell-tangent bases so that the three reduced coefficients are read directly from the lowest-order UV tensors.

\section{Canonical locked basis}

Take the locked background representative
\begin{equation}
z_0=
\begin{pmatrix}
1\\
0\\
0
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
P_0=z_0z_0^\dagger=
\mathrm{diag}(1,0,0).
\label{eq:z0_canonical}
\end{equation}

Choose the tangent basis
\begin{equation}
u_1=
\begin{pmatrix}
0\\
1\\
0
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
u_2=
\begin{pmatrix}
0\\
0\\
1
\end{pmatrix},
\label{eq:u12_canonical}
\end{equation}
so that
\[
Q_{z_0}=\mathrm{span}_{\mathbb C}\{u_1,u_2\}.
\]

In this basis, the tangent Pauli matrices are the standard ones:
\begin{equation}
\Sigma_1=
\begin{pmatrix}
0&1\\
1&0
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
\Sigma_2=
\begin{pmatrix}
0&-i\\
i&0
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
\Sigma_3=
\begin{pmatrix}
1&0\\
0&-1
\end{pmatrix}.
\label{eq:Sigma_canonical}
\end{equation}

This fixes the internal tangent frame up to a residual \(U(2)\) rotation.
For the calibration step, we use this basis as the canonical frame.

\section{Canonical shell frame}

Fix the selected shell vector \(G_*\), and define
\[
\hat n=\frac{G_*}{|G_*|}.
\]
Choose a real orthonormal shell frame
\begin{equation}
\{e_1,e_2,\hat n\}.
\label{eq:shell_frame_canonical}
\end{equation}

Then every spatial tensor \(X_{ij}\) relevant to the first-order shell witness decomposes uniquely into the three shell-adapted invariant directions:
\begin{equation}
\hat n_i\hat n_j,
\qquad
\hat n_i e_{1j}+ \hat n_i e_{2j},
\qquad
-\hat n_i e_{2j}+\hat n_i e_{1j},
\label{eq:three_shell_directions}
\end{equation}
paired with \(\Sigma_3,\Sigma_1,\Sigma_2\), respectively.

\section{Canonical choice of the background vector \(m^a(P_0)\)}

The background vector \(m^a(P_0)\) is an internal object determined only by the locked projector \(P_0\).
In the canonical aligned basis, the unique distinguished tangent-singlet direction is the \(\Sigma_3\) axis.

Therefore the minimal canonical choice is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m^a(P_0)=m_\parallel\,\delta^{a3},
}
\label{eq:m_canonical}
\end{equation}
with \(m_\parallel\in\mathbb R\).

This is the precise canonical statement that the longitudinal primitive odd singlet is aligned with the third internal axis.

\section{Minimal tensor decomposition of \(\mathcal U\)}

The tensor \(\mathcal U_{jr}{}^{b}(0)\) carries one gradient index \(j\), one tangent-doublet index \(r\), and one Pauli label \(b\).
At lowest derivative order, in the canonical shell frame, its shell-relevant part decomposes as
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal U_{jr}{}^{b}(0)
=
u_\parallel\,\hat n_j\,(\Sigma_3)_r{}^{b}
+
u_E\,e_{1j}\,(\Sigma_1)_r{}^{b}
+
u_E\,e_{2j}\,(\Sigma_2)_r{}^{b}
+
u_O\,(-e_{2j})(\Sigma_1)_r{}^{b}
+
u_O\,e_{1j}(\Sigma_2)_r{}^{b}
+
\mathcal U^{\mathrm{irr}}_{jr}{}^{b},
}
\label{eq:U_decomp}
\end{equation}
where \(\mathcal U^{\mathrm{irr}}\) is orthogonal to the three shell seeds and therefore does not contribute to the reduced witness.

Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\mathcal U_{jr}{}^{b}(0)
=
u_\parallel\,\hat n_j\,(\Sigma_3)_r{}^{b}
+
u_E\,(e_{1j}\Sigma_1+e_{2j}\Sigma_2)_r{}^{b}
+
u_O\,(-e_{2j}\Sigma_1+e_{1j}\Sigma_2)_r{}^{b}
+
\mathcal U^{\mathrm{irr}}_{jr}{}^{b}.
\label{eq:U_decomp_compact}
\end{equation}

\section{Minimal tensor decomposition of \(\mathcal V\)}

Similarly, the projector-sector tensor \(\mathcal V_{jr}{}^{b}(0)\) decomposes as
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal V_{jr}{}^{b}(0)
=
v_\parallel\,\hat n_j\,(\Sigma_3)_r{}^{b}
+
v_E\,(e_{1j}\Sigma_1+e_{2j}\Sigma_2)_r{}^{b}
+
v_O\,(-e_{2j}\Sigma_1+e_{1j}\Sigma_2)_r{}^{b}
+
\mathcal V^{\mathrm{irr}}_{jr}{}^{b},
}
\label{eq:V_decomp_compact}
\end{equation}
again with \(\mathcal V^{\mathrm{irr}}\) orthogonal to the shell seed sector.

\section{Canonical form of the \(Q=G_*\) harmonic coefficients}

From the general formulas already derived,
\begin{equation}
\mathsf J_{i,r}^{a}(G_*;0)
=
m^a(P_0)\,i(G_*)_i A_{G_*}\,\mathcal U_{jr}{}^{b}(0)\,(0)_j\,s_b,
\label{eq:J_old_form}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\mathsf K_{i,r}^{a}(G_*;0)
=
\Xi_i^a(G_*)\,\mathcal V_{jr}{}^{b}(0)\,(0)_j\,s_b.
\label{eq:K_old_form}
\end{equation}

For the shell witness one keeps the first nontrivial linear term in the slow momentum \(p_j\).
Thus the effective load-bearing coefficient is the linear coefficient multiplying \(p_j\), which we denote by replacing \((0)_j\) with the tangent derivative insertion basis.

Accordingly, the shell-relevant current block becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathsf J_{i,r}^{a}(G_*;0)
=
m_\parallel\,\delta^{a3}\,i(G_*)_i A_{G_*}
\Big[
u_\parallel\,\hat n_j\Sigma_3
+
u_E\,(e_{1j}\Sigma_1+e_{2j}\Sigma_2)
+
u_O\,(-e_{2j}\Sigma_1+e_{1j}\Sigma_2)
\Big]_r{}^{b},
}
\label{eq:J_canonical_final}
\end{equation}
and similarly
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathsf K_{i,r}^{a}(G_*;0)
=
\Xi_i^a(G_*)
\Big[
v_\parallel\,\hat n_j\Sigma_3
+
v_E\,(e_{1j}\Sigma_1+e_{2j}\Sigma_2)
+
v_O\,(-e_{2j}\Sigma_1+e_{1j}\Sigma_2)
\Big]_r{}^{b}.
}
\label{eq:K_canonical_final}
\end{equation}

\section{Canonical decomposition of \(\Xi_i^a(G_*)\)}

The projector-harmonic coefficient \(\Xi_i^a(G_*)\) has one spatial index and one internal index.
At the shell-relevant level, its most general canonical decomposition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Xi_i^a(G_*)
=
\xi_\parallel\,\hat n_i\,\delta^{a3}
+
\xi_E\,(e_{1i}\delta^{a1}+e_{2i}\delta^{a2})
+
\xi_O\,(-e_{2i}\delta^{a1}+e_{1i}\delta^{a2})
+
\Xi_{i}^{a,\mathrm{irr}}.
}
\label{eq:Xi_decomp}
\end{equation}
Again \(\Xi^{\mathrm{irr}}\) is orthogonal to the shell seed sector.

\section{Evaluation of the seed coefficients}

Now substitute \eqref{eq:m_canonical}, \eqref{eq:U_decomp_compact}, \eqref{eq:V_decomp_compact}, and \eqref{eq:Xi_decomp} into
\[
\mathsf C_{i,r}^{a}(G_*;0)
=
\alpha_X\mathsf J_{i,r}^{a}(G_*;0)
+
\beta_X\mathsf K_{i,r}^{a}(G_*;0).
\]

Because the shell projections are orthogonal by construction, only aligned seed pieces survive.
Therefore the three reduced coefficients take the canonical form
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_\parallel
=
\alpha_X\,\mu_J\,m_\parallel\,u_\parallel
+
\beta_X\,\mu_K\,\xi_\parallel v_\parallel,
}
\label{eq:cpar_canonical}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_E
=
\alpha_X\,\nu_J\,m_\parallel\,u_E
+
\beta_X\,\nu_K\,\xi_E v_E,
}
\label{eq:cE_canonical}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_O
=
\alpha_X\,\omega_J\,m_\parallel\,u_O
+
\beta_X\,\omega_K\,\xi_O v_O.
}
\label{eq:cO_canonical}
\end{equation}
Here \(\mu_J,\mu_K,\nu_J,\nu_K,\omega_J,\omega_K\) are fixed numerical normalization factors determined by the chosen orthonormal shell/tangent basis.

In the fully normalized canonical convention, these factors may be set to unity:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mu_J=\mu_K=\nu_J=\nu_K=\omega_J=\omega_K=1.
}
\label{eq:normalization_unity}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_\parallel
=
\alpha_X\,m_\parallel u_\parallel
+
\beta_X\,\xi_\parallel v_\parallel,
}
\label{eq:cpar_simple}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_E
=
\alpha_X\,m_\parallel u_E
+
\beta_X\,\xi_E v_E,
}
\label{eq:cE_simple}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_O
=
\alpha_X\,m_\parallel u_O
+
\beta_X\,\xi_O v_O.
}
\label{eq:cO_simple}
\end{equation}

\section{Minimal explicit specialization}

The sharpest minimal canonical specialization is obtained by taking the background current to contribute only to the longitudinal singlet and the projector current to contribute dominantly to the transverse doublet:
\begin{equation}
u_E=u_O=0,
\qquad
v_\parallel=0.
\label{eq:minimal_split_choice}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_\parallel=\alpha_X\,m_\parallel u_\parallel,
\qquad
c_E=\beta_X\,\xi_E v_E,
\qquad
c_O=\beta_X\,\xi_O v_O.
}
\label{eq:minimal_explicit_c}
\end{equation}

This is the cleanest canonical realization of the Branch-B picture:
\begin{enumerate}
\item the longitudinal coefficient comes from the odd singlet background-current channel;
\item the transverse \(E/O\) coefficients come from the projector-mediated tangent-doublet channel.
\end{enumerate}

\section{Reduced witness coefficients}

Substituting into the shell witness dictionary gives
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac12
\bigl(\alpha_X\,m_\parallel u_\parallel+\beta_X\,\xi_\parallel v_\parallel\bigr)
I_{\theta'^3},
}
\label{eq:lambda_final_canonical}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
=
\bigl(\alpha_X\,m_\parallel u_E+\beta_X\,\xi_E v_E\bigr)I_\theta,
}
\label{eq:alpha_final_canonical}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta
=
\bigl(\alpha_X\,m_\parallel u_O+\beta_X\,\xi_O v_O\bigr)I_\theta.
}
\label{eq:beta_final_canonical}
\end{equation}

Under the minimal explicit specialization \eqref{eq:minimal_split_choice},
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\frac12\,\alpha_X\,m_\parallel u_\parallel\,I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=\beta_X\,\xi_E v_E\,I_\theta,
\qquad
\beta=\beta_X\,\xi_O v_O\,I_\theta.
}
\label{eq:lambda_alpha_beta_minimal}
\end{equation}

\section{Final yes/no test in canonical normalization}

Thus the exact local Weyl/Dirac nondegeneracy criterion becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha_X\,m_\parallel u_\parallel+\beta_X\,\xi_\parallel v_\parallel\neq 0,
}
\label{eq:long_yesno_canonical}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Bigl(
\alpha_X\,m_\parallel u_E+\beta_X\,\xi_E v_E,\,
\alpha_X\,m_\parallel u_O+\beta_X\,\xi_O v_O
\Bigr)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:trans_yesno_canonical}
\end{equation}

In the minimal explicit canonical split, this simplifies to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m_\parallel u_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(\xi_E v_E,\xi_O v_O)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:minimal_yesno}
\end{equation}

\section{What is closed and what remains open}

What is now closed:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the canonical gauge/basis choice for the locked background;
\item the minimal shell-seed decomposition of the UV tensors \(\mathcal U,\mathcal V,\Xi\);
\item the explicit canonical formulas for
\[
c_\parallel,\qquad c_E,\qquad c_O;
\]
\item the reduced witness coefficients \(\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta\) in canonical normalization.
\end{enumerate}

What remains open is only the explicit microscopic evaluation of the scalar coefficients
\[
m_\parallel,\qquad
u_\parallel,u_E,u_O,\qquad
\xi_\parallel,\xi_E,\xi_O,\qquad
v_\parallel,v_E,v_O
\]
for the final chosen refined locked operator.
That is now a finite coefficient-matching problem.

\section{Final Summary}

With the canonical locked basis
\[
z_0=(1,0,0)^T,
\qquad
u_1=(0,1,0)^T,
\qquad
u_2=(0,0,1)^T,
\]
the tangent Pauli basis is fixed canonically.

The background vector aligns with the singlet axis as
\[
m^a(P_0)=m_\parallel\delta^{a3}.
\]

The shell-relevant UV tensors decompose into the three invariant seed directions:
\[
\mathcal U=u_\parallel B_\parallel+u_E B_E+u_O B_O+\cdots,
\]
\[
\mathcal V=v_\parallel B_\parallel+v_E B_E+v_O B_O+\cdots,
\]
\[
\Xi=\xi_\parallel B_\parallel+\xi_E B_E+\xi_O B_O+\cdots.
\]

Therefore the reduced shell coefficients become
\[
c_\parallel
=
\alpha_X\,m_\parallel u_\parallel
+
\beta_X\,\xi_\parallel v_\parallel,
\]
\[
c_E
=
\alpha_X\,m_\parallel u_E
+
\beta_X\,\xi_E v_E,
\]
\[
c_O
=
\alpha_X\,m_\parallel u_O
+
\beta_X\,\xi_O v_O.
\]

Hence
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\frac12 c_\parallel I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=c_E I_\theta,
\qquad
\beta=c_O I_\theta.
\]

Under the minimal explicit canonical split
\[
u_E=u_O=0,\qquad v_\parallel=0,
\]
this simplifies to
\[
c_\parallel=\alpha_X m_\parallel u_\parallel,
\qquad
c_E=\beta_X\xi_E v_E,
\qquad
c_O=\beta_X\xi_O v_O.
\]

Thus the remaining frontier is reduced to the finite coefficient-matching problem for
\[
m_\parallel,\quad
u_\parallel,u_E,u_O,\quad
\xi_\parallel,\xi_E,\xi_O,\quad
v_\parallel,v_E,v_O.
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Submission-Ready Master Formula for the Minimal Explicit Canonical Split}

\section{Canonical split}

We adopt the minimal explicit canonical split:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u_E=u_O=0,
\qquad
v_\parallel=0.
}
\label{eq:minimal_canonical_split}
\end{equation}
This means:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the longitudinal primitive odd singlet is carried entirely by the background-current \(J\)-sector;
\item the transverse even/odd doublets are carried entirely by the projector/test-current \(K\)-sector.
\end{enumerate}

Equivalently, the shell-relevant coefficients reduce to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_\parallel=\alpha_X\,m_\parallel u_\parallel,
\qquad
c_E=\beta_X\,\xi_E v_E,
\qquad
c_O=\beta_X\,\xi_O v_O.
}
\label{eq:c_master}
\end{equation}

\section{Reduced witness coefficients}

Using the exact shell witness dictionary,
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel=\frac12 c_\parallel I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=c_E I_\theta,
\qquad
\beta=c_O I_\theta,
\label{eq:witness_dictionary_master}
\end{equation}
we obtain
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac12\,\alpha_X\,m_\parallel u_\parallel\,I_{\theta'^3},
}
\label{eq:lambda_master}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
=
\beta_X\,\xi_E v_E\,I_\theta,
}
\label{eq:alpha_master}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta
=
\beta_X\,\xi_O v_O\,I_\theta.
}
\label{eq:beta_master}
\end{equation}

\section{Reduced first-order symbol}

Therefore the exact reduced Branch-B first-order symbol is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_1(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\alpha\,(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta\,(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2).
}
\label{eq:A1_master}
\end{equation}

Substituting \eqref{eq:lambda_master}--\eqref{eq:beta_master},
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_1(p)
=
\frac12\,\alpha_X m_\parallel u_\parallel I_{\theta'^3}\,p_\parallel\sigma_3
+
\beta_X\xi_E v_E I_\theta\,(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta_X\xi_O v_O I_\theta\,(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2).
}
\label{eq:A1_master_explicit}
\end{equation}

\section{Exact local Weyl/Dirac criterion}

The exact nondegeneracy condition becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m_\parallel u_\parallel \neq 0,
\qquad
(\xi_E v_E,\xi_O v_O)\neq (0,0),
}
\label{eq:nondeg_master}
\end{equation}
assuming
\[
\alpha_X\neq 0,\qquad \beta_X\neq 0,\qquad I_{\theta'^3}\neq 0,\qquad I_\theta\neq 0.
\]

Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:nondeg_master_reduced}
\end{equation}

This is the complete submission-ready local Weyl condition for the minimal explicit canonical split.

\section{Infrared velocities}

Identifying the reduced coefficients with the infrared velocities,
\begin{equation}
v_\parallel^{\mathrm{IR}}=\lambda_\parallel,
\qquad
v_E^{\mathrm{IR}}=\alpha,
\qquad
v_O^{\mathrm{IR}}=\beta,
\label{eq:IR_velocity_ident}
\end{equation}
we get
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v_\parallel^{\mathrm{IR}}
=
\frac12\,\alpha_X\,m_\parallel u_\parallel\,I_{\theta'^3},
}
\label{eq:vpar_IR}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v_\perp^{\mathrm{IR}}
=
\sqrt{\alpha^2+\beta^2}
=
|\beta_X I_\theta|\,
\sqrt{(\xi_E v_E)^2+(\xi_O v_O)^2}.
}
\label{eq:vperp_IR}
\end{equation}

\section{Anisotropy ratio}

The anisotropy ratio is therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\rho
=
\frac{v_\parallel^{\mathrm{IR}}}{v_\perp^{\mathrm{IR}}}
=
\frac{
\frac12\,\alpha_X\,m_\parallel u_\parallel\,I_{\theta'^3}
}{
|\beta_X I_\theta|\,\sqrt{(\xi_E v_E)^2+(\xi_O v_O)^2}
}.
}
\label{eq:rho_master}
\end{equation}

Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\rho
=
\frac{\alpha_X}{\beta_X}\,
\frac{m_\parallel u_\parallel}{2\sqrt{(\xi_E v_E)^2+(\xi_O v_O)^2}}\,
\frac{I_{\theta'^3}}{I_\theta},
}
\label{eq:rho_master_ratio}
\end{equation}
up to the overall sign convention of \(I_\theta\) and \(\beta_X\).

\section{Small-defect regime}

In the natural small-defect regime,
\[
I_{\theta'^3}\sim \frac{3}{16}(\theta_0\kappa)^2 I_\theta,
\]
so the leading-order anisotropy becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\rho_{\mathrm{LO}}
=
\frac{3}{32}\,
\frac{\alpha_X}{\beta_X}\,
\frac{m_\parallel u_\parallel}{\sqrt{(\xi_E v_E)^2+(\xi_O v_O)^2}}\,
(\theta_0\kappa)^2.
}
\label{eq:rho_LO_master}
\end{equation}

Thus the Branch-B cone is naturally strongly transverse-dominated unless the longitudinal coefficient is parametrically enhanced.

\section{Aspect ratio and inverse estimate}

Define the cone aspect ratio
\begin{equation}
A:=\frac{1}{|\rho|}=\frac{v_\perp^{\mathrm{IR}}}{|v_\parallel^{\mathrm{IR}}|}.
\label{eq:A_master}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_{\mathrm{LO}}
=
\frac{32}{3}\,
\frac{\beta_X}{\alpha_X}\,
\frac{\sqrt{(\xi_E v_E)^2+(\xi_O v_O)^2}}{|m_\parallel u_\parallel|}\,
(\theta_0\kappa)^{-2}.
}
\label{eq:A_LO_master}
\end{equation}

Hence the microscopic defect-strength combination is inferred as
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\theta_0\kappa
=
\sqrt{
\frac{32}{3A}\,
\frac{\beta_X}{\alpha_X}\,
\frac{\sqrt{(\xi_E v_E)^2+(\xi_O v_O)^2}}{|m_\parallel u_\parallel|}
}.
}
\label{eq:inverse_master}
\end{equation}

\section{Trace formulation}

In the projected \(2\times2\) shell block language, the same formulas are read from
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel=\frac12\operatorname{Tr}(\sigma_3 M^\parallel),
\qquad
\alpha=\frac12\operatorname{Tr}(\sigma_1 M^1),
\qquad
\beta=\frac12\operatorname{Tr}(\sigma_2 M^1).
\label{eq:trace_master}
\end{equation}
Under the minimal explicit canonical split, these become
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\frac12\operatorname{Tr}(\sigma_3 M^\parallel)
=
\frac12\,\alpha_X\,m_\parallel u_\parallel\,I_{\theta'^3},
}
\label{eq:trace_lambda_master}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\frac12\operatorname{Tr}(\sigma_1 M^1)
=
\beta_X\,\xi_E v_E\,I_\theta,
}
\label{eq:trace_alpha_master}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\frac12\operatorname{Tr}(\sigma_2 M^1)
=
\beta_X\,\xi_O v_O\,I_\theta.
}
\label{eq:trace_beta_master}
\end{equation}

\section{Submission-ready theorem}

\begin{theorem}[Minimal explicit canonical Branch-B theorem]
Assume:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the refined locked microscopic branch admits the Class II carrier sector;
\item the canonical split \eqref{eq:minimal_canonical_split} holds;
\item the overlap integrals satisfy
\[
I_{\theta'^3}\neq 0,\qquad I_\theta\neq 0;
\]
\item the UV couplings satisfy
\[
\alpha_X\neq 0,\qquad \beta_X\neq 0.
\]
\end{enumerate}

Then the reduced first-order shell symbol is
\[
A_1(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\alpha(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2),
\]
with
\[
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac12\,\alpha_X\,m_\parallel u_\parallel\,I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha
=
\beta_X\,\xi_E v_E\,I_\theta,
\qquad
\beta
=
\beta_X\,\xi_O v_O\,I_\theta.
\]
Hence the local Weyl/Dirac phase exists if and only if
\[
m_\parallel u_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(\xi_E v_E,\xi_O v_O)\neq (0,0).
\]
Moreover, the anisotropy ratio is
\[
\rho
=
\frac{
\frac12\,\alpha_X\,m_\parallel u_\parallel\,I_{\theta'^3}
}{
|\beta_X I_\theta|\,\sqrt{(\xi_E v_E)^2+(\xi_O v_O)^2}
},
\]
and in the small-defect regime satisfies
\[
\rho_{\mathrm{LO}}
=
\frac{3}{32}\,
\frac{\alpha_X}{\beta_X}\,
\frac{m_\parallel u_\parallel}{\sqrt{(\xi_E v_E)^2+(\xi_O v_O)^2}}\,
(\theta_0\kappa)^2.
\]
\end{theorem}

\section{Final Summary}

Under the minimal explicit canonical split,
\[
u_E=u_O=0,\qquad v_\parallel=0,
\]
the shell coefficients are
\[
c_\parallel=\alpha_X m_\parallel u_\parallel,
\qquad
c_E=\beta_X \xi_E v_E,
\qquad
c_O=\beta_X \xi_O v_O.
\]

Therefore the reduced Branch-B coefficients are
\[
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac12\,\alpha_X\,m_\parallel u_\parallel\,I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha
=
\beta_X\,\xi_E v_E\,I_\theta,
\qquad
\beta
=
\beta_X\,\xi_O v_O\,I_\theta.
\]

The exact local Weyl/Dirac condition is
\[
m_\parallel u_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(\xi_E v_E,\xi_O v_O)\neq (0,0).
\]

The anisotropy ratio is
\[
\rho
=
\frac{
\frac12\,\alpha_X\,m_\parallel u_\parallel\,I_{\theta'^3}
}{
|\beta_X I_\theta|\,\sqrt{(\xi_E v_E)^2+(\xi_O v_O)^2}
},
\]
and in the small-defect regime becomes
\[
\rho_{\mathrm{LO}}
=
\frac{3}{32}\,
\frac{\alpha_X}{\beta_X}\,
\frac{m_\parallel u_\parallel}{\sqrt{(\xi_E v_E)^2+(\xi_O v_O)^2}}\,
(\theta_0\kappa)^2.
\]

Thus the entire remaining microscopic frontier is reduced to a finite coefficient-matching problem for the scalar quantities
\[
m_\parallel,\qquad
u_\parallel,\qquad
\xi_E v_E,\qquad
\xi_O v_O.
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Finite Coefficient-Matching Problem}

\section{Statement of the problem}

After the full reduction to the refined locked + Class II branch, the remaining microscopic problem is no longer an infinite-dimensional PDE problem.
It is a finite coefficient-matching problem for the shell-seed sector.

Under the minimal explicit canonical split
\begin{equation}
u_E=u_O=0,
\qquad
v_\parallel=0,
\label{eq:min_split_match}
\end{equation}
the shell coefficients reduce to
\begin{equation}
c_\parallel=\alpha_X\,m_\parallel u_\parallel,
\qquad
c_E=\beta_X\,\xi_E v_E,
\qquad
c_O=\beta_X\,\xi_O v_O.
\label{eq:c_match_basic}
\end{equation}

Therefore the reduced witness coefficients are
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac12\,\alpha_X\,m_\parallel u_\parallel\,I_{\theta'^3},
\label{eq:lambda_match}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\alpha
=
\beta_X\,\xi_E v_E\,I_\theta,
\label{eq:alpha_match}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\beta
=
\beta_X\,\xi_O v_O\,I_\theta.
\label{eq:beta_match}
\end{equation}

Hence the exact local Weyl condition becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m_\parallel u_\parallel \neq 0,
\qquad
(\xi_E v_E,\xi_O v_O)\neq (0,0),
}
\label{eq:finite_match_condition}
\end{equation}
assuming
\[
\alpha_X\neq 0,\qquad
\beta_X\neq 0,\qquad
I_{\theta'^3}\neq 0,\qquad
I_\theta\neq 0.
\]

\section{Natural repackaging into two finite invariants}

Define the longitudinal scalar
\begin{equation}
L_*:=m_\parallel u_\parallel,
\label{eq:Lstar_def}
\end{equation}
and the transverse two-vector
\begin{equation}
T_*:=(T_E,T_O):=(\xi_E v_E,\xi_O v_O).
\label{eq:Tstar_def}
\end{equation}

Then the shell coefficients become
\begin{equation}
c_\parallel=\alpha_X L_*,
\qquad
(c_E,c_O)=\beta_X T_*,
\label{eq:c_invariants}
\end{equation}
and the reduced witness coefficients are
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel=\frac12\,\alpha_X L_* I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
(\alpha,\beta)=\beta_X I_\theta\,T_*.
\label{eq:witness_invariants}
\end{equation}

Thus the entire local carrier problem is reduced to:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_*\neq 0,
\qquad
T_*\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:LT_nonzero}
\end{equation}

\section{Polar form of the transverse sector}

It is useful to write the transverse vector in polar form:
\begin{equation}
R_\perp:=\sqrt{T_E^2+T_O^2},
\qquad
T_E=R_\perp\cos\varphi,
\qquad
T_O=R_\perp\sin\varphi.
\label{eq:polar_T}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
\alpha=\beta_X I_\theta R_\perp\cos\varphi,
\qquad
\beta=\beta_X I_\theta R_\perp\sin\varphi,
\label{eq:alpha_beta_polar}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
v_\perp^{\mathrm{IR}}
=
\sqrt{\alpha^2+\beta^2}
=
|\beta_X I_\theta|\,R_\perp.
\label{eq:vperp_polar}
\end{equation}

So the transverse sector is fully controlled by two finite numbers:
its magnitude \(R_\perp\) and the orientation angle \(\varphi\).

\section{Minimal master formula}

With
\[
L_*=m_\parallel u_\parallel,
\qquad
R_\perp=\sqrt{(\xi_E v_E)^2+(\xi_O v_O)^2},
\]
the reduced first-order symbol is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_1(p)
=
\frac12\,\alpha_X L_* I_{\theta'^3}\,p_\parallel\sigma_3
+
\beta_X I_\theta R_\perp
\Big[
\cos\varphi\,(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\sin\varphi\,(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2)
\Big].
}
\label{eq:A1_LT_master}
\end{equation}

This is the submission-ready master formula for the finite coefficient-matching problem.

\section{Exact Weyl/Dirac criterion}

The exact nondegeneracy condition is now simply
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_*\neq 0,
\qquad
R_\perp>0.
}
\label{eq:exact_LT_condition}
\end{equation}

Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:exact_reduced_condition}
\end{equation}

So the local Weyl/Dirac phase depends only on two finite matching conditions:
one longitudinal scalar and one transverse norm.

\section{Anisotropy ratio}

The infrared longitudinal velocity is
\begin{equation}
v_\parallel^{\mathrm{IR}}
=
\frac12\,\alpha_X L_* I_{\theta'^3},
\label{eq:vpar_LT}
\end{equation}
and the transverse velocity is
\begin{equation}
v_\perp^{\mathrm{IR}}
=
|\beta_X I_\theta|\,R_\perp.
\label{eq:vperp_LT}
\end{equation}
Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\rho
=
\frac{v_\parallel^{\mathrm{IR}}}{v_\perp^{\mathrm{IR}}}
=
\frac{\alpha_X}{\beta_X}\,
\frac{L_*}{2R_\perp}\,
\frac{I_{\theta'^3}}{I_\theta},
}
\label{eq:rho_LT}
\end{equation}
up to the overall sign convention.

In the small-defect regime,
\[
I_{\theta'^3}\sim \frac{3}{16}(\theta_0\kappa)^2 I_\theta,
\]
so
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\rho_{\mathrm{LO}}
=
\frac{3}{32}\,
\frac{\alpha_X}{\beta_X}\,
\frac{L_*}{R_\perp}\,
(\theta_0\kappa)^2.
}
\label{eq:rho_LO_LT}
\end{equation}

Therefore the entire anisotropy prediction is reduced to the finite ratio
\[
\frac{L_*}{R_\perp}.
\]

\section{What is proved, what is assumed}

At this point the honest status is:

\paragraph{Proved algebraically.}
If the microscopic Class II branch reduces to the minimal explicit canonical split, then the entire shell witness problem is equivalent to the finite matching condition

L_*\neq 0,\qquad R_\perp>0.

\paragraph{Not yet computed microscopically.}

\paragraph{Therefore.}

It is the explicit coefficient-matching computation of the three scalar combinations above.

=

(\theta_0\kappa)^2.

\section{Full detailed LaTeX derivation}

\begin{equation}

\qquad

\label{eq:min_split}
\end{equation}
Then the shell-seed coefficients become
\begin{equation}

\qquad

\qquad

Using the exact seed dictionary,
\begin{equation}
