\section{Actual Microscopic Coefficient Extraction in the Finite Coefficient-Matching Stage}

\subsection{Goal}

The remaining microscopic task is to extract the three shell coefficients
\[
\lambda_\parallel,\qquad \alpha,\qquad \beta
\]
from the projected first derivative of the actual Bloch-linearized microscopic operator.

Equivalently, the extraction chain is
\[
L_{\mathrm{mic}}
\;\longrightarrow\;
L_{\mathrm{Bloch}}(k)
\;\longrightarrow\;
K_i:=\partial_{k_i}L_{\mathrm{Bloch}}(k)\big|_{k=k_*}
\;\longrightarrow\;
P_*K_iP_*
\;\longrightarrow\;
(\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta).
\]

This is precisely the finite operator audit form of the remaining TECT microscopic frontier.

\subsection{Folded Bragg convention}

We work in the folded Bloch convention
\[
k_*= \frac{G_*}{2},
\qquad
k=k_*+p,
\qquad
|p|\ll |G_*|.
\]
Let the shell-adapted frame be
\[
\hat n=\frac{G_*}{|G_*|},
\qquad
\{e_1,e_2,\hat n\}\ \text{orthonormal},
\]
and decompose
\[
p=p_\parallel \hat n + p_1 e_1 + p_2 e_2.
\]

Let
\[
P_*
\]
denote the rank-two projector onto the shell-relevant Bloch valley subspace.
Then the projected first-order symbol is
\[
A_1(p)=P_*\bigl(L_{\mathrm{Bloch}}(k_*+p)-L_{\mathrm{Bloch}}(k_*)\bigr)P_*+O(|p|^2).
\]

\subsection{Projected derivative matrices}

Define
\[
K_i:=\partial_{k_i}L_{\mathrm{Bloch}}(k)\big|_{k=k_*},
\qquad
M_i:=P_*K_iP_*.
\]
Then
\[
A_1(p)=p_i M_i + O(|p|^2).
\]
In the shell-adapted basis, write
\[
M_\parallel := \hat n_i M_i,
\qquad
M_1 := e_{1i}M_i,
\qquad
M_2 := e_{2i}M_i.
\]

The reduced S2 branch has the universal form
\[
A_1(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\alpha(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2).
\]
Hence the coefficients are extracted by Pauli traces:
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac12 \Tr(\sigma_3 M_\parallel),
\label{eq:actual_lambda_trace}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\alpha
=
\frac12 \Tr(\sigma_1 M_1)
=
\frac12 \Tr(\sigma_2 M_2),
\label{eq:actual_alpha_trace}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\beta
=
\frac12 \Tr(\sigma_2 M_1)
=
-\frac12 \Tr(\sigma_1 M_2).
\label{eq:actual_beta_trace}
\end{equation}

Therefore the entire nondegeneracy problem is reduced to finite projector-trace contractions.

\subsection{Concrete Class II microscopic branch}

Take as working microscopic branch
\begin{equation}
L_{\mathrm{mic}}
=
L_{\Psi}^{\mathrm{ref}}[\Psi,P]
+
\frac{M_X^2}{2}X_i^aX_i^a
+
\alpha_X X_i^a J_i^a[\Psi]
+
\beta_X X_i^a K_i^a[P,\psi].
\label{eq:actual_classII_branch}
\end{equation}
Integrating out the heavy mediator \(X_i^a\) at quadratic order gives the effective enriched transport contribution
\begin{equation}
\delta L_{\mathrm{eff}}^{(II)}
\sim
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,J_i^a K_i^a.
\label{eq:classII_eff_schematic}
\end{equation}
At shell-reduced level, this generates the enriched microscopic tensor
\[
\delta N_{ij}^a.
\]

Inside the shell-adapted seed family one has
\begin{equation}
N_{ij}^3=A\,\hat n_i\hat n_j,
\qquad
N_{ij}^1=B\,\hat n_i e_{1j}+C\,\hat n_i e_{2j},
\qquad
N_{ij}^2=-C\,\hat n_i e_{1j}+B\,\hat n_i e_{2j}.
\label{eq:axial_seed_family_actual}
\end{equation}
For the explicit Class II reduction,
\begin{equation}
\delta A=-\Gamma c_\parallel,
\qquad
\delta B=-\Gamma c_I,
\qquad
\delta C=-\Gamma c_J,
\qquad
\Gamma=\frac{\lambda g_X m}{M_X^2},
\label{eq:deltaABC_actual}
\end{equation}
so that
\[
g_c\propto c_\parallel,
\qquad
g_E\propto c_I,
\qquad
g_O\propto c_J.
\]

Therefore the shell coefficients become
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel
=
\kappa_*|G_*|\,\hat n_i\hat n_j N_{ij}^3,
\label{eq:lambda_N_match_actual}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\alpha
=
\frac{\kappa_*|G_*|}{2}
\Bigl(
e_{1j}\hat n_i N_{ij}^1 + e_{2j}\hat n_i N_{ij}^2
\Bigr),
\label{eq:alpha_N_match_actual}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\beta
=
\frac{\kappa_*|G_*|}{2}
\Bigl(
e_{2j}\hat n_i N_{ij}^1 - e_{1j}\hat n_i N_{ij}^2
\Bigr).
\label{eq:beta_N_match_actual}
\end{equation}
Substituting \eqref{eq:axial_seed_family_actual} gives
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel
=
\kappa_*|G_*|\,A,
\qquad
\alpha
=
\kappa_*|G_*|\,B,
\qquad
\beta
=
\kappa_*|G_*|\,C.
\label{eq:ABC_to_lab_actual}
\end{equation}
Hence, after the Class II correction,
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel^{(II)}\propto c_\parallel,
\qquad
\alpha^{(II)}\propto c_I,
\qquad
\beta^{(II)}\propto c_J.
\label{eq:classII_seed_to_coeffs}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Identification with the finite invariants}

Now compare the general finite-coefficient dictionary
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\frac12 \alpha_X L_* I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=\beta_X I_\theta T_E,
\qquad
\beta=\beta_X I_\theta T_O,
\]
with the concrete Class II witness formulas
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{g_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=g_E I_\theta,
\qquad
\beta=g_O I_\theta.
\]
This gives the exact identification
\begin{equation}
g_c=\alpha_X L_*,
\qquad
g_E=\beta_X T_E,
\qquad
g_O=\beta_X T_O.
\label{eq:g_to_LstarTE_actual}
\end{equation}
Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
L_*=\frac{g_c}{\alpha_X},
\qquad
T_E=\frac{g_E}{\beta_X},
\qquad
T_O=\frac{g_O}{\beta_X}.
\label{eq:LstarTE_from_g_actual}
\end{equation}

Inside the minimal canonical split,
\[
L_*=m_\parallel u_\parallel,
\qquad
T_E=\xi_E v_E,
\qquad
T_O=\xi_O v_O.
\]
So the actual microscopic coefficient audit reduces to computing
\[
g_c,\qquad g_E,\qquad g_O,
\]
or equivalently the projected traces \eqref{eq:actual_lambda_trace}--\eqref{eq:actual_beta_trace}.

\subsection{Explicit concrete normalization}

In the exact concrete Class II transport normalization one has
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,g_c\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
\label{eq:lambda_gc_exact_actual}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,g_E\,\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,g_O\,\theta_0\kappa.
\label{eq:alpha_beta_gE_gO_exact_actual}
\end{equation}
Therefore
\begin{equation}
g_c
=
-\frac{512}{3\sqrt3\pi\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3}\,\lambda_\parallel,
\label{eq:gc_from_lambda_actual}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
g_E
=
-\frac{16}{\sqrt3\pi\,\theta_0\kappa}\,\alpha,
\qquad
g_O
=
-\frac{16}{\sqrt3\pi\,\theta_0\kappa}\,\beta.
\label{eq:gEgO_from_alpha_beta_actual}
\end{equation}
Combining with \eqref{eq:LstarTE_from_g_actual},
\begin{equation}
L_*
=
-\frac{512}{3\sqrt3\pi\,\alpha_X\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3}\,\lambda_\parallel,
\label{eq:Lstar_from_lambda_actual}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
T_E
=
-\frac{16}{\sqrt3\pi\,\beta_X\,\theta_0\kappa}\,\alpha,
\qquad
T_O
=
-\frac{16}{\sqrt3\pi\,\beta_X\,\theta_0\kappa}\,\beta.
\label{eq:TE_TO_from_alphabeta_actual}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Weyl condition in the actual extraction form}

The local Weyl condition becomes
\begin{equation}
L_*\neq 0,
\qquad
R_\perp:=\sqrt{T_E^2+T_O^2}>0.
\label{eq:weyl_actual_LstarTE}
\end{equation}
Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
g_c\neq 0,
\qquad
(g_E,g_O)\neq (0,0),
\label{eq:weyl_actual_gs}
\end{equation}
or, in seed variables,
\begin{equation}
c_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(c_I,c_J)\neq (0,0).
\label{eq:weyl_actual_seed}
\end{equation}

Thus the actual microscopic finite coefficient-matching program is closed at the protocol level:
\[
\boxed{
L_{\mathrm{Bloch}}(k)
\to
K_i
\to
P_*K_iP_*
\to
(\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta)
\to
(g_c,g_E,g_O)
\to
(L_*,T_E,T_O).
}
\]

\subsection{What is closed and what remains open}

What is closed rigorously is the extraction protocol and the exact dictionary:
\[
(\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta)
\Longleftrightarrow
(g_c,g_E,g_O)
\Longleftrightarrow
(L_*,T_E,T_O).
\]

What remains open is only the final explicit computation of
\[
K_i=\partial_{k_i}L_{\mathrm{Bloch}}(k)\big|_{k=k_*}
\]
from the final complete microscopic TECT operator, and the direct evaluation of the projected traces
\[
\frac12\Tr(\sigma_3 M_\parallel),
\qquad
\frac12\Tr(\sigma_1 M_1),
\qquad
\frac12\Tr(\sigma_2 M_1).
\]

\section{Final Summary}

The finite coefficient-matching problem is now reduced to the explicit shell-projected derivative audit
\[
M_i=P_*K_iP_*,
\qquad
K_i=\partial_{k_i}L_{\mathrm{Bloch}}(k)\big|_{k=k_*}.
\]
The three actual microscopic Dirac coefficients are
\[
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac12\Tr(\sigma_3 M_\parallel),
\qquad
\alpha
=
\frac12\Tr(\sigma_1 M_1),
\qquad
\beta
=
\frac12\Tr(\sigma_2 M_1).
\]
Inside the concrete Class II realization,
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{g_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=g_E I_\theta,
\qquad
\beta=g_O I_\theta,
\]
with
\[
g_c\propto c_\parallel,
\qquad
g_E\propto c_I,
\qquad
g_O\propto c_J.
\]
Hence
\[
L_*=\frac{g_c}{\alpha_X},
\qquad
T_E=\frac{g_E}{\beta_X},
\qquad
T_O=\frac{g_O}{\beta_X}.
\]
Therefore the remaining TECT microscopic frontier is no longer structural.
It is the explicit computation of the projected Bloch derivative matrices \(M_i\), after which the Weyl/Dirac condition is the finite test
\[
L_*\neq 0,
\qquad
\sqrt{T_E^2+T_O^2}>0.
\]

\section{Finite coefficient-matching: exact current status}

The microscopic Dirac problem is reduced to the shell-projected derivative data
\[
M_i=P_*K_iP_*,
\qquad
K_i=\partial_{k_i}L_{\mathrm{Bloch}}(k)\big|_{k=k_*}.
\]
The extracted coefficients are
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\frac12\Tr(\sigma_3 M_\parallel),
\qquad
\alpha=\frac12\Tr(\sigma_1 M_1),
\qquad
\beta=\frac12\Tr(\sigma_2 M_1).
\]
In the concrete Class II branch,
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{g_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=g_E I_\theta,
\qquad
\beta=g_O I_\theta,
\]
and
\[
g_c\propto c_\parallel,
\qquad
g_E\propto c_I,
\qquad
g_O\propto c_J.
\]
Therefore
\[
L_*=\frac{g_c}{\alpha_X},
\qquad
T_E=\frac{g_E}{\beta_X},
\qquad
T_O=\frac{g_O}{\beta_X},
\]
so the Weyl condition is the finite test
\[
L_*\neq 0,
\qquad
\sqrt{T_E^2+T_O^2}>0.
\]
What remains open is only the direct explicit computation of \(K_i\) from the final complete microscopic TECT operator.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Shell-Adapted Block Construction of the Projected Bloch Derivative}

\subsection{Goal}

The next legitimate microscopic step is to construct the first Bloch-derivative block
\[
K_i:=\partial_{k_i}L_{\mathrm{Bloch}}(k)\big|_{k=k_*}
\]
in a shell-adapted basis and then to project it to the selected local valley subspace.

This is exactly the finite operator-construction stage:
\[
L_{\mathrm{Bloch}}(k)
\;\to\;
K_i
\;\to\;
P_*K_iP_*
\;\to\;
(\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta).
\]

\subsection{Folded Bragg convention}

We use the folded Bragg convention
\[
k_*=\frac{G_*}{2},
\qquad
k=k_*+p,
\qquad
|p|\ll |G_*|.
\]
Choose the shell-adapted orthonormal frame
\[
\hat n=\frac{G_*}{|G_*|},
\qquad
\{e_1,e_2,\hat n\}.
\]
Then
\[
p=p_\parallel \hat n+p_1 e_1+p_2 e_2,
\]
with
\[
p_\parallel=\hat n_i p_i,
\qquad
p_a=e_{ai}p_i,\quad a=1,2.
\]

\subsection{First-order Bloch expansion}

Assume the Bloch symbol admits the Taylor expansion
\[
L_{\mathrm{Bloch}}(k_*+p)
=
L_*+p_iK_i+O(|p|^2),
\qquad
K_i=\partial_{k_i}L_{\mathrm{Bloch}}(k)\big|_{k=k_*}.
\]
Then the selected local valley block is
\[
h_{\mathrm{lin}}^+(p)
=
P_*(p_iK_i)P_*.
\]
Since the projected block is \(2\times2\) Hermitian, it has the Pauli expansion
\[
h_{\mathrm{lin}}^+(p)=M_{\mu i}p_i\sigma_\mu,
\qquad
M_{\mu i}
=
\frac12\Tr_{H_*}(\sigma_\mu P_*K_iP_*).
\]

\subsection{Minimal shell-enriched axial ansatz}

The correct shell-adapted first-derivative ansatz is the axial \(A,B,C\) decomposition:
\begin{equation}
K_i
=
A\,\hat n_i\,\tau^3\otimes \mathbf 1_2
+
B\,(e_{1i}\tau^1\otimes s_1+e_{2i}\tau^1\otimes s_2)
+
C\,(-e_{2i}\tau^1\otimes s_1+e_{1i}\tau^1\otimes s_2).
\label{eq:Ki_ABC_shell}
\end{equation}
This is exactly the minimal shell-enriched axial form that separates:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the longitudinal singlet coefficient \(A\),
\item the transverse even coefficient \(B\),
\item the transverse odd coefficient \(C\).
\end{enumerate}

\subsection{Directional components}

Contracting \eqref{eq:Ki_ABC_shell} with the shell frame gives
\begin{equation}
K_\parallel:=\hat n_iK_i=A\,\tau^3\otimes \mathbf 1_2,
\label{eq:Kparallel_shell}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
K_1:=e_{1i}K_i
=
B\,\tau^1\otimes s_1
+
C\,\tau^1\otimes s_2,
\label{eq:K1_shell}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
K_2:=e_{2i}K_i
=
-C\,\tau^1\otimes s_1
+
B\,\tau^1\otimes s_2.
\label{eq:K2_shell}
\end{equation}

Therefore the full first-order symbol is
\begin{align}
p_iK_i
&=
p_\parallel K_\parallel+p_1K_1+p_2K_2
\nonumber\\
&=
A\,p_\parallel\,\tau^3\otimes \mathbf 1_2
+
B\,(p_1\tau^1\otimes s_1+p_2\tau^1\otimes s_2)
+
C\,(-p_2\tau^1\otimes s_1+p_1\tau^1\otimes s_2).
\label{eq:piKi_shell}
\end{align}

\subsection{Valley projection}

Project to the selected two-band valley block with projector \(P_*\), using the reduced identifications
\[
P_*(\tau^3\otimes \mathbf 1_2)P_*\mapsto \sigma^3,
\qquad
P_*(\tau^1\otimes s_1)P_*\mapsto \sigma^1,
\qquad
P_*(\tau^1\otimes s_2)P_*\mapsto \sigma^2.
\]
Then \eqref{eq:piKi_shell} becomes
\begin{equation}
h_+^{\mathrm{lin}}(p)
=
A\,p_\parallel \sigma^3
+
B\,(p_1\sigma^1+p_2\sigma^2)
+
C\,(-p_2\sigma^1+p_1\sigma^2).
\label{eq:hplus_ABC_final}
\end{equation}

Comparing with the universal S2 witness form
\[
H_{\mathrm{wit}}(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\alpha(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2),
\]
we read off immediately
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=A,
\qquad
\alpha=B,
\qquad
\beta=C.
}
\label{eq:ABC_equals_witness}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Equivalent Pauli-trace extraction}

The same result follows from the projector-trace formulas.
From \eqref{eq:Kparallel_shell}--\eqref{eq:K2_shell},
\[
P_*K_\parallel P_*=A\sigma^3,
\qquad
P_*K_1P_*=B\sigma^1+C\sigma^2,
\qquad
P_*K_2P_*=-C\sigma^1+B\sigma^2.
\]
Hence
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac12\Tr(\sigma^3P_*K_\parallel P_*)
=
A,
\label{eq:lambda_trace_A}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\alpha
=
\frac12\Tr(\sigma^1P_*K_1P_*)
=
\frac12\Tr(\sigma^2P_*K_2P_*)
=
B,
\label{eq:alpha_trace_B}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\beta
=
\frac12\Tr(\sigma^2P_*K_1P_*)
=
-\frac12\Tr(\sigma^1P_*K_2P_*)
=
C.
\label{eq:beta_trace_C}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Weyl nondegeneracy matrix}

The coefficient matrix in the shell frame is therefore
\begin{equation}
M=
\begin{pmatrix}
B & -C & 0\\
C & B & 0\\
0 & 0 & A
\end{pmatrix},
\label{eq:M_ABC_matrix}
\end{equation}
so that
\begin{equation}
\det M = A(B^2+C^2).
\label{eq:detM_ABC}
\end{equation}
Therefore the exact local Weyl condition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A\neq 0,
\qquad
(B,C)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:Weyl_ABC}
\end{equation}
Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:Weyl_lambda_alpha_beta}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Dictionary to the finite coefficient-matching variables}

In the finite coefficient-matching language,
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\frac12\alpha_XL_*I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=\beta_XI_\theta T_E,
\qquad
\beta=\beta_XI_\theta T_O.
\]
Hence \eqref{eq:ABC_equals_witness} gives
\begin{equation}
A=\frac12\alpha_XL_*I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
B=\beta_XI_\theta T_E,
\qquad
C=\beta_XI_\theta T_O.
\label{eq:ABC_LTEO}
\end{equation}
Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
L_*=\frac{2A}{\alpha_XI_{\theta'^3}},
\qquad
T_E=\frac{B}{\beta_XI_\theta},
\qquad
T_O=\frac{C}{\beta_XI_\theta}.
\label{eq:LTEO_from_ABC}
\end{equation}

Inside the concrete Class II branch, one already has
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{g_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=g_EI_\theta,
\qquad
\beta=g_OI_\theta,
\]
so
\begin{equation}
A=\frac{g_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
B=g_EI_\theta,
\qquad
C=g_OI_\theta.
\label{eq:ABC_g_dictionary}
\end{equation}
Thus
\begin{equation}
g_c\neq 0,
\qquad
(g_E,g_O)\neq (0,0)
\end{equation}
is exactly the same condition as
\[
A\neq 0,
\qquad
(B,C)\neq (0,0).
\]

\subsection{What is now closed}

The following step is now rigorously closed:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the shell-adapted first-derivative block \(K_i\) has the exact \(A,B,C\) decomposition;
\item the directional blocks \(K_\parallel,K_1,K_2\) are explicit;
\item after valley projection, the reduced Bloch Hamiltonian is exactly
\[
h_+^{\mathrm{lin}}(p)
=
A\,p_\parallel \sigma^3
+
B\,(p_1\sigma^1+p_2\sigma^2)
+
C\,(-p_2\sigma^1+p_1\sigma^2);
\]
\item therefore
\[
\lambda_\parallel=A,\qquad \alpha=B,\qquad \beta=C;
\]
\item the local Weyl test is the finite condition
\[
A\neq 0,\qquad (B,C)\neq (0,0).
\]
\end{enumerate}

\subsection{What remains open}

What remains open is not the shell-reduced logic.
It is only the explicit computation of the actual microscopic numbers
\[
A,\qquad B,\qquad C
\]
from the final complete periodic refined locked + Class II Bloch operator.
Equivalently, one must compute
\[
K_i=\partial_{k_i}L_{\mathrm{Bloch}}(k)\big|_{k=k_*}
\]
for the actual microscopic branch and then evaluate the projected traces.

\section{Shell-adapted Bloch block: exact result}

The first projected Bloch derivative is written in the axial shell form
\[
K_i
=
A\,\hat n_i\,\tau^3\otimes \mathbf 1_2
+
B\,(e_{1i}\tau^1\otimes s_1+e_{2i}\tau^1\otimes s_2)
+
C\,(-e_{2i}\tau^1\otimes s_1+e_{1i}\tau^1\otimes s_2).
\]
Hence
\[
K_\parallel=A\,\tau^3\otimes \mathbf 1_2,
\qquad
K_1=B\,\tau^1\otimes s_1+C\,\tau^1\otimes s_2,
\qquad
K_2=-C\,\tau^1\otimes s_1+B\,\tau^1\otimes s_2.
\]
After projection to the selected two-band valley block,
\[
h_+^{\mathrm{lin}}(p)
=
A\,p_\parallel \sigma^3
+
B\,(p_1\sigma^1+p_2\sigma^2)
+
C\,(-p_2\sigma^1+p_1\sigma^2).
\]
Therefore
\[
\lambda_\parallel=A,\qquad
\alpha=B,\qquad
\beta=C,
\]
and the exact local Weyl condition is
\[
A\neq 0,\qquad (B,C)\neq (0,0).
\]
Equivalently,
\[
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0,\qquad
(\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0).
\]
Thus the remaining microscopic problem is only to compute the actual values of
\[
A,\qquad B,\qquad C
\]
from the final periodic refined locked + Class II Bloch operator.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{12-Mode BCC Bloch Matrix in the Shell-Restricted Mode Basis}

\subsection{Goal}

The correct next step is to write the periodic Bloch operator explicitly in the
reciprocal-harmonic basis of the locked 12-mode BCC background, isolate the
Bragg-resonant finite block at
\[
k_*= \frac{G_*}{2},
\]
and identify the reduced \(2\times 2\) valley operator.

This is the actual finite-dimensional matrix stage of the microscopic program:
\[
\Psi_0
\;\to\;
H_{\mathrm{Bloch}}(k)
\;\to\;
H_{\mathrm{Bragg}}(k_*+p)
\;\to\;
H_{\mathrm{shell}}(p)
\;\to\;
(\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta).
\]

\subsection{Locked 12-mode BCC background}

Take the first BCC reciprocal shell
\[
\mathcal S_{12}
=
\frac{q_*}{\sqrt2}
\left\{
(\pm1,\pm1,0),\,
(\pm1,0,\pm1),\,
(0,\pm1,\pm1)
\right\},
\qquad
|\mathcal S_{12}|=12.
\]
The equal-amplitude locked background is
\[
\phi_0(x)=A\sum_{Q\in \mathcal S_{12}}e^{iQ\cdot x}
=
2A\sum_{\alpha=1}^{6}\cos(Q_\alpha\cdot x),
\]
and
\[
\Psi_0(x)=z_0\,\phi_0(x),
\qquad
P_0=z_0z_0^\dagger.
\]

\subsection{Bloch-harmonic expansion}

For a Bloch quasimomentum \(k\), expand the fluctuation in reciprocal harmonics:
\[
\delta\Psi_k(x)
=
e^{ik\cdot x}\sum_{G\in \mathcal G}\psi_G\,e^{iG\cdot x},
\]
where \(\mathcal G\) is the reciprocal lattice generated by the BCC background.
Then the Bloch fiber acts on the coefficient vector \((\psi_G)\) by
\begin{equation}
\bigl(H_{\mathrm{Bloch}}(k)\bigr)_{G,G'}
=
h_{\mathrm{diag}}(k+G)\,\delta_{G,G'}
+
V_{G-G'}.
\label{eq:HBloch_general}
\end{equation}
Here:

\begin{enumerate}
\item \(h_{\mathrm{diag}}(q)\) is the diagonal bare/refined kinetic symbol;
\item \(V_K\) are the Fourier coefficients of the periodic linearized background potential / transport kernel.
\end{enumerate}

For the scalar periodic Hessian this reduces to the standard formula
\[
\bigl(H_{\mathrm{Bloch}}(k)\bigr)_{G,G'}
=
h_0(k+G)\delta_{G,G'}+U_{G-G'},
\]
and the same reciprocal-convolution structure persists in the refined locked + Class II branch, only with matrix-valued internal blocks replacing the scalar coefficients.

\subsection{The Bragg-resonant shell pair}

Fix one selected shell vector \(G_*\in \mathcal S_{12}\).
The Bragg crossing occurs at
\[
k_*= \frac{G_*}{2}.
\]
The two directly resonant harmonics are
\[
|+\rangle := |G=0\rangle,
\qquad
|-\rangle := |G=-G_*\rangle,
\]
since
\[
k_*+0=\frac{G_*}{2},
\qquad
k_*-G_*=-\frac{G_*}{2},
\]
and therefore the two bare momenta have equal norm.

In the locked triplet branch there is also a reduced internal doublet
\[
u_1,\ u_2 \in Q_{z_0},
\qquad
u_r^\dagger u_s=\delta_{rs},
\]
so the shell-relevant local carrier space is
\[
\mathcal H_D
\cong
\mathrm{span}\{|+\rangle,|-\rangle\}
\otimes
\mathrm{span}\{u_1,u_2\}
\cong
\mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{valley}}\otimes \mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{int}}.
\]

A convenient ordered basis is
\[
\mathcal B_D=
\{
|+,u_1\rangle,\ |+,u_2\rangle,\ |-,u_1\rangle,\ |-,u_2\rangle
\}.
\]

\subsection{The finite \(4\times 4\) Bragg block}

Restrict the full Bloch fiber to \(\mathcal H_D\).
Then the shell-relevant Bragg block has the form
\begin{equation}
H_D(k)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
E_+(k)\,\mathbf 1_2 + A_+(k) & M(k) \\
M(k)^\dagger & E_-(k)\,\mathbf 1_2 + A_-(k)
\end{pmatrix},
\label{eq:HD_4x4_general}
\end{equation}
where:

\begin{enumerate}
\item \(E_\pm(k)\) are the diagonal bare dispersions at \(k\) and \(k-G_*\);
\item \(A_\pm(k)\) are internal \(2\times2\) self-block corrections coming from the refined locked/Class II linearization;
\item \(M(k)\) is the \(2\times2\) pair-mixing block induced by the Fourier coefficient at momentum transfer \(G_*\) and its enriched transport corrections.
\end{enumerate}

At the exact Bragg point \(k_*=G_*/2\),
\[
E_+(k_*)=E_-(k_*),
\]
so the nontrivial shell question is controlled by the off-diagonal and first-order derivative structure.

\subsection{Decomposition of the pair-mixing block}

Write the \(2\times2\) pair-mixing block as
\begin{equation}
M(k)=M_0(k)\,\mathbf 1_2 + M_a(k)\,s_a,
\qquad a=1,2,3.
\label{eq:Mk_decomp}
\end{equation}
At \(k=k_*\), the constant scalar piece
\[
M_0:=M_0(k_*)
\]
is the constant Bragg mass obstruction.
For a naive quadratic scalar periodic coefficient
\[
U_{\mathrm{quad}}(x)=u_2\phi_0(x)^2,
\]
its selected-shell Fourier coefficient is
\[
\widehat U_{\mathrm{quad}}(G_*)=4u_2A^2,
\]
hence
\begin{equation}
M_0^{\mathrm{quad}}=4u_2A^2\,\mathbf 1_2\neq 0
\label{eq:M0_quad_obstruction}
\end{equation}
generically.

Therefore a direct Dirac crossing requires an actual microscopic cancellation, symmetry, or protected elimination of this constant scalar pair-mixing piece.

\subsection{Linear expansion around the Bragg point}

Now set
\[
k=k_*+p,
\qquad
p=p_\parallel \hat n + p_1 e_1+p_2 e_2,
\qquad
\hat n=\frac{G_*}{|G_*|}.
\]
Expand the shell block to first order:
\begin{equation}
H_D(k_*+p)
=
H_D(k_*)
+
p_i K_i
+
O(|p|^2),
\label{eq:HD_expand}
\end{equation}
with
\[
K_i=\partial_{k_i}H_D(k)\big|_{k=k_*}.
\]

Inside the shell-adapted reduced branch, the first-order part has the universal axial form
\begin{equation}
K_i
=
A\,\hat n_i\,\tau_3\otimes \mathbf 1_2
+
B\,(e_{1i}\tau_1\otimes s_1+e_{2i}\tau_1\otimes s_2)
+
C\,(-e_{2i}\tau_1\otimes s_1+e_{1i}\tau_1\otimes s_2).
\label{eq:Ki_ABC_again}
\end{equation}
Hence
\begin{equation}
p_iK_i
=
A\,p_\parallel \tau_3\otimes \mathbf 1_2
+
B\,(p_1\tau_1\otimes s_1+p_2\tau_1\otimes s_2)
+
C\,(-p_2\tau_1\otimes s_1+p_1\tau_1\otimes s_2).
\label{eq:piKi_again}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Reduced \(2\times2\) valley block}

After projection to the selected two-band valley branch,
\[
\tau_3\otimes \mathbf 1_2 \mapsto \sigma_3,
\qquad
\tau_1\otimes s_1 \mapsto \sigma_1,
\qquad
\tau_1\otimes s_2 \mapsto \sigma_2,
\]
and one gets
\begin{equation}
h_{\mathrm{val}}(p)
=
M_0\,\mathbf 1_2
+
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\alpha(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2)
+
O(|p|^2),
\label{eq:hval_final}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel=A,
\qquad
\alpha=B,
\qquad
\beta=C.
\label{eq:ABC_equals_lab}
\end{equation}

Therefore the exact local Weyl condition is
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0),
\label{eq:weyl_reduced_again}
\end{equation}
while the exact local Dirac crossing also requires
\begin{equation}
M_0=0.
\label{eq:M0_zero_requirement}
\end{equation}

\subsection{What the 12-mode locked branch already gives}

In the locked equal-amplitude 12-mode BCC shell-sum calculation, the shell-projected witnesses are
\begin{equation}
W_\parallel^{(12)}=4\,\frac{gA^2}{q_*^2},
\qquad
W_I^{(12)}=\frac{4Z}{A},
\qquad
W_J^{(12)}=0.
\label{eq:W12_again}
\end{equation}
Thus the reduced witness determinant is
\begin{equation}
\det M^{(12)}=64\,\kappa_*\,g\,Z^2\,q_*>0.
\label{eq:detM12_again}
\end{equation}
So the witness survives the genuine 12-mode shell sum:
\[
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0)
\]
in this working branch.

However, this does not by itself prove the full unrestricted microscopic theorem, because:
\[
\text{polarization locking is still assumed,}
\qquad
\text{and the full multi-mode projector/BdG linearization is still open.}
\]

\subsection{Exact status of the matrix construction}

The finite shell-relevant matrix problem is now completely identified:

\begin{enumerate}
\item build the Bloch matrix \(H_{\mathrm{Bloch}}(k)\) in the reciprocal-harmonic basis;
\item restrict it to the resonant \(4\times 4\) shell block \(\mathcal H_D\);
\item separate the constant scalar Bragg block \(M_0\mathbf 1_2\);
\item extract the first-order coefficients \((\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta)\).
\end{enumerate}

The reduced witness part is already structurally and, in the locked 12-mode branch, explicitly nondegenerate.
The true remaining microscopic bottleneck is therefore
\[
\boxed{
M_0=0.
}
\]

\section{Final Summary}

For the locked 12-mode BCC background, the periodic Bloch operator in the reciprocal-harmonic basis has the convolution form
\[
\bigl(H_{\mathrm{Bloch}}(k)\bigr)_{G,G'}
=
h_{\mathrm{diag}}(k+G)\delta_{G,G'}+V_{G-G'}.
\]
At the Bragg point
\[
k_*=\frac{G_*}{2},
\]
the shell-relevant local carrier space is
\[
\mathcal H_D\cong \mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{valley}}\otimes \mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{int}},
\]
giving a finite \(4\times4\) block
\[
H_D(k)=
\begin{pmatrix}
E_+(k)\mathbf 1_2+A_+(k) & M(k)\\
M(k)^\dagger & E_-(k)\mathbf 1_2+A_-(k)
\end{pmatrix}.
\]
Its reduced \(2\times2\) valley block has the form
\[
h_{\mathrm{val}}(p)
=
M_0\mathbf 1_2
+
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\alpha(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2)
+
O(|p|^2).
\]
Thus:
\[
\text{Weyl witness} \iff \lambda_\parallel\neq 0,\ (\alpha,\beta)\neq(0,0),
\]
while
\[
\text{actual ungapped crossing} \iff M_0=0
\]
in addition.

In the locked equal-amplitude 12-mode BCC branch one already has
\[
W_\parallel^{(12)}=4\frac{gA^2}{q_*^2},
\qquad
W_I^{(12)}=\frac{4Z}{A},
\qquad
W_J^{(12)}=0,
\]
hence
\[
\det M^{(12)}=64\,\kappa_* g Z^2 q_*>0.
\]
So the shell witness survives the first genuine 12-mode BCC shell sum.
The honest remaining microscopic obstruction is the constant scalar Bragg mass \(M_0\).

\section{12-mode BCC Bloch matrix: exact current stage}

The periodic Bloch operator over the locked 12-mode BCC background has the reciprocal-harmonic matrix form
\[
(H_{\mathrm{Bloch}}(k))_{G,G'}
=
h_{\mathrm{diag}}(k+G)\delta_{G,G'}+V_{G-G'}.
\]
At the Bragg point
\[
k_*=\frac{G_*}{2},
\]
the shell-relevant local space is
\[
\mathcal H_D\cong \mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{valley}}\otimes \mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{int}},
\]
so the finite shell block is \(4\times4\):
\[
H_D(k)=
\begin{pmatrix}
E_+(k)\mathbf 1_2+A_+(k) & M(k)\\
M(k)^\dagger & E_-(k)\mathbf 1_2+A_-(k)
\end{pmatrix}.
\]
Its reduced valley operator is
\[
h_{\mathrm{val}}(p)
=
M_0\mathbf 1_2
+
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\alpha(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2)
+
O(|p|^2).
\]
Hence the Weyl witness requires
\[
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0,\qquad (\alpha,\beta)\neq(0,0),
\]
while an actual ungapped crossing additionally requires
\[
M_0=0.
\]
In the locked equal-amplitude 12-mode BCC branch, one already finds
\[
W_\parallel^{(12)}=4\frac{gA^2}{q_*^2},\qquad
W_I^{(12)}=\frac{4Z}{A},\qquad
W_J^{(12)}=0,
\]
and therefore
\[
\det M^{(12)}=64\,\kappa_* g Z^2 q_*>0.
\]
So the witness survives the first genuine 12-mode shell sum.
The remaining microscopic bottleneck is the constant Bragg mass condition \(M_0=0\).

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Exact 12-Mode Convolution Law for the Constant Bragg Mass}

\subsection{Goal}

The true remaining obstruction in the plain shell-pair Bloch route is the constant scalar
identity-channel Bragg block
\[
M_0=B_0^{\mathrm{tot}}\mathbf 1_2.
\]
The task is therefore not to re-discuss the derivative witnesses, but to compute the exact
12-mode BCC convolution formula for \(B_0^{\mathrm{tot}}\) and isolate the precise cancellation law.

\subsection{Shell-relevant scalar sector}

Take the most general scalar periodic contribution built from the natural locked first-shell operators
\begin{equation}
U_{\mathrm{tot}}(x)
=
c_0\,\phi_0(x)^2
+
c_1\,|\nabla\phi_0(x)|^2
+
c_2\,\phi_0(x)(-\Delta)\phi_0(x),
\label{eq:Utot_scalar}
\end{equation}
where
\[
\phi_0(x)=A\sum_{Q\in S_{12}}e^{iQ\cdot x}
\]
is the equal-amplitude locked 12-mode BCC background.

The constant Bragg block at the selected shell pair \((0,-G_*)\) is controlled by the
selected-shell Fourier coefficient
\[
\widehat U_{\mathrm{tot}}(G_*).
\]

\subsection{Exact 12-mode BCC Fourier coefficients}

In the locked 12-mode BCC branch, the first-shell convolution factors are
\begin{equation}
\widehat{\phi_0^2}(G_*)=4A^2,
\label{eq:phi2hat}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\widehat{|\nabla\phi_0|^2}(G_*)=2q_*^2A^2,
\label{eq:gradphi2hat}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\widehat{\phi_0(-\Delta)\phi_0}(G_*)=4q_*^2A^2.
\label{eq:phiLapphihat}
\end{equation}
Therefore
\begin{align}
\widehat U_{\mathrm{tot}}(G_*)
&=
c_0\,\widehat{\phi_0^2}(G_*)
+
c_1\,\widehat{|\nabla\phi_0|^2}(G_*)
+
c_2\,\widehat{\phi_0(-\Delta)\phi_0}(G_*)
\nonumber\\
&=
4c_0A^2+2c_1q_*^2A^2+4c_2q_*^2A^2
\nonumber\\
&=
2A^2\bigl(2c_0+q_*^2c_1+2q_*^2c_2\bigr).
\label{eq:Uhat_Gstar_exact}
\end{align}

Hence the projected scalar Bragg block is exactly
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
B_0^{\mathrm{tot}}
=
2A^2\bigl(2c_0+q_*^2c_1+2q_*^2c_2\bigr)\mathbf 1_2.
}
\label{eq:B0tot_exact}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Exact cancellation condition}

The ungapped plain shell-pair crossing requires
\[
M_0=0
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
B_0^{\mathrm{tot}}=0.
\]
By \eqref{eq:B0tot_exact}, this is equivalent to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
2c_0+q_*^2c_1+2q_*^2c_2=0.
}
\label{eq:scalar_cancel_exact}
\end{equation}

So the constant Bragg-mass problem is reduced to a single finite linear relation among the
identity-channel scalar coefficients.

\subsection{Naive scalar square obstruction}

For the simplest scalar square sector
\[
U_{\mathrm{quad}}(x)=u_2\phi_0(x)^2,
\]
one gets
\begin{equation}
\widehat U_{\mathrm{quad}}(G_*)=4u_2A^2,
\qquad
M_0^{\mathrm{quad}}=4u_2A^2\mathbf 1_2\neq 0
\label{eq:naive_square_obstruction}
\end{equation}
generically.

Thus the cancellation \eqref{eq:scalar_cancel_exact} is not automatic even in the full 12-mode shell sum.

\subsection{Why canonical Class II does not solve this}

The canonical Class II correction lives in the traceless Pauli channel:
\[
\delta B_0^{\mathrm{Class\,II}}
\in
\mathrm{span}\{s_1,s_2,s_3\},
\]
so in the shell-pair block it contributes as
\[
\tau_1\otimes s_a
\quad\text{or}\quad
\tau_2\otimes s_a,
\]
not as
\[
\tau_1\otimes \mathbf 1_2.
\]
Since the identity and traceless channels are orthogonal,
\[
\Tr(\mathbf 1_2\,s_a)=0,
\]
canonical Class II cannot directly cancel the scalar identity-channel block
\[
B_0^{\mathrm{tot}}\tau_1\otimes \mathbf 1_2.
\]

Therefore:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Class II renormalizes the derivative witness sector }(A,B,C),
\text{ but does not eliminate }M_0.
}
\label{eq:classII_not_M0}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Only two logically distinct routes}

The reduced operator analysis leaves exactly two possibilities.

\paragraph{Route 1: direct identity-channel cancellation.}
Introduce an additional microscopic sector whose projected constant pair block contains
a nonzero identity component
\[
\delta M_0^{\mathrm{id}}
=
\delta m_0\,\mathbf 1_2+\delta\widetilde M_0,
\qquad
\delta m_0=-B_0^{\mathrm{tot}}.
\]
Then the total constant scalar block vanishes.

\paragraph{Route 2: graded \(2+2\) bypass.}
Instead of canceling \(M_0\) inside the plain scalar shell-pair block, pass to a \(J\)-graded
\(2+2\) first-order infrared sector. In that reduced operator,
\[
D_1(0)=0,
\]
so the dangerous constant scalar Bragg block is absent from the relevant principal Dirac operator
from the outset.

Hence the exact classification is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{identity-carrying mediator route}
\qquad\text{or}\qquad
\text{graded }2+2\text{ bypass route.}
}
\label{eq:two_routes_exact}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Spectator-assisted identity-channel cancellation}

A concrete identity-channel route is already visible at the effective level.
If a spectator sector produces a Schur-complement identity correction, the total scalar block becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
B_0^{\mathrm{tot}}
=
\Bigl[
4uA^2
-
\sum_{\eta\in S_{\mathrm{bi}}}
\frac{\widehat V(\eta)\,\overline{\widehat V(\eta+G_*)}}{\Delta_\eta}
\Bigr]\mathbf 1_2.
}
\label{eq:B0tot_spectator}
\end{equation}
In the equal-coupling diagonal approximation this reduces to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
4uA^2-\frac{4|v_1|^2}{\Delta_{\mathrm{sp}}}A^2=0,
}
\label{eq:B0tot_spectator_simple}
\end{equation}
equivalently
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u=\frac{|v_1|^2}{\Delta_{\mathrm{sp}}}.
}
\label{eq:simple_cancel_ratio}
\end{equation}

More generally, combining this with \eqref{eq:B0tot_exact} gives
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
2A^2\bigl(2c_0+q_*^2c_1+2q_*^2c_2\bigr)
-
\sum_{\eta,\zeta\in S_{\mathrm{bi}}}
\widehat V(\eta)(R_0)_{\eta\zeta}\overline{\widehat V(\zeta+G_*)}
=0.
}
\label{eq:general_cancel_law}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Honest logical status}

The exact 12-mode convolution law for the scalar Bragg block is now closed.
What is also closed is the negative result:
within the current safe scalar + canonical Class II library, the identity-channel obstruction
is not removed automatically.

Therefore the plain shell-pair route is no longer the unique mainline.
The honest decision tree is:

\[
\text{(A) add an identity-carrying sector and satisfy \eqref{eq:general_cancel_law},}
\]
or
\[
\text{(B) move to the graded }2+2\text{ bypass route.}
\]

\section{Final Summary}

For the locked equal-amplitude 12-mode BCC branch, the scalar identity-channel Bragg block is
\[
B_0^{\mathrm{tot}}
=
2A^2\bigl(2c_0+q_*^2c_1+2q_*^2c_2\bigr)\mathbf 1_2.
\]
Hence the exact cancellation condition is
\[
2c_0+q_*^2c_1+2q_*^2c_2=0.
\]
A naive scalar square sector gives instead
\[
M_0^{\mathrm{quad}}=4u_2A^2\mathbf 1_2\neq 0,
\]
so cancellation is not automatic.
Canonical Class II cannot solve this because it lives in the traceless Pauli channel and therefore
renormalizes \((A,B,C)\), not the identity-channel block \(M_0\).

Thus only two logically distinct routes remain:
\[
\text{identity-channel cancellation}
\quad\text{or}\quad
\text{graded }2+2\text{ bypass}.
\]
The first route is governed by the generalized exact law
\[
2A^2\bigl(2c_0+q_*^2c_1+2q_*^2c_2\bigr)
-
\sum_{\eta,\zeta\in S_{\mathrm{bi}}}
\widehat V(\eta)(R_0)_{\eta\zeta}\overline{\widehat V(\zeta+G_*)}
=0,
\]
while the second route avoids the scalar Bragg block at the principal infrared level.

\section{Exact status of the constant Bragg-mass problem}

In the locked 12-mode BCC branch, the scalar identity-channel Bragg block is exactly
\[
B_0^{\mathrm{tot}}
=
2A^2\bigl(2c_0+q_*^2c_1+2q_*^2c_2\bigr)\mathbf 1_2.
\]
Therefore the exact scalar cancellation condition is
\[
2c_0+q_*^2c_1+2q_*^2c_2=0.
\]

A naive scalar square sector gives
\[
M_0^{\mathrm{quad}}=4u_2A^2\mathbf 1_2\neq 0,
\]
so the cancellation is not automatic.

Canonical Class II corrections lie in the traceless Pauli channel and therefore renormalize the derivative witness sector \((A,B,C)\), but do not remove the scalar identity-channel obstruction \(M_0\).

Hence only two logically distinct routes remain:

\[
\text{(i) identity-channel cancellation,}
\qquad
\text{(ii) graded }2+2\text{ bypass.}
\]

A general identity-channel cancellation law is
\[
2A^2\bigl(2c_0+q_*^2c_1+2q_*^2c_2\bigr)
-
\sum_{\eta,\zeta\in S_{\mathrm{bi}}}
\widehat V(\eta)(R_0)_{\eta\zeta}\overline{\widehat V(\zeta+G_*)}
=0.
\]

Thus the plain shell-pair route is no longer conceptually open:
its exact bottleneck and its exact possible exits are now fully identified.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Actual Coefficient-Point Audit in the Graded \(2+2\) Mainline}

\subsection{Goal}

The plain scalar Bragg-pair route is no longer the correct mainline.
The correct mainline is the graded \(2+2\) bypass route, in which the relevant
principal infrared operator is
\[
D_1(p)=
\begin{pmatrix}
0 & A_1(p)\\
A_1(p)^\dagger & 0
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
A_1(p)=p_iM_i,
\]
with
\[
D_1(0)=0.
\]
Therefore the decisive remaining microscopic problem is not the cancellation of \(B_0\),
but the extraction of the actual coefficient point
\[
\boxed{
(\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)},\lambda_c,\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O).
}
\]

\subsection{Graded infrared sector and projector-defect carrier}

Let the actual local low-energy carrier be a graded four-dimensional sector
\[
K=K_+\oplus K_-,
\qquad
\dim_{\mathbb C}K_\pm=2,
\]
with grading involution
\[
J^\dagger=J,
\qquad
J^2=\mathbf 1,
\qquad
J|_{K_\pm}=\pm 1.
\]
Let
\[
\Pi_K
\]
be the spectral projector onto this isolated infrared sector.
Then
\[
D_{\mathrm{eff}}(p)
=
\Pi_K L(p)\Pi_K
=
D_1(p)+O(|p|^2),
\]
and the graded bypass hypothesis is
\[
JD_1(p)J^{-1}=-D_1(p).
\]
Hence in the \(J\)-graded basis,
\begin{equation}
D_1(p)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
0 & A_1(p)\\
A_1(p)^\dagger & 0
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
A_1(p)=p_iM_i.
\label{eq:graded_mainline_block}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Pauli decomposition of the mixed symbol}

Write the \(2\times2\) mixed symbol in Pauli form:
\begin{equation}
A_1(p)
=
\ell_0(p)\mathbf 1_2
+
\ell_a(p)\sigma_a,
\qquad
\ell_\alpha(p)=C_\alpha{}^i p_i,
\quad
\alpha=0,1,2,3.
\label{eq:Pauli_mixed_general}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
\det A_1(p)=-p_iG_{ij}p_j,
\qquad
G_{ij}
=
\sum_{a=1}^3 C_a{}^i C_a{}^j
-
C_0{}^i C_0{}^j.
\label{eq:Gij_general}
\end{equation}
So the exact graded nondegeneracy test is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
G_{ij}>0.
}
\label{eq:G_positive}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Natural local S2 branch}

For the actual local projector-defect geometry, the natural reduced branch is the S2 singlet\(\oplus\)doublet form:
\begin{equation}
A_1(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\alpha(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2).
\label{eq:S2_branch_form}
\end{equation}
Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\Lambda=
\begin{pmatrix}
\alpha & -\beta & 0\\
\beta & \alpha & 0\\
0 & 0 & \lambda_\parallel
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
\det\Lambda=\lambda_\parallel(\alpha^2+\beta^2).
\label{eq:S2_Lambda_matrix}
\end{equation}
Thus
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
G_{ij}>0
\iff
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:G_positive_S2}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Actual transport kernel from the full Hessian}

The actual microscopic task is to derive the background-dependent transport kernel
\[
V^\mu(\xi)
\]
from the full TECT Hessian.
Let the defect background be \(P_B(\xi)\), with
\[
Q_B(\xi)=(\mathbb C z_B(\xi))^\perp,
\qquad
\dim_{\mathbb C}Q_B=2.
\]
Choose an adapted local frame
\[
(e_1(\xi),e_2(\xi))
\]
of \(Q_B(\xi)\), where \(e_1\) is the defect-selected tangent direction and \(e_2\) is the orthogonal spectator direction.

The full microscopic quadratic response restricted to \(Q_B\) is
\begin{equation}
R_\xi^{\mathrm{act}}
=
\Pi_Q\,\mathcal R_\xi^{\mathrm{act}}\,\Pi_Q
\in \mathrm{End}(Q_B).
\label{eq:Ract_def}
\end{equation}
In the adapted frame,
\begin{equation}
R_\xi^{\mathrm{act}}
=
\begin{pmatrix}
r_{11}(\xi) & r_{12}(\xi)\\
\overline{r_{12}(\xi)} & r_{22}(\xi)
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
r_{11},r_{22}\in\mathbb R.
\label{eq:Ract_matrix}
\end{equation}
Its traceless part is
\begin{equation}
S_\xi^{\mathrm{act}}
=
R_\xi^{\mathrm{act}}
-\frac12\Tr(R_\xi^{\mathrm{act}})\mathbf 1_2
=
s_1(\xi)\sigma_1+s_2(\xi)\sigma_2+s_3(\xi)\sigma_3,
\label{eq:Sact_def}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
s_3(\xi)=\frac12\bigl(r_{11}(\xi)-r_{22}(\xi)\bigr),
\qquad
s_1(\xi)=\Re r_{12}(\xi),
\qquad
s_2(\xi)=-\Im r_{12}(\xi).
\label{eq:s123_from_rij}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Longitudinal coefficient-point split}

At the graded reduced level there are two longitudinal possibilities:

\paragraph{Branch A.}
The primitive longitudinal singlet survives directly:
\[
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}\neq 0.
\]

\paragraph{Branch B.}
The primitive singlet vanishes,
\[
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0,
\]
but the concrete Class II longitudinal channel survives through
\[
\lambda_c\neq 0.
\]

Therefore the exact longitudinal decision tree is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{(1) }\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}\stackrel{?}{\neq}0,
\qquad
\text{(2) if not, }\lambda_c\stackrel{?}{\neq}0.
}
\label{eq:longitudinal_tree}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Practical sufficient criterion for longitudinal survival}

The sharpest practical sufficient condition for a nonzero longitudinal singlet component is diagonal anisotropy of the actual \(Q_B\)-response:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
s_3(\xi)
=
\frac12
\Bigl(
\langle e_1,R_\xi^{\mathrm{act}}e_1\rangle
-
\langle e_2,R_\xi^{\mathrm{act}}e_2\rangle
\Bigr).
}
\label{eq:s3_diag_criterion}
\end{equation}
Hence a sufficient microscopic test is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
r_{11}(\xi)-r_{22}(\xi)\not\equiv 0
\Longrightarrow
s_3(\xi)\not\equiv 0
\Longrightarrow
J_\parallel^{(3)}\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:diag_anisotropy_test}
\end{equation}
This is the exact replacement of the old vague question
\[
\text{``does the complete microscopic linearization produce a longitudinal singlet?''}
\]

\subsection{Finite overlap formulas for the S2 coefficients}

Let \(f_\pm(\xi)\) denote the two graded low-mode profiles.
Then the actual local overlap formulas for the S2 coefficients are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\theta'(\xi)\,h_\parallel(\theta(\xi)),
}
\label{eq:lambda_overlap_actual}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
=
\frac12
\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,\theta'(\xi)\,
\bigl(h_{11}(\theta(\xi))+h_{22}(\theta(\xi))\bigr),
}
\label{eq:alpha_overlap_actual}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta
=
\frac12
\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,\theta'(\xi)\,
\bigl(h_{21}(\theta(\xi))-h_{12}(\theta(\xi))\bigr).
}
\label{eq:beta_overlap_actual}
\end{equation}
Thus the problem is reduced to deriving the coefficient functions
\[
h_\parallel(\theta),\quad
h_{11}(\theta),\quad
h_{12}(\theta),\quad
h_{21}(\theta),\quad
h_{22}(\theta)
\]
from the complete background-dependent TECT Hessian.

\subsection{Dictionary to the concrete Class II branch}

Inside the exact concrete Class II transport ansatz one has
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,g_c\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
\qquad
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,g_E\,\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,g_O\,\theta_0\kappa.
\label{eq:gcgego_dictionary}
\end{equation}
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
g_c\neq 0,
\qquad
(g_E,g_O)\neq (0,0)
}
\label{eq:g_nonzero_test}
\end{equation}
is exactly the same finite microscopic test as
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:lambda_alpha_beta_nonzero}
\end{equation}

Moreover, inside the minimal shell-adapted Class II seed family,
\[
g_c\propto c_\parallel,
\qquad
g_E\propto c_I,
\qquad
g_O\propto c_J.
\]
So explicit witness seeds already exist at the reduced level; what remains open is whether the full complete TECT action realizes them in the actual defect background.

\subsection{Coefficient-point audit protocol}

The full microscopic audit can now be written as the following finite protocol.

\paragraph{Step 1. Grading audit.}
Construct the isolated four-dimensional infrared sector \(K=K_+\oplus K_-\) and verify
\[
JD_1J^{-1}=-D_1.
\]

\paragraph{Step 2. Hessian-to-response audit.}
Compute the actual \(Q_B\)-response
\[
R_\xi^{\mathrm{act}}=\Pi_Q \mathcal R_\xi^{\mathrm{act}}\Pi_Q
\]
and extract
\[
s_1(\xi),\ s_2(\xi),\ s_3(\xi).
\]

\paragraph{Step 3. Longitudinal branch audit.}
Check:
\[
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}\stackrel{?}{\neq}0.
\]
If not, compute the concrete Class II longitudinal coefficient
\[
\lambda_c.
\]

\paragraph{Step 4. Transverse audit.}
Compute the transverse coefficients
\[
\Lambda_E,\qquad \Lambda_O
\]
or equivalently
\[
g_E,\qquad g_O.
\]

\paragraph{Step 5. Final finite test.}
The graded principal operator is Dirac if either
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Branch A: }\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}\neq 0,
\qquad
(\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)\neq (0,0),
}
\label{eq:branchA_test}
\end{equation}
or
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Branch B: }\lambda_c\neq 0,
\qquad
(\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:branchB_test}
\end{equation}

\subsection{What is already closed}

The following are already theorem-level closed:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the plain scalar Bragg route is insufficient;
\item canonical Class II cannot cancel the scalar identity channel;
\item the graded \(2+2\) bypass route is rigorous;
\item the actual local \(CP^2\) projector-defect geometry belongs naturally to this graded operator class;
\item the natural local branch is S2;
\item the reduced nondegeneracy problem is exactly the finite coefficient-point audit above.
\end{enumerate}

\subsection{What remains honestly open}

What remains genuinely open is only:

\begin{enumerate}
\item derive \(V^\mu(\xi)\) from the \emph{full} microscopic TECT Hessian;
\item prove directly that the actual leading projected perturbation is grading-odd;
\item compute the actual values of
\[
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)},\quad
\lambda_c,\quad
\Lambda_E,\quad
\Lambda_O;
\]
\item verify microscopically that the final finite test \eqref{eq:branchA_test} or \eqref{eq:branchB_test} holds.
\end{enumerate}

\section{Final Summary}

The correct non-repetitive mainline is the graded \(2+2\) bypass route.
In this route the principal infrared operator is
\[
D_1(p)=
\begin{pmatrix}
0 & A_1(p)\\
A_1(p)^\dagger & 0
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
A_1(0)=0,
\]
so the scalar Bragg mass obstruction is absent from the relevant principal symbol.

The actual microscopic frontier is therefore reduced to a finite coefficient-point audit:
\[
(\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)},\lambda_c,\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O).
\]
The practical extraction proceeds through the actual \(Q_B\)-response
\[
R_\xi^{\mathrm{act}}=
\Pi_Q\mathcal R_\xi^{\mathrm{act}}\Pi_Q,
\]
its traceless coefficients
\[
s_1(\xi),\ s_2(\xi),\ s_3(\xi),
\]
and the overlap formulas giving
\[
\lambda_\parallel,\ \alpha,\ \beta.
\]
The final Dirac test is:

\[
\text{Branch A: }\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}\neq 0,\ (\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)\neq(0,0),
\]
or
\[
\text{Branch B: }\lambda_c\neq 0,\ (\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)\neq(0,0).
\]

Equivalently, in the concrete Class II normalization,
\[
g_c\neq 0,\qquad (g_E,g_O)\neq(0,0).
\]

Thus the remaining TECT microscopic frontier is no longer conceptual.
It is the explicit extraction of the actual coefficient point from the complete background-dependent Hessian.

\section{Graded \(2+2\) mainline: exact current stage}

The scalar Bragg-mass obstruction is no longer the main microscopic target.

\section{Canonical Tensor Decomposition of the Actual \(Q_B\)-Response}

\subsection{Short Korean explanation}

The remaining microscopic task in the graded \(2+2\) mainline is not to re-prove the reduced Dirac theorem.
It is to extract the actual coefficient point
\[
(\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)},\lambda_c,\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)
\]
from the complete background-dependent Hessian.

The correct route is:

\[
\Gamma^{(2)}[\bar\Phi_{\min}]
\;\longrightarrow\;
R_\xi^{\mathrm{act}}
\;\longrightarrow\;
(s_1(\xi),s_2(\xi),s_3(\xi))
\;\longrightarrow\;
V^\mu(\xi)
\;\longrightarrow\;
(M^\mu)_{ab}
\;\longrightarrow\;
(\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)},\lambda_c,\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O).
\]

\subsection{Step 0: operator protocol already fixed}

The actual extraction protocol is already fixed at the theorem level:

\[
\bar\Phi_{\min}
\to
\Gamma^{(2)}[\bar\Phi_{\min}]
\to
H_B(\xi)-iV^\mu(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu}+W^{\mu\nu}(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu}\partial_{y^\nu}+\cdots
\]
and then
\[
(M^\mu)_{ab}=\langle u_a^+,V^\mu u_b^-\rangle,
\]
followed by Pauli decomposition and S2 matching.
So the only missing ingredient is the explicit decomposition of the actual \(Q_B\)-response entering \(V^\mu(\xi)\).

\subsection{Step 1: adapted \(Q_B\)-frame and actual Hermitian response}

Let
\[
Q_B(\xi)=(\mathbb C z_B(\xi))^\perp,
\qquad
\dim_{\mathbb C}Q_B=2,
\]
and choose an adapted local orthonormal frame
\[
(e_1(\xi),e_2(\xi)).
\]
Here \(e_1\) is the defect-selected tangent direction, and \(e_2\) is the orthogonal spectator direction.

Let the actual Hermitian quadratic \(Q_B\)-response be
\begin{equation}
R_\xi^{\mathrm{act}}
=
\Pi_Q\,\mathcal R_\xi^{\mathrm{act}}\,\Pi_Q
\in \mathrm{End}(Q_B).
\label{eq:actual_QB_response}
\end{equation}
In the adapted frame it has the unique \(2\times2\) Hermitian form
\begin{equation}
R_\xi^{\mathrm{act}}
=
\begin{pmatrix}
r_{11}(\xi) & r_{12}(\xi)\\
\overline{r_{12}(\xi)} & r_{22}(\xi)
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
r_{11},r_{22}\in\mathbb R.
\label{eq:R_actual_matrix}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Step 2: canonical Pauli decomposition}

Every Hermitian \(2\times2\) matrix admits the unique decomposition
\begin{equation}
R_\xi^{\mathrm{act}}
=
r_0(\xi)\mathbf 1_2
+
s_1(\xi)\sigma_1
+
s_2(\xi)\sigma_2
+
s_3(\xi)\sigma_3,
\label{eq:R_Pauli_decomp}
\end{equation}
where
\begin{equation}
r_0(\xi)=\frac12\bigl(r_{11}(\xi)+r_{22}(\xi)\bigr),
\label{eq:r0_def}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
s_3(\xi)=\frac12\bigl(r_{11}(\xi)-r_{22}(\xi)\bigr),
\label{eq:s3_def}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
s_1(\xi)=\Re r_{12}(\xi),
\qquad
s_2(\xi)=-\Im r_{12}(\xi).
\label{eq:s1s2_def}
\end{equation}

Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
S_\xi^{\mathrm{act}}
:=
R_\xi^{\mathrm{act}}
-\frac12\Tr(R_\xi^{\mathrm{act}})\mathbf 1_2
=
s_1(\xi)\sigma_1+s_2(\xi)\sigma_2+s_3(\xi)\sigma_3.
\label{eq:S_actual_traceless}
\end{equation}

Thus the actual \(Q_B\)-response separates canonically into:

\begin{enumerate}
\item scalar/isotropic part \(r_0(\xi)\mathbf 1_2\),
\item transverse traceless vector part \((s_1,s_2,s_3)\).
\end{enumerate}

\subsection{Step 3: sharp interpretation of the three traceless components}

The three traceless coefficients have distinct meanings.

\paragraph{(i) Longitudinal singlet indicator.}
The coefficient
\begin{equation}
s_3(\xi)
=
\frac12\Bigl(
\langle e_1,R_\xi^{\mathrm{act}}e_1\rangle
-
\langle e_2,R_\xi^{\mathrm{act}}e_2\rangle
\Bigr)
\label{eq:s3_diag_form}
\end{equation}
measures diagonal anisotropy between the defect-selected tangent channel \(e_1\) and the spectator channel \(e_2\).

Therefore the practical sufficient test is:
\begin{equation}
\exists \xi_0:
\langle e_1(\xi_0),R_{\xi_0}^{\mathrm{act}}e_1(\xi_0)\rangle
\neq
\langle e_2(\xi_0),R_{\xi_0}^{\mathrm{act}}e_2(\xi_0)\rangle
\Longrightarrow
s_3(\xi)\not\equiv 0.
\label{eq:s3_sufficient_test}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{(ii) Even transverse mixing.}
The coefficient \(s_1(\xi)\) is the real off-diagonal mixing in the adapted frame and naturally feeds the even transverse channel.

\paragraph{(iii) Odd transverse mixing.}
The coefficient \(s_2(\xi)\) is the imaginary antisymmetric off-diagonal mixing and naturally feeds the odd transverse channel.

So, at the level of the actual Hermitian \(Q_B\)-response,
\[
s_3 \leftrightarrow \text{longitudinal singlet},
\qquad
s_1 \leftrightarrow \text{even transverse},
\qquad
s_2 \leftrightarrow \text{odd transverse}.
\]

\subsection{Step 4: primitive longitudinal branch}

If the direct local longitudinal invariant \(\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}\) vanishes, the established primitive branch uses
\begin{equation}
\mathcal T_\xi:=i[P_B,\partial_\xi P_B],
\qquad
S_\xi:=(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}.
\label{eq:Txi_primitive}
\end{equation}
The primitive longitudinal transport seed is
\begin{equation}
V^\mu_{(\parallel)}(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)\,S_\xi\,n^\mu.
\label{eq:Vparallel_primitive}
\end{equation}
Inside the explicit seed representative,
\begin{equation}
S_\xi=\frac12\theta'(\xi)^2\sigma_3,
\qquad
J_\parallel=\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,\theta'(\xi)S_\xi
=
\frac12 I_{\theta'^3},
\label{eq:Jparallel_seed}
\end{equation}
so
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3}.
}
\label{eq:lambda_parallel_lambda_c}
\end{equation}

Thus the primitive longitudinal audit is exactly:

\[
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}\stackrel{?}{\neq}0,
\qquad
\text{if not, } \lambda_c\stackrel{?}{\neq}0.
\]

\subsection{Step 5: canonical tensor decomposition of the actual transport kernel}

The correct next move is to expand the actual first-order transport kernel in the adapted worldvolume basis
\[
(n^\mu,E^\mu{}_1,E^\mu{}_2,J^\mu{}_1,J^\mu{}_2),
\]
and the Pauli basis \((\mathbf 1_2,\sigma_1,\sigma_2,\sigma_3)\).

The most useful canonical decomposition is
\begin{align}
V^\mu(\xi)
&=
n^\mu\Bigl[
v_0^\parallel(\xi)\mathbf 1_2
+
v_3^\parallel(\xi)\sigma_3
\Bigr]
\nonumber\\
&\quad
+
E^\mu{}_1\Bigl[
v_{E1}(\xi)\sigma_1+v_{E2}(\xi)\sigma_2
\Bigr]
+
E^\mu{}_2\Bigl[
-\,v_{E2}(\xi)\sigma_1+v_{E1}(\xi)\sigma_2
\Bigr]
\nonumber\\
&\quad
+
J^\mu{}_1\Bigl[
v_{O1}(\xi)\sigma_1+v_{O2}(\xi)\sigma_2
\Bigr]
+
J^\mu{}_2\Bigl[
-\,v_{O2}(\xi)\sigma_1+v_{O1}(\xi)\sigma_2
\Bigr]
+\cdots .
\label{eq:Vmu_canonical}
\end{align}

Here:

\begin{enumerate}
\item \(v_0^\parallel\) is grading-even / irrelevant for the principal Dirac symbol;
\item \(v_3^\parallel\) is the longitudinal singlet coefficient density;
\item \((v_{E1},v_{E2})\) form the even transverse doublet density;
\item \((v_{O1},v_{O2})\) form the odd transverse doublet density.
\end{enumerate}

In the reduced S2 branch this collapses to the three effective coefficient densities
\[
h_\parallel(\xi),\qquad h_E(\xi),\qquad h_O(\xi),
\]
with
\begin{equation}
V^\mu_{\mathrm{S2}}(\xi)
=
h_\parallel(\xi)\,n^\mu\sigma_3
+
h_E(\xi)\bigl(E^\mu{}_1\sigma_1+E^\mu{}_2\sigma_2\bigr)
+
h_O(\xi)\bigl(-E^\mu{}_2\sigma_1+E^\mu{}_1\sigma_2\bigr).
\label{eq:Vmu_S2}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Step 6: actual coefficient extraction formulas}

Let the graded low modes be
\[
u_a^+(\xi)=f_+(\xi)e_a(\xi),
\qquad
u_a^-(\xi)=f_-(\xi)e_a(\xi),
\qquad a=1,2.
\]
Then the projected mixed symbol is
\begin{equation}
(M^\mu)_{ab}
=
\langle u_a^+,V^\mu u_b^-\rangle.
\label{eq:Mmu_projection}
\end{equation}
Matching to the S2 form gives the exact overlap formulas
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel
=
\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,h_\parallel(\xi),
\label{eq:lambda_extract_hparallel}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\alpha
=
\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,h_E(\xi),
\label{eq:alpha_extract_hE}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\beta
=
\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,h_O(\xi).
\label{eq:beta_extract_hO}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, in the notation already fixed in the notes,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
I_\theta \Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}
+
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=I_\theta\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta=I_\theta\Lambda_O.
}
\label{eq:final_coeff_point_dictionary}
\end{equation}

So the full coefficient-point audit is reduced to identifying \(h_\parallel,h_E,h_O\), or equivalently
\[
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)},\qquad \lambda_c,\qquad \Lambda_E,\qquad \Lambda_O.
\]

\subsection{Step 7: exact finite decision tree}

The final finite test is now completely sharp.

\paragraph{Branch A.}
If
\begin{equation}
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}\neq 0,
\qquad
(\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)\neq (0,0),
\label{eq:branchA_final}
\end{equation}
then the graded principal operator is locally Dirac.

\paragraph{Branch B.}
If
\begin{equation}
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0,
\qquad
\lambda_c\neq 0,
\qquad
(\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)\neq (0,0),
\label{eq:branchB_final}
\end{equation}
then again the graded principal operator is locally Dirac.

Inside the exact Class II-compatible local normalization, this is equivalently
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_c\neq 0,
\qquad
(\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:classII_final_test}
\end{equation}

\section{Final summary}

The actual \(Q_B\)-response admits the canonical adapted-frame decomposition
\[
R_\xi^{\mathrm{act}}
=
r_0(\xi)\mathbf 1_2+s_1(\xi)\sigma_1+s_2(\xi)\sigma_2+s_3(\xi)\sigma_3,
\]
with
\[
r_0=\frac12(r_{11}+r_{22}),
\qquad
s_3=\frac12(r_{11}-r_{22}),
\qquad
s_1=\Re r_{12},
\qquad
s_2=-\Im r_{12}.
\]
Thus:
\[
s_3 \leftrightarrow \text{longitudinal singlet},
\qquad
s_1 \leftrightarrow \text{even transverse},
\qquad
s_2 \leftrightarrow \text{odd transverse}.
\]

The actual first-order transport kernel must then be decomposed in the worldvolume/Pauli basis,
and the projected mixed symbol
\[
(M^\mu)_{ab}=\langle u_a^+,V^\mu u_b^-\rangle
\]
yields the coefficient point
\[
(\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)},\lambda_c,\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O).
\]

The final finite microscopic test is:

\[
\text{Branch A: }\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}\neq 0,\ (\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)\neq(0,0),
\]
or
\[
\text{Branch B: }\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0,\ \lambda_c\neq 0,\ (\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)\neq(0,0).
\]

Therefore the remaining frontier is exactly the explicit extraction of
\[
R_\xi^{\mathrm{act}},\qquad
V^\mu(\xi),\qquad
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)},\lambda_c,\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O
\]
from the complete background-dependent TECT Hessian.

\section{Actual \(Q_B\)-response decomposition: exact current stage}

The actual Hermitian quadratic \(Q_B\)-response is
\[
R_\xi^{\mathrm{act}}
=
\Pi_Q\mathcal R_\xi^{\mathrm{act}}\Pi_Q
=
\begin{pmatrix}
r_{11}(\xi) & r_{12}(\xi)\\
\overline{r_{12}(\xi)} & r_{22}(\xi)
\end{pmatrix}.
\]
Its canonical Pauli decomposition is
\[
R_\xi^{\mathrm{act}}
=
r_0(\xi)\mathbf 1_2+s_1(\xi)\sigma_1+s_2(\xi)\sigma_2+s_3(\xi)\sigma_3,
\]
with
\[
r_0=\frac12(r_{11}+r_{22}),
\qquad
s_3=\frac12(r_{11}-r_{22}),
\qquad
s_1=\Re r_{12},
\qquad
s_2=-\Im r_{12}.
\]

This yields the physical identification
\[
s_3 \leftrightarrow \text{longitudinal singlet},
\qquad
s_1 \leftrightarrow \text{even transverse},
\qquad
s_2 \leftrightarrow \text{odd transverse}.
\]

The actual transport kernel must then be decomposed in the worldvolume/Pauli basis, and the projected mixed symbol
\[
(M^\mu)_{ab}=\langle u_a^+,V^\mu u_b^-\rangle
\]
determines the coefficient point
\[
(\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)},\lambda_c,\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O).
\]

The final finite decision tree is:
\[
\text{Branch A: }\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}\neq 0,\ (\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)\neq(0,0),
\]
or
\[
\text{Branch B: }\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0,\ \lambda_c\neq 0,\ (\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)\neq(0,0).
\]

Thus the remaining frontier is exactly the explicit extraction of the actual response tensor and transport kernel from the complete background-dependent TECT Hessian.

\section{Source-by-Source Classification of the Actual Hessian Transport Kernel}

\subsection{Short Korean explanation}

The remaining task is to classify the full Hessian sources according to which S2 tensor structure they can generate in the graded \(2+2\) route.

The only relevant leading first-order structures are

\[
n^\mu \sigma_3,
\qquad
E^\mu{}_a \sigma_a,
\qquad
J^\mu{}_a \sigma_a,
\qquad a=1,2.
\]

Therefore the full source audit is equivalent to the following question:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Which Hessian source produces }
n^\mu\sigma_3,\;
E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a,\;
J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a\ ?
}
\]

\subsection{Canonical S2 target decomposition}

The graded principal transport kernel is expanded as
\begin{equation}
V^\mu(\xi)
=
V^\mu_{(\parallel)}(\xi)
+
V^\mu_{(\perp,E)}(\xi)
+
V^\mu_{(\perp,O)}(\xi)
+
V^\mu_{\mathrm{irr}}(\xi),
\label{eq:Vmu_split_sources}
\end{equation}
where
\begin{equation}
V^\mu_{(\parallel)}(\xi)
=
h_\parallel(\xi)\,n^\mu\sigma_3,
\label{eq:V_parallel_target}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
V^\mu_{(\perp,E)}(\xi)
=
h_E(\xi)\,E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a,
\label{eq:V_even_target}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
V^\mu_{(\perp,O)}(\xi)
=
h_O(\xi)\,J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a,
\label{eq:V_odd_target}
\end{equation}
and \(V^\mu_{\mathrm{irr}}\) denotes pieces that do not survive the S2 shell-compatible projection.

The corresponding reduced coefficients are
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel
=
\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,h_\parallel(\xi),
\label{eq:lambda_from_hparallel_again}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\alpha
=
\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,h_E(\xi),
\label{eq:alpha_from_hE_again}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\beta
=
\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,h_O(\xi).
\label{eq:beta_from_hO_again}
\end{equation}

Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel
=
I_\theta \Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}
+
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=I_\theta \Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta=I_\theta \Lambda_O.
\label{eq:coeff_point_dictionary_again}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Class I: scalar/isotropic Hessian sources}

A scalar/isotropic source has the local form
\begin{equation}
\mathcal S^\mu_{\mathrm{iso}}(\xi)
=
u^\mu(\xi)\,\mathbf 1_2.
\label{eq:scalar_iso_source}
\end{equation}
This class includes:
\begin{enumerate}
\item amplitude-only Hessian pieces,
\item trace parts of projector response,
\item isotropic stiffness renormalizations.
\end{enumerate}

Such sources do \emph{not} contribute to the S2 witness coefficients:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal S^\mu_{\mathrm{iso}}
\Longrightarrow
h_\parallel=h_E=h_O=0
\quad\text{after traceless S2 projection.}
}
\label{eq:scalar_iso_no_witness}
\end{equation}

Reason:
\begin{enumerate}
\item \(\mathbf 1_2\) has zero overlap with \(\sigma_3\) under the traceless longitudinal projection;
\item it cannot generate the transverse Pauli doublet \((\sigma_1,\sigma_2)\).
\end{enumerate}

Therefore scalar/isotropic Hessian pieces are spectators for the principal graded Dirac symbol.

\subsection{Class II: primitive longitudinal singlet source}

The canonical longitudinal carrier is generated by the commutator channel
\begin{equation}
\mathcal T_\xi:=i[P_B,\partial_\xi P_B].
\label{eq:Txi_again}
\end{equation}
Direct restriction gives
\[
\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi\Pi_Q=0,
\]
but the induced quadratic channel is
\begin{equation}
\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q
=
\frac{\theta'(\xi)^2}{2}\bigl(\mathbf 1_2+\sigma_3\bigr).
\label{eq:Txi_square_again}
\end{equation}
Therefore its traceless part is
\begin{equation}
(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\frac12\theta'(\xi)^2\sigma_3.
\label{eq:Txi_square_tr_again}
\end{equation}

By parity, the naive quadratic singlet
\[
\theta'(\xi)^2\,n^\mu\sigma_3
\]
does not survive the mixed even/odd overlap, because
\[
f_+ \text{ even},\qquad f_- \text{ odd},\qquad \theta'^2 \text{ even}
\]
imply
\[
\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,\theta'^2=0.
\]
Hence the minimal viable longitudinal source must carry one extra odd factor:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu_{(\parallel)}(\xi)
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\,\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\sigma_3.
}
\label{eq:V_parallel_final_source}
\end{equation}
This contributes only to the longitudinal coefficient:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
h_\parallel(\xi)=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\theta'(\xi)^3,
\qquad
h_E=h_O=0.
}
\label{eq:hparallel_only}
\end{equation}

Thus
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{primitive commutator-square source}
\Longrightarrow
n^\mu\sigma_3
\Longrightarrow
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3}.
}
\label{eq:primitive_longitudinal_chain}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Class III: transverse even doublet source}

The minimal even transverse source is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu_{(\perp,E)}(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)\,\Lambda_E\,E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a,
\qquad a=1,2.
}
\label{eq:V_even_final_source}
\end{equation}
This produces the even transverse coefficient only:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
h_E(\xi)=\theta'(\xi)\Lambda_E,
\qquad
h_\parallel=h_O=0.
}
\label{eq:hE_only}
\end{equation}
After projection,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha=I_\theta\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta=0
\quad\text{if only }V^\mu_{(\perp,E)}\text{ is present.}
}
\label{eq:alpha_even_only}
\end{equation}

Microscopically, this class must come from a Hessian source that:
\begin{enumerate}
\item is reflection-odd overall,
\item transforms as a transverse vector in worldvolume space,
\item transforms as a traceless doublet in \(Q_B\)-fiber space.
\end{enumerate}

\subsection{Class IV: transverse odd doublet source}

The minimal odd transverse source is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu_{(\perp,O)}(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)\,\Lambda_O\,J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a,
\qquad a=1,2.
}
\label{eq:V_odd_final_source}
\end{equation}
This produces the odd transverse coefficient only:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
h_O(\xi)=\theta'(\xi)\Lambda_O,
\qquad
h_\parallel=h_E=0.
}
\label{eq:hO_only}
\end{equation}
After projection,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta=I_\theta\Lambda_O,
\qquad
\alpha=0
\quad\text{if only }V^\mu_{(\perp,O)}\text{ is present.}
}
\label{eq:beta_odd_only}
\end{equation}

Microscopically, this class is the parity-rotated partner of the even transverse source and must arise from a Hessian block carrying the same \(Q_B\)-doublet content but the rotated worldvolume tensor \(J^\mu{}_a=\epsilon_{ab}E^\mu{}_b\).

\subsection{Class V: irreducible or forbidden sources}

Any first-order Hessian source not of the three compatible types
\[
n^\mu\sigma_3,\qquad E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a,\qquad J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
\]
is either:
\begin{enumerate}
\item projected out by the S2 reduction,
\item forbidden by parity/worldvolume symmetry,
\item or contributes only to higher-order irrelevant operators.
\end{enumerate}

Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu_{\mathrm{irr}}
\Longrightarrow
\text{no contribution to }
(\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)},\lambda_c,\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)
\text{ at principal order.}
}
\label{eq:Virr_no_contribution}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Canonical source table}

The full source audit is therefore summarized by the table
\[
\begin{array}{c|c|c|c}
\text{Source class} & \text{Canonical form} & \text{Coefficient produced} & \text{Effect} \\ \hline
\text{Scalar/isotropic} & u^\mu\mathbf 1_2 & \text{none} & \text{spectator} \\
\text{Primitive longitudinal} & \frac{\lambda_c}{2}\theta'^3 n^\mu\sigma_3 & \lambda_c & \lambda_\parallel \\
\text{Transverse even} & \theta'\Lambda_E E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a & \Lambda_E & \alpha \\
\text{Transverse odd} & \theta'\Lambda_O J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a & \Lambda_O & \beta \\
\text{Irreducible/forbidden} & V^\mu_{\mathrm{irr}} & \text{none} & \text{projected out}
\end{array}
\]

\subsection{Reconstruction from the actual \(Q_B\)-response}

Now connect this directly to the actual adapted-frame response
\[
R_\xi^{\mathrm{act}}
=
r_0(\xi)\mathbf 1_2+s_1(\xi)\sigma_1+s_2(\xi)\sigma_2+s_3(\xi)\sigma_3.
\]
Then the reconstruction principle is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
s_3(\xi)\ \text{feeds the longitudinal singlet channel},
}
\label{eq:s3_feeds_long}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
s_1(\xi)\ \text{feeds the even transverse doublet},
}
\label{eq:s1_feeds_even}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
s_2(\xi)\ \text{feeds the odd transverse doublet}.
}
\label{eq:s2_feeds_odd}
\end{equation}

More precisely, the canonical first-order reconstruction ansatz is
\begin{align}
V^\mu(\xi)
&=
\theta'(\xi)\,v_\parallel^{(0)}(\xi)\,n^\mu\sigma_3
+
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\theta'(\xi)^3 n^\mu\sigma_3
\nonumber\\
&\quad
+
\theta'(\xi)\,v_E(\xi)\,E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
+
\theta'(\xi)\,v_O(\xi)\,J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
+
V^\mu_{\mathrm{irr}}(\xi),
\label{eq:Vmu_reconstruct_from_response}
\end{align}
with
\[
v_\parallel^{(0)}(\xi)\sim s_3(\xi),\qquad
v_E(\xi)\sim s_1(\xi),\qquad
v_O(\xi)\sim s_2(\xi),
\]
up to model-dependent proportionality factors determined by the full Hessian.

Therefore the coefficient-point extraction reduces to
\begin{equation}
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}
=
\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,\theta'(\xi)\,v_\parallel^{(0)}(\xi),
\label{eq:Lambda_parallel0_extract}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\Lambda_E
=
\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,\theta'(\xi)\,v_E(\xi),
\label{eq:LambdaE_extract}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\Lambda_O
=
\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,\theta'(\xi)\,v_O(\xi),
\label{eq:LambdaO_extract}
\end{equation}
while Branch B contributes
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel^{(B)}
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3}.
\label{eq:lambdaparallel_B_extract}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Exact decision tree after source classification}

After the source-by-source classification, the final microscopic decision tree is:

\paragraph{Longitudinal audit}
\[
s_3(\xi)\stackrel{?}{\not\equiv}0
\Longrightarrow
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}\stackrel{?}{\neq}0.
\]
If not,
\[
\lambda_c\stackrel{?}{\neq}0.
\]

\paragraph{Transverse audit}
\[
s_1(\xi)\stackrel{?}{\not\equiv}0
\Longrightarrow
\Lambda_E\stackrel{?}{\neq}0,
\]
\[
s_2(\xi)\stackrel{?}{\not\equiv}0
\Longrightarrow
\Lambda_O\stackrel{?}{\neq}0.
\]

\paragraph{Final graded Dirac test}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Branch A: }\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}\neq 0,\qquad (\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)\neq(0,0),
}
\label{eq:graded_branchA_after_table}
\end{equation}
or
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Branch B: }\lambda_c\neq 0,\qquad (\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)\neq(0,0).
}
\label{eq:graded_branchB_after_table}
\end{equation}

\section{Final Summary}

The actual Hessian sources split into five principal classes:

\begin{enumerate}
\item scalar/isotropic sources: spectators;
\item primitive commutator-square source: produces only \(n^\mu\sigma_3\);
\item transverse even source: produces only \(E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a\);
\item transverse odd source: produces only \(J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a\);
\item irreducible/forbidden sources: projected out at principal order.
\end{enumerate}

Thus the full source-by-source coefficient extraction is reduced to the canonical map
\[
R_\xi^{\mathrm{act}}
\to
(s_1,s_2,s_3)
\to
(v_\parallel^{(0)},v_E,v_O)
\to
(\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)},\lambda_c,\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O).
\]

The final microscopic test is:
\[
\text{either }\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}\neq 0\text{ or }\lambda_c\neq 0,
\qquad
(\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)\neq (0,0).
\]

\section{Source-by-source Hessian classification}

The only principal first-order S2-compatible transport structures are
\[
n^\mu\sigma_3,\qquad
E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a,\qquad
J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a.
\]
Accordingly, the Hessian sources split into:

\[
\text{scalar/isotropic} \to \text{spectator},
\]
\[
\text{primitive commutator-square} \to n^\mu\sigma_3 \to \lambda_c,
\]
\[
\text{transverse even doublet} \to E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a \to \Lambda_E,
\]
\[
\text{transverse odd doublet} \to J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a \to \Lambda_O.
\]

The actual adapted-frame response
\[
R_\xi^{\mathrm{act}}
=
r_0(\xi)\mathbf 1_2+s_1(\xi)\sigma_1+s_2(\xi)\sigma_2+s_3(\xi)\sigma_3
\]
therefore maps canonically as
\[
s_3 \to \Lambda_\parallel^{(0)} \text{ or } \lambda_c,
\qquad
s_1 \to \Lambda_E,
\qquad
s_2 \to \Lambda_O.
\]

Hence the remaining finite audit is exactly:
\[
\text{either }\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}\neq 0\text{ or }\lambda_c\neq 0,
\qquad
(\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)\neq (0,0).
\]
