\section{Blockwise Contribution Formulas for the Actual \(Q_B\)-Response}

\subsection{Short Korean explanation}

We now decompose the full background-dependent Hessian into the minimal source blocks
that can contribute to the graded \(2+2\) principal transport kernel.

The purpose is to derive, source by source, the induced coefficients
\[
r_0(\xi),\qquad s_1(\xi),\qquad s_2(\xi),\qquad s_3(\xi)
\]
in
\[
R_\xi^{\mathrm{act}}
=
r_0(\xi)\mathbf 1_2+s_1(\xi)\sigma_1+s_2(\xi)\sigma_2+s_3(\xi)\sigma_3.
\]

These coefficients then feed
\[
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)},\qquad \lambda_c,\qquad \Lambda_E,\qquad \Lambda_O.
\]

\subsection{Step 1: block decomposition of the full Hessian}

Let the complete quadratic operator around the actual defect/background be
\[
\Gamma^{(2)}[\bar\Phi_{\min}].
\]
Decompose it into the minimal source blocks
\begin{equation}
\Gamma^{(2)}
=
\Gamma^{(2)}_{\mathrm{amp}}
+
\Gamma^{(2)}_{\mathrm{align,tree}}
+
\Gamma^{(2)}_{\mathrm{comm}^2}
+
\Gamma^{(2)}_{\mathrm{med}}
+
\Gamma^{(2)}_{\mathrm{rem}},
\label{eq:full_hessian_split}
\end{equation}
where:

\begin{enumerate}
\item \(\Gamma^{(2)}_{\mathrm{amp}}\): amplitude / scalar / isotropic shell block,
\item \(\Gamma^{(2)}_{\mathrm{align,tree}}\): direct tree-level projector-stiffness block,
\item \(\Gamma^{(2)}_{\mathrm{comm}^2}\): primitive commutator-square longitudinal block,
\item \(\Gamma^{(2)}_{\mathrm{med}}\): explicit mediated anisotropic/transport block,
\item \(\Gamma^{(2)}_{\mathrm{rem}}\): all higher-order, remote, or not-yet-closed pieces.
\end{enumerate}

Projecting to the \(Q_B\)-doublet sector gives
\begin{equation}
R_\xi^{\mathrm{act}}
=
R_\xi^{\mathrm{amp}}
+
R_\xi^{\mathrm{align,tree}}
+
R_\xi^{\mathrm{comm}^2}
+
R_\xi^{\mathrm{med}}
+
R_\xi^{\mathrm{rem}},
\label{eq:Ract_split}
\end{equation}
with each term in \(\mathrm{Herm}(Q_B)\).

\subsection{Step 2: universal Pauli decomposition for each block}

For each block \(X\in\{\mathrm{amp},\mathrm{align,tree},\mathrm{comm}^2,\mathrm{med},\mathrm{rem}\}\), write
\begin{equation}
R_\xi^{X}
=
r_0^{X}(\xi)\mathbf 1_2
+
s_1^{X}(\xi)\sigma_1
+
s_2^{X}(\xi)\sigma_2
+
s_3^{X}(\xi)\sigma_3.
\label{eq:RX_Pauli}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
r_0(\xi)=\sum_X r_0^X(\xi),
\qquad
s_a(\xi)=\sum_X s_a^X(\xi),
\quad a=1,2,3.
\label{eq:r0s_sum}
\end{equation}

In the adapted frame \((e_1,e_2)\),
\begin{equation}
r_0^X=\frac12\bigl(r_{11}^X+r_{22}^X\bigr),
\qquad
s_3^X=\frac12\bigl(r_{11}^X-r_{22}^X\bigr),
\qquad
s_1^X=\Re r_{12}^X,
\qquad
s_2^X=-\Im r_{12}^X.
\label{eq:r0s_from_rij_X}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Step 3: amplitude/scalar block}

The amplitude/scalar block is the restriction of the scalar shell Hessian to the \(Q_B\)-doublet:
\begin{equation}
R_\xi^{\mathrm{amp}}
=
\Pi_Q\,\mathcal R_\xi^{\mathrm{amp}}\,\Pi_Q.
\label{eq:R_amp_def}
\end{equation}
Because this block is scalar/isotropic in fiber space at principal order, it has the form
\begin{equation}
R_\xi^{\mathrm{amp}}
=
r_0^{\mathrm{amp}}(\xi)\mathbf 1_2,
\qquad
s_1^{\mathrm{amp}}=s_2^{\mathrm{amp}}=s_3^{\mathrm{amp}}=0.
\label{eq:R_amp_result}
\end{equation}
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
R_\xi^{\mathrm{amp}}
\Longrightarrow
\text{no direct contribution to }
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)},\lambda_c,\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O.
}
\label{eq:amp_no_witness}
\end{equation}

This includes:
\begin{enumerate}
\item pure scalar terms,
\item pure amplitude-only terms,
\item scalar drift terms,
\item isotropic shell renormalizations.
\end{enumerate}

\subsection{Step 4: direct projector-stiffness tree block}

For the refined locked constant-projector background,
\[
P_0=\mathrm{const},
\qquad
\partial_iP_0=0.
\]
Hence the quadratic Hessian is block diagonal between shell and tangent-projector sectors,
\[
\delta^2F_{\mathrm{ref}}=\delta^2F_\sigma+\delta^2F_\xi,
\qquad
J=0.
\]
Therefore the direct tree-level projector-stiffness block contributes no shell-projector mixing at quadratic order:
\begin{equation}
R_\xi^{\mathrm{align,tree}}=0.
\label{eq:R_align_tree_zero}
\end{equation}
Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
r_0^{\mathrm{align,tree}}
=
s_1^{\mathrm{align,tree}}
=
s_2^{\mathrm{align,tree}}
=
s_3^{\mathrm{align,tree}}
=
0.
}
\label{eq:align_tree_all_zero}
\end{equation}

So the current projector-stiffness sector has no direct principal witness effect at tree level.

\subsection{Step 5: primitive commutator-square block}

Define
\[
\mathcal T_\xi:=i[P_B,\partial_\xi P_B].
\]
Direct \(Q_B\)-restriction vanishes:
\[
\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi\Pi_Q=0.
\]
But the induced quadratic channel is
\[
\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q
=
\frac{\theta'(\xi)^2}{2}\bigl(\mathbf 1_2+\sigma_3\bigr).
\]
Hence the traceless part is
\begin{equation}
R_\xi^{\mathrm{comm}^2,\mathrm{tr}}
=
\frac12\theta'(\xi)^2\sigma_3.
\label{eq:R_comm2_tr}
\end{equation}
Therefore the primitive commutator-square block contributes
\begin{equation}
r_0^{\mathrm{comm}^2}(\xi)=\frac12\theta'(\xi)^2,
\qquad
s_3^{\mathrm{comm}^2}(\xi)=\frac12\theta'(\xi)^2,
\qquad
s_1^{\mathrm{comm}^2}=s_2^{\mathrm{comm}^2}=0.
\label{eq:r0s_comm2}
\end{equation}

However, parity kills the naive longitudinal first-order overlap:
\[
f_+ \text{ even},\qquad
f_- \text{ odd},\qquad
\theta'^2 \text{ even}
\Longrightarrow
\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,\theta'^2=0.
\]
Hence this block contributes to the principal transport kernel only after multiplication by one extra odd factor \(\theta'(\xi)\):
\begin{equation}
V^\mu_{(\parallel)}(\xi)
=
\lambda_c\,\theta'(\xi)\,R_\xi^{\mathrm{comm}^2,\mathrm{tr}}\,n^\mu
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\theta'(\xi)^3 n^\mu\sigma_3.
\label{eq:V_comm2_final}
\end{equation}
Thus
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{primitive commutator-square block}
\Longrightarrow
s_3 \text{ channel only}
\Longrightarrow
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3}.
}
\label{eq:comm2_chain_final}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Step 6: mediated anisotropic/transport block}

This is the first source that can generate the full S2 triplet explicitly.
Inside the exact concrete quadratic reduction template, one has
\[
L_X^{(2)}
=
\frac{M_X^2}{2}X_i^aX_i^a
+
\lambda\,m^aX_i^a\,\partial_i\phi_0
+
g_X\,X_i^a\,C_{ij}^{ab}(D_j\psi)\,\xi^b
+\mathrm{h.c.}
\]
Integrating out \(X_i^a\) gives
\[
\delta N_{ij}^b
=
-\frac{\lambda g_X}{M_X^2}\,m^aC_{ij}^{ab}.
\]
At the local projector-defect transport level this matches
\begin{equation}
V^\mu_{\mathrm{med}}(\xi)
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\theta'(\xi)^3 n^\mu\sigma_3
+
\theta'(\xi)\Bigl[
\Lambda_E E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
+
\Lambda_O J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
\Bigr]
+\cdots .
\label{eq:V_med_full}
\end{equation}
Therefore the mediated block contributes
\begin{equation}
s_3^{\mathrm{med}}(\xi)\sim \frac{\lambda_c}{2}\theta'(\xi)^2,
\qquad
s_1^{\mathrm{med}}(\xi)\sim \Lambda_E,
\qquad
s_2^{\mathrm{med}}(\xi)\sim \Lambda_O,
\label{eq:s_med_proto}
\end{equation}
up to the universal overall \(\theta'(\xi)\) factor needed in \(V^\mu\).

More invariantly, the corresponding principal transport densities are
\begin{equation}
h_\parallel^{\mathrm{med}}(\xi)=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\theta'(\xi)^3,
\qquad
h_E^{\mathrm{med}}(\xi)=\theta'(\xi)\Lambda_E,
\qquad
h_O^{\mathrm{med}}(\xi)=\theta'(\xi)\Lambda_O.
\label{eq:h_med}
\end{equation}
Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel^{\mathrm{med}}=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha^{\mathrm{med}}=I_\theta\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta^{\mathrm{med}}=I_\theta\Lambda_O.
}
\label{eq:coeffs_med_final}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Step 7: remote / heavy-mode induced projector-stiffness block}

Although the tree-level projector stiffness gives zero direct mixing,
heavy-mode elimination can induce an effective correction:
\[
\delta L_{\mathrm{eff}}
=
-\frac12 J\,G_\pi\,J,
\]
provided a nonzero microscopic shell-projector mixing source \(J\) exists beyond the present tree-level locked background truncation.

Thus the induced projector-stiffness response has the formal structure
\begin{equation}
R_\xi^{\mathrm{stiff,ind}}
=
\Pi_Q\bigl(-J\,G_\pi\,J\bigr)\Pi_Q.
\label{eq:R_stiff_ind_def}
\end{equation}
At the current theorem level, its detailed coefficients are not closed, but its possible contributions are:
\begin{equation}
r_0^{\mathrm{stiff,ind}}\ \text{allowed},
\qquad
s_3^{\mathrm{stiff,ind}}\ \text{allowed},
\qquad
s_1^{\mathrm{stiff,ind}},\,s_2^{\mathrm{stiff,ind}}\ \text{allowed in principle}.
\label{eq:stiff_ind_allowed}
\end{equation}
So
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{projector stiffness contributes only indirectly, through heavy-mode elimination.}
}
\label{eq:stiff_ind_only}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Step 8: remainder block}

All not-yet-closed microscopic sources are collected into
\[
R_\xi^{\mathrm{rem}}.
\]
By definition,
\begin{equation}
R_\xi^{\mathrm{rem}}
=
r_0^{\mathrm{rem}}\mathbf 1_2+s_1^{\mathrm{rem}}\sigma_1+s_2^{\mathrm{rem}}\sigma_2+s_3^{\mathrm{rem}}\sigma_3.
\label{eq:R_rem}
\end{equation}
This block is not known explicitly, but it can be audited source-by-source once the complete final TECT Hessian is specified.

\subsection{Step 9: total source table}

Combining all blocks:

\[
\begin{array}{c|c|c|c|c}
\text{Block} & r_0 & s_1 & s_2 & s_3 \\ \hline
\mathrm{amp} & \checkmark & 0 & 0 & 0 \\
\mathrm{align,tree} & 0 & 0 & 0 & 0 \\
\mathrm{comm}^2 & \checkmark & 0 & 0 & \checkmark \\
\mathrm{med} & \checkmark? & \checkmark & \checkmark & \checkmark \\
\mathrm{stiff,ind} & \checkmark & \checkmark? & \checkmark? & \checkmark? \\
\mathrm{rem} & ? & ? & ? & ?
\end{array}
\]

At principal order, the currently closed direct witness carriers are:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
s_3:\ \mathrm{comm}^2 \text{ or med},
\qquad
s_1:\ \mathrm{med},
\qquad
s_2:\ \mathrm{med}.
}
\label{eq:closed_direct_carriers}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Step 10: coefficient reconstruction}

The total transport reconstruction is
\begin{align}
V^\mu(\xi)
&=
\theta'(\xi)\,v_\parallel^{(0)}(\xi)\,n^\mu\sigma_3
+
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\theta'(\xi)^3 n^\mu\sigma_3
\nonumber\\
&\quad
+
\theta'(\xi)\,v_E(\xi)\,E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
+
\theta'(\xi)\,v_O(\xi)\,J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
+
V^\mu_{\mathrm{irr}}(\xi),
\label{eq:V_reconstruct_total}
\end{align}
with
\[
v_\parallel^{(0)}\sim s_3^{\mathrm{lead}},
\qquad
v_E\sim s_1^{\mathrm{lead}},
\qquad
v_O\sim s_2^{\mathrm{lead}}.
\]
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}
=
\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,\theta'(\xi)\,v_\parallel^{(0)}(\xi),
\label{eq:Lambda0_rec}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\Lambda_E
=
\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,\theta'(\xi)\,v_E(\xi),
\qquad
\Lambda_O
=
\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,\theta'(\xi)\,v_O(\xi),
\label{eq:LambdaEO_rec}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel
=
I_\theta\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}
+
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=I_\theta\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta=I_\theta\Lambda_O.
\label{eq:final_rec_formula}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Step 11: actual decision tree after blockwise audit}

The final microscopic decision tree is now:

\paragraph{Longitudinal}
\[
s_3^{\mathrm{lead}}\stackrel{?}{\not\equiv}0
\Longrightarrow
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}\stackrel{?}{\neq}0.
\]
If not,
\[
\lambda_c\stackrel{?}{\neq}0
\]
through the primitive commutator-square channel.

\paragraph{Transverse}
\[
s_1^{\mathrm{lead}}\stackrel{?}{\not\equiv}0
\Longrightarrow
\Lambda_E\stackrel{?}{\neq}0,
\]
\[
s_2^{\mathrm{lead}}\stackrel{?}{\not\equiv}0
\Longrightarrow
\Lambda_O\stackrel{?}{\neq}0.
\]

\paragraph{Final finite test}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Branch A: }\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}\neq 0,\qquad
(\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)\neq (0,0),
}
\label{eq:blockwise_branchA}
\end{equation}
or
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Branch B: }\lambda_c\neq 0,\qquad
(\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:blockwise_branchB}
\end{equation}

\section{Final Summary}

The full Hessian source audit is now reduced to a blockwise \(Q_B\)-response decomposition:
\[
\Gamma^{(2)}
=
\Gamma^{(2)}_{\mathrm{amp}}
+
\Gamma^{(2)}_{\mathrm{align,tree}}
+
\Gamma^{(2)}_{\mathrm{comm}^2}
+
\Gamma^{(2)}_{\mathrm{med}}
+
\Gamma^{(2)}_{\mathrm{rem}}.
\]
After projection to the \(Q_B\)-doublet, each block contributes to
\[
R_\xi^{\mathrm{act}}
=
r_0\mathbf 1_2+s_1\sigma_1+s_2\sigma_2+s_3\sigma_3.
\]

The currently closed direct principal contributions are:

\[
\text{amplitude/scalar} \to r_0 \text{ only},
\]
\[
\text{direct projector-stiffness tree level} \to 0,
\]
\[
\text{primitive commutator-square} \to s_3 \text{ only},
\]
\[
\text{mediated anisotropic/transport block} \to s_3,s_1,s_2.
\]

Thus the actual finite coefficient-point extraction is
\[
R_\xi^{\mathrm{act}}
\to
(s_3,s_1,s_2)
\to
(\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)},\lambda_c,\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O),
\]
with
\[
\lambda_\parallel
=
I_\theta\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}
+
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=I_\theta\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta=I_\theta\Lambda_O.
\]

The remaining microscopic frontier is therefore the explicit evaluation of the mediated and remote/heavy-mode-induced blocks in the complete final TECT Hessian.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Explicit Adapted-Frame Evaluation of the Mediated Block}

\subsection{Short Korean explanation}

The mediated block is the only currently explicit microscopic source that can generate all three principal witness channels
\[
s_3,\qquad s_1,\qquad s_2.
\]
So the next exact task is to write the induced \(Q_B\)-response
\[
R_\xi^{\mathrm{med}}
\]
in the adapted frame \((e_1,e_2)\), and then extract
\[
r_{11}^{\mathrm{med}},\quad r_{22}^{\mathrm{med}},\quad r_{12}^{\mathrm{med}}.
\]

Once that is done, the coefficient point follows immediately.

\subsection{Step 1: mediated quadratic completion}

Let the microscopic mediator field be \(X_i^a\), with quadratic block
\begin{equation}
L_X^{(2)}
=
\frac{M_X^2}{2}X_i^aX_i^a
+
X_i^a\,\mathcal J_i^a[\delta\Phi]
\label{eq:LX2_start}
\end{equation}
where \(\delta\Phi\) denotes the shell/projector fluctuation multiplet, and
\[
\mathcal J_i^a[\delta\Phi]
=
\mathcal J_{i,\mathrm{bg}}^a+\mathcal J_{i,\mathrm{lin}}^a[\delta\Phi]+\cdots.
\]

Integrating out \(X_i^a\) at quadratic order gives
\begin{equation}
\delta L_{\mathrm{eff}}^{\mathrm{med}}
=
-\frac{1}{2M_X^2}\,
\mathcal J_i^a[\delta\Phi]\,
\mathcal J_i^a[\delta\Phi].
\label{eq:Leff_med_general}
\end{equation}
The quadratic response relevant for the \(Q_B\)-sector is therefore
\begin{equation}
\mathcal R_\xi^{\mathrm{med}}
=
-\frac{1}{M_X^2}\,
\Bigl(\mathcal J_{i,\mathrm{lin}}^a\Bigr)^\dagger
\mathcal J_{i,\mathrm{lin}}^a.
\label{eq:Rmed_operator}
\end{equation}

Restricting to \(Q_B\),
\begin{equation}
R_\xi^{\mathrm{med}}
=
\Pi_Q\mathcal R_\xi^{\mathrm{med}}\Pi_Q
=
-\frac{1}{M_X^2}\,
\Pi_Q
\Bigl(\mathcal J_{i,\mathrm{lin}}^a\Bigr)^\dagger
\mathcal J_{i,\mathrm{lin}}^a
\Pi_Q.
\label{eq:Rmed_Q}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Step 2: adapted-frame matrix elements}

Choose the adapted orthonormal basis
\[
(e_1(\xi),e_2(\xi))
\]
of \(Q_B(\xi)\).
Define the mediator current matrix elements
\begin{equation}
\mathcal C_{i a; m}(\xi)
:=
\langle e_m(\xi),\,\mathcal J_{i,\mathrm{lin}}^a\,\rangle,
\qquad
m=1,2.
\label{eq:Ciam_def}
\end{equation}
Equivalently, for each \(\xi\), \(\mathcal C(\xi)\) is a collection of two-component amplitudes labeled by \((i,a)\).

Then the \(Q_B\)-response matrix is
\begin{equation}
r_{mn}^{\mathrm{med}}(\xi)
=
-\frac{1}{M_X^2}
\sum_{i,a}
\overline{\mathcal C_{i a; m}(\xi)}\,
\mathcal C_{i a; n}(\xi),
\qquad
m,n=1,2.
\label{eq:rmn_med_master}
\end{equation}

So explicitly,
\begin{equation}
r_{11}^{\mathrm{med}}(\xi)
=
-\frac{1}{M_X^2}\sum_{i,a}
\bigl|\mathcal C_{i a;1}(\xi)\bigr|^2,
\label{eq:r11_med}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
r_{22}^{\mathrm{med}}(\xi)
=
-\frac{1}{M_X^2}\sum_{i,a}
\bigl|\mathcal C_{i a;2}(\xi)\bigr|^2,
\label{eq:r22_med}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
r_{12}^{\mathrm{med}}(\xi)
=
-\frac{1}{M_X^2}\sum_{i,a}
\overline{\mathcal C_{i a;1}(\xi)}\,
\mathcal C_{i a;2}(\xi).
\label{eq:r12_med}
\end{equation}

This is the exact adapted-frame evaluation formula.

\subsection{Step 3: Pauli coefficients of the mediated response}

From the universal Hermitian decomposition,
\[
R_\xi^{\mathrm{med}}
=
r_0^{\mathrm{med}}(\xi)\mathbf 1_2
+
s_1^{\mathrm{med}}(\xi)\sigma_1
+
s_2^{\mathrm{med}}(\xi)\sigma_2
+
s_3^{\mathrm{med}}(\xi)\sigma_3,
\]
we get
\begin{equation}
r_0^{\mathrm{med}}(\xi)
=
-\frac{1}{2M_X^2}\sum_{i,a}
\left(
|\mathcal C_{i a;1}|^2+|\mathcal C_{i a;2}|^2
\right),
\label{eq:r0_med}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
s_3^{\mathrm{med}}(\xi)
=
-\frac{1}{2M_X^2}\sum_{i,a}
\left(
|\mathcal C_{i a;1}|^2-|\mathcal C_{i a;2}|^2
\right),
\label{eq:s3_med}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
s_1^{\mathrm{med}}(\xi)
=
-\frac{1}{M_X^2}\sum_{i,a}
\Re\!\left(
\overline{\mathcal C_{i a;1}}\mathcal C_{i a;2}
\right),
\label{eq:s1_med}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
s_2^{\mathrm{med}}(\xi)
=
\frac{1}{M_X^2}\sum_{i,a}
\Im\!\left(
\overline{\mathcal C_{i a;1}}\mathcal C_{i a;2}
\right).
\label{eq:s2_med}
\end{equation}

These are the exact source-by-source formulas we needed.

\subsection{Step 4: interpretation of the three witness channels}

The mediated block therefore generates:

\paragraph{Longitudinal singlet}
\begin{equation}
s_3^{\mathrm{med}}(\xi)\neq 0
\iff
\sum_{i,a}
|\mathcal C_{i a;1}|^2
\neq
\sum_{i,a}
|\mathcal C_{i a;2}|^2.
\label{eq:s3_condition}
\end{equation}
So the longitudinal singlet appears when the mediator couples with unequal strength to the tangent channel \(e_1\) and the spectator channel \(e_2\).

\paragraph{Even transverse doublet}
\begin{equation}
s_1^{\mathrm{med}}(\xi)\neq 0
\iff
\sum_{i,a}
\Re\!\left(\overline{\mathcal C_{i a;1}}\mathcal C_{i a;2}\right)\neq 0.
\label{eq:s1_condition}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Odd transverse doublet}
\begin{equation}
s_2^{\mathrm{med}}(\xi)\neq 0
\iff
\sum_{i,a}
\Im\!\left(\overline{\mathcal C_{i a;1}}\mathcal C_{i a;2}\right)\neq 0.
\label{eq:s2_condition}
\end{equation}

Thus:
\[
\text{norm imbalance } \longrightarrow s_3,
\qquad
\text{real coherence } \longrightarrow s_1,
\qquad
\text{imaginary coherence } \longrightarrow s_2.
\]

\subsection{Step 5: decomposition into worldvolume tensors}

Now separate the \((i,a)\)-dependence into the shell/worldvolume basis.
Write
\begin{equation}
\mathcal C_{i a;m}(\xi)
=
n_i\,u_{a;m}^{(\parallel)}(\xi)
+
E_{i a}\,u_m^{(E)}(\xi)
+
J_{i a}\,u_m^{(O)}(\xi)
+
\mathcal C_{i a;m}^{(\mathrm{irr})}(\xi),
\label{eq:C_worldvolume_decomp}
\end{equation}
where:

\begin{enumerate}
\item \(n_i\) is the longitudinal unit direction,
\item \(E_{i a}\) is the even transverse tensor,
\item \(J_{i a}\) is the odd transverse tensor,
\item \(\mathcal C^{(\mathrm{irr})}\) is projected out at S2 principal order.
\end{enumerate}

Then the mediated response splits accordingly:
\begin{equation}
R_\xi^{\mathrm{med}}
=
R_\xi^{(\parallel)}
+
R_\xi^{(E)}
+
R_\xi^{(O)}
+
R_\xi^{(\mathrm{mix})}
+
R_\xi^{(\mathrm{irr})}.
\label{eq:Rmed_split_tensor}
\end{equation}

At principal order, the S2-compatible sector is obtained by keeping only the diagonal channel-matched pieces:
\begin{equation}
R_\xi^{(\parallel)}
\rightsquigarrow s_3^{(\parallel)}(\xi)\sigma_3,
\label{eq:R_parallel_principal}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
R_\xi^{(E)}
\rightsquigarrow s_1^{(E)}(\xi)\sigma_1,
\label{eq:R_E_principal}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
R_\xi^{(O)}
\rightsquigarrow s_2^{(O)}(\xi)\sigma_2.
\label{eq:R_O_principal}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Step 6: minimal transport ansatz induced by the mediated response}

The canonical first-order transport reconstruction is therefore
\begin{align}
V^\mu_{\mathrm{med}}(\xi)
&=
\theta'(\xi)\,v_\parallel^{(0),\mathrm{med}}(\xi)\,n^\mu\sigma_3
+
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\sigma_3
\nonumber\\
&\quad
+
\theta'(\xi)\,v_E^{\mathrm{med}}(\xi)\,E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
+
\theta'(\xi)\,v_O^{\mathrm{med}}(\xi)\,J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
+
V_{\mathrm{irr}}^\mu(\xi),
\label{eq:Vmed_reconstruct}
\end{align}
with
\begin{equation}
v_\parallel^{(0),\mathrm{med}}(\xi)\sim s_3^{\mathrm{med}}(\xi),
\qquad
v_E^{\mathrm{med}}(\xi)\sim s_1^{\mathrm{med}}(\xi),
\qquad
v_O^{\mathrm{med}}(\xi)\sim s_2^{\mathrm{med}}(\xi).
\label{eq:v_from_s_med}
\end{equation}

Hence the coefficient-point contribution of the mediated block is
\begin{equation}
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0),\mathrm{med}}
=
\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,\theta'(\xi)\,v_\parallel^{(0),\mathrm{med}}(\xi),
\label{eq:Lambda0_med}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\Lambda_E^{\mathrm{med}}
=
\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,\theta'(\xi)\,v_E^{\mathrm{med}}(\xi),
\label{eq:LambdaE_med}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\Lambda_O^{\mathrm{med}}
=
\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,\theta'(\xi)\,v_O^{\mathrm{med}}(\xi).
\label{eq:LambdaO_med}
\end{equation}

So the full coefficient dictionary becomes
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel
=
I_\theta\Lambda_\parallel^{(0),\mathrm{med}}
+
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3}
+\cdots,
\label{eq:lambdapar_med}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\alpha
=
I_\theta\Lambda_E^{\mathrm{med}}+\cdots,
\qquad
\beta
=
I_\theta\Lambda_O^{\mathrm{med}}+\cdots .
\label{eq:alphabeta_med}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Step 7: sufficient nonvanishing criteria}

The mediated block passes the finite audit if the following hold.

\paragraph{Longitudinal}
\begin{equation}
\exists \xi_0:
\sum_{i,a}
|\mathcal C_{i a;1}(\xi_0)|^2
\neq
\sum_{i,a}
|\mathcal C_{i a;2}(\xi_0)|^2
\Longrightarrow
s_3^{\mathrm{med}}\not\equiv 0.
\label{eq:longitudinal_sufficient_med}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Even transverse}
\begin{equation}
\exists \xi_0:
\sum_{i,a}
\Re\!\left(
\overline{\mathcal C_{i a;1}(\xi_0)}\mathcal C_{i a;2}(\xi_0)
\right)\neq 0
\Longrightarrow
s_1^{\mathrm{med}}\not\equiv 0.
\label{eq:even_sufficient_med}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Odd transverse}
\begin{equation}
\exists \xi_0:
\sum_{i,a}
\Im\!\left(
\overline{\mathcal C_{i a;1}(\xi_0)}\mathcal C_{i a;2}(\xi_0)
\right)\neq 0
\Longrightarrow
s_2^{\mathrm{med}}\not\equiv 0.
\label{eq:odd_sufficient_med}
\end{equation}

These are exact finite checks.

\subsection{Step 8: final mediated-block decision tree}

The mediated block alone is sufficient for local Dirac emergence if either

\begin{equation}
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0),\mathrm{med}}\neq 0,
\qquad
(\Lambda_E^{\mathrm{med}},\Lambda_O^{\mathrm{med}})\neq (0,0),
\label{eq:med_branchA}
\end{equation}
or
\begin{equation}
\lambda_c\neq 0,
\qquad
(\Lambda_E^{\mathrm{med}},\Lambda_O^{\mathrm{med}})\neq (0,0).
\label{eq:med_branchB}
\end{equation}

In the exact concrete Class II normalization this is the same as
\begin{equation}
g_c\neq 0,
\qquad
(g_E,g_O)\neq (0,0).
\label{eq:gcgego_again}
\end{equation}

\section{Final Summary}

The mediated block in the adapted \(Q_B\)-frame is determined by the current amplitudes
\[
\mathcal C_{i a;m}(\xi)=\langle e_m(\xi),\mathcal J_{i,\mathrm{lin}}^a\rangle.
\]
Its exact Hermitian response matrix is
\[
r_{mn}^{\mathrm{med}}(\xi)
=
-\frac{1}{M_X^2}
\sum_{i,a}
\overline{\mathcal C_{i a;m}(\xi)}\mathcal C_{i a;n}(\xi).
\]
Therefore
\[
r_{11}^{\mathrm{med}}
=
-\frac{1}{M_X^2}\sum_{i,a}|\mathcal C_{i a;1}|^2,
\qquad
r_{22}^{\mathrm{med}}
=
-\frac{1}{M_X^2}\sum_{i,a}|\mathcal C_{i a;2}|^2,
\]
\[
r_{12}^{\mathrm{med}}
=
-\frac{1}{M_X^2}\sum_{i,a}\overline{\mathcal C_{i a;1}}\mathcal C_{i a;2}.
\]
Hence the Pauli coefficients are
\[
s_3^{\mathrm{med}}
=
-\frac{1}{2M_X^2}\sum_{i,a}\left(|\mathcal C_{i a;1}|^2-|\mathcal C_{i a;2}|^2\right),
\]
\[
s_1^{\mathrm{med}}
=
-\frac{1}{M_X^2}\sum_{i,a}\Re(\overline{\mathcal C_{i a;1}}\mathcal C_{i a;2}),
\qquad
s_2^{\mathrm{med}}
=
\frac{1}{M_X^2}\sum_{i,a}\Im(\overline{\mathcal C_{i a;1}}\mathcal C_{i a;2}).
\]

Thus the mediated block is the explicit microscopic carrier of:

\[
\text{norm imbalance } \to s_3 \to \Lambda_\parallel^{(0)} \text{ or } \lambda_c,
\]
\[
\text{real coherence } \to s_1 \to \Lambda_E,
\]
\[
\text{imaginary coherence } \to s_2 \to \Lambda_O.
\]

So the remaining frontier is the explicit evaluation of the current amplitudes \(\mathcal C_{i a;m}(\xi)\) from the complete final TECT mediator/current sector.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%


\section{Explicit Tensor-Contraction Form of the Linearized Mediator Current}

\subsection{Short Korean explanation}

The only remaining concrete step is to write the linearized mediator current
\[
\mathcal J_{i,\mathrm{lin}}^a
\]
in a basis adapted to:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the shell direction \(\hat n_i\),
\item the transverse shell basis \((e_{1j},e_{2j})\),
\item the defect-frame basis \((e_1(\xi),e_2(\xi))\subset Q_B(\xi)\).
\end{enumerate}

Once this is done, the adapted-frame amplitudes
\[
\mathcal C_{ia;m}(\xi)=\langle e_m(\xi),\mathcal J_{i,\mathrm{lin}}^a(\xi)\rangle
\]
are explicit, and then
\[
r_{11}^{\mathrm{med}},\quad r_{22}^{\mathrm{med}},\quad r_{12}^{\mathrm{med}}
\]
follow immediately.

\subsection{Step 1: linearized Class II current split}

For the Class II UV structure
\[
L_{\mathrm{UV}}^{(II)}
=
\frac{M_X^2}{2}X_i^aX_i^a
+\alpha\,X_i^a J_i^a(\Psi)
+\beta\,X_i^a K_i^a(P,\delta P),
\]
the linearized mediator current is the sum of two pieces:
\begin{equation}
\mathcal J_{i,\mathrm{lin}}^a
=
\alpha\,J_{i,\mathrm{lin}}^a
+
\beta\,K_{i,\mathrm{lin}}^a.
\label{eq:Jlin_split}
\end{equation}

We now parametrize them in the minimal shell-defect carrier form.

\subsection{Step 2: shell-gradient factorization}

The shell current must carry one spatial index and one internal index, so the minimal first-order shell-gradient factorization is
\begin{equation}
J_{i,\mathrm{lin}}^a(\xi)
=
m^a(\xi)\,C_{ij}^{ab}(\xi)\,\partial_j \psi_b(\xi),
\label{eq:Jlin_factorized}
\end{equation}
where:

\begin{itemize}
\item \(m^a(\xi)\) is the defect/background-dependent internal selector,
\item \(C_{ij}^{ab}(\xi)\) is the shell-adapted carrier tensor,
\item \(\psi_b(\xi)\) is the reduced \(Q_B\)-doublet fluctuation in the adapted frame.
\end{itemize}

In the explicit minimal Class II seed basis,
\begin{equation}
m^a(P_0)=m\,\delta^{a3},
\label{eq:m_a_seed}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
C^{33}_{ij}=c_\parallel \hat n_i\hat n_j,
\label{eq:C33_seed}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
C^{31}_{ij}
=
c_I \hat n_i e_{1j}
+
c_J \hat n_i e_{2j},
\label{eq:C31_seed}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
C^{32}_{ij}
=
- c_J \hat n_i e_{1j}
+
c_I \hat n_i e_{2j}.
\label{eq:C32_seed}
\end{equation}

Thus only the \(a=3\) mediator direction is populated in the minimal longitudinal selector, while the \(b=1,2,3\) labels resolve the reduced shell channels.

\subsection{Step 3: adapted doublet expansion of the fluctuation}

Expand the reduced projector/shell fluctuation in the defect frame:
\begin{equation}
\psi(\xi)=\psi_1(\xi)e_1(\xi)+\psi_2(\xi)e_2(\xi).
\label{eq:psi_expand_e}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
\partial_j \psi
=
(\partial_j\psi_1)e_1+(\partial_j\psi_2)e_2
+
\psi_1\,\partial_j e_1+\psi_2\,\partial_j e_2.
\label{eq:dpsi_expand}
\end{equation}

At principal local transport order, we keep only the direct amplitude-gradient part and absorb frame-rotation terms into higher-order or connection-like remainders. Thus
\begin{equation}
\partial_j\psi
\approx
(\partial_j\psi_1)e_1+(\partial_j\psi_2)e_2.
\label{eq:dpsi_local_principal}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Step 4: explicit current amplitudes in the seed basis}

Using \eqref{eq:Jlin_factorized}--\eqref{eq:dpsi_local_principal}, the adapted current amplitudes are
\begin{equation}
\mathcal C_{ia;m}
=
\langle e_m,\mathcal J_{i,\mathrm{lin}}^a\rangle
=
\alpha\,m^a C_{ij}^{ab}\,\partial_j\psi_b^{(m)}
+
\beta\,\mathcal K_{ia;m},
\label{eq:Ciam_general}
\end{equation}
where \(\mathcal K_{ia;m}:=\langle e_m,K_{i,\mathrm{lin}}^a\rangle\) is the projector/tangent source amplitude.

Inside the minimal seed family, the shell-current part becomes:

\paragraph{Longitudinal channel.}
For \(b=3\),
\begin{equation}
\mathcal C_{i3;m}^{(\parallel)}
=
\alpha\,m\,c_\parallel\,\hat n_i\hat n_j\,\partial_j\psi_m.
\label{eq:Cparallel_explicit}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Even/odd transverse channels.}
For \(b=1,2\),
\begin{equation}
\mathcal C_{i1;m}^{(\perp)}
=
\alpha\,m\,
\bigl(
c_I \hat n_i e_{1j}+c_J \hat n_i e_{2j}
\bigr)\partial_j\psi_m,
\label{eq:C1perp_explicit}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\mathcal C_{i2;m}^{(\perp)}
=
\alpha\,m\,
\bigl(
- c_J \hat n_i e_{1j}+c_I \hat n_i e_{2j}
\bigr)\partial_j\psi_m.
\label{eq:C2perp_explicit}
\end{equation}

Thus the mediator current amplitudes are explicitly axial in \(i\) and decompose into the three shell channels \((\parallel,E,O)\).

\subsection{Step 5: contraction with the shell frame}

Introduce the directional derivatives
\[
\partial_\parallel:=\hat n_j\partial_j,
\qquad
\partial_1:=e_{1j}\partial_j,
\qquad
\partial_2:=e_{2j}\partial_j.
\]
Then \eqref{eq:Cparallel_explicit}--\eqref{eq:C2perp_explicit} simplify to
\begin{equation}
\mathcal C_{i3;m}^{(\parallel)}
=
\alpha\,m\,c_\parallel\,\hat n_i\,\partial_\parallel\psi_m,
\label{eq:Cparallel_dir}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\mathcal C_{i1;m}^{(\perp)}
=
\alpha\,m\,\hat n_i\,
\bigl(
c_I\partial_1+c_J\partial_2
\bigr)\psi_m,
\label{eq:C1perp_dir}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\mathcal C_{i2;m}^{(\perp)}
=
\alpha\,m\,\hat n_i\,
\bigl(
- c_J\partial_1+c_I\partial_2
\bigr)\psi_m.
\label{eq:C2perp_dir}
\end{equation}

This is the exact tensor-contraction form of the current amplitudes at principal order.

\subsection{Step 6: induced adapted-frame response}

Substituting \eqref{eq:Cparallel_dir}--\eqref{eq:C2perp_dir} into
\[
r_{mn}^{\mathrm{med}}
=
-\frac{1}{M_X^2}\sum_{i,a}
\overline{\mathcal C_{ia;m}}\mathcal C_{ia;n},
\]
we get the shell-current contribution
\begin{align}
r_{mn}^{\mathrm{med,shell}}
&=
-\frac{\alpha^2 m^2}{M_X^2}
\Big[
c_\parallel^2\,
\overline{\partial_\parallel\psi_m}\,\partial_\parallel\psi_n
\nonumber\\
&\qquad\qquad
+
(c_I^2+c_J^2)\,
\Big(
\overline{\partial_1\psi_m}\,\partial_1\psi_n
+
\overline{\partial_2\psi_m}\,\partial_2\psi_n
\Big)
\nonumber\\
&\qquad\qquad
+
2c_Ic_J\,
\Re\!\Big(
\overline{\partial_1\psi_m}\,\partial_2\psi_n
\Big)_{\mathrm{sym}}
+
2c_Ic_J\,
\Im\!\Big(
\overline{\partial_1\psi_m}\,\partial_2\psi_n
\Big)_{\mathrm{asym}}
\Big]
+\cdots .
\label{eq:rmed_shell_full}
\end{align}

More transparently, define
\begin{equation}
Q_{\parallel;mn}
:=
\overline{\partial_\parallel\psi_m}\,\partial_\parallel\psi_n,
\label{eq:Qparallel_def}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
Q_{E;mn}
:=
\overline{\partial_1\psi_m}\,\partial_1\psi_n
+
\overline{\partial_2\psi_m}\,\partial_2\psi_n,
\label{eq:QE_def}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
Q_{O;mn}
:=
\overline{\partial_1\psi_m}\,\partial_2\psi_n
-
\overline{\partial_2\psi_m}\,\partial_1\psi_n.
\label{eq:QO_def}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
r_{mn}^{\mathrm{med,shell}}
=
-\frac{\alpha^2 m^2}{M_X^2}
\Bigl[
c_\parallel^2\,Q_{\parallel;mn}
+
(c_I^2+c_J^2)\,Q_{E;mn}
+
c_Ic_J\,Q_{O;mn}
\Bigr]
+\cdots .
\label{eq:rmed_shell_compact}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Step 7: reading the three witness channels}

From
\[
s_3^{\mathrm{med}}=\frac12(r_{11}^{\mathrm{med}}-r_{22}^{\mathrm{med}}),
\qquad
s_1^{\mathrm{med}}=\Re r_{12}^{\mathrm{med}},
\qquad
s_2^{\mathrm{med}}=-\Im r_{12}^{\mathrm{med}},
\]
we obtain:

\paragraph{Longitudinal singlet.}
\begin{equation}
s_3^{\mathrm{med}}
=
-\frac{\alpha^2 m^2}{2M_X^2}
\Bigl[
c_\parallel^2\,(Q_{\parallel;11}-Q_{\parallel;22})
+
(c_I^2+c_J^2)(Q_{E;11}-Q_{E;22})
+
c_Ic_J(Q_{O;11}-Q_{O;22})
\Bigr]
+\cdots
\label{eq:s3_med_explicit}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Even transverse.}
\begin{equation}
s_1^{\mathrm{med}}
=
-\frac{\alpha^2 m^2}{M_X^2}
\Re\Bigl[
c_\parallel^2\,Q_{\parallel;12}
+
(c_I^2+c_J^2)\,Q_{E;12}
+
c_Ic_J\,Q_{O;12}
\Bigr]
+\cdots
\label{eq:s1_med_explicit}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Odd transverse.}
\begin{equation}
s_2^{\mathrm{med}}
=
\frac{\alpha^2 m^2}{M_X^2}
\Im\Bigl[
c_\parallel^2\,Q_{\parallel;12}
+
(c_I^2+c_J^2)\,Q_{E;12}
+
c_Ic_J\,Q_{O;12}
\Bigr]
+\cdots
\label{eq:s2_med_explicit}
\end{equation}

So the full microscopic meaning is now explicit:

\begin{itemize}
\item \(c_\parallel\) controls the longitudinal axial carrier,
\item \(c_I^2+c_J^2\) controls the magnitude of the transverse doublet sector,
\item \(c_Ic_J\) controls the mixed even/odd interference structure.
\end{itemize}

\subsection{Step 8: minimal seed limits}

The three pure seed limits are immediate.

\paragraph{Pure longitudinal seed}
\[
c_\parallel\neq 0,\qquad c_I=c_J=0
\]
gives
\begin{equation}
s_3^{\mathrm{med}}\sim -\frac{\alpha^2m^2}{2M_X^2}c_\parallel^2(Q_{\parallel;11}-Q_{\parallel;22}),
\qquad
s_1^{\mathrm{med}}\sim -\frac{\alpha^2m^2}{M_X^2}\Re(c_\parallel^2Q_{\parallel;12}),
\qquad
s_2^{\mathrm{med}}\sim \frac{\alpha^2m^2}{M_X^2}\Im(c_\parallel^2Q_{\parallel;12}).
\label{eq:pure_long_seed_limit}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Pure even transverse seed}
\[
c_\parallel=0,\qquad c_I\neq 0,\qquad c_J=0
\]
gives
\begin{equation}
r_{mn}^{\mathrm{med,shell}}
=
-\frac{\alpha^2m^2}{M_X^2}c_I^2\,Q_{E;mn},
\label{eq:pure_even_seed_limit}
\end{equation}
hence \(s_1,s_2\) arise from the coherence structure of \(Q_{E;12}\).

\paragraph{Pure odd transverse seed}
\[
c_\parallel=0,\qquad c_I=0,\qquad c_J\neq 0
\]
gives again
\begin{equation}
r_{mn}^{\mathrm{med,shell}}
=
-\frac{\alpha^2m^2}{M_X^2}c_J^2\,Q_{E;mn},
\label{eq:pure_odd_seed_limit}
\end{equation}
so the difference between \(g_E\) and \(g_O\) is not the norm sector alone, but the shell-frame orientation built into the basis choice \((C^{31},C^{32})\).

\subsection{Step 9: coefficient-point extraction}

Therefore the induced principal transport densities are, schematically,
\begin{equation}
v_\parallel^{(0),\mathrm{med}}(\xi)\sim s_3^{\mathrm{med}}(\xi),
\qquad
v_E^{\mathrm{med}}(\xi)\sim s_1^{\mathrm{med}}(\xi),
\qquad
v_O^{\mathrm{med}}(\xi)\sim s_2^{\mathrm{med}}(\xi),
\label{eq:v_from_s_final}
\end{equation}
and hence
\begin{equation}
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0),\mathrm{med}}
=
\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,\theta'(\xi)\,v_\parallel^{(0),\mathrm{med}}(\xi),
\label{eq:Lambda0_med_final}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\Lambda_E^{\mathrm{med}}
=
\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,\theta'(\xi)\,v_E^{\mathrm{med}}(\xi),
\qquad
\Lambda_O^{\mathrm{med}}
=
\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,\theta'(\xi)\,v_O^{\mathrm{med}}(\xi).
\label{eq:LambdaEO_med_final}
\end{equation}

In the exact reduced Class II dictionary this is summarized as
\[
g_c\propto c_\parallel,\qquad
g_E\propto c_I,\qquad
g_O\propto c_J,
\]
which is exactly the already-established witness map.

\section{Final Summary}

The linearized mediator current in the minimal Class II seed basis is explicitly
\[
\mathcal C_{i3;m}
=
\alpha m c_\parallel\,\hat n_i\,\partial_\parallel\psi_m,
\]
\[
\mathcal C_{i1;m}
=
\alpha m \hat n_i(c_I\partial_1+c_J\partial_2)\psi_m,
\]
\[
\mathcal C_{i2;m}
=
\alpha m \hat n_i(-c_J\partial_1+c_I\partial_2)\psi_m.
\]

Therefore the mediated \(Q_B\)-response is
\[
r_{mn}^{\mathrm{med}}
=
-\frac{1}{M_X^2}\sum_{i,a}\overline{\mathcal C_{ia;m}}\mathcal C_{ia;n},
\]
which yields explicit formulas for
\[
s_3^{\mathrm{med}},\qquad s_1^{\mathrm{med}},\qquad s_2^{\mathrm{med}}.
\]

At the coefficient level:

\[
c_\parallel \text{ controls the longitudinal carrier,}
\]
\[
(c_I,c_J) \text{ control the transverse doublet carrier,}
\]
\[
c_Ic_J \text{ controls even/odd interference.}
\]

Thus the remaining microscopic work is no longer structural.
It is the explicit evaluation of the local derivative bilinears
\[
Q_{\parallel;mn},\qquad Q_{E;mn},\qquad Q_{O;mn}
\]
in the actual defect background, after which
\[
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0),\mathrm{med}},\ \Lambda_E^{\mathrm{med}},\ \Lambda_O^{\mathrm{med}}
\]
follow immediately.

\section{Explicit current-amplitude form of the mediated block}

In the minimal Class II seed basis,
\[
m^a(P_0)=m\delta^{a3},
\qquad
C^{33}_{ij}=c_\parallel \hat n_i\hat n_j,
\]
\[
C^{31}_{ij}=c_I\hat n_i e_{1j}+c_J\hat n_i e_{2j},
\qquad
C^{32}_{ij}=-c_J\hat n_i e_{1j}+c_I\hat n_i e_{2j}.
\]

Therefore the adapted current amplitudes are
\[
\mathcal C_{i3;m}
=
\alpha m c_\parallel\,\hat n_i\,\partial_\parallel\psi_m,
\]
\[
\mathcal C_{i1;m}
=
\alpha m \hat n_i(c_I\partial_1+c_J\partial_2)\psi_m,
\]
\[
\mathcal C_{i2;m}
=
\alpha m \hat n_i(-c_J\partial_1+c_I\partial_2)\psi_m.
\]

The mediated response matrix is then
\[
r_{mn}^{\mathrm{med}}
=
-\frac{1}{M_X^2}\sum_{i,a}\overline{\mathcal C_{ia;m}}\mathcal C_{ia;n},
\]
so the Pauli coefficients \(s_3^{\mathrm{med}},s_1^{\mathrm{med}},s_2^{\mathrm{med}}\) are explicit functions of the local derivative bilinears
\[
Q_{\parallel;mn},\qquad Q_{E;mn},\qquad Q_{O;mn}.
\]

Thus the remaining microscopic task is exactly the evaluation of these bilinears in the actual defect background.


%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Principal First-Order Mediated Symbol from the Background-Linear Cross Term}

\subsection{Short Korean explanation}

For the actual graded \(2+2\) coefficient extraction, the relevant mediated contribution is not the quadratic norm piece
\[
J_{\mathrm{lin}}J_{\mathrm{lin}},
\]
but the background-linear cross term
\[
J_{\mathrm{bg}}J_{\mathrm{lin}}.
\]
This is the unique part that is:

\begin{enumerate}
\item first order in the fluctuation,
\item first order in the transport derivative,
\item linear in the seed coefficients \(c_\parallel,c_I,c_J\),
\item consistent with the already-established dictionary
\[
g_c\propto c_\parallel,\qquad
g_E\propto c_I,\qquad
g_O\propto c_J.
\]
\end{enumerate}

\subsection{Step 1: mediator elimination and transport-relevant cross term}

Let the mediator sector be
\begin{equation}
L_X
=
\frac{M_X^2}{2}X_i^aX_i^a
+
X_i^a\,\mathcal J_i^a[\Phi].
\label{eq:LX_start_final}
\end{equation}
Expand the current around the defect/background:
\begin{equation}
\mathcal J_i^a[\Phi_0+\delta\Phi]
=
\mathcal J_{i,\mathrm{bg}}^a
+
\mathcal J_{i,\mathrm{lin}}^a[\delta\Phi]
+
O(\delta\Phi^2).
\label{eq:J_expand_bg_lin}
\end{equation}
Integrating out \(X_i^a\) gives
\begin{equation}
\delta L_{\mathrm{eff}}^{\mathrm{med}}
=
-\frac{1}{2M_X^2}
\bigl(
\mathcal J_{i,\mathrm{bg}}^a+\mathcal J_{i,\mathrm{lin}}^a
\bigr)
\bigl(
\mathcal J_{i,\mathrm{bg}}^a+\mathcal J_{i,\mathrm{lin}}^a
\bigr).
\label{eq:Leff_after_X}
\end{equation}

The principal first-order transport piece is the cross term
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta L_{\mathrm{eff}}^{(1)}
=
-\frac{1}{M_X^2}\,
\mathcal J_{i,\mathrm{bg}}^a\,
\mathcal J_{i,\mathrm{lin}}^a.
}
\label{eq:cross_term_principal}
\end{equation}
This is the correct source of the coefficient point
\[
(\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)},\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O).
\]

\subsection{Step 2: minimal shell-defect current ansatz}

We now take the minimal shell-defect carrier form
\begin{equation}
\mathcal J_{i,\mathrm{bg}}^a(\xi)
=
\mu_X\,\theta'(\xi)\,\hat n_i\,m^a,
\label{eq:Jbg_minimal}
\end{equation}
where \(m^a\) is the background internal selector.

For the linearized current, use the shell-gradient factorization
\begin{equation}
\mathcal J_{i,\mathrm{lin}}^a
=
\nu_X\,m^b C_{ij}^{ba}\,\partial_j\psi
+
\mathcal J_{i,\mathrm{lin}}^{a,\mathrm{rem}},
\label{eq:Jlin_factor_final}
\end{equation}
with the explicit minimal Class II seed basis
\begin{equation}
m^a=m\,\delta^{a3},
\label{eq:m_seed_final}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
C_{ij}^{33}=c_\parallel \hat n_i\hat n_j,
\label{eq:C33_final}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
C_{ij}^{31}=c_I \hat n_i e_{1j}+c_J \hat n_i e_{2j},
\label{eq:C31_final}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
C_{ij}^{32}=-c_J \hat n_i e_{1j}+c_I \hat n_i e_{2j}.
\label{eq:C32_final}
\end{equation}

Thus the effective transport prefactor is
\begin{equation}
\Gamma_X:=\frac{\mu_X\nu_X m^2}{M_X^2}.
\label{eq:GammaX_def}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Step 3: adapted defect mode ansatz}

Take the graded low modes in the standard factorized form
\begin{equation}
u_m^\pm(\xi,y)
=
f_\pm(\xi)\,e_m(\xi)\,\chi^\pm(y),
\qquad
m=1,2,
\label{eq:um_pm_factorized}
\end{equation}
where \(y^\mu\) are slow worldvolume coordinates and \(\xi\) is the normal/defect coordinate.

At principal order, the frame \(e_m(\xi)\) depends only on \(\xi\), so the worldvolume derivatives act only on \(\chi^\pm(y)\):
\begin{equation}
\partial_\parallel u_m^\pm
=
f_\pm(\xi)e_m(\xi)\,\partial_\parallel\chi^\pm(y)
+
O(\partial_\xi),
\label{eq:dpar_u}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\partial_1 u_m^\pm
=
f_\pm(\xi)e_m(\xi)\,\partial_1\chi^\pm(y),
\qquad
\partial_2 u_m^\pm
=
f_\pm(\xi)e_m(\xi)\,\partial_2\chi^\pm(y).
\label{eq:d12_u}
\end{equation}

For a local plane-wave symbol extraction, write
\[
\chi^\pm(y)\sim e^{ip\cdot y},
\]
so that
\[
\partial_\parallel\chi^\pm=i p_\parallel\chi^\pm,
\qquad
\partial_1\chi^\pm=i p_1\chi^\pm,
\qquad
\partial_2\chi^\pm=i p_2\chi^\pm.
\]

\subsection{Step 4: projected mixed matrix elements}

The transport matrix elements are obtained from the mixed graded projection
\begin{equation}
(M^\mu)_{mn}
=
\langle u_m^+,\;V^\mu_{\mathrm{med}}\;u_n^-\rangle.
\label{eq:Mmu_mixed_def}
\end{equation}
Using \eqref{eq:cross_term_principal}--\eqref{eq:d12_u}, the principal mediated symbol is linear in \(p\) and factorizes as
\begin{equation}
(M^\mu)_{mn}
=
I_\theta\,
\Bigl[
\Gamma_X c_\parallel\,n^\mu p_\parallel\,(\sigma_3)_{mn}
+
\Gamma_X c_I\,E^\mu{}_a p_a\,(\sigma_a)_{mn}
+
\Gamma_X c_J\,J^\mu{}_a p_a\,(\sigma_a)_{mn}
\Bigr]
+
O(p^2),
\label{eq:Mmu_factorized_symbol}
\end{equation}
where the universal defect overlap is
\begin{equation}
I_\theta
:=
\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,\theta'(\xi).
\label{eq:Itheta_def_final}
\end{equation}

This is the exact first-order mediated symbol in the minimal seed basis.

\subsection{Step 5: direct reading of the coefficient point}

Comparing \eqref{eq:Mmu_factorized_symbol} with the canonical S2 transport form
\begin{equation}
V^\mu_{\mathrm{S2}}
=
h_\parallel(\xi)\,n^\mu\sigma_3
+
h_E(\xi)\,E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
+
h_O(\xi)\,J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a,
\label{eq:VS2_target_final}
\end{equation}
we read off immediately
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0),\mathrm{med}}=\Gamma_X c_\parallel,
\qquad
\Lambda_E^{\mathrm{med}}=\Gamma_X c_I,
\qquad
\Lambda_O^{\mathrm{med}}=\Gamma_X c_J.
}
\label{eq:Lambda_med_direct}
\end{equation}

Therefore the mediated contribution to the reduced coefficients is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel^{(A),\mathrm{med}}
=
I_\theta\,\Gamma_X c_\parallel,
\qquad
\alpha^{\mathrm{med}}
=
I_\theta\,\Gamma_X c_I,
\qquad
\beta^{\mathrm{med}}
=
I_\theta\,\Gamma_X c_J.
}
\label{eq:lamb_alpha_beta_med_A}
\end{equation}

This is exactly the desired linear seed dictionary.

\subsection{Step 6: Branch B longitudinal term}

Independently of the direct mediated longitudinal branch above, the primitive commutator-square source gives
\begin{equation}
V^\mu_{(\parallel),B}
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\sigma_3,
\label{eq:VB_longitudinal}
\end{equation}
hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel^{(B)}
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
I_{\theta'^3}:=
\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\theta'(\xi)^3.
}
\label{eq:lambdaB_final}
\end{equation}

Combining Branch A and Branch B,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
I_\theta\,\Gamma_X c_\parallel
+
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=I_\theta\,\Gamma_X c_I,
\qquad
\beta=I_\theta\,\Gamma_X c_J.
}
\label{eq:final_combined_coeffs}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Step 7: exact Weyl/Dirac finite test}

The principal graded Dirac condition is therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
I_\theta\,\Gamma_X c_\parallel+\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3}\neq 0,
\qquad
(c_I,c_J)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:principal_finite_test}
\end{equation}

More explicitly:

\paragraph{Branch A}
\begin{equation}
\Gamma_X c_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(c_I,c_J)\neq (0,0).
\label{eq:branchA_final_final}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Branch B}
\begin{equation}
\Gamma_X c_\parallel=0,
\qquad
\lambda_c\neq 0,
\qquad
(c_I,c_J)\neq (0,0).
\label{eq:branchB_final_final}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Step 8: matching to the established reduced dictionary}

Define
\begin{equation}
g_c:=\Gamma_X c_\parallel,
\qquad
g_E:=\Gamma_X c_I,
\qquad
g_O:=\Gamma_X c_J.
\label{eq:g_match_def}
\end{equation}
Then \eqref{eq:final_combined_coeffs} becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
I_\theta g_c+\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=I_\theta g_E,
\qquad
\beta=I_\theta g_O.
}
\label{eq:g_dictionary_final}
\end{equation}

So the exact current-level computation reproduces the reduced witness map
\[
g_c\propto c_\parallel,\qquad
g_E\propto c_I,\qquad
g_O\propto c_J,
\]
now with the explicit proportionality constant
\[
\Gamma_X=\frac{\mu_X\nu_Xm^2}{M_X^2}.
\]

\section{Final Summary}

The principal first-order mediated transport symbol comes from the background-linear cross term
\[
-\frac{1}{M_X^2}\mathcal J_{i,\mathrm{bg}}^a\mathcal J_{i,\mathrm{lin}}^a,
\]
not from the quadratic norm piece \(J_{\mathrm{lin}}J_{\mathrm{lin}}\).

With the minimal seed basis
\[
C^{33}_{ij}=c_\parallel\hat n_i\hat n_j,\qquad
C^{31}_{ij}=c_I\hat n_i e_{1j}+c_J\hat n_i e_{2j},\qquad
C^{32}_{ij}=-c_J\hat n_i e_{1j}+c_I\hat n_i e_{2j},
\]
and the factorized low-mode ansatz
\[
u_m^\pm=f_\pm(\xi)e_m(\xi)\chi^\pm(y),
\]
the mediated coefficient point is read off exactly as
\[
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0),\mathrm{med}}=\Gamma_X c_\parallel,\qquad
\Lambda_E^{\mathrm{med}}=\Gamma_X c_I,\qquad
\Lambda_O^{\mathrm{med}}=\Gamma_X c_J,
\]
with
\[
\Gamma_X=\frac{\mu_X\nu_Xm^2}{M_X^2}.
\]

Hence the full reduced coefficients are
\[
\lambda_\parallel
=
I_\theta\,\Gamma_X c_\parallel
+
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=I_\theta\,\Gamma_X c_I,
\qquad
\beta=I_\theta\,\Gamma_X c_J.
\]

Therefore the remaining microscopic task is no longer structural.
It is only the explicit evaluation of the background prefactors \(\mu_X,\nu_X,m\) and the overlap integrals \(I_\theta,I_{\theta'^3}\) for the actual defect profile.

\section{Principal mediated coefficient extraction}

The principal first-order mediated symbol is generated by the background-linear cross term
\[
-\frac{1}{M_X^2}\mathcal J_{i,\mathrm{bg}}^a\mathcal J_{i,\mathrm{lin}}^a.
\]
Using the minimal Class II seed basis, one obtains
\[
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0),\mathrm{med}}=\Gamma_X c_\parallel,\qquad
\Lambda_E^{\mathrm{med}}=\Gamma_X c_I,\qquad
\Lambda_O^{\mathrm{med}}=\Gamma_X c_J,
\]
with
\[
\Gamma_X=\frac{\mu_X\nu_Xm^2}{M_X^2}.
\]
Hence the reduced coefficients are
\[
\lambda_\parallel
=
I_\theta\,\Gamma_X c_\parallel
+\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=I_\theta\,\Gamma_X c_I,
\qquad
\beta=I_\theta\,\Gamma_X c_J.
\]
So the final finite test is
\[
I_\theta\,\Gamma_X c_\parallel+\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3}\neq 0,
\qquad
(c_I,c_J)\neq (0,0).
\]
The remaining work is the explicit evaluation of \(\mu_X,\nu_X,m\) and the overlap integrals \(I_\theta,I_{\theta'^3}\) in the actual defect background.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Explicit Overlap Completion of the Graded \(2+2\) Coefficient Point}

\subsection{Short Korean explanation}

At this stage, the overlap integrals are already explicitly known.
Therefore the reduced S2 coefficients can now be written in fully explicit closed form.

This finishes the overlap-completion step of the graded \(2+2\) mainline.

\subsection{Step 1: explicit overlap values}

For the explicit defect and low-mode profiles already used in the concrete seed/Class II branch,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
I_\theta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\theta_0\kappa
\neq 0,
}
\label{eq:Itheta_closed}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
I_{\theta'^3}
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{256}\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3
\neq 0,
}
\label{eq:Itheta3_closed}
\end{equation}
for nontrivial defect amplitude
\[
\theta_0\kappa\neq 0.
\]

\subsection{Step 2: exact Class II coefficient dictionary}

In the exact concrete Class II-compatible local branch, the reduced coefficients are
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=I_\theta\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta=I_\theta\Lambda_O.
\label{eq:coeff_dictionary_exact}
\end{equation}
Substituting \eqref{eq:Itheta_closed}--\eqref{eq:Itheta3_closed} gives
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,\lambda_c\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
}
\label{eq:lambda_explicit_closed}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\Lambda_E\,\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\Lambda_O\,\theta_0\kappa.
}
\label{eq:alphabeta_explicit_closed}
\end{equation}

Thus the full coefficient point is now explicit.

\subsection{Step 3: reduced principal symbol}

The reduced S2 symbol is therefore
\begin{equation}
A_1(p)
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,\lambda_c\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3\,p_\parallel\sigma_3
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\theta_0\kappa
\left[
\Lambda_E(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\Lambda_O(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2)
\right].
\label{eq:A1_explicit_closed}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, the coefficient matrix is
\begin{equation}
\Lambda_{\mathrm{eff}}
=
\begin{pmatrix}
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa\,\Lambda_E
&
+\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa\,\Lambda_O
&
0
\\[1ex]
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa\,\Lambda_O
&
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa\,\Lambda_E
&
0
\\[1ex]
0&0&
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\lambda_c\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3
\end{pmatrix}.
\label{eq:Lambda_eff_matrix}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Step 4: determinant and exact nondegeneracy test}

The determinant is
\begin{equation}
\det\Lambda_{\mathrm{eff}}
=
\lambda_\parallel(\alpha^2+\beta^2).
\label{eq:det_general_again}
\end{equation}
Substituting \eqref{eq:lambda_explicit_closed}--\eqref{eq:alphabeta_explicit_closed},
\begin{align}
\det\Lambda_{\mathrm{eff}}
&=
\left(
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\lambda_c\theta_0^3\kappa^3
\right)
\left[
\left(
\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa
\right)^2
(\Lambda_E^2+\Lambda_O^2)
\right]
\nonumber\\
&=
-\frac{9\sqrt3\,\pi^3}{131072}\,
\lambda_c\,\theta_0^5\kappa^5\,
(\Lambda_E^2+\Lambda_O^2).
\label{eq:det_explicit_closed}
\end{align}

Therefore the exact finite nondegeneracy condition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\theta_0\kappa\neq 0,
\qquad
\lambda_c\neq 0,
\qquad
(\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:nondeg_exact_closed}
\end{equation}

This is precisely the already-established branch-B criterion, now with all overlap constants inserted explicitly.

\subsection{Step 5: explicit transverse magnitude and anisotropy ratio}

Define the transverse magnitude
\begin{equation}
\Lambda_\perp:=\sqrt{\Lambda_E^2+\Lambda_O^2}.
\label{eq:Lambda_perp_def}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
v_\perp
=
\sqrt{\alpha^2+\beta^2}
=
\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,|\theta_0\kappa|\,\Lambda_\perp,
\label{eq:vperp_closed}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
v_\parallel
=
|\lambda_\parallel|
=
\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,|\lambda_c|\,|\theta_0|^3|\kappa|^3.
\label{eq:vpar_closed}
\end{equation}

Hence the explicit anisotropy ratio is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\rho_{\mathrm{eff}}
:=
\frac{v_\parallel}{v_\perp}
=
\frac{3}{32}\,
\frac{|\lambda_c|}{\Lambda_\perp}\,
\theta_0^2\kappa^2.
}
\label{eq:rho_closed}
\end{equation}

So the graded Dirac cone is automatically anisotropic unless the microscopic coefficients are tuned so that
\[
\frac{|\lambda_c|}{\Lambda_\perp}\sim \frac{32}{3}\frac{1}{\theta_0^2\kappa^2}.
\]

\subsection{Step 6: branch-sensitive interpretation}

We now separate the two logically possible longitudinal branches.

\paragraph{Branch A.}
If the actual full microscopic transport extraction yields a constant-leading longitudinal invariant
\[
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}\neq 0,
\]
then one has instead
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel
=
I_\theta\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}\,\theta_0\kappa
+O(\theta_0^3\kappa^3).
\label{eq:branchA_lambda_explicit}
\end{equation}
In that case the leading anisotropy is
\begin{equation}
\rho_A
=
\frac{|\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}|}{\sqrt{\Lambda_E^2+\Lambda_O^2}}
+O(\theta_0^2\kappa^2).
\label{eq:rhoA_closed}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Branch B.}
If
\[
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0,
\]
then the first nonzero longitudinal term is the primitive channel:
\[
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\lambda_c\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
\]
and the anisotropy is given by \eqref{eq:rho_closed}.

Thus the full microscopic branch-selection problem is now sharply visible:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Branch A gives } \lambda_\parallel\sim O(\theta_0\kappa),
\qquad
\text{Branch B gives } \lambda_\parallel\sim O(\theta_0^3\kappa^3).
}
\label{eq:branch_scaling_difference}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Step 7: exact current status}

At the overlap-completed level, the following are now fully explicit:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the defect overlap constants \(I_\theta\) and \(I_{\theta'^3}\);
\item the reduced coefficient point \((\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta)\);
\item the reduced determinant \(\det\Lambda_{\mathrm{eff}}\);
\item the exact finite nondegeneracy criterion;
\item the branch-sensitive scaling of the longitudinal coefficient.
\end{enumerate}

What remains open is not the reduced symbol.
It is only the actual microscopic extraction of:
\[
\Lambda_E,\qquad
\Lambda_O,\qquad
\lambda_c,
\]
and, at a deeper level, whether the complete microscopic theory realizes Branch A or Branch B.

\section{Final Summary}

Using the explicitly evaluated defect overlaps
\[
I_\theta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
I_{\theta'^3}
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{256}\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
\]
the exact concrete Class II reduced coefficients become
\[
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\lambda_c\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
\qquad
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\Lambda_E\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\Lambda_O\theta_0\kappa.
\]

Therefore
\[
\det\Lambda_{\mathrm{eff}}
=
-\frac{9\sqrt3\pi^3}{131072}
\lambda_c\theta_0^5\kappa^5(\Lambda_E^2+\Lambda_O^2),
\]
so the exact graded nondegeneracy criterion is
\[
\theta_0\kappa\neq 0,
\qquad
\lambda_c\neq 0,
\qquad
(\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)\neq (0,0).
\]

The effective anisotropy ratio on Branch B is
\[
\rho_{\mathrm{eff}}
=
\frac{3}{32}\frac{|\lambda_c|}{\sqrt{\Lambda_E^2+\Lambda_O^2}}\theta_0^2\kappa^2.
\]

Thus the reduced symbol is now completely explicit.
The only remaining microscopic frontier is the actual extraction of
\(\lambda_c,\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O\) and the branch selection of the full TECT transport kernel.

\section{Actual-Local Invariant Expansion of the Complete TECT Transport Kernel}

\subsection{Short Korean explanation}

The reduced symbol is already closed at the structural level.
What remains is to express the complete local transport kernel in the defect background in terms of the minimal symmetry-allowed local invariants.

The goal is to derive canonical local expansions for
\[
h_\parallel(\xi),\qquad h_E(\xi),\qquad h_O(\xi),
\]
and then read off the leading coefficient point
\[
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)},\qquad \lambda_c,\qquad \Lambda_E^{(0)},\qquad \Lambda_O^{(0)}.
\]

\subsection{Step 1: canonical S2 transport form}

At principal first order, the complete local transport kernel must have the S2-compatible form
\begin{equation}
V^\mu(\xi)
=
h_\parallel(\xi)\,n^\mu\sigma_3
+
h_E(\xi)\,E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
+
h_O(\xi)\,J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
+
V^\mu_{\mathrm{irr}}(\xi),
\label{eq:Vmu_S2_complete}
\end{equation}
where \(a=1,2\), and \(V^\mu_{\mathrm{irr}}\) is projected out at principal S2 order.

The reduced coefficients are therefore
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel=\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,h_\parallel(\xi),
\label{eq:lambda_from_hpar_complete}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\alpha=\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,h_E(\xi),
\label{eq:alpha_from_hE_complete}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\beta=\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,h_O(\xi).
\label{eq:beta_from_hO_complete}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Step 2: local invariant algebra}

Let the defect profile be described by \(\theta(\xi)\).
The complete local transport density can depend only on scalar local invariants built from the defect background.

At the lowest derivative orders, the parity-even scalar invariants are generated by
\begin{equation}
X_0(\xi):=\theta(\xi)^2,
\qquad
X_1(\xi):=\theta'(\xi)^2,
\qquad
X_2(\xi):=\theta(\xi)\theta''(\xi),
\qquad
X_3(\xi):=\theta''(\xi)^2,
\quad \dots
\label{eq:Xi_def}
\end{equation}
More generally, write the complete parity-even local invariant list as
\begin{equation}
\mathcal X(\xi)=\bigl(X_0(\xi),X_1(\xi),X_2(\xi),\dots\bigr).
\label{eq:Xlist_def}
\end{equation}

The key symmetry fact is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{All scalar coefficient functions multiplying principal first-order transport tensors must be functions of } \mathcal X(\xi),
}
\label{eq:coeff_even_function}
\end{equation}
because \(\mathcal X\) is parity-even.

\subsection{Step 3: parity constraint on principal transport}

The graded mixed overlap involves
\[
f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi),
\]
with the standard parity assignment
\[
f_+(\xi)\ \text{even},
\qquad
f_-(\xi)\ \text{odd}.
\]
Hence
\[
f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)
\]
is odd.

Therefore only the odd part of each transport density contributes to
\eqref{eq:lambda_from_hpar_complete}--\eqref{eq:beta_from_hO_complete}.

Since every coefficient function of \(\mathcal X\) is parity-even, the principal transport densities must contain one explicit odd factor.
The lowest such factor is \(\theta'(\xi)\).

Thus the most general principal local expansions are
\begin{equation}
h_\parallel(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)\,\mathcal L_1(\mathcal X(\xi))
+
\theta'(\xi)^3\,\mathcal L_3(\mathcal X(\xi))
+
O_{\mathrm{odd},\ge 5},
\label{eq:hpar_general_expansion}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
h_E(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)\,\mathcal E_1(\mathcal X(\xi))
+
\theta'(\xi)^3\,\mathcal E_3(\mathcal X(\xi))
+
O_{\mathrm{odd},\ge 5},
\label{eq:hE_general_expansion}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
h_O(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)\,\mathcal O_1(\mathcal X(\xi))
+
\theta'(\xi)^3\,\mathcal O_3(\mathcal X(\xi))
+
O_{\mathrm{odd},\ge 5}.
\label{eq:hO_general_expansion}
\end{equation}

Here \(O_{\mathrm{odd},\ge 5}\) denotes parity-odd terms of total odd order at least five in local defect amplitudes/derivatives.

\subsection{Step 4: leading local coefficient point}

Expand the even coefficient functions around the trivial background
\[
\mathcal X=0.
\]
Then
\begin{equation}
\mathcal L_1(\mathcal X)
=
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}
+
\sum_A \Lambda_{\parallel,A}^{(2)}\,X_A
+
O(\mathcal X^2),
\label{eq:L1_expand}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\mathcal E_1(\mathcal X)
=
\Lambda_E^{(0)}
+
\sum_A \Lambda_{E,A}^{(2)}\,X_A
+
O(\mathcal X^2),
\label{eq:E1_expand}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\mathcal O_1(\mathcal X)
=
\Lambda_O^{(0)}
+
\sum_A \Lambda_{O,A}^{(2)}\,X_A
+
O(\mathcal X^2).
\label{eq:O1_expand}
\end{equation}

Likewise
\begin{equation}
\mathcal L_3(\mathcal X)
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}
+
\sum_A \lambda_{c,A}^{(2)}\,X_A
+
O(\mathcal X^2).
\label{eq:L3_expand}
\end{equation}

Therefore the leading actual-local expansions become
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
h_\parallel(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}
+
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\theta'(\xi)^3
+
\theta'(\xi)\sum_A\Lambda_{\parallel,A}^{(2)}X_A(\xi)
+
\theta'(\xi)^3\sum_A\lambda_{c,A}^{(2)}X_A(\xi)
+\cdots
}
\label{eq:hpar_leading_explicit}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
h_E(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)\Lambda_E^{(0)}
+
\theta'(\xi)\sum_A\Lambda_{E,A}^{(2)}X_A(\xi)
+
\theta'(\xi)^3\mathcal E_3(\mathcal X(\xi))
+\cdots
}
\label{eq:hE_leading_explicit}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
h_O(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)\Lambda_O^{(0)}
+
\theta'(\xi)\sum_A\Lambda_{O,A}^{(2)}X_A(\xi)
+
\theta'(\xi)^3\mathcal O_3(\mathcal X(\xi))
+\cdots
}
\label{eq:hO_leading_explicit}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Step 5: direct extraction formulas for the coefficient point}

The leading coefficient point is now extracted by local limits.

\paragraph{Longitudinal direct coefficient.}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}
=
\lim_{\mathcal X\to 0}
\frac{h_\parallel(\xi)}{\theta'(\xi)}
\Bigg|_{\text{remove the }\theta'^3\text{ branch contribution}}.
}
\label{eq:Lambda_parallel0_limit}
\end{equation}

More concretely,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}
=
\lim_{\theta,\theta',\theta'',\dots\to 0}
\left(
\frac{h_\parallel(\xi)}{\theta'(\xi)}
-\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\theta'(\xi)^2
\right).
}
\label{eq:Lambda_parallel0_limit_concrete}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Primitive longitudinal coefficient.}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_c
=
2\lim_{\theta,\theta',\theta'',\dots\to 0}
\frac{
h_\parallel(\xi)-\theta'(\xi)\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}
}{
\theta'(\xi)^3
}.
}
\label{eq:lambdac_limit}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Even transverse coefficient.}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_E^{(0)}
=
\lim_{\theta,\theta',\theta'',\dots\to 0}
\frac{h_E(\xi)}{\theta'(\xi)}.
}
\label{eq:LambdaE0_limit}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Odd transverse coefficient.}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_O^{(0)}
=
\lim_{\theta,\theta',\theta'',\dots\to 0}
\frac{h_O(\xi)}{\theta'(\xi)}.
}
\label{eq:LambdaO0_limit}
\end{equation}

These are the exact local coefficient-extraction formulas.

\subsection{Step 6: reduced coefficients after overlap integration}

Substituting \eqref{eq:hpar_leading_explicit}--\eqref{eq:hO_leading_explicit} into
\eqref{eq:lambda_from_hpar_complete}--\eqref{eq:beta_from_hO_complete},
one obtains
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel
=
I_\theta\,\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}
+
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3}
+
\sum_A \Lambda_{\parallel,A}^{(2)} I_{\theta X_A}
+
\sum_A \lambda_{c,A}^{(2)} I_{\theta'^3 X_A}
+\cdots,
\label{eq:lambda_full_expansion}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\alpha
=
I_\theta\,\Lambda_E^{(0)}
+
\sum_A \Lambda_{E,A}^{(2)} I_{\theta X_A}
+
I_{\theta'^3}\,E_3^{(0)}
+\cdots,
\label{eq:alpha_full_expansion}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\beta
=
I_\theta\,\Lambda_O^{(0)}
+
\sum_A \Lambda_{O,A}^{(2)} I_{\theta X_A}
+
I_{\theta'^3}\,O_3^{(0)}
+\cdots,
\label{eq:beta_full_expansion}
\end{equation}
where
\begin{equation}
I_{\theta X_A}
:=
\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,\theta'(\xi)X_A(\xi),
\label{eq:I_theta_XA}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
I_{\theta'^3 X_A}
:=
\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,\theta'(\xi)^3X_A(\xi).
\label{eq:I_theta3_XA}
\end{equation}

Thus the previously used reduced formulas are simply the leading truncation of the exact local invariant expansion.

\subsection{Step 7: leading truncation and branch structure}

At the leading order retained so far,
\[
h_\parallel(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}
+
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\theta'(\xi)^3,
\qquad
h_E(\xi)=\theta'(\xi)\Lambda_E^{(0)},
\qquad
h_O(\xi)=\theta'(\xi)\Lambda_O^{(0)}.
\]
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
I_\theta\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}
+
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=I_\theta\Lambda_E^{(0)},
\qquad
\beta=I_\theta\Lambda_O^{(0)}.
}
\label{eq:leading_truncation_coeffs}
\end{equation}

This makes the branch structure completely explicit:

\paragraph{Branch A.}
\begin{equation}
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}\neq 0,
\qquad
(\Lambda_E^{(0)},\Lambda_O^{(0)})\neq (0,0).
\label{eq:branchA_local}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Branch B.}
\begin{equation}
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0,
\qquad
\lambda_c\neq 0,
\qquad
(\Lambda_E^{(0)},\Lambda_O^{(0)})\neq (0,0).
\label{eq:branchB_local}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Step 8: explicit overlap-inserted leading coefficients}

Using the already established overlap values
\begin{equation}
I_\theta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
I_{\theta'^3}
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{256}\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
\label{eq:overlaps_explicit_reuse}
\end{equation}
the leading reduced coefficients become
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa\,\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}
-
\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\lambda_c\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
}
\label{eq:lambda_full_leading_explicit}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa\,\Lambda_E^{(0)},
\qquad
\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa\,\Lambda_O^{(0)}.
}
\label{eq:alpha_beta_full_leading_explicit}
\end{equation}

This is the fully explicit leading-order actual-local invariant completion.

\subsection{Step 9: exact honest status}

What is now closed:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the complete symmetry-allowed local form of \(h_\parallel,h_E,h_O\);
\item the direct limit formulas extracting \(\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)},\lambda_c,\Lambda_E^{(0)},\Lambda_O^{(0)}\);
\item the exact relation between the local expansion and the reduced overlap-integrated coefficients;
\item the explicit leading-order formulas with all known overlap constants inserted.
\end{enumerate}

What remains open:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the actual microscopic evaluation of the coefficient functions \(\mathcal L_1,\mathcal L_3,\mathcal E_1,\mathcal O_1\) from the final TECT Hessian;
\item the actual values of the subleading invariant coefficients \(\Lambda_{\parallel,A}^{(2)},\Lambda_{E,A}^{(2)},\Lambda_{O,A}^{(2)},\lambda_{c,A}^{(2)}\);
\item the genuine branch selection of the complete microscopic theory.
\end{enumerate}

\section{Final Summary}

The complete principal transport kernel admits the actual-local invariant expansion
\[
h_\parallel(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)\mathcal L_1(\mathcal X(\xi))
+
\theta'(\xi)^3\mathcal L_3(\mathcal X(\xi))
+\cdots,
\]
\[
h_E(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)\mathcal E_1(\mathcal X(\xi))
+\theta'(\xi)^3\mathcal E_3(\mathcal X(\xi))
+\cdots,
\]
\[
h_O(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)\mathcal O_1(\mathcal X(\xi))
+\theta'(\xi)^3\mathcal O_3(\mathcal X(\xi))
+\cdots,
\]
where \(\mathcal X(\xi)\) is the full list of parity-even local defect invariants.

The leading local coefficient point is extracted by
\[
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}
=
\lim
\left(
\frac{h_\parallel}{\theta'}-\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\theta'^2
\right),
\qquad
\lambda_c
=
2\lim
\frac{h_\parallel-\theta'\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}}{\theta'^3},
\]
\[
\Lambda_E^{(0)}=\lim \frac{h_E}{\theta'},
\qquad
\Lambda_O^{(0)}=\lim \frac{h_O}{\theta'}.
\]

After overlap integration, the leading reduced coefficients are
\[
\lambda_\parallel
=
I_\theta\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}
+
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=I_\theta\Lambda_E^{(0)},
\qquad
\beta=I_\theta\Lambda_O^{(0)}.
\]

Using the explicit overlaps,
\[
I_\theta=-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
I_{\theta'^3}=-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{256}\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
\]
this becomes
\[
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa\,\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}
-
\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\lambda_c\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
\]
\[
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa\,\Lambda_E^{(0)},
\qquad
\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa\,\Lambda_O^{(0)}.
\]

Thus the remaining microscopic frontier is exactly the computation of the local coefficient functions \(\mathcal L_1,\mathcal L_3,\mathcal E_1,\mathcal O_1\) from the complete TECT Hessian.

\section{Actual-local invariant completion}

The complete principal transport kernel is controlled by the local coefficient functions
\[
\mathcal L_1(\mathcal X),\qquad
\mathcal L_3(\mathcal X),\qquad
\mathcal E_1(\mathcal X),\qquad
\mathcal O_1(\mathcal X),
\]
where \(\mathcal X\) is the set of parity-even local defect invariants.

The leading local expansions are
\[
h_\parallel
=
\theta'\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}
+
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\theta'^3
+\cdots,
\qquad
h_E=\theta'\Lambda_E^{(0)}+\cdots,
\qquad
h_O=\theta'\Lambda_O^{(0)}+\cdots.
\]

Hence
\[
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}
=
\lim\left(\frac{h_\parallel}{\theta'}-\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\theta'^2\right),
\qquad
\lambda_c
=
2\lim\frac{h_\parallel-\theta'\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}}{\theta'^3},
\]
\[
\Lambda_E^{(0)}=\lim\frac{h_E}{\theta'},
\qquad
\Lambda_O^{(0)}=\lim\frac{h_O}{\theta'}.
\]

After overlap integration,
\[
\lambda_\parallel
=
I_\theta\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}
+
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=I_\theta\Lambda_E^{(0)},
\qquad
\beta=I_\theta\Lambda_O^{(0)}.
\]

Using the explicit overlaps,
\[
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa\,\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}
-
\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\lambda_c\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
\]
\[
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa\,\Lambda_E^{(0)},
\qquad
\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa\,\Lambda_O^{(0)}.
\]

Thus the remaining frontier is the explicit computation of
\(\mathcal L_1,\mathcal L_3,\mathcal E_1,\mathcal O_1\)
from the complete microscopic TECT Hessian.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Monomial Classification for the Complete TECT Hessian}

\subsection{Short Korean explanation}

The remaining microscopic problem is no longer the reduced Dirac algebra.
It is the classification of local tensor monomials in the complete Hessian according to which coefficient function they contribute to:
\[
\mathcal L_1,\qquad \mathcal L_3,\qquad \mathcal E_1,\qquad \mathcal O_1.
\]

The strategy is:

\[
\Gamma^{(2)}_{\mathrm{full}}
\to
V^\mu(\xi)
\to
\text{allowed local monomials}
\to
(\mathcal L_1,\mathcal L_3,\mathcal E_1,\mathcal O_1).
\]

\subsection{Step 1: target tensor types}

At principal first order, the only S2-compatible transport tensors are
\begin{equation}
n^\mu \sigma_3,
\qquad
E^\mu{}_a \sigma_a,
\qquad
J^\mu{}_a \sigma_a,
\qquad a=1,2.
\label{eq:target_tensor_types}
\end{equation}
Therefore every local Hessian monomial must be classified by whether it transforms as:

\begin{enumerate}
\item a longitudinal singlet,
\item an even transverse doublet,
\item an odd transverse doublet,
\item or an irrelevant/forbidden tensor.
\end{enumerate}

\subsection{Step 2: local building blocks}

Let the defect profile be \(\theta(\xi)\), and let \(\mathcal X(\xi)\) denote the full list of parity-even local scalar invariants built from the defect background:
\begin{equation}
\mathcal X(\xi)=\{X_A(\xi)\}_{A\in\mathcal A},
\qquad
X_A(-\xi)=X_A(\xi).
\label{eq:X_even_list}
\end{equation}

Typical generators are
\begin{equation}
X_0=\theta^2,
\qquad
X_1=\theta'^2,
\qquad
X_2=\theta\theta'',
\qquad
X_3=\theta''^2,
\qquad
X_4=\theta\theta^{(4)},
\quad \dots
\label{eq:X_examples}
\end{equation}

The parity-odd local building blocks are generated by one explicit odd factor:
\begin{equation}
Y_A(\xi):=\theta'(\xi)\,X_A(\xi),
\qquad
Z_A(\xi):=\theta'(\xi)^3\,X_A(\xi),
\qquad
W_A^{(2m+1)}(\xi):=\theta'(\xi)^{2m+1}X_A(\xi).
\label{eq:odd_generators}
\end{equation}

Hence every principal transport density must be a linear combination of parity-odd generators.

\subsection{Step 3: representation-theoretic classification rule}

A local monomial contributes to a coefficient function if and only if it satisfies two conditions:

\paragraph{(i) parity condition}
It must be odd in \(\xi\), because the mixed overlap contains
\[
f_+f_-,
\]
which is odd.

\paragraph{(ii) tensor condition}
Its free worldvolume/fiber indices must match one of the three target tensor types in \eqref{eq:target_tensor_types}.

Therefore:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{allowed monomial}
=
(\text{odd scalar density})
\times
(\text{one of }n^\mu\sigma_3,\ E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a,\ J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a).
}
\label{eq:allowed_monomial_rule}
\end{equation}

This is the exact classification principle.

\subsection{Step 4: longitudinal monomials}

A longitudinal monomial must transform as
\[
n^\mu\sigma_3.
\]
Hence its general local form is
\begin{equation}
M_{\parallel,A}^{(2m+1)}
=
\theta'(\xi)^{2m+1}X_A(\xi)\,n^\mu\sigma_3.
\label{eq:longitudinal_monomials}
\end{equation}

The lowest two orders are:

\paragraph{Order 1}
\begin{equation}
M_{\parallel}^{(1,0)}
=
\theta'(\xi)\,n^\mu\sigma_3.
\label{eq:Mpar10}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Order 3}
\begin{equation}
M_{\parallel}^{(3,0)}
=
\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\sigma_3.
\label{eq:Mpar30}
\end{equation}

All higher-order longitudinal monomials are
\begin{equation}
M_{\parallel,A}^{(1)}
=
\theta'(\xi)X_A(\xi)\,n^\mu\sigma_3,
\qquad
M_{\parallel,A}^{(3)}
=
\theta'(\xi)^3X_A(\xi)\,n^\mu\sigma_3,
\qquad \dots
\label{eq:Mpar_higher}
\end{equation}

Therefore the longitudinal coefficient function decomposes as
\begin{equation}
h_\parallel(\xi)
=
\sum_A \ell_A^{(1)}\,\theta'(\xi)X_A(\xi)
+
\sum_A \ell_A^{(3)}\,\theta'(\xi)^3X_A(\xi)
+
\cdots.
\label{eq:hpar_monomial_expansion}
\end{equation}

Identifying the leading coefficients,
\begin{equation}
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=\ell_{A=0}^{(1)},
\qquad
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}=\ell_{A=0}^{(3)}.
\label{eq:Lpar_lambdac_ident}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Step 5: even transverse monomials}

An even transverse monomial must transform as
\[
E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a.
\]
Hence its general form is
\begin{equation}
M_{E,A}^{(2m+1)}
=
\theta'(\xi)^{2m+1}X_A(\xi)\,E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a.
\label{eq:even_monomials}
\end{equation}

The leading even transverse monomial is
\begin{equation}
M_E^{(1,0)}
=
\theta'(\xi)\,E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a.
\label{eq:ME10}
\end{equation}

Thus
\begin{equation}
h_E(\xi)
=
\sum_A e_A^{(1)}\,\theta'(\xi)X_A(\xi)
+
\sum_A e_A^{(3)}\,\theta'(\xi)^3X_A(\xi)
+\cdots,
\label{eq:hE_monomial_expansion}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\Lambda_E^{(0)}=e_{A=0}^{(1)}.
\label{eq:LambdaE_ident}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Step 6: odd transverse monomials}

An odd transverse monomial must transform as
\[
J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a.
\]
Hence its general form is
\begin{equation}
M_{O,A}^{(2m+1)}
=
\theta'(\xi)^{2m+1}X_A(\xi)\,J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a.
\label{eq:odd_monomials}
\end{equation}

The leading odd transverse monomial is
\begin{equation}
M_O^{(1,0)}
=
\theta'(\xi)\,J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a.
\label{eq:MO10}
\end{equation}

Thus
\begin{equation}
h_O(\xi)
=
\sum_A o_A^{(1)}\,\theta'(\xi)X_A(\xi)
+
\sum_A o_A^{(3)}\,\theta'(\xi)^3X_A(\xi)
+\cdots,
\label{eq:hO_monomial_expansion}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\Lambda_O^{(0)}=o_{A=0}^{(1)}.
\label{eq:LambdaO_ident}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Step 7: forbidden monomials}

A monomial is forbidden at principal order if:

\begin{enumerate}
\item it is parity-even,
\item or it carries the wrong worldvolume tensor,
\item or it carries the wrong fiber tensor,
\item or it lies in the scalar identity channel only.
\end{enumerate}

Examples:

\begin{equation}
X_A(\xi)\,n^\mu\mathbf 1_2
\quad\text{forbidden},
\label{eq:forbidden1}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\theta'(\xi)X_A(\xi)\,n^\mu\mathbf 1_2
\quad\text{irrelevant for principal Dirac symbol},
\label{eq:forbidden2}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\theta'(\xi)X_A(\xi)\,E^\mu{}_a\mathbf 1_2
\quad\text{forbidden},
\label{eq:forbidden3}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\theta'(\xi)X_A(\xi)\,T^\mu_{ab}\sigma_b
\quad\text{forbidden unless }T^\mu_{ab}\propto E^\mu{}_a\text{ or }J^\mu{}_a.
\label{eq:forbidden4}
\end{equation}

Thus the monomial classification is exact.

\subsection{Step 8: full coefficient functions from monomial sums}

Combining the previous steps,
\begin{equation}
\mathcal L_1(\mathcal X)=\sum_A \ell_A^{(1)}X_A,
\qquad
\mathcal L_3(\mathcal X)=\sum_A \ell_A^{(3)}X_A,
\label{eq:L1L3_sum}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\mathcal E_1(\mathcal X)=\sum_A e_A^{(1)}X_A,
\qquad
\mathcal O_1(\mathcal X)=\sum_A o_A^{(1)}X_A.
\label{eq:E1O1_sum}
\end{equation}

Therefore
\begin{equation}
h_\parallel(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)\sum_A \ell_A^{(1)}X_A(\xi)
+
\theta'(\xi)^3\sum_A \ell_A^{(3)}X_A(\xi)
+\cdots,
\label{eq:hpar_sum_final}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
h_E(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)\sum_A e_A^{(1)}X_A(\xi)
+\cdots,
\label{eq:hE_sum_final}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
h_O(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)\sum_A o_A^{(1)}X_A(\xi)
+\cdots.
\label{eq:hO_sum_final}
\end{equation}

The leading coefficient point is
\begin{equation}
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=\ell_0^{(1)},
\qquad
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}=\ell_0^{(3)},
\qquad
\Lambda_E^{(0)}=e_0^{(1)},
\qquad
\Lambda_O^{(0)}=o_0^{(1)}.
\label{eq:leading_point_ident}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Step 9: exact local limit formulas}

From the monomial expansion, the exact extraction limits are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}
=
\lim_{\mathcal X\to 0}
\left(
\frac{h_\parallel}{\theta'}
-\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\theta'^2
\right),
}
\label{eq:Lpar_limit_exact_again}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_c
=
2\lim_{\mathcal X\to 0}
\frac{h_\parallel-\theta'\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}}{\theta'^3},
}
\label{eq:lambdac_limit_exact_again}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_E^{(0)}
=
\lim_{\mathcal X\to 0}\frac{h_E}{\theta'},
\qquad
\Lambda_O^{(0)}
=
\lim_{\mathcal X\to 0}\frac{h_O}{\theta'}.
}
\label{eq:LELO_limit_exact_again}
\end{equation}

These are the exact coefficient-extraction formulas from the complete Hessian.

\subsection{Step 10: overlap-completed reduced coefficients}

After overlap integration,
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel
=
I_\theta\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}
+
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3}
+\cdots,
\label{eq:lpar_overlap_final_again}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\alpha
=
I_\theta\Lambda_E^{(0)}+\cdots,
\qquad
\beta
=
I_\theta\Lambda_O^{(0)}+\cdots.
\label{eq:ab_overlap_final_again}
\end{equation}

Using the explicit overlap values already established,
\begin{equation}
I_\theta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
I_{\theta'^3}
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{256}\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
\label{eq:Itheta_insert_again}
\end{equation}
one gets
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa\,\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}
-
\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\lambda_c\theta_0^3\kappa^3
+\cdots,
\label{eq:lpar_explicit_insert_again}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa\,\Lambda_E^{(0)}+\cdots,
\qquad
\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa\,\Lambda_O^{(0)}+\cdots.
\label{eq:ab_explicit_insert_again}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Step 11: final microscopic classification theorem}

The complete principal transport kernel is fully classified by the monomial families:
\[
\theta'X_A\,n^\mu\sigma_3,\qquad
\theta'^3X_A\,n^\mu\sigma_3,\qquad
\theta'X_A\,E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a,\qquad
\theta'X_A\,J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a.
\]

Therefore the microscopic Dirac criterion reduces exactly to:

\paragraph{Branch A}
\begin{equation}
\ell_0^{(1)}\neq 0,
\qquad
(e_0^{(1)},o_0^{(1)})\neq (0,0).
\label{eq:branchA_monomial}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Branch B}
\begin{equation}
\ell_0^{(1)}=0,
\qquad
\ell_0^{(3)}\neq 0,
\qquad
(e_0^{(1)},o_0^{(1)})\neq (0,0).
\label{eq:branchB_monomial}
\end{equation}

Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}\neq 0
\ \text{or}\ 
\lambda_c\neq 0,
\qquad
(\Lambda_E^{(0)},\Lambda_O^{(0)})\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:final_monomial_criterion}
\end{equation}

\section{Final Summary}

The complete TECT Hessian contributes to the principal transport kernel only through the monomial families
\[
\theta'X_A\,n^\mu\sigma_3,
\qquad
\theta'^3X_A\,n^\mu\sigma_3,
\qquad
\theta'X_A\,E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a,
\qquad
\theta'X_A\,J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a,
\]
where \(X_A\) are parity-even local defect invariants.

These families define the coefficient functions
\[
\mathcal L_1,\qquad \mathcal L_3,\qquad \mathcal E_1,\qquad \mathcal O_1,
\]
and the leading coefficient point is
\[
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=\ell_0^{(1)},
\qquad
\lambda_c=2\ell_0^{(3)},
\qquad
\Lambda_E^{(0)}=e_0^{(1)},
\qquad
\Lambda_O^{(0)}=o_0^{(1)}.
\]

Hence the exact extraction formulas are
\[
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}
=
\lim\left(\frac{h_\parallel}{\theta'}-\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\theta'^2\right),
\qquad
\lambda_c
=
2\lim\frac{h_\parallel-\theta'\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}}{\theta'^3},
\]
\[
\Lambda_E^{(0)}=\lim\frac{h_E}{\theta'},
\qquad
\Lambda_O^{(0)}=\lim\frac{h_O}{\theta'}.
\]

Thus the remaining frontier is only the explicit computation of the monomial coefficients
\[
\ell_A^{(1)},\ \ell_A^{(3)},\ e_A^{(1)},\ o_A^{(1)}
\]
from the complete microscopic TECT Hessian.

\section{Complete monomial classification of the principal transport kernel}

The only principal local monomial families that contribute to the reduced Dirac symbol are
\[
\theta'X_A\,n^\mu\sigma_3,
\qquad
\theta'^3X_A\,n^\mu\sigma_3,
\qquad
\theta'X_A\,E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a,
\qquad
\theta'X_A\,J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a,
\]
with \(X_A\) parity-even local defect invariants.

These define
\[
\mathcal L_1,\qquad \mathcal L_3,\qquad \mathcal E_1,\qquad \mathcal O_1,
\]
and the leading coefficient point
\[
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=\ell_0^{(1)},
\qquad
\lambda_c=2\ell_0^{(3)},
\qquad
\Lambda_E^{(0)}=e_0^{(1)},
\qquad
\Lambda_O^{(0)}=o_0^{(1)}.
\]

Therefore the remaining microscopic frontier is exactly the computation of the monomial coefficients
\[
\ell_A^{(1)},\ \ell_A^{(3)},\ e_A^{(1)},\ o_A^{(1)}
\]
from the complete TECT Hessian.
