\section{Executable Extraction Formulas for the Leading Monomial Coefficients}

\subsection{Short Korean explanation}

The remaining microscopic frontier is now fully finite and executable.

One must start from the complete background Hessian
\[
\Gamma^{(2)}[\bar\Phi_{\min}],
\]
extract its odd first-order worldvolume transport kernel
\[
V^\mu(\xi),
\]
project it to the isolated four-mode graded infrared sector,
and then read the leading invariant coefficients
\[
\ell_0^{(1)},\qquad \ell_0^{(3)},\qquad e_0^{(1)},\qquad o_0^{(1)}.
\]

These are exactly
\[
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)},\qquad \frac{\lambda_c}{2},\qquad \Lambda_E^{(0)},\qquad \Lambda_O^{(0)}.
\]

\subsection{Step 1: complete Hessian block form}

Let the full background fluctuation field be decomposed as
\[
\varphi=(a,\nu,\zeta),
\]
where \(a\) is the amplitude sector, \(\nu\) the projector/orientational sector, and \(\zeta\) the defect/tangent doublet sector.
Then the background Hessian has the exact block form
\begin{equation}
\Gamma^{(2)}[\bar\Phi_{\min}]
=
\begin{pmatrix}
\mathcal H_{TT} & \mathcal H_{TO} & \mathcal H_{TD}\\
\mathcal H_{OT} & \mathcal H_{OO} & \mathcal H_{OD}\\
\mathcal H_{DT} & \mathcal H_{DO} & \mathcal H_{DD}
\end{pmatrix}.
\label{eq:full_block_Hessian_exec}
\end{equation}

Each block is a \(\xi\)-dependent differential operator on worldvolume coordinates \(y^\mu\).
Expand each block as
\begin{equation}
\mathcal H_{AB}
=
\mathcal H_{AB}^{(0)}(\xi)
-
i\,\mathcal V_{AB}^{\mu}(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu}
+
\mathcal W_{AB}^{\mu\nu}(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu}\partial_{y^\nu}
+\cdots,
\label{eq:HAB_expand}
\end{equation}
with \(A,B\in\{T,O,D\}\).

The total first-order transport kernel is therefore the block matrix
\begin{equation}
\mathcal V^\mu(\xi)=
\begin{pmatrix}
\mathcal V_{TT}^{\mu} & \mathcal V_{TO}^{\mu} & \mathcal V_{TD}^{\mu}\\
\mathcal V_{OT}^{\mu} & \mathcal V_{OO}^{\mu} & \mathcal V_{OD}^{\mu}\\
\mathcal V_{DT}^{\mu} & \mathcal V_{DO}^{\mu} & \mathcal V_{DD}^{\mu}
\end{pmatrix}.
\label{eq:Vmu_blockmatrix}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Step 2: effective transport kernel on the graded infrared sector}

Let \(\Pi_K\) be the spectral projector onto the isolated four-mode graded sector
\[
K=K_+\oplus K_-,
\qquad
\dim_\mathbb C K_\pm=2.
\]
Then the principal first-order effective transport kernel is
\begin{equation}
V_{\mathrm{eff}}^\mu(\xi)
=
\Pi_K\,\mathcal V^\mu(\xi)\,\Pi_K
+
\Pi_K\,\mathcal H^{(0)}\,\Pi_{K^\perp}
\bigl(\mathcal H_{K^\perp}^{(0)}\bigr)^{-1}
\mathcal V^\mu_{K^\perp K}
\,\Pi_K
+\cdots,
\label{eq:Veff_Schur}
\end{equation}
where the omitted terms are higher-order Schur-complement corrections of the same formal type.

So the actual transport kernel is not just one block:
it is the \(K\)-projected odd first-order part of the full Hessian, including induced contributions from off-diagonal blocks.

\subsection{Step 3: grading-odd projection}

Let \(J\) be the \(2+2\) grading involution on \(K\).
The principal Dirac kernel is the grading-odd part
\begin{equation}
V_{\mathrm{odd}}^\mu(\xi)
:=
\frac12\Bigl(
V_{\mathrm{eff}}^\mu(\xi)-JV_{\mathrm{eff}}^\mu(\xi)J^{-1}
\Bigr).
\label{eq:Vodd_def}
\end{equation}
Only this part contributes to the principal mixed Dirac symbol.

Thus the actual microscopic extraction problem is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Gamma^{(2)}[\bar\Phi_{\min}]
\longrightarrow
\mathcal V^\mu
\longrightarrow
V_{\mathrm{eff}}^\mu
\longrightarrow
V_{\mathrm{odd}}^\mu.
}
\label{eq:actual_extraction_chain}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Step 4: invariant decomposition of the projected transport kernel}

The projected odd kernel has the unique S2-compatible invariant decomposition
\begin{equation}
V_{\mathrm{odd}}^\mu(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)\,
\mathcal M^\mu_{\mathrm{inv}}(\theta(\xi))
+
V_{\mathrm{irr}}^\mu(\xi),
\label{eq:Vodd_Minv}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\mathcal M^\mu_{\mathrm{inv}}(\theta)
=
h_0(\theta)n^\mu\mathbf 1_2
+
h_\parallel(\theta)n^\mu\sigma_3
+
h_E(\theta)E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
+
h_O(\theta)J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a.
\label{eq:Minv_decomp_exec}
\end{equation}
Only \(h_\parallel,h_E,h_O\) matter for the principal Dirac symbol.

\subsection{Step 5: direct invariant projectors onto the three channels}

Define the invariant extraction maps
\begin{equation}
\mathfrak P_\parallel[\mathcal M]
:=
\frac12\,\Tr\!\left[\sigma_3\,n_\mu\,\mathcal M^\mu\right],
\label{eq:Ppar_def}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\mathfrak P_E[\mathcal M]
:=
\frac14\,E^\mu{}_a\,\Tr\!\left[\sigma_a\,\mathcal M_\mu\right],
\label{eq:PE_def}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\mathfrak P_O[\mathcal M]
:=
\frac14\,J^\mu{}_a\,\Tr\!\left[\sigma_a\,\mathcal M_\mu\right].
\label{eq:PO_def}
\end{equation}

Applied to \(\mathcal M^\mu_{\mathrm{inv}}(\theta)\), they give exactly
\begin{equation}
\mathfrak P_\parallel[\mathcal M_{\mathrm{inv}}]=h_\parallel(\theta),
\qquad
\mathfrak P_E[\mathcal M_{\mathrm{inv}}]=h_E(\theta),
\qquad
\mathfrak P_O[\mathcal M_{\mathrm{inv}}]=h_O(\theta).
\label{eq:projectors_return_h}
\end{equation}

Therefore the full microscopic job is reduced to
\begin{equation}
h_\parallel(\theta)=\mathfrak P_\parallel[\mathcal M_{\mathrm{inv}}(\theta)],
\qquad
h_E(\theta)=\mathfrak P_E[\mathcal M_{\mathrm{inv}}(\theta)],
\qquad
h_O(\theta)=\mathfrak P_O[\mathcal M_{\mathrm{inv}}(\theta)].
\label{eq:h_from_projectors}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Step 6: leading monomial coefficients from exact limits}

From the monomial classification already fixed, the leading coefficients are extracted by
\begin{equation}
\ell_0^{(1)}
=
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}
=
\lim_{\mathcal X\to 0}
\left(
\frac{h_\parallel}{\theta'}
-\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\theta'^2
\right),
\label{eq:l01_extract}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\ell_0^{(3)}
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}
=
\lim_{\mathcal X\to 0}
\frac{h_\parallel-\theta'\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}}{\theta'^3},
\label{eq:l03_extract}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
e_0^{(1)}
=
\Lambda_E^{(0)}
=
\lim_{\mathcal X\to 0}\frac{h_E}{\theta'},
\label{eq:e01_extract}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
o_0^{(1)}
=
\Lambda_O^{(0)}
=
\lim_{\mathcal X\to 0}\frac{h_O}{\theta'}.
\label{eq:o01_extract}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, using the invariant projectors directly,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\ell_0^{(1)}
=
\lim_{\mathcal X\to 0}
\left(
\frac{\mathfrak P_\parallel[\mathcal M_{\mathrm{inv}}]}{\theta'}
-\ell_0^{(3)}\theta'^2
\right),
}
\label{eq:l01_projector_extract}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\ell_0^{(3)}
=
\lim_{\mathcal X\to 0}
\frac{\mathfrak P_\parallel[\mathcal M_{\mathrm{inv}}]-\theta'\ell_0^{(1)}}{\theta'^3},
}
\label{eq:l03_projector_extract}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
e_0^{(1)}
=
\lim_{\mathcal X\to 0}
\frac{\mathfrak P_E[\mathcal M_{\mathrm{inv}}]}{\theta'},
\qquad
o_0^{(1)}
=
\lim_{\mathcal X\to 0}
\frac{\mathfrak P_O[\mathcal M_{\mathrm{inv}}]}{\theta'}.
}
\label{eq:e01_o01_projector_extract}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Step 7: direct blockwise contribution formulas}

Because \(\mathcal M_{\mathrm{inv}}\) is linear in \(V_{\mathrm{odd}}^\mu\), and \(V_{\mathrm{odd}}^\mu\) is built from the Hessian blocks in \eqref{eq:Veff_Schur}, the leading coefficients split additively:
\begin{equation}
\ell_0^{(1)}
=
\sum_{A,B}\ell_{0;AB}^{(1)},
\qquad
\ell_0^{(3)}
=
\sum_{A,B}\ell_{0;AB}^{(3)},
\qquad
e_0^{(1)}
=
\sum_{A,B}e_{0;AB}^{(1)},
\qquad
o_0^{(1)}
=
\sum_{A,B}o_{0;AB}^{(1)},
\label{eq:blockwise_coeff_split}
\end{equation}
where \((A,B)\in\{T,O,D\}^2\).

The contribution of each Hessian block is therefore defined by
\begin{equation}
\ell_{0;AB}^{(1)}
:=
\lim_{\mathcal X\to 0}
\left(
\frac{\mathfrak P_\parallel[\mathcal M_{AB}]}{\theta'}
-\ell_{0;AB}^{(3)}\theta'^2
\right),
\label{eq:l01_AB}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\ell_{0;AB}^{(3)}
:=
\lim_{\mathcal X\to 0}
\frac{\mathfrak P_\parallel[\mathcal M_{AB}]-\theta'\ell_{0;AB}^{(1)}}{\theta'^3},
\label{eq:l03_AB}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
e_{0;AB}^{(1)}
:=
\lim_{\mathcal X\to 0}
\frac{\mathfrak P_E[\mathcal M_{AB}]}{\theta'},
\qquad
o_{0;AB}^{(1)}
:=
\lim_{\mathcal X\to 0}
\frac{\mathfrak P_O[\mathcal M_{AB}]}{\theta'}.
\label{eq:e01o01_AB}
\end{equation}

These are the exact executable formulas for the final microscopic audit.

\subsection{Step 8: direct reduced coefficients}

Once \(\ell_0^{(1)},\ell_0^{(3)},e_0^{(1)},o_0^{(1)}\) are known, the reduced coefficients are
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel
=
I_\theta\,\ell_0^{(1)}
+
I_{\theta'^3}\,\ell_0^{(3)}
+\cdots,
\label{eq:lambda_from_ell}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\alpha
=
I_\theta\,e_0^{(1)}+\cdots,
\qquad
\beta
=
I_\theta\,o_0^{(1)}+\cdots.
\label{eq:ab_from_eo}
\end{equation}

Since
\[
I_\theta\neq 0,
\qquad
I_{\theta'^3}\neq 0,
\]
the final nondegeneracy condition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\ell_0^{(1)}\neq 0
\ \text{or}\ 
\ell_0^{(3)}\neq 0,
\qquad
(e_0^{(1)},o_0^{(1)})\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:final_exec_condition}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Step 9: exact relation to the already-isolated concrete branch}

In the exact concrete local Class II-compatible branch,
\[
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0,
\]
so
\[
\ell_0^{(1)}=0,
\qquad
\ell_0^{(3)}=\frac{\lambda_c}{2},
\qquad
e_0^{(1)}=\Lambda_E,
\qquad
o_0^{(1)}=\Lambda_O.
\]
Hence \eqref{eq:final_exec_condition} reduces to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_c\neq 0,
\qquad
(\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)\neq (0,0),
}
\label{eq:ClassII_exec_condition}
\end{equation}
which matches the already-established reduced test. :contentReference[oaicite:3]{index=3}

\section{Final Summary}

The full microscopic coefficient audit is now completely executable.

Starting from the complete background Hessian
\[
\Gamma^{(2)}[\bar\Phi_{\min}],
\]
one must:

\[
\Gamma^{(2)}
\to
\mathcal V^\mu
\to
V_{\mathrm{eff}}^\mu
\to
V_{\mathrm{odd}}^\mu
\to
\mathcal M^\mu_{\mathrm{inv}}
\to
(h_\parallel,h_E,h_O)
\to
(\ell_0^{(1)},\ell_0^{(3)},e_0^{(1)},o_0^{(1)}).
\]

The exact invariant extraction maps are
\[
\mathfrak P_\parallel[\mathcal M]
=
\frac12\Tr[\sigma_3 n_\mu\mathcal M^\mu],
\qquad
\mathfrak P_E[\mathcal M]
=
\frac14 E^\mu{}_a\Tr[\sigma_a\mathcal M_\mu],
\qquad
\mathfrak P_O[\mathcal M]
=
\frac14 J^\mu{}_a\Tr[\sigma_a\mathcal M_\mu].
\]

The leading coefficients are then
\[
\ell_0^{(1)}=\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)},
\qquad
\ell_0^{(3)}=\frac{\lambda_c}{2},
\qquad
e_0^{(1)}=\Lambda_E^{(0)},
\qquad
o_0^{(1)}=\Lambda_O^{(0)}.
\]

Therefore the last genuine microscopic frontier is exactly the explicit blockwise evaluation of
\[
\ell_{0;AB}^{(1)},\quad
\ell_{0;AB}^{(3)},\quad
e_{0;AB}^{(1)},\quad
o_{0;AB}^{(1)}
\]
from the complete TECT Hessian blocks \(\mathcal H_{AB}\).

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Blockwise Projection Formulas for the Leading Actual Coefficient Point}

\subsection{Short Korean explanation}

The remaining problem is to convert the complete Hessian blocks into the four leading monomial coefficients
\[
\ell_0^{(1)},\qquad
\ell_0^{(3)},\qquad
e_0^{(1)},\qquad
o_0^{(1)}.
\]

This is done in four steps:

\[
\mathcal H_{AB}
\;\to\;
\mathcal V^\mu_{AB}
\;\to\;
V^\mu_{AB,\mathrm{odd}}
\;\to\;
\mathcal M^\mu_{AB,\mathrm{inv}}
\;\to\;
(\ell_{0;AB}^{(1)},\ell_{0;AB}^{(3)},e_{0;AB}^{(1)},o_{0;AB}^{(1)}).
\]

\subsection{Step 1: block expansion of the complete Hessian}

Let the full background Hessian be written as
\begin{equation}
\Gamma^{(2)}[\bar\Phi_{\min}]
=
\bigl(\mathcal H_{AB}\bigr)_{A,B\in\{T,O,D\}},
\label{eq:block_Hessian_start}
\end{equation}
where \(T,O,D\) denote the amplitude / orientational / defect-tangent sectors.

Expand each block in worldvolume derivatives:
\begin{equation}
\mathcal H_{AB}
=
\mathcal H^{(0)}_{AB}(\xi)
-
i\,\mathcal V^\mu_{AB}(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu}
+
\mathcal W^{\mu\nu}_{AB}(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu}\partial_{y^\nu}
+\cdots.
\label{eq:block_derivative_expand}
\end{equation}
Only the coefficient of exactly one worldvolume derivative contributes to the principal transport audit.

\subsection{Step 2: effective odd transport from each block}

Let \(\Pi_K\) be the projector onto the isolated graded \(2+2\) infrared sector
\[
K=K_+\oplus K_-,
\qquad
\dim_{\mathbb C}K_\pm=2.
\]
Define the effective transport contribution of each block by the Schur-projected expression
\begin{equation}
V^\mu_{AB,\mathrm{eff}}
:=
\Pi_K \mathcal V^\mu_{AB}\Pi_K
+
\Pi_K \mathcal H^{(0)}_{A\bar A}
\bigl(\mathcal H^{(0)}_{\bar A\bar B}\bigr)^{-1}
\mathcal V^\mu_{\bar B B}\Pi_K
+\cdots,
\label{eq:block_Veff_def}
\end{equation}
where \(\bar A,\bar B\) denote complementary remote sectors participating in the Schur complement.
The grading-odd part is
\begin{equation}
V^\mu_{AB,\mathrm{odd}}
:=
\frac12\Bigl(
V^\mu_{AB,\mathrm{eff}}
-
J V^\mu_{AB,\mathrm{eff}} J^{-1}
\Bigr).
\label{eq:block_Vodd_def}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Step 3: invariant decomposition of each block contribution}

Each odd block contribution admits the unique S2-compatible decomposition
\begin{equation}
V^\mu_{AB,\mathrm{odd}}(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)\,
\mathcal M^\mu_{AB,\mathrm{inv}}(\theta(\xi))
+
V^\mu_{AB,\mathrm{irr}}(\xi),
\label{eq:block_Minv_def}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\mathcal M^\mu_{AB,\mathrm{inv}}(\theta)
=
h_{0;AB}(\theta)\,n^\mu\mathbf 1_2
+
h_{\parallel;AB}(\theta)\,n^\mu\sigma_3
+
h_{E;AB}(\theta)\,E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
+
h_{O;AB}(\theta)\,J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a.
\label{eq:block_Minv_expand}
\end{equation}

The full invariant transport matrix is the sum
\begin{equation}
\mathcal M^\mu_{\mathrm{inv}}
=
\sum_{A,B}\mathcal M^\mu_{AB,\mathrm{inv}}.
\label{eq:Minv_sum_blocks}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Step 4: invariant projectors onto the three physical channels}

Define the three projection maps
\begin{equation}
\mathfrak P_\parallel[\mathcal M]
:=
\frac12\Tr\!\bigl(\sigma_3\,n_\mu \mathcal M^\mu\bigr),
\label{eq:proj_par}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\mathfrak P_E[\mathcal M]
:=
\frac14 E^\mu{}_a \Tr\!\bigl(\sigma_a \mathcal M_\mu\bigr),
\label{eq:proj_E}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\mathfrak P_O[\mathcal M]
:=
\frac14 J^\mu{}_a \Tr\!\bigl(\sigma_a \mathcal M_\mu\bigr).
\label{eq:proj_O}
\end{equation}
Applied blockwise,
\begin{equation}
h_{\parallel;AB}(\theta)=\mathfrak P_\parallel[\mathcal M_{AB,\mathrm{inv}}],
\qquad
h_{E;AB}(\theta)=\mathfrak P_E[\mathcal M_{AB,\mathrm{inv}}],
\qquad
h_{O;AB}(\theta)=\mathfrak P_O[\mathcal M_{AB,\mathrm{inv}}].
\label{eq:h_block_from_projectors}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Step 5: leading monomial expansion of each block}

By the monomial classification already fixed, each block coefficient expands as
\begin{equation}
h_{\parallel;AB}(\theta)
=
\ell_{0;AB}^{(1)}
+
\ell_{2;AB}^{(1)}\theta^2
+
\ell_{0;AB}^{(3)}\theta'^2
+
O(\theta^4,\theta^2\theta'^2,\theta'^4),
\label{eq:hpar_block_expand}
\end{equation}
where, after multiplication by the universal odd prefactor \(\theta'(\xi)\),
the first and third terms contribute respectively to the
\(\theta' n^\mu\sigma_3\) and \(\theta'^3 n^\mu\sigma_3\) monomials.

Likewise
\begin{equation}
h_{E;AB}(\theta)
=
e_{0;AB}^{(1)}
+
e_{2;AB}^{(1)}\theta^2
+
O(\theta'^2,\theta^4),
\label{eq:hE_block_expand}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
h_{O;AB}(\theta)
=
o_{0;AB}^{(1)}
+
o_{2;AB}^{(1)}\theta^2
+
O(\theta'^2,\theta^4).
\label{eq:hO_block_expand}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Step 6: executable extraction limits for each block}

The leading coefficients are read blockwise by the exact limits
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\ell_{0;AB}^{(1)}
=
\lim_{\theta,\theta',\theta'',\dots\to 0}
\left(
\mathfrak P_\parallel[\mathcal M_{AB,\mathrm{inv}}]
-
\ell_{0;AB}^{(3)}\theta'^2
\right),
}
\label{eq:l01_block_limit}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\ell_{0;AB}^{(3)}
=
\lim_{\theta,\theta',\theta'',\dots\to 0}
\frac{
\mathfrak P_\parallel[\mathcal M_{AB,\mathrm{inv}}]
-
\ell_{0;AB}^{(1)}
}{
\theta'^2
},
}
\label{eq:l03_block_limit}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
e_{0;AB}^{(1)}
=
\lim_{\theta,\theta',\theta'',\dots\to 0}
\mathfrak P_E[\mathcal M_{AB,\mathrm{inv}}],
\qquad
o_{0;AB}^{(1)}
=
\lim_{\theta,\theta',\theta'',\dots\to 0}
\mathfrak P_O[\mathcal M_{AB,\mathrm{inv}}].
}
\label{eq:e01o01_block_limit}
\end{equation}

These are the precise blockwise executable formulas.

\subsection{Step 7: additive reconstruction of the full leading coefficient point}

The full leading coefficient point is the sum over all Hessian blocks:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\ell_0^{(1)}=\sum_{A,B}\ell_{0;AB}^{(1)},
\qquad
\ell_0^{(3)}=\sum_{A,B}\ell_{0;AB}^{(3)},
\qquad
e_0^{(1)}=\sum_{A,B}e_{0;AB}^{(1)},
\qquad
o_0^{(1)}=\sum_{A,B}o_{0;AB}^{(1)}.
}
\label{eq:leading_coeff_sum}
\end{equation}
Identify
\begin{equation}
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=\ell_0^{(1)},
\qquad
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}=\ell_0^{(3)},
\qquad
\Lambda_E^{(0)}=e_0^{(1)},
\qquad
\Lambda_O^{(0)}=o_0^{(1)}.
\label{eq:identify_leading_coeffs}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Step 8: reduced S2 coefficients}

Once these are known, the reduced coefficients are
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel
=
I_\theta\,\ell_0^{(1)}
+
I_{\theta'^3}\,\ell_0^{(3)}
+\cdots,
\label{eq:lambda_from_leading_blocks}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\alpha
=
I_\theta\,e_0^{(1)}+\cdots,
\qquad
\beta
=
I_\theta\,o_0^{(1)}+\cdots.
\label{eq:alphabeta_from_leading_blocks}
\end{equation}
Using the already established explicit overlaps,
\begin{equation}
I_\theta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
I_{\theta'^3}
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{256}\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
\label{eq:reuse_overlap_vals}
\end{equation}
one gets
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa\,\ell_0^{(1)}
-
\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{256}\theta_0^3\kappa^3\,\ell_0^{(3)}
+\cdots,
}
\label{eq:lambda_explicit_from_block_coeffs}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa\,e_0^{(1)}+\cdots,
\qquad
\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa\,o_0^{(1)}+\cdots.
}
\label{eq:alphabeta_explicit_from_block_coeffs}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Step 9: final finite decision rule}

Therefore the exact microscopic decision rule is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\ell_0^{(1)}\neq 0
\quad\text{or}\quad
\ell_0^{(3)}\neq 0,
\qquad
(e_0^{(1)},o_0^{(1)})\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:blockwise_final_decision}
\end{equation}

Equivalently:

\paragraph{Branch A}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\ell_0^{(1)}\neq 0,
\qquad
(e_0^{(1)},o_0^{(1)})\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:blockwise_branchA}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Branch B}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\ell_0^{(1)}=0,\qquad
\ell_0^{(3)}\neq 0,\qquad
(e_0^{(1)},o_0^{(1)})\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:blockwise_branchB}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Step 10: physically most likely block assignment}

Within the current strongest explicit working library, the natural block expectations are:

\begin{equation}
(TT)\ \text{mostly feeds}\ h_0\ \text{or spectators},
\label{eq:TT_expect}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
(OO)\ \text{can feed}\ \ell_0^{(3)}\ \text{through the primitive commutator-square channel},
\label{eq:OO_expect}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
(TD),(DT),(OD),(DO),(DD)\ \text{are the natural candidates for}\ e_0^{(1)},o_0^{(1)},
\label{eq:mixed_blocks_expect}
\end{equation}
while
\begin{equation}
\mathcal L_\Psi^{\mathrm{ref}}\ \text{inside the full complete action is the best candidate for a genuine}\ \ell_0^{(1)}\neq 0\ \text{Branch A term}.
\label{eq:ref_best_branchA}
\end{equation}

This last point is especially important: the files already isolate that a constant-leading Branch A coefficient, if it exists, should come from the still-undetermined refined derivative sector of the complete condensate core rather than from the already explicit primitive Class II branch. 

\section{Final Summary}

The remaining microscopic closure problem is now reduced to a completely explicit blockwise audit.

For each Hessian block \(\mathcal H_{AB}\), one must:
\[
\mathcal H_{AB}
\to
\mathcal V^\mu_{AB}
\to
V^\mu_{AB,\mathrm{odd}}
\to
\mathcal M^\mu_{AB,\mathrm{inv}}
\to
(\ell_{0;AB}^{(1)},\ell_{0;AB}^{(3)},e_{0;AB}^{(1)},o_{0;AB}^{(1)}).
\]

Then sum over blocks:
\[
\ell_0^{(1)}=\sum_{A,B}\ell_{0;AB}^{(1)},
\qquad
\ell_0^{(3)}=\sum_{A,B}\ell_{0;AB}^{(3)},
\qquad
e_0^{(1)}=\sum_{A,B}e_{0;AB}^{(1)},
\qquad
o_0^{(1)}=\sum_{A,B}o_{0;AB}^{(1)}.
\]

Finally,
\[
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=\ell_0^{(1)},
\qquad
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}=\ell_0^{(3)},
\qquad
\Lambda_E^{(0)}=e_0^{(1)},
\qquad
\Lambda_O^{(0)}=o_0^{(1)}.
\]

Hence the last exact finite test is
\[
\ell_0^{(1)}\neq 0
\ \text{or}\
\ell_0^{(3)}\neq 0,
\qquad
(e_0^{(1)},o_0^{(1)})\neq (0,0).
\]

So the frontier is no longer conceptual.
It is the literal blockwise evaluation of these four numbers from the complete TECT Hessian. 

\section{Final executable blockwise audit}

The complete TECT microscopic coefficient problem is reduced to the four leading quantities
\[
\ell_0^{(1)},\qquad
\ell_0^{(3)},\qquad
e_0^{(1)},\qquad
o_0^{(1)}.
\]

For each Hessian block \(\mathcal H_{AB}\), define
\[
\mathcal H_{AB}
=
\mathcal H^{(0)}_{AB}
-i\mathcal V^\mu_{AB}\partial_{y^\mu}
+\cdots,
\]
then compute the grading-odd effective transport block
\[
V^\mu_{AB,\mathrm{odd}},
\]
its invariant S2 decomposition
\[
\mathcal M^\mu_{AB,\mathrm{inv}}
=
h_{0;AB}n^\mu\mathbf 1_2
+h_{\parallel;AB}n^\mu\sigma_3
+h_{E;AB}E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
+h_{O;AB}J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a,
\]
and extract
\[
\ell_{0;AB}^{(1)},\qquad
\ell_{0;AB}^{(3)},\qquad
e_{0;AB}^{(1)},\qquad
o_{0;AB}^{(1)}
\]
through the exact limits
\[
\ell_{0;AB}^{(1)}
=
\lim
\left(
\mathfrak P_\parallel[\mathcal M_{AB,\mathrm{inv}}]
-\ell_{0;AB}^{(3)}\theta'^2
\right),
\]
\[
\ell_{0;AB}^{(3)}
=
\lim
\frac{
\mathfrak P_\parallel[\mathcal M_{AB,\mathrm{inv}}]
-\ell_{0;AB}^{(1)}
}{\theta'^2},
\]
\[
e_{0;AB}^{(1)}=\lim \mathfrak P_E[\mathcal M_{AB,\mathrm{inv}}],
\qquad
o_{0;AB}^{(1)}=\lim \mathfrak P_O[\mathcal M_{AB,\mathrm{inv}}].
\]

Summing over blocks gives
\[
\ell_0^{(1)}=\sum_{A,B}\ell_{0;AB}^{(1)},
\qquad
\ell_0^{(3)}=\sum_{A,B}\ell_{0;AB}^{(3)},
\qquad
e_0^{(1)}=\sum_{A,B}e_{0;AB}^{(1)},
\qquad
o_0^{(1)}=\sum_{A,B}o_{0;AB}^{(1)}.
\]

Identify
\[
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=\ell_0^{(1)},
\qquad
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}=\ell_0^{(3)},
\qquad
\Lambda_E^{(0)}=e_0^{(1)},
\qquad
\Lambda_O^{(0)}=o_0^{(1)}.
\]

The exact final microscopic decision rule is therefore
\[
\ell_0^{(1)}\neq 0
\quad\text{or}\quad
\ell_0^{(3)}\neq 0,
\qquad
(e_0^{(1)},o_0^{(1)})\neq (0,0).
\]

\section{First Explicit Blockwise Audit: \(OO\) Primitive and Mixed-Block Transverse Carriers}

\subsection{Short Korean explanation}

The next non-repetitive step is to identify which Hessian blocks are the natural microscopic carriers of the four leading coefficients
\[
\ell_0^{(1)},\qquad
\ell_0^{(3)},\qquad
e_0^{(1)},\qquad
o_0^{(1)}.
\]

At the current rigorous stage, the sharpest blockwise statement is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
OO \text{ is the natural primitive longitudinal block for } \ell_0^{(3)},
}
\end{equation}
while
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
TD,DT,OD,DO,DD
\text{ are the natural transverse candidate blocks for }
e_0^{(1)},o_0^{(1)}.
}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Step 1: why \(OO\) is the primitive longitudinal block}

The orientational diagonal block has the form
\begin{equation}
\mathcal H_{OO}
=
-Z_{O,k}\partial^2
+
\mathcal M_{OO}^{\mathrm{pot}}(\xi)
+
Y_k\mathcal K_{OO}^{\nabla\mathrm{ani}}(\xi,\partial)
+
\mathcal T_{OO}(\xi,\partial_y),
\label{eq:OO_block_recall}
\end{equation}
where the final term
\[
\mathcal T_{OO}(\xi,\partial_y)
\]
is explicitly identified as the background-induced first-order transport operator. 

The primitive longitudinal seed is
\begin{equation}
\mathcal T_\xi:=i[P_B,\partial_\xi P_B],
\qquad
S_\xi:=(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}.
\label{eq:primitive_seed_recall}
\end{equation}
For the explicit defect representative,
\begin{equation}
S_\xi=\frac12\theta'(\xi)^2\sigma_3.
\label{eq:Sxi_sigma3}
\end{equation}
Hence the primitive longitudinal transport block is
\begin{equation}
V^\mu_{\parallel,\mathrm{prim}}(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)\,S_\xi\,n^\mu
=
\frac12\theta'(\xi)^3 n^\mu\sigma_3.
\label{eq:Vparallel_prim_again}
\end{equation}
This is exactly the Branch-B longitudinal mechanism. 

Therefore the \(OO\) block is the natural microscopic source of the coefficient
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)}=\frac{\lambda_{c;OO}}{2},
}
\label{eq:l03_OO_def}
\end{equation}
defined by
\begin{equation}
\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)}
=
\lim_{\theta,\theta',\dots\to 0}
\frac{
\mathfrak P_\parallel[\mathcal M_{OO,\mathrm{inv}}]
-
\ell_{0;OO}^{(1)}
}{
\theta'^2
}.
\label{eq:l03_OO_limit}
\end{equation}

Inside the exact primitive Class-II-compatible realization,
\[
\ell_{0;OO}^{(1)}=0,
\]
so this reduces to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)}
=
\lim_{\theta,\theta',\dots\to 0}
\frac{\mathfrak P_\parallel[\mathcal M_{OO,\mathrm{inv}}]}{\theta'^2}.
}
\label{eq:l03_OO_limit_reduced}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Step 2: why \(OO\) does not naturally produce the transverse doublet at leading order}

The primitive commutator-square channel produces only the traceless singlet
\[
\sigma_3,
\]
not the Pauli doublet
\[
(\sigma_1,\sigma_2).
\]
This is an already-closed structural fact. 

Therefore:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
OO \text{ is the canonical source of } \ell_0^{(3)},
\quad
OO \text{ is not the natural leading source of } e_0^{(1)},o_0^{(1)}.
}
\label{eq:OO_role_statement}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Step 3: transverse carriers require mixed shell-defect/current structure}

The transverse channels require the minimal doublet source
\begin{equation}
V^\mu_{\perp}(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)\Bigl[
\Lambda_E E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a+\Lambda_O J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
\Bigr].
\label{eq:Vperp_recall}
\end{equation}
This does not arise from the primitive commutator-square singlet.
It requires an explicit transverse carrier structure. 

In the minimal complete Class II current realization,
\[
J_i^a[\Psi]
=
(\partial_i\Psi^\dagger)T_a\Psi+\mathrm{h.c.},
\qquad
K_i^a[P,\psi]
=
\Tr(T_a\partial_iP)\,\mathcal O[\psi],
\]
and after eliminating the heavy mediator,
the effective source splits into a transverse part and a primitive longitudinal part:
\begin{equation}
\mathcal L_{\perp}^{(1)}
\sim
(\partial_\xi\phi_0)\phi_0\,\theta'(\xi)\,[m_a k_a]\,\mathcal O[\psi],
\label{eq:Lperp_split}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\mathcal L_{\parallel}^{\mathrm{prim}}
\sim
\phi_0^2\,\theta'(\xi)\,[\mathcal A_\xi^a k_a]\,\mathcal O[\psi].
\label{eq:Lpar_split}
\end{equation}
The first generates \(V^\mu_\perp\), while the second reduces to the primitive \(I_{\theta'^3}\) singlet. :contentReference[oaicite:7]{index=7}

This means the transverse doublet is carried by blocks that mix shell-gradient/current data with defect/projector/tangent data.

\subsection{Step 4: candidate block assignment for \(e_0^{(1)}\) and \(o_0^{(1)}\)}

Using the sector labels
\[
T=\text{shell/amplitude},\qquad
O=\text{orientational/projector},\qquad
D=\text{defect-tangent},
\]
the natural candidates for the transverse doublet coefficients are:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
TD,\ DT,\ OD,\ DO,\ DD.
}
\label{eq:transverse_candidate_blocks}
\end{equation}

The reason is simple:

\begin{enumerate}
\item \(TD\) and \(DT\) carry the shell-gradient/current side needed to generate the worldvolume doublet;
\item \(OD\) and \(DO\) carry projector-defect mixing into the \(Q_B\)-fiber doublet;
\item \(DD\) can renormalize or directly support the final \(Q_B\)-endomorphism-valued doublet structure after Schur reduction.
\end{enumerate}

By contrast, the pure \(TT\) block is mostly scalar/potential/anisotropy at current explicit level and is therefore expected to feed either the spectator channel \(h_0\) or subleading corrections, not the essential transverse witness pair. 

So the sharp current assignment is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
e_0^{(1)},o_0^{(1)}
\text{ should be audited first in }
TD/DT/OD/DO/DD.
}
\label{eq:EO_blocks_first}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Step 5: executable projector formulas for the first transverse audit}

For each candidate block \(AB\in\{TD,DT,OD,DO,DD\}\), define
\begin{equation}
e_{0;AB}^{(1)}
=
\lim_{\theta,\theta',\dots\to 0}
\mathfrak P_E[\mathcal M_{AB,\mathrm{inv}}],
\label{eq:e01_AB_exec}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
o_{0;AB}^{(1)}
=
\lim_{\theta,\theta',\dots\to 0}
\mathfrak P_O[\mathcal M_{AB,\mathrm{inv}}],
\label{eq:o01_AB_exec}
\end{equation}
where
\begin{equation}
\mathfrak P_E[\mathcal M]
=
\frac14 E^\mu{}_a\Tr(\sigma_a\mathcal M_\mu),
\qquad
\mathfrak P_O[\mathcal M]
=
\frac14 J^\mu{}_a\Tr(\sigma_a\mathcal M_\mu).
\label{eq:EO_projectors_exec}
\end{equation}

The first nonzero block among these candidates determines the leading transverse source:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
e_0^{(1)}=\sum_{AB\in\{TD,DT,OD,DO,DD\}} e_{0;AB}^{(1)},
\qquad
o_0^{(1)}=\sum_{AB\in\{TD,DT,OD,DO,DD\}} o_{0;AB}^{(1)}.
}
\label{eq:EO_sum_candidates}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Step 6: executable projector formula for the primitive \(OO\) block}

The primitive longitudinal audit is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)}
=
\lim_{\theta,\theta',\dots\to 0}
\frac{
\frac12\Tr\!\bigl(\sigma_3 n_\mu \mathcal M^\mu_{OO,\mathrm{inv}}\bigr)
-
\ell_{0;OO}^{(1)}
}{\theta'^2}.
}
\label{eq:l03_OO_projector_exec}
\end{equation}
In the exact currently explicit primitive branch,
\[
\ell_{0;OO}^{(1)}=0,
\]
so
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)}
=
\lim_{\theta,\theta',\dots\to 0}
\frac{
\frac12\Tr\!\bigl(\sigma_3 n_\mu \mathcal M^\mu_{OO,\mathrm{inv}}\bigr)
}{\theta'^2}.
}
\label{eq:l03_OO_projector_exec_reduced}
\end{equation}

Then
\begin{equation}
\ell_0^{(3)}=\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)}+\sum_{(A,B)\neq(OO)}\ell_{0;AB}^{(3)},
\label{eq:l03_full_split}
\end{equation}
but at the current explicit stage the best supported leading contributor is \(OO\). 

\subsection{Step 7: sharp current blockwise roadmap}

The literal next audit order should be:

\paragraph{(1) Primitive longitudinal}
Evaluate
\[
\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)}.
\]

\paragraph{(2) Transverse even/odd}
Evaluate in order
\[
(TD),(DT),(OD),(DO),(DD)
\]
for
\[
e_{0;AB}^{(1)},\qquad o_{0;AB}^{(1)}.
\]

\paragraph{(3) Branch-A check}
Only after this, check whether a genuine
\[
\ell_0^{(1)}\neq 0
\]
constant-leading longitudinal term survives in the refined complete core sector.

This matches the current strongest honest status:
the reduced PDE form is closed, the exact concrete explicit branch is Branch B, and the true complete microscopic closure is the actual coefficient-point extraction from the final Hessian. 

\section{Final Summary}

The first explicit blockwise audit gives the following sharp assignment:

\[
\boxed{
OO \text{ is the natural primitive longitudinal block for } \ell_0^{(3)}=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}.
}
\]

The exact executable formula is
\[
\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)}
=
\lim_{\theta,\theta',\dots\to 0}
\frac{
\frac12\Tr(\sigma_3 n_\mu \mathcal M^\mu_{OO,\mathrm{inv}})
-
\ell_{0;OO}^{(1)}
}{\theta'^2},
\]
and in the explicit primitive branch,
\[
\ell_{0;OO}^{(1)}=0.
\]

The transverse witness coefficients require an explicit doublet source and therefore should be audited first in the mixed carrier blocks
\[
\boxed{
TD,\ DT,\ OD,\ DO,\ DD.
}
\]
Their exact projector formulas are
\[
e_{0;AB}^{(1)}
=
\lim \mathfrak P_E[\mathcal M_{AB,\mathrm{inv}}],
\qquad
o_{0;AB}^{(1)}
=
\lim \mathfrak P_O[\mathcal M_{AB,\mathrm{inv}}],
\]
with
\[
\mathfrak P_E[\mathcal M]
=
\frac14 E^\mu{}_a\Tr(\sigma_a\mathcal M_\mu),
\qquad
\mathfrak P_O[\mathcal M]
=
\frac14 J^\mu{}_a\Tr(\sigma_a\mathcal M_\mu).
\]

Thus the literal next microscopic task is:
\[
\boxed{
\text{compute }\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)}
\text{ and then audit }TD,DT,OD,DO,DD\text{ for }e_0^{(1)},o_0^{(1)}.
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{First Nontrivial Blockwise Closure: the \(OO\) Primitive Coefficient and the Mixed Transverse Audit}

\subsection{Short Korean explanation}

The first block that can be closed explicitly is the \(OO\) block.
It carries the primitive longitudinal channel and therefore determines the leading Branch-B coefficient
\[
\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)}=\frac{\lambda_{c;OO}}{2}.
\]

The transverse coefficients
\[
e_0^{(1)},\qquad o_0^{(1)}
\]
should then be audited in the mixed carrier blocks
\[
TD,\ DT,\ OD,\ DO,\ DD.
\]

\subsection{1. The \(OO\)-block as the primitive longitudinal carrier}

The orientational diagonal block has the form
\begin{equation}
\mathcal H_{OO}
=
-Z_{O,k}\partial^2
+
\mathcal M_{OO}^{\mathrm{pot}}(\xi)
+
Y_k\mathcal K_{OO}^{\nabla\mathrm{ani}}(\xi,\partial)
+
\mathcal T_{OO}(\xi,\partial_y),
\label{eq:OO_block_start_now}
\end{equation}
where \(\mathcal T_{OO}\) is the background-induced first-order transport operator.

The primitive longitudinal seed is
\begin{equation}
\mathcal T_\xi:=i[P_B,\partial_\xi P_B],
\qquad
S_\xi:=(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}.
\label{eq:primitive_seed_now}
\end{equation}
For the explicit defect representative,
\begin{equation}
S_\xi=\frac12\theta'(\xi)^2\sigma_3.
\label{eq:Sxi_explicit_now}
\end{equation}
Hence the primitive longitudinal transport kernel is
\begin{equation}
V^\mu_{\parallel,\mathrm{prim}}(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)S_\xi n^\mu
=
\frac12\theta'(\xi)^3 n^\mu\sigma_3.
\label{eq:Vprim_OO_now}
\end{equation}

Therefore the \(OO\)-block contributes naturally to the cubic longitudinal coefficient and not to the linear one:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\ell_{0;OO}^{(1)}=0,
\qquad
\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)}=\frac{\lambda_{c;OO}}{2}.
}
\label{eq:OO_coeff_ident}
\end{equation}

\subsection{2. Explicit projector formula for \(\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)}\)}

Let
\begin{equation}
\mathcal M^\mu_{OO,\mathrm{inv}}(\theta)
=
h_{0;OO}(\theta)n^\mu\mathbf 1_2
+
h_{\parallel;OO}(\theta)n^\mu\sigma_3
+
h_{E;OO}(\theta)E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
+
h_{O;OO}(\theta)J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a.
\label{eq:MOO_inv_now}
\end{equation}
Since the primitive channel is purely longitudinal singlet,
\begin{equation}
h_{\parallel;OO}(\theta)
=
\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)}\theta'(\xi)^2
+
O(\theta'^4,\theta^2\theta'^2),
\label{eq:hpar_OO_expand_now}
\end{equation}
with no constant-leading \(\theta'^0\) term.

Thus the exact executable extraction formula is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)}
=
\lim_{\theta,\theta',\theta'',\dots\to 0}
\frac{
\frac12\Tr\!\left[\sigma_3 n_\mu \mathcal M^\mu_{OO,\mathrm{inv}}\right]
}{\theta'(\xi)^2}.
}
\label{eq:l03_OO_final_exec}
\end{equation}

Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_{c;OO}
=
2\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)}.
}
\label{eq:lambdac_OO_from_l03}
\end{equation}

\subsection{3. Reduced contribution of the \(OO\) primitive block}

After overlap projection,
\begin{equation}
\lambda_{\parallel;OO}
=
I_{\theta'^3}\,\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)}
=
\frac{\lambda_{c;OO}}{2}I_{\theta'^3}.
\label{eq:lambda_OO_reduced}
\end{equation}
Using the already established explicit overlap,
\begin{equation}
I_{\theta'^3}
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{256}\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
\label{eq:I3_reuse_now}
\end{equation}
we obtain
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_{\parallel;OO}
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{256}\theta_0^3\kappa^3\,\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)}
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\lambda_{c;OO}\theta_0^3\kappa^3.
}
\label{eq:lambda_OO_explicit}
\end{equation}

\subsection{4. Why the \(OO\) block is not the leading transverse carrier}

The primitive commutator-square channel produces only
\[
\sigma_3,
\]
that is, the longitudinal singlet. It does not generate the transverse Pauli doublet
\[
(\sigma_1,\sigma_2)
\]
at leading order. Therefore:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
e_{0;OO}^{(1)}=0,
\qquad
o_{0;OO}^{(1)}=0
\quad
\text{at primitive leading order.}
}
\label{eq:OO_no_transverse}
\end{equation}

\subsection{5. Mixed-block candidates for the transverse coefficients}

The transverse source must have the form
\begin{equation}
V^\mu_\perp(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)\Bigl[
\Lambda_E E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
+
\Lambda_O J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
\Bigr].
\label{eq:Vperp_target_now}
\end{equation}
Hence the natural candidate blocks are precisely the mixed carrier blocks
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
TD,\ DT,\ OD,\ DO,\ DD.
}
\label{eq:transverse_candidates_now}
\end{equation}

For each such block \(AB\), define
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
e_{0;AB}^{(1)}
=
\lim_{\theta,\theta',\dots\to 0}
\frac14 E^\mu{}_a\Tr\!\left[\sigma_a\mathcal M_{AB,\mu}^{\mathrm{inv}}\right],
}
\label{eq:e01_AB_now}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
o_{0;AB}^{(1)}
=
\lim_{\theta,\theta',\dots\to 0}
\frac14 J^\mu{}_a\Tr\!\left[\sigma_a\mathcal M_{AB,\mu}^{\mathrm{inv}}\right].
}
\label{eq:o01_AB_now}
\end{equation}

Then the full transverse leading coefficients are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
e_0^{(1)}
=
\sum_{AB\in\{TD,DT,OD,DO,DD\}} e_{0;AB}^{(1)},
\qquad
o_0^{(1)}
=
\sum_{AB\in\{TD,DT,OD,DO,DD\}} o_{0;AB}^{(1)}.
}
\label{eq:EO_sum_now}
\end{equation}

\subsection{6. Practical audit order}

The correct audit sequence is now fixed:

\paragraph{(i) Primitive longitudinal}
Compute
\begin{equation}
\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)}
=
\lim_{\theta,\theta',\dots\to 0}
\frac{
\frac12\Tr[\sigma_3 n_\mu \mathcal M^\mu_{OO,\mathrm{inv}}]
}{\theta'^2}.
\label{eq:practical_step1}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{(ii) Transverse mixed blocks}
Evaluate in order
\[
TD,\ DT,\ OD,\ DO,\ DD
\]
using
\eqref{eq:e01_AB_now} and \eqref{eq:o01_AB_now}.

\paragraph{(iii) Final reduced coefficients}
Assemble
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel
=
I_\theta\,\ell_0^{(1)}
+
I_{\theta'^3}\,\ell_0^{(3)},
\qquad
\alpha=I_\theta e_0^{(1)},
\qquad
\beta=I_\theta o_0^{(1)}.
\label{eq:final_assembly_now}
\end{equation}
In the currently explicit primitive Branch-B realization,
\[
\ell_0^{(1)}=0,
\]
so
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=I_{\theta'^3}\ell_0^{(3)},
\qquad
\alpha=I_\theta e_0^{(1)},
\qquad
\beta=I_\theta o_0^{(1)}.
}
\label{eq:branchB_assembly_now}
\end{equation}

\section{Final Summary}

The first blockwise closure is:

\[
\boxed{
OO \text{ is the primitive longitudinal carrier block.}
}
\]

Its leading coefficient is
\[
\boxed{
\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)}
=
\lim_{\theta,\theta',\dots\to 0}
\frac{
\frac12\Tr[\sigma_3 n_\mu \mathcal M^\mu_{OO,\mathrm{inv}}]
}{\theta'^2},
\qquad
\lambda_{c;OO}=2\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)}.
}
\]

Its reduced contribution is
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_{\parallel;OO}
=
I_{\theta'^3}\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)}
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\lambda_{c;OO}\theta_0^3\kappa^3.
}
\]

At primitive leading order,
\[
\boxed{
e_{0;OO}^{(1)}=o_{0;OO}^{(1)}=0.
}
\]

The transverse coefficients must therefore be audited in the mixed carrier blocks
\[
\boxed{
TD,\ DT,\ OD,\ DO,\ DD,
}
\]
through
\[
e_{0;AB}^{(1)}
=
\lim \frac14 E^\mu{}_a\Tr(\sigma_a\mathcal M_{AB,\mu}^{\mathrm{inv}}),
\qquad
o_{0;AB}^{(1)}
=
\lim \frac14 J^\mu{}_a\Tr(\sigma_a\mathcal M_{AB,\mu}^{\mathrm{inv}}).
\]

So the literal next microscopic step is to compute \(\mathcal M^\mu_{OO,\mathrm{inv}}\) explicitly and then audit the mixed blocks for the transverse pair.


%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{First Explicit Blockwise Closure from the Current Complete Library}

\subsection{Short Korean explanation}

Inside the current explicit complete Hessian library, the first blockwise closure is now sharp:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the \(OO\)-block carries the primitive longitudinal Branch-B coefficient;
\item the leading transverse coefficients are most directly carried by the \(K\)-sector contribution inside the mixed tangent transport block.
\end{enumerate}

So the first actual coefficient-point split is:

\[
OO \longrightarrow \ell_{0;OO}^{(3)},
\qquad
K\text{-sector} \longrightarrow e_0^{(1)},o_0^{(1)}.
\]

\subsection{1. Explicit primitive longitudinal coefficient from the \(OO\)-block}

The primitive seed is
\begin{equation}
\mathcal T_\xi=i[P_B,\partial_\xi P_B],
\qquad
S_\xi=(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}.
\label{eq:OO_primitive_seed_final}
\end{equation}
For the explicit defect representative,
\begin{equation}
S_\xi=\frac12\,\theta'(\xi)^2\,\sigma_3.
\label{eq:OO_Sxi_final}
\end{equation}
Hence the primitive longitudinal transport kernel is
\begin{equation}
V^\mu_{OO,\mathrm{prim}}(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)\,S_\xi\,n^\mu
=
\frac12\,\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\sigma_3.
\label{eq:OO_Vprim_final}
\end{equation}

Therefore the invariant longitudinal coefficient in the \(OO\)-block has no constant-leading term and starts at the primitive cubic order:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\ell_{0;OO}^{(1)}=0,
\qquad
\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)}=\frac{\lambda_{c;OO}}{2}.
}
\label{eq:OO_coefficients_final}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, if
\begin{equation}
\mathcal M^\mu_{OO,\mathrm{inv}}
=
h_{0;OO}n^\mu\mathbf 1_2
+
h_{\parallel;OO}n^\mu\sigma_3
+
h_{E;OO}E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
+
h_{O;OO}J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a,
\label{eq:OO_Minv_final}
\end{equation}
then
\begin{equation}
h_{\parallel;OO}(\theta)
=
\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)}\,\theta'(\xi)^2
+
O(\theta'^4,\theta^2\theta'^2),
\label{eq:OO_hpar_final}
\end{equation}
and the exact executable projector formula is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)}
=
\lim_{\theta,\theta',\theta'',\dots\to 0}
\frac{
\frac12\Tr\!\left[\sigma_3\,n_\mu \mathcal M^\mu_{OO,\mathrm{inv}}\right]
}{\theta'(\xi)^2}.
}
\label{eq:OO_projector_final}
\end{equation}

The reduced longitudinal witness from this block is therefore
\begin{equation}
\lambda_{\parallel;OO}
=
I_{\theta'^3}\,\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)}
=
\frac{\lambda_{c;OO}}{2}I_{\theta'^3}.
\label{eq:OO_reduced_lambda_final}
\end{equation}
Using
\begin{equation}
I_{\theta'^3}
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{256}\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
\label{eq:Itheta3_reuse_final}
\end{equation}
one gets
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_{\parallel;OO}
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{256}\theta_0^3\kappa^3\,\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)}
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\lambda_{c;OO}\theta_0^3\kappa^3.
}
\label{eq:OO_lambda_explicit_final}
\end{equation}

\subsection{2. Why the \(J\)-sector alone does not close the transverse leading coefficients}

For
\begin{equation}
J_i^a[\Psi]=(\partial_i\Psi^\dagger)T_a\Psi+\Psi^\dagger T_a(\partial_i\Psi),
\label{eq:Jsector_def_final}
\end{equation}
the lowest worldvolume-derivative contribution is
\begin{equation}
\delta J_i^a\big|_{\partial_y}
=
(\partial_i\Psi_B^\dagger)T_a\,\delta\Psi_{\partial_y}
+
\delta\Psi_{\partial_y}^\dagger T_a(\partial_i\Psi_B).
\label{eq:Jsector_dy_final}
\end{equation}
Its projected tangent transport contribution is
\begin{equation}
V_J^\mu
=
\Pi_Q
\frac{\partial(\delta^2 S_J)}{\partial(-i\partial_{y^\mu})}
\Pi_Q.
\label{eq:VJ_final}
\end{equation}
At lowest order, in the explicit real defect representative with embedded \(SU(2)_{(13)}\),
this sector contributes only to the primitive longitudinal channel and does not by itself generate the transverse \(E/O\) pair.
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
J\text{-sector alone} \Rightarrow \text{primitive longitudinal, not leading transverse }e_0^{(1)},o_0^{(1)}.
}
\label{eq:J_no_transverse_final}
\end{equation}

\subsection{3. The \(K\)-sector as the explicit transverse carrier}

Take the minimal complete \(K\)-sector choice
\begin{equation}
K_i^a[P,\psi]
=
\Tr(T_a\partial_iP)\,
(\Lambda_E^{(0)}E_j+\Lambda_O^{(0)}J_j)D_j\psi.
\label{eq:Ksector_choice_final}
\end{equation}
On the defect background,
\begin{equation}
\partial_iP_B
=
\delta_{i\xi}\theta'(\xi)\bigl(e_1 z_B^\dagger+z_B e_1^\dagger\bigr),
\label{eq:dPB_final}
\end{equation}
so
\begin{equation}
K_i^a[P_B,\psi]
=
\delta_{i\xi}\theta'(\xi)\,k_a(\theta)\,
(\Lambda_E^{(0)}E_j+\Lambda_O^{(0)}J_j)D_j\psi.
\label{eq:K_background_final}
\end{equation}
Therefore the induced tangent transport block has the explicit form
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V_K^\mu
=
\theta'(\xi)
\Bigl[
\kappa_E(\xi)\,E^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
+
\kappa_O(\xi)\,J^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
\Bigr],
}
\label{eq:VK_explicit_final}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\kappa_E(\xi)\propto k_a(\theta)\Lambda_E^{(0)},
\qquad
\kappa_O(\xi)\propto k_a(\theta)\Lambda_O^{(0)}.
\label{eq:kappaEO_final}
\end{equation}
Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_3^{(K)}=0,
\qquad
b_E^{(K)}=\kappa_E(\xi)\theta'(\xi),
\qquad
b_O^{(K)}=\kappa_O(\xi)\theta'(\xi).
}
\label{eq:Ksector_coeffs_final}
\end{equation}

This means that the explicit transverse-leading coefficients are naturally extracted from the \(K\)-sector:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
e_{0;K}^{(1)}
=
\lim_{\theta,\theta',\dots\to 0}
\frac14 E^\mu{}_a\Tr\!\left[\sigma_a\mathcal M^{(K)}_\mu\right],
}
\label{eq:e0K_final}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
o_{0;K}^{(1)}
=
\lim_{\theta,\theta',\dots\to 0}
\frac14 J^\mu{}_a\Tr\!\left[\sigma_a\mathcal M^{(K)}_\mu\right].
}
\label{eq:o0K_final}
\end{equation}

At the leading explicit level,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
e_{0;K}^{(1)}\propto \Lambda_E^{(0)},
\qquad
o_{0;K}^{(1)}\propto \Lambda_O^{(0)}.
}
\label{eq:e0o0K_prop_final}
\end{equation}

\subsection{4. First closed blockwise coefficient point inside the current library}

Thus, inside the currently explicit complete operator library, the leading coefficient point decomposes as
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\ell_0^{(1)}=0,
\qquad
\ell_0^{(3)}=\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)},
\qquad
e_0^{(1)}=e_{0;K}^{(1)},
\qquad
o_0^{(1)}=o_{0;K}^{(1)},
}
\label{eq:first_closed_point_final}
\end{equation}
up to additional unclosed contributions from the final full TECT completion.

Therefore the reduced coefficients are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
I_{\theta'^3}\,\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)},
\qquad
\alpha
=
I_\theta\,e_{0;K}^{(1)},
\qquad
\beta
=
I_\theta\,o_{0;K}^{(1)}.
}
\label{eq:first_closed_reduced_final}
\end{equation}

Using
\begin{equation}
I_\theta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
I_{\theta'^3}
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{256}\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
\label{eq:overlap_reuse_final2}
\end{equation}
this becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{256}\theta_0^3\kappa^3\,\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)},
\qquad
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa\,e_{0;K}^{(1)},
\qquad
\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa\,o_{0;K}^{(1)}.
}
\label{eq:first_closed_explicit_final}
\end{equation}

\subsection{5. Exact finite test inside the current explicit library}

Hence the finite microscopic closure test inside the currently explicit library is simply
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)}\neq 0,
\qquad
\bigl(e_{0;K}^{(1)},o_{0;K}^{(1)}\bigr)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:first_explicit_finite_test}
\end{equation}
Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_{c;OO}\neq 0,
\qquad
\bigl(\Lambda_E^{(0)},\Lambda_O^{(0)}\bigr)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:first_explicit_finite_test_alt}
\end{equation}

\section{Final Summary}

The first genuinely explicit blockwise closure inside the current complete operator library is:

\[
\boxed{
OO \text{ carries the primitive longitudinal Branch-B coefficient,}
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
K\text{-sector carries the leading transverse pair.}
}
\]

More precisely,
\[
\ell_{0;OO}^{(1)}=0,
\qquad
\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)}=\frac{\lambda_{c;OO}}{2},
\]
with
\[
\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)}
=
\lim
\frac{
\frac12\Tr[\sigma_3 n_\mu\mathcal M^\mu_{OO,\mathrm{inv}}]
}{\theta'^2},
\]
and
\[
e_{0;K}^{(1)}
=
\lim
\frac14 E^\mu{}_a\Tr[\sigma_a\mathcal M^{(K)}_\mu],
\qquad
o_{0;K}^{(1)}
=
\lim
\frac14 J^\mu{}_a\Tr[\sigma_a\mathcal M^{(K)}_\mu].
\]

Thus the reduced coefficients are explicitly
\[
\lambda_\parallel
=
I_{\theta'^3}\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)},
\qquad
\alpha=I_\theta e_{0;K}^{(1)},
\qquad
\beta=I_\theta o_{0;K}^{(1)}.
\]

So the current explicit finite closure condition is
\[
\boxed{
\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)}\neq 0,
\qquad
(e_{0;K}^{(1)},o_{0;K}^{(1)})\neq (0,0).
}
\]

This is the sharpest blockwise audit result available before inserting the final fully completed TECT Hessian.

\section{First explicit blockwise closure inside the current complete library}

Inside the current explicit complete operator library, the first closed blockwise coefficient-point assignment is
\[
\ell_0^{(1)}=0,
\qquad
\ell_0^{(3)}=\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)},
\qquad
e_0^{(1)}=e_{0;K}^{(1)},
\qquad
o_0^{(1)}=o_{0;K}^{(1)}.
\]

The primitive longitudinal coefficient is
\[
\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)}
=
\lim_{\theta,\theta',\dots\to 0}
\frac{
\frac12\Tr[\sigma_3 n_\mu \mathcal M^\mu_{OO,\mathrm{inv}}]
}{\theta'^2}
=
\frac{\lambda_{c;OO}}{2},
\]
while the leading transverse coefficients are
\[
e_{0;K}^{(1)}
=
\lim_{\theta,\theta',\dots\to 0}
\frac14 E^\mu{}_a\Tr[\sigma_a\mathcal M^{(K)}_\mu],
\qquad
o_{0;K}^{(1)}
=
\lim_{\theta,\theta',\dots\to 0}
\frac14 J^\mu{}_a\Tr[\sigma_a\mathcal M^{(K)}_\mu].
\]

Therefore
\[
\lambda_\parallel
=
I_{\theta'^3}\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)},
\qquad
\alpha=I_\theta e_{0;K}^{(1)},
\qquad
\beta=I_\theta o_{0;K}^{(1)}.
\]

Using the explicit overlaps,
\[
I_\theta=-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
I_{\theta'^3}=-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{256}\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
\]
this becomes
\[
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{256}\theta_0^3\kappa^3\,\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)},
\qquad
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa\,e_{0;K}^{(1)},
\qquad
\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa\,o_{0;K}^{(1)}.
\]

Hence the explicit finite closure test inside the current library is
\[
\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)}\neq 0,
\qquad
(e_{0;K}^{(1)},o_{0;K}^{(1)})\neq (0,0).
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Low–Mode Projection of the \(K\)-Sector Transport Operator}

\subsection{Short explanation}

The transverse coefficients
\[
e_{0;K}^{(1)},\qquad o_{0;K}^{(1)}
\]
are determined by projecting the induced tangent transport operator
onto the defect worldvolume zero modes.

\subsection{1. Tangent transport operator from the \(K\)-sector}

The explicit induced operator has the form
\begin{equation}
V_K^\mu(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)
\Bigl[
\kappa_E(\xi)E^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
+
\kappa_O(\xi)J^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
\Bigr].
\end{equation}

At leading order near the defect center,
\[
\kappa_E(\xi)\simeq \Lambda_E^{(0)},\qquad
\kappa_O(\xi)\simeq \Lambda_O^{(0)}.
\]

Thus
\begin{equation}
V_K^\mu
=
\theta'(\xi)
\left[
\Lambda_E^{(0)}E^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
+
\Lambda_O^{(0)}J^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
\right].
\end{equation}

---

\subsection{2. Zero-mode structure}

The fermion zero mode localized on the defect takes the separable form

\begin{equation}
\Psi_0(x)
=
\psi_0(y)\,f(\xi),
\end{equation}

where

\[
\int d\xi\,|f(\xi)|^2=1.
\]

For the tanh defect

\begin{equation}
f(\xi)\propto
\exp
\left[
-\int^\xi m(\xi')d\xi'
\right].
\end{equation}

---

\subsection{3. Projection formula}

The effective worldvolume operator is obtained by

\begin{equation}
\mathcal M_\mu^{\mathrm{eff}}
=
\int d\xi
\,f(\xi)^2
V_{K,\mu}(\xi).
\end{equation}

Substituting the explicit form,

\begin{equation}
\mathcal M_\mu^{\mathrm{eff}}
=
\Bigl[
\Lambda_E^{(0)}E^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
+
\Lambda_O^{(0)}J^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
\Bigr]
\int d\xi\,f(\xi)^2\theta'(\xi).
\end{equation}

Define the overlap

\begin{equation}
I_{\psi\theta}
=
\int d\xi\,f(\xi)^2\theta'(\xi).
\end{equation}

Then

\begin{equation}
\mathcal M_\mu^{\mathrm{eff}}
=
I_{\psi\theta}
\left[
\Lambda_E^{(0)}E^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
+
\Lambda_O^{(0)}J^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
\right].
\end{equation}

---

\subsection{4. Extraction of coefficients}

By definition

\begin{equation}
e_{0;K}^{(1)}
=
\frac14
E^\mu{}_a
\Tr
\left[
\sigma_a\mathcal M_\mu^{\mathrm{eff}}
\right],
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
o_{0;K}^{(1)}
=
\frac14
J^\mu{}_a
\Tr
\left[
\sigma_a\mathcal M_\mu^{\mathrm{eff}}
\right].
\end{equation}

Substituting the operator,

\begin{equation}
e_{0;K}^{(1)}
=
\frac14 I_{\psi\theta}
\Lambda_E^{(0)}
E^\mu_aE_{\mu b}
\Tr(\sigma_a\sigma_b),
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
o_{0;K}^{(1)}
=
\frac14 I_{\psi\theta}
\Lambda_O^{(0)}
J^\mu_aJ_{\mu b}
\Tr(\sigma_a\sigma_b).
\end{equation}

Using

\[
E^\mu_aE_{\mu b}=\delta_{ab},\qquad
J^\mu_aJ_{\mu b}=\delta_{ab},
\]

\[
\Tr(\sigma_a\sigma_b)=2\delta_{ab},
\]

we obtain

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
e_{0;K}^{(1)}
=
\frac12\,I_{\psi\theta}\Lambda_E^{(0)},
}
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
o_{0;K}^{(1)}
=
\frac12\,I_{\psi\theta}\Lambda_O^{(0)}.
}
\end{equation}

---

\subsection{5. Explicit overlap}

For the tanh defect

\[
\theta(\xi)=\theta_0\tanh(\kappa\xi)
\]

\[
\theta'(\xi)=\theta_0\kappa\,\mathrm{sech}^2(\kappa\xi)
\]

and the localized zero mode gives

\begin{equation}
I_{\psi\theta}
=
C_\psi\,\theta_0\kappa.
\end{equation}

Therefore

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
e_{0;K}^{(1)}
=
\frac12 C_\psi\,\theta_0\kappa\,\Lambda_E^{(0)},
}
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
o_{0;K}^{(1)}
=
\frac12 C_\psi\,\theta_0\kappa\,\Lambda_O^{(0)}.
}
\end{equation}

\section{Result of the \(K\)-sector projection}

The transverse coefficients produced by the \(K\)-sector are

\[
e_{0;K}^{(1)}
=
\frac12 I_{\psi\theta}\Lambda_E^{(0)},
\qquad
o_{0;K}^{(1)}
=
\frac12 I_{\psi\theta}\Lambda_O^{(0)}.
\]

For the tanh defect,

\[
I_{\psi\theta}=C_\psi\,\theta_0\kappa.
\]

Therefore

\[
e_{0;K}^{(1)}
=
\frac12 C_\psi\theta_0\kappa\,\Lambda_E^{(0)},
\]

\[
o_{0;K}^{(1)}
=
\frac12 C_\psi\theta_0\kappa\,\Lambda_O^{(0)}.
\]

The reduced IR coefficients become

\[
\alpha
=
I_\theta e_{0;K}^{(1)},
\qquad
\beta
=
I_\theta o_{0;K}^{(1)}.
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Final Full-Hessian Transport Audit for the Remaining Blocks}

\subsection{Short Korean explanation}

The remaining microscopic problem is to audit the first-order transport content of the unreduced Hessian blocks
\[
TT,\qquad TD,\qquad DT,\qquad DD,
\]
and determine their actual contributions to the leading coefficient point
\[
\ell_0^{(1)},\qquad \ell_0^{(3)},\qquad e_0^{(1)},\qquad o_0^{(1)}.
\]

This is a finite blockwise projection problem.

\subsection{1. General blockwise expansion}

For each block \(AB\in\{TT,TD,DT,DD\}\), write the worldvolume derivative expansion
\begin{equation}
\mathcal H_{AB}
=
\mathcal H^{(0)}_{AB}(\xi)
-
i\,\mathcal V^\mu_{AB}(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu}
+
\mathcal W^{\mu\nu}_{AB}(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu}\partial_{y^\nu}
+\cdots.
\label{eq:HAB_remaining_expand}
\end{equation}
Only \(\mathcal V^\mu_{AB}\) contributes to the principal first-order transport audit.

Project to the isolated graded infrared sector \(K=K_+\oplus K_-\):
\begin{equation}
V^\mu_{AB,\mathrm{eff}}
=
\Pi_K \mathcal V^\mu_{AB}\Pi_K
+
\Pi_K \mathcal H^{(0)}_{A\bar A}
\bigl(\mathcal H^{(0)}_{\bar A\bar B}\bigr)^{-1}
\mathcal V^\mu_{\bar B B}\Pi_K
+\cdots.
\label{eq:Veff_remaining}
\end{equation}
Take the grading-odd part
\begin{equation}
V^\mu_{AB,\mathrm{odd}}
=
\frac12\left(
V^\mu_{AB,\mathrm{eff}}
-
J V^\mu_{AB,\mathrm{eff}}J^{-1}
\right).
\label{eq:Vodd_remaining}
\end{equation}

Then decompose
\begin{equation}
V^\mu_{AB,\mathrm{odd}}(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)\,
\mathcal M^\mu_{AB,\mathrm{inv}}(\theta(\xi))
+
V^\mu_{AB,\mathrm{irr}}(\xi),
\label{eq:Vodd_remaining_decomp}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\mathcal M^\mu_{AB,\mathrm{inv}}
=
h_{0;AB}n^\mu\mathbf 1_2
+
h_{\parallel;AB}n^\mu\sigma_3
+
h_{E;AB}E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
+
h_{O;AB}J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a.
\label{eq:Minv_remaining}
\end{equation}

\subsection{2. Universal projector formulas}

The invariant projections are
\begin{equation}
\mathfrak P_\parallel[\mathcal M]
=
\frac12\Tr(\sigma_3 n_\mu \mathcal M^\mu),
\label{eq:Ppar_remaining}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\mathfrak P_E[\mathcal M]
=
\frac14 E^\mu{}_a \Tr(\sigma_a\mathcal M_\mu),
\label{eq:PE_remaining}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\mathfrak P_O[\mathcal M]
=
\frac14 J^\mu{}_a \Tr(\sigma_a\mathcal M_\mu).
\label{eq:PO_remaining}
\end{equation}

Hence
\begin{equation}
h_{\parallel;AB}=\mathfrak P_\parallel[\mathcal M_{AB,\mathrm{inv}}],
\qquad
h_{E;AB}=\mathfrak P_E[\mathcal M_{AB,\mathrm{inv}}],
\qquad
h_{O;AB}=\mathfrak P_O[\mathcal M_{AB,\mathrm{inv}}].
\label{eq:hAB_from_proj}
\end{equation}

The leading block coefficients are defined by
\begin{equation}
\ell_{0;AB}^{(1)}
=
\lim_{\theta,\theta',\dots\to 0}
\left(
h_{\parallel;AB}-\ell_{0;AB}^{(3)}\theta'^2
\right),
\label{eq:l01_AB_remaining}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\ell_{0;AB}^{(3)}
=
\lim_{\theta,\theta',\dots\to 0}
\frac{
h_{\parallel;AB}-\ell_{0;AB}^{(1)}
}{\theta'^2},
\label{eq:l03_AB_remaining}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
e_{0;AB}^{(1)}
=
\lim_{\theta,\theta',\dots\to 0} h_{E;AB},
\qquad
o_{0;AB}^{(1)}
=
\lim_{\theta,\theta',\dots\to 0} h_{O;AB}.
\label{eq:e01o01_AB_remaining}
\end{equation}

\subsection{3. \(TT\)-block audit}

The \(TT\)-block is the pure shell/amplitude block.
Its natural first-order transport structures come from scalar shell drift and anisotropic shell transport.

At principal order, its generic invariant form is
\begin{equation}
\mathcal M^\mu_{TT,\mathrm{inv}}
=
u_{0;TT}(\theta)\,n^\mu\mathbf 1_2
+
u_{\parallel;TT}(\theta)\,n^\mu\sigma_3
+
u_{E;TT}(\theta)\,E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
+
u_{O;TT}(\theta)\,J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a.
\label{eq:MTT_generic}
\end{equation}

However, in the current explicit working library, the pure shell block is dominantly scalar/isotropic and therefore expected to satisfy
\begin{equation}
u_{\parallel;TT}(0)=0,
\qquad
u_{E;TT}(0)=0,
\qquad
u_{O;TT}(0)=0,
\label{eq:TT_expected_zero}
\end{equation}
so that
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\ell_{0;TT}^{(1)}=0,
\qquad
\ell_{0;TT}^{(3)}=0,
\qquad
e_{0;TT}^{(1)}=0,
\qquad
o_{0;TT}^{(1)}=0
}
\label{eq:TT_expected_coeffs}
\end{equation}
unless the final refined derivative core generates an unexpected genuine Branch-A singlet.
Thus \(TT\) is best treated as a Branch-A check block rather than a primary carrier block.

\subsection{4. \(TD\)- and \(DT\)-block audit}

These are the most important remaining mixed blocks, because they directly mix shell-gradient carriers with defect-localized doublet carriers.

Their generic invariant form is
\begin{equation}
\mathcal M^\mu_{TD,\mathrm{inv}}
=
a_{\parallel;TD}(\theta)\,n^\mu\sigma_3
+
a_{E;TD}(\theta)\,E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
+
a_{O;TD}(\theta)\,J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a,
\label{eq:MTD_generic}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\mathcal M^\mu_{DT,\mathrm{inv}}
=
a_{\parallel;DT}(\theta)\,n^\mu\sigma_3
+
a_{E;DT}(\theta)\,E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
+
a_{O;DT}(\theta)\,J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a.
\label{eq:MDT_generic}
\end{equation}

Because these blocks contain one shell-gradient side and one defect/tangent side, they are the natural carrier of the linear transverse monomials
\[
\theta' E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a,
\qquad
\theta' J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a.
\]
Hence their leading coefficients are
\begin{equation}
e_{0;TD}^{(1)}
=
\lim_{\theta,\theta',\dots\to 0}
\frac14 E^\mu{}_a\Tr(\sigma_a\mathcal M^{TD}_{\mu}),
\label{eq:e01_TD}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
o_{0;TD}^{(1)}
=
\lim_{\theta,\theta',\dots\to 0}
\frac14 J^\mu{}_a\Tr(\sigma_a\mathcal M^{TD}_{\mu}),
\label{eq:o01_TD}
\end{equation}
and analogously for \(DT\).

At the current explicit structural level, the sharp expectation is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
e_{0;TD}^{(1)},\ o_{0;TD}^{(1)},\ e_{0;DT}^{(1)},\ o_{0;DT}^{(1)}
\text{ are the first nontrivial transverse candidates.}
}
\label{eq:TD_DT_main_candidates}
\end{equation}

\subsection{5. \(DD\)-block audit}

The \(DD\)-block acts entirely inside the defect-tangent doublet sector.
It therefore can contribute in two distinct ways:

\begin{enumerate}
\item direct support of the transverse doublet;
\item renormalization of already-induced \(TD/DT\) transport.
\end{enumerate}

Write
\begin{equation}
\mathcal M^\mu_{DD,\mathrm{inv}}
=
a_{\parallel;DD}(\theta)\,n^\mu\sigma_3
+
a_{E;DD}(\theta)\,E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
+
a_{O;DD}(\theta)\,J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a.
\label{eq:MDD_generic}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
e_{0;DD}^{(1)}
=
\lim_{\theta,\theta',\dots\to 0}
\frac14 E^\mu{}_a\Tr(\sigma_a\mathcal M^{DD}_{\mu}),
\label{eq:e01_DD}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
o_{0;DD}^{(1)}
=
\lim_{\theta,\theta',\dots\to 0}
\frac14 J^\mu{}_a\Tr(\sigma_a\mathcal M^{DD}_{\mu}).
\label{eq:o01_DD}
\end{equation}

The \(DD\)-block is therefore a genuine transverse candidate, but structurally it is more likely to renormalize the mixed-shell carrier than to generate it from nothing.

\subsection{6. Current best-supported decomposition}

Combining the already-closed \(OO\) primitive result with the remaining mixed-block expectations, the sharp current decomposition is
\begin{equation}
\ell_0^{(1)}
=
\ell_{0;TT}^{(1)}+\ell_{0;TD}^{(1)}+\ell_{0;DT}^{(1)}+\ell_{0;DD}^{(1)},
\label{eq:l01_remaining_sum}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\ell_0^{(3)}
=
\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)}
+\ell_{0;TT}^{(3)}+\ell_{0;TD}^{(3)}+\ell_{0;DT}^{(3)}+\ell_{0;DD}^{(3)},
\label{eq:l03_remaining_sum}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
e_0^{(1)}
=
e_{0;K}^{(1)}
+
e_{0;TD}^{(1)}+e_{0;DT}^{(1)}+e_{0;DD}^{(1)},
\label{eq:e01_remaining_sum}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
o_0^{(1)}
=
o_{0;K}^{(1)}
+
o_{0;TD}^{(1)}+o_{0;DT}^{(1)}+o_{0;DD}^{(1)}.
\label{eq:o01_remaining_sum}
\end{equation}

Inside the currently explicit library, the most conservative working truncation is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\ell_0^{(1)}\approx 0,
\qquad
\ell_0^{(3)}\approx \ell_{0;OO}^{(3)},
\qquad
e_0^{(1)}\approx e_{0;K}^{(1)},
\qquad
o_0^{(1)}\approx o_{0;K}^{(1)}.
}
\label{eq:conservative_truncation}
\end{equation}

\subsection{7. Reduced coefficients under the conservative truncation}

Then
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel
=
I_{\theta'^3}\,\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)},
\qquad
\alpha=I_\theta\,e_{0;K}^{(1)},
\qquad
\beta=I_\theta\,o_{0;K}^{(1)}.
\label{eq:reduced_under_truncation}
\end{equation}
Using
\begin{equation}
I_\theta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
I_{\theta'^3}
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{256}\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
\label{eq:reuse_overlaps_last}
\end{equation}
one obtains
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{256}\theta_0^3\kappa^3\,\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)},
}
\label{eq:lambda_last}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa\,e_{0;K}^{(1)},
\qquad
\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa\,o_{0;K}^{(1)}.
}
\label{eq:alphabeta_last}
\end{equation}

\subsection{8. Final microscopic tasks}

At this point, only two genuinely microscopic audits remain:

\paragraph{(A) Branch-A audit}
Determine whether the final refined complete core generates a genuine
\[
\ell_0^{(1)}\neq 0
\]
through \(TT/TD/DT/DD\).

\paragraph{(B) Mixed transverse audit}
Compute explicitly
\[
e_{0;TD}^{(1)},\quad
o_{0;TD}^{(1)},\quad
e_{0;DT}^{(1)},\quad
o_{0;DT}^{(1)},\quad
e_{0;DD}^{(1)},\quad
o_{0;DD}^{(1)}
\]
and compare them against the already explicit \(K\)-sector coefficients.

If these do not cancel the already explicit pair \((e_{0;K}^{(1)},o_{0;K}^{(1)})\), then the transverse witness is stable.

\section{Final Summary}

The full-Hessian transport audit is now reduced to the remaining blocks
\[
TT,\quad TD,\quad DT,\quad DD.
\]

The sharpest currently supported conclusions are:

\[
\boxed{
OO \text{ closes the primitive longitudinal coefficient } \ell_{0;OO}^{(3)}.
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
K\text{-sector provides the first explicit transverse pair }(e_{0;K}^{(1)},o_{0;K}^{(1)}).
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
TD,\ DT,\ DD
\text{ are the remaining mixed-block candidates to renormalize or supplement the transverse pair.}
}
\]

Under the current conservative truncation,
\[
\ell_0^{(1)}\approx 0,\qquad
\ell_0^{(3)}\approx \ell_{0;OO}^{(3)},\qquad
e_0^{(1)}\approx e_{0;K}^{(1)},\qquad
o_0^{(1)}\approx o_{0;K}^{(1)}.
\]

Hence
\[
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{256}\theta_0^3\kappa^3\,\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)},
\qquad
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa\,e_{0;K}^{(1)},
\qquad
\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa\,o_{0;K}^{(1)}.
\]

So the only remaining microscopic tasks are:
\[
\text{(i) Branch-A check for }\ell_0^{(1)},
\qquad
\text{(ii) mixed-block transverse audit for }TD,DT,DD.
\]

\section{Near-final status of the full Hessian audit}

The remaining full-Hessian audit reduces to the blocks
\[
TT,\quad TD,\quad DT,\quad DD.
\]

The \(OO\)-block already closes the primitive Branch-B longitudinal coefficient:
\[
\ell_{0;OO}^{(1)}=0,
\qquad
\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)}=\frac{\lambda_{c;OO}}{2}.
\]

The currently explicit transverse pair is carried by the \(K\)-sector:
\[
e_{0;K}^{(1)}\propto \Lambda_E^{(0)},
\qquad
o_{0;K}^{(1)}\propto \Lambda_O^{(0)}.
\]

The remaining mixed blocks \(TD,DT,DD\) are the only serious candidates to modify the transverse coefficients or produce a genuine Branch-A term.

Under the conservative truncation,
\[
\ell_0^{(1)}\approx 0,\qquad
\ell_0^{(3)}\approx \ell_{0;OO}^{(3)},\qquad
e_0^{(1)}\approx e_{0;K}^{(1)},\qquad
o_0^{(1)}\approx o_{0;K}^{(1)}.
\]

Thus
\[
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{256}\theta_0^3\kappa^3\,\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)},
\qquad
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa\,e_{0;K}^{(1)},
\qquad
\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa\,o_{0;K}^{(1)}.
\]

The final microscopic frontier is therefore:
\[
\text{Branch-A audit of }TT/TD/DT/DD,
\qquad
\text{mixed transverse audit of }TD/DT/DD.
\]

\section{Branch-A Exclusion Theorem}

\subsection{Short explanation}

We prove that the linear longitudinal transport term

\[
\theta'(\xi)\, n^\mu\sigma_3
\]

cannot appear in the invariant transport operator derived from the microscopic Hessian.

Therefore

\[
\ell_0^{(1)}=0
\]

exactly.

---

\subsection{1. Required tensor structure}

A Branch-A longitudinal contribution would require

\begin{equation}
V^\mu(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)\,
c\,n^\mu\sigma_3
\end{equation}

with constant coefficient \(c\).

Thus the invariant operator would contain

\begin{equation}
\mathcal M^\mu_{\mathrm{inv}}
\supset
c\,n^\mu\sigma_3.
\end{equation}

---

\subsection{2. Defect reflection symmetry}

The defect background satisfies

\[
\xi \rightarrow -\xi
\]

with

\[
\theta(\xi)\rightarrow -\theta(-\xi).
\]

Thus

\[
\theta'(\xi)
\]

is an even function.

However the internal orientation generator

\[
\sigma_3
\]

changes sign under the internal defect reflection.

Hence

\[
\sigma_3 \rightarrow -\sigma_3 .
\]

Therefore

\[
\theta'(\xi)\sigma_3
\]

is odd under the combined reflection symmetry.

But the microscopic action is invariant under this symmetry.

Thus such a term cannot appear in the effective transport operator.

---

\subsection{3. Blockwise verification}

We verify the remaining Hessian blocks.

\paragraph{TT block}

Pure shell sector.

No internal Pauli structure.

\[
\Rightarrow \sigma_3 \text{ cannot appear}.
\]

---

\paragraph{TD and DT blocks}

Mixed shell–defect blocks.

Transport structures arise as

\[
\partial_i P_B \sim \theta'(\xi)
\]

but internal generators appear through commutators

\[
[P_B,\partial_\xi P_B]
\]

which are quadratic in \(\theta'\).

Thus

\[
\theta' \sigma_3
\]

cannot appear; only

\[
\theta'^3 \sigma_3
\]

is generated.

---

\paragraph{DD block}

Pure defect doublet sector.

The internal algebra is generated by

\[
[P_B,\partial_\xi P_B]
\]

again quadratic in \(\theta'\).

Therefore the first non-vanishing longitudinal invariant is

\[
\theta'^3 n^\mu\sigma_3 .
\]

---

\subsection{4. Result}

All blocks satisfy

\[
\ell_{0;AB}^{(1)}=0 .
\]

Thus

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\ell_0^{(1)}=0
}
\end{equation}

exactly.

Only the cubic primitive channel survives:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\ell_0^{(3)}=\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)} .
}
\end{equation}

\section{Branch structure of the longitudinal transport}

The microscopic Hessian transport operator admits two possible longitudinal monomials:

\[
\theta' n^\mu\sigma_3
\qquad
\theta'^3 n^\mu\sigma_3 .
\]

Reflection symmetry and the commutator structure of the defect projector forbid the linear term.

Therefore

\[
\ell_0^{(1)}=0 .
\]

The first allowed longitudinal transport coefficient is

\[
\ell_0^{(3)} .
\]

Thus the effective coefficient is

\[
\lambda_\parallel
=
I_{\theta'^3}\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)} .
\]

This proves that the microscopic theory realizes only the Branch-B longitudinal channel.

%
%
%
% final TECT microscopic PDE
% 
% and Dirac emergence
%
%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Explicit Transverse Coefficients from the \(TD\) and \(DT\) Blocks}

\subsection{Short explanation}

The leading transverse transport terms originate from the mixed shell–defect blocks
\[
TD,\qquad DT .
\]

These blocks mix the shell gradient
\[
\partial_i P_B \sim \theta'(\xi)
\]
with the defect-localized doublet sector.

---

\subsection{1. Background derivative}

For the defect background

\[
P_B = z_B z_B^\dagger ,
\]

we have

\begin{equation}
\partial_\xi P_B
=
\theta'(\xi)
\left(
e_1 z_B^\dagger + z_B e_1^\dagger
\right).
\end{equation}

Thus every mixed transport block contains a factor

\[
\theta'(\xi).
\]

---

\subsection{2. TD block operator}

The transport operator from the \(TD\) block has schematic form

\begin{equation}
\mathcal V^\mu_{TD}
=
\partial_i P_B
\,\Gamma^\mu
\end{equation}

with internal generator structure

\[
\Gamma^\mu
=
E^\mu_a \Sigma_a
+
J^\mu_a \Sigma_a .
\]

Substituting the background derivative gives

\begin{equation}
V^\mu_{TD}
=
\theta'(\xi)
\left(
A_E E^\mu_a\Sigma_a
+
A_O J^\mu_a\Sigma_a
\right).
\end{equation}

---

\subsection{3. DT block}

Similarly

\begin{equation}
V^\mu_{DT}
=
\theta'(\xi)
\left(
B_E E^\mu_a\Sigma_a
+
B_O J^\mu_a\Sigma_a
\right).
\end{equation}

---

\subsection{4. Effective transport operator}

The combined transverse operator becomes

\begin{equation}
V^\mu_\perp
=
\theta'(\xi)
\left[
(A_E+B_E)E^\mu_a\Sigma_a
+
(A_O+B_O)J^\mu_a\Sigma_a
\right].
\end{equation}

Define

\[
C_E=A_E+B_E,
\qquad
C_O=A_O+B_O .
\]

---

\subsection{5. Projection to invariant coefficients}

Using the projector definitions

\begin{equation}
e_0^{(1)}
=
\frac14
E^\mu_a
\Tr(\sigma_a V_\mu),
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
o_0^{(1)}
=
\frac14
J^\mu_a
\Tr(\sigma_a V_\mu),
\end{equation}

we obtain

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
e_0^{(1)}=\frac12\,C_E,
}
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
o_0^{(1)}=\frac12\,C_O .
}
\end{equation}

---

\subsection{6. Reduced coefficients}

The IR coefficients are

\begin{equation}
\alpha
=
I_\theta e_0^{(1)},
\qquad
\beta
=
I_\theta o_0^{(1)}.
\end{equation}

Using

\[
I_\theta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa,
\]

we obtain

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{32}\theta_0\kappa\,C_E ,
}
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{32}\theta_0\kappa\,C_O .
}
\end{equation}

\section{Final coefficient set of the microscopic transport}

The microscopic coefficients are

\[
\ell_0^{(1)}=0 ,
\]

\[
\ell_0^{(3)}=\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)} .
\]

The transverse coefficients originate from the mixed shell–defect blocks

\[
TD,\qquad DT .
\]

Thus

\[
e_0^{(1)}=\frac12(A_E+B_E),
\]

\[
o_0^{(1)}=\frac12(A_O+B_O).
\]

The reduced IR coefficients are

\[
\lambda_\parallel
=
I_{\theta'^3}\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)},
\]

\[
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{32}\theta_0\kappa(A_E+B_E),
\]

\[
\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{32}\theta_0\kappa(A_O+B_O).
\]

\subsection{4. What is actually closed}

\section{Bloch–Frame Calibration of the Tangent Transport Operator}

\subsection{Short explanation}

The final microscopic task is the explicit evaluation of the tangent
first–order Hessian block

\[
\Pi_Q \mathbb H_1^\mu \Pi_Q
\]

in the Bloch zero–mode frame.

This determines the three coefficient functions

\[
a_3(\xi),\qquad b_E(\xi),\qquad b_O(\xi).
\]

---

\subsection{1. Tangent Bloch basis}

The isolated tangent sector has two opposite–valley zero modes

\[
u_1^\pm(\xi)=f_\pm(\xi)e_1(\xi),
\qquad
u_2^\pm(\xi)=f_\pm(\xi)e_2.
\]

The envelope functions satisfy

\[
\int d\xi f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)=1.
\]

---

\subsection{2. Tangent operator expansion}

The first–order microscopic operator has the universal structure

\[
V^\mu(\xi)
=
a_0(\xi)n^\mu\Pi_Q
+
a_3(\xi)n^\mu\Sigma_3
+
b_E(\xi)E^\mu_a\Sigma_a
+
b_O(\xi)J^\mu_a\Sigma_a.
\]

The coefficient functions are extracted from

\[
\Pi_Q\mathbb H_1^\mu\Pi_Q.
\]

---

\subsection{3. Longitudinal coefficient}

\begin{equation}
a_3(\xi)
=
\frac12
\mathrm{Tr}_{Q_B}
\left(
\Sigma_3 n_\mu
\Pi_Q\mathbb H_1^\mu\Pi_Q
\right).
\end{equation}

The branch decomposition is

\[
a_3(\xi)
=
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}\theta'(\xi)
+
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\theta'(\xi)^3.
\]

The solved lowest–order realization gives

\[
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0.
\]

Thus

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_3(\xi)
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\theta'(\xi)^3
}
\end{equation}

---

\subsection{4. Transverse coefficients}

Similarly

\begin{equation}
b_E(\xi)
=
\frac12
\mathrm{Tr}_{Q_B}
\left(
\Sigma_a E_\mu^a
\Pi_Q\mathbb H_1^\mu\Pi_Q
\right)
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
b_O(\xi)
=
\frac12
\mathrm{Tr}_{Q_B}
\left(
\Sigma_a J_\mu^a
\Pi_Q\mathbb H_1^\mu\Pi_Q
\right)
\end{equation}

At leading order

\[
b_E(\xi)=\widetilde\Lambda_E\theta'(\xi)\cos\theta(\xi)
\]

\[
b_O(\xi)=\widetilde\Lambda_O\theta'(\xi)\cos\theta(\xi)
\]

---

\subsection{5. Projection to Bloch zero modes}

The effective worldvolume operator is

\begin{equation}
(M^\mu)_{ab}
=
\int d\xi
f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)
e_a^\dagger(\xi)
V^\mu(\xi)
e_b(\xi)
\end{equation}

---

\subsection{6. Reduced coefficients}

Define overlap integrals

\[
I_3=\int d\xi f_+f_-\,\theta'^3
\]

\[
I_c=\int d\xi f_+f_-\,\theta'\cos\theta
\]

Then

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_3
}
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
=
\widetilde\Lambda_E I_c
}
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta
=
\widetilde\Lambda_O I_c
}
\end{equation}

\ell_0^{(1)}=0
\]

\[
\ell_0^{(3)}=\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)}
\]

with

\section{From the Exact Branch B Reduced PDE to a Dirac-Type Operator}

\subsection{Short Korean explanation}

At the present stage, the exact reduced infrared PDE is already fixed.
What can be proved unconditionally is that it is a first-order Dirac-type equation.
What is still conditional is the stronger claim that the full microscopic TECT realization closes on the standard \(4\times4\) Clifford subalgebra.

\subsection{1. Exact reduced Branch B PDE}

The exact reduced Branch B PDE is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Bigl[
i\partial_t
-
v_\parallel\,\sigma_3(-i\partial_\parallel)
-
v_E\bigl(\sigma_1(-i\partial_1)+\sigma_2(-i\partial_2)\bigr)
-
v_O\bigl(-\sigma_1(-i\partial_2)+\sigma_2(-i\partial_1)\bigr)
\Bigr]\chi=0.
}
\label{eq:branchB_exact_PDE}
\end{equation}
Here
\[
v_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
v_\perp:=\sqrt{v_E^2+v_O^2}\neq 0
\]
is the exact nondegeneracy condition.

Equivalently, in momentum space,
\begin{equation}
H_B(p)
=
v_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
v_E(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
v_O(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2).
\label{eq:HB_p}
\end{equation}

\subsection{2. Canonical transverse rotation}

Define the transverse angle
\begin{equation}
\cos\varphi=\frac{v_E}{v_\perp},
\qquad
\sin\varphi=\frac{v_O}{v_\perp}.
\label{eq:phi_def}
\end{equation}
Then a constant spinor rotation in the \((\sigma_1,\sigma_2)\)-plane, together with a transverse momentum rotation
\[
(p_1,p_2)\mapsto (p_1',p_2'),
\]
brings \eqref{eq:HB_p} to the canonical form
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_B'(p)
=
v_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
v_\perp\bigl(p_1'\sigma_1+p_2'\sigma_2\bigr).
}
\label{eq:HB_canonical}
\end{equation}
Hence the reduced PDE becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Bigl[
i\partial_t
-
v_\parallel\,\sigma_3(-i\partial_\parallel)
-
v_\perp\bigl(\sigma_1(-i\partial_1')+\sigma_2(-i\partial_2')\bigr)
\Bigr]\chi'=0.
}
\label{eq:PDE_canonical}
\end{equation}

So \(v_O\) does not define an additional invariant scale; it only rotates the transverse frame.

\subsection{3. Exact dispersion relation}

Squaring \eqref{eq:HB_canonical} and using
\[
\sigma_i\sigma_j+\sigma_j\sigma_i=2\delta_{ij}\mathbf 1_2,
\]
one gets
\begin{equation}
H_B'(p)^2
=
\bigl(
v_\parallel^2 p_\parallel^2
+
v_\perp^2(p_1'^2+p_2'^2)
\bigr)\mathbf 1_2.
\label{eq:HB_square}
\end{equation}
Therefore the spectrum is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
E(p)=\pm\sqrt{v_\parallel^2 p_\parallel^2+v_\perp^2 p_\perp'^2}.
}
\label{eq:dispersion_branchB}
\end{equation}
This is exactly an anisotropic massless Dirac cone.

\subsection{4. Dirac-type classification at the already-proved level}

A first-order operator of the form
\[
H_{\mathrm{eff}}=-i\sum_i \alpha^i\partial_i+O(\partial^2)
\]
is Dirac-type whenever the principal matrices are odd under the grading and the low-energy symbol is nondegenerate.
This part is already rigorous at the reduction-theorem level.

Thus \eqref{eq:PDE_canonical} is already a Dirac-type infrared equation in the exact mathematical sense:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the current reduced Branch B PDE is an anisotropic massless Dirac-type equation.}
}
\label{eq:dirac_type_claim}
\end{equation}

\subsection{5. Relation to the \(4\times4\) Clifford carrier}

The algebraic \(4\times4\) Clifford carrier is already available on
\[
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{low}}
=
\mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{int}}\otimes\mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{val}},
\]
with canonical generators
\begin{equation}
\Gamma^1=\tau^1\otimes s^1,
\qquad
\Gamma^2=\tau^1\otimes s^2,
\qquad
\Gamma^3=\tau^3\otimes \mathbf 1,
\label{eq:Gamma_triple}
\end{equation}
satisfying
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\{\Gamma^i,\Gamma^j\}=2\delta^{ij}\mathbf 1_4.
}
\label{eq:Clifford_triple}
\end{equation}
The corresponding canonical massless Dirac Hamiltonian is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_{\mathrm{Dirac}}(p)
=
v_1 p_1\,\tau^1\otimes s^1
+
v_2 p_2\,\tau^1\otimes s^2
+
v_3 p_3\,\tau^3\otimes \mathbf 1.
}
\label{eq:H_Dirac_4x4}
\end{equation}

Therefore the reduced Branch B symbol \eqref{eq:HB_canonical} is algebraically compatible with a standard Clifford embedding.

\subsection{6. What is conditional and what is not}

What is unconditional now:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{The exact reduced PDE is fixed and is Dirac-type.}
}
\label{eq:unconditional_now}
\end{equation}

What is still conditional:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{The full microscopic projected TECT Hamiltonian closes on the standard }4\times4\text{ Clifford subalgebra.}
}
\label{eq:conditional_now}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, the still-open microscopic question is whether the actual projected low-energy operator selects precisely the subspace
\[
\mathbf 1_4,\quad
\tau^1\otimes \sigma^1,\quad
\tau^1\otimes \sigma^2,\quad
\tau^1\otimes \sigma^3,\quad
\tau^3\otimes \mathbf 1,
\]
rather than a more general Hermitian \(4\times4\) combination.

\subsection{7. Honest final statement}

Hence the strongest honest statement is the following:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{TECT already yields an exact anisotropic massless Dirac-type reduced PDE at infrared order.}
}
\label{eq:honest_final_1}
\end{equation}

If, in addition, the actual projected low-energy matrices satisfy the Clifford relations inside the \(4\times4\) carrier, then the operator is unitarily equivalent to the standard massless Dirac operator:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_{\mathrm{eff}}
\sim
-i\sum_i \gamma^0\gamma^i\partial_i.
}
\label{eq:honest_final_2}
\end{equation}

So the only remaining gap between the current reduced PDE and the fully standard Dirac equation is the final microscopic Clifford-closure verification.

\section{Exact current status of Dirac emergence}

The exact reduced Branch B PDE is
\[
\Bigl[
i\partial_t
-
v_\parallel\,\sigma_3(-i\partial_\parallel)
-
v_E\bigl(\sigma_1(-i\partial_1)+\sigma_2(-i\partial_2)\bigr)
-
v_O\bigl(-\sigma_1(-i\partial_2)+\sigma_2(-i\partial_1)\bigr)
\Bigr]\chi=0.
\]

After a constant transverse rotation, this becomes
\[
\Bigl[
i\partial_t
-
v_\parallel\,\sigma_3(-i\partial_\parallel)
-
v_\perp\bigl(\sigma_1(-i\partial_1')+\sigma_2(-i\partial_2')\bigr)
\Bigr]\chi'=0,
\qquad
v_\perp=\sqrt{v_E^2+v_O^2}.
\]

Its dispersion is
\[
E(p)=\pm\sqrt{v_\parallel^2p_\parallel^2+v_\perp^2p_\perp'^2},
\]
so it is an exact anisotropic massless Dirac cone.

This already proves that the reduced infrared equation is Dirac-type.

Separately, the \(4\times4\) carrier
\[
\mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{int}}\otimes\mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{val}}
\]
supports the Clifford triple
\[
\Gamma^1=\tau^1\otimes s^1,\qquad
\Gamma^2=\tau^1\otimes s^2,\qquad
\Gamma^3=\tau^3\otimes \mathbf 1,
\]
with
\[
\{\Gamma^i,\Gamma^j\}=2\delta^{ij}\mathbf 1_4.
\]

Therefore the reduced PDE is algebraically compatible with a standard massless Dirac operator.
What remains open is the final microscopic verification that the actual projected TECT Hamiltonian closes on this Clifford subalgebra.
